when you say she's a programmer , she did do some , but the real thing is to have said the future is going to be much , much more than this .	當你說她是程式設計師 , 確實有所貢獻 , 但真正重要的是 , 她說未來會遠遠超過這個 。
now , a hundred years later , this guy comes along , alan turing , and in 1936 , and invents the computer all over again .	一百年後 , 這個傢伙出現了 , 艾倫•圖靈 , 1936年 , 再一次發明電腦 。
now , of course , babbage's machine was entirely mechanical .	當然 , babbage的機器是純機械的
turing's machine was entirely theoretical .	turing的機器是理論性的
both of these guys were coming from a mathematical perspective , but turing told us something very important .	這兩個人都是從數學的觀點來的 , 但turing告訴我們一些非常重要的事 。
he laid down the mathematical foundations for computer science , and said , " it doesn't matter how you make a computer . "	他為電腦科學奠定了數學基礎 , 說: 「 不論你怎麼創造電腦都無所謂 。 」
it doesn't matter if your computer's mechanical , like babbage's was , or electronic , like computers are today , or perhaps in the future , cells , or , again , mechanical again , once we get into nanotechnology .	不管你的電腦是不是像babbage那樣 , 或是電子 , 都不重要就像現在的電腦 , 或是未來的電腦 , 或是細胞 , 或是再一次 , 又或者 , 又一次 , 機械性 , 一旦我們進入了奈米科技 。
we could go back to babbage's machine and just make it tiny . all those things are computers .	我們可以回到babbage的機器 , 讓它變得很小 。 這些都是電腦 。
there is in a sense a computing essence .	有一種計算的本質 。
this is called the church–turing thesis .	這叫做church-turing理論
and so suddenly , you get this link where you say this thing babbage had built really was a computer .	突然間 , 你看到一個連結 , 那個連結是babbage建造的機器 , 其實就是電腦 。
in fact , it was capable of doing everything we do today with computers , only really slowly .	事實上 , 它可以做到今天我們用電腦可以做到的所有事情 , 只是真的很慢 。
to give you an idea of how slowly , it had about 1k of memory .	為了讓你知道它有多慢 , 它有大約1k的記憶體 。
it used punch cards , which were being fed in , and it ran about 10 , 000 times slower the first zx81 .	它使用打孔卡 , 也就是被餵食的 , 打孔卡的速度比第一台zx81還要慢一萬倍 。
it did have a ram pack .	它的確有一群ram包 。
you could add on a lot of extra memory if you wanted to .	如果你想要的話 , 你可以加入很多額外的記憶 。
so , where does that bring us today ?	所以 , 這又帶我們到哪裡去 ?
so there are plans .	所以 , 有一些計畫 。
over in swindon , the science museum archives , there are hundreds of plans and thousands of pages of notes written by charles babbage about this analytical engine .	在swindon科學博物館的檔案中 , 有數百個計劃和數千頁的筆記 , 由charlesbabbage撰寫 , 內容是這個分析引擎 。
one of those is a set of plans that we call plan 28 , and that is also the name of a charity that i started with doron swade , who was the curator of computing at the science museum , and also the person who drove the project to build a difference engine , and our plan is to build it .	其中有一系列計畫我們稱之為計劃28這同時也是我和doronswade所創立的一個慈善機構的名字他是科學博物館的管理者還有推動計劃要建造出一個不一樣引擎的人我們的計劃就是建造它
here in south kensington , we will build the analytical engine .	在肯辛頓南部 , 我們會建造分析引擎 。
the project has a number of parts to it .	這個專案有幾個部分 。
one was the scanning of babbage's archive .	第一是掃描babbage的文獻
that's been done . the second is now the study of all of those plans to determine what to build .	這是已經完成的 。 第二個是關於所有計劃的研究 , 來決定要建造什麼 。
the third part is a computer simulation of that machine , and the last part is to physically build it at the science museum .	第三部分是模擬那台機器的電腦 , 最後一部分是在科學博物館裡進行的 。
when it's built , you'll finally be able to understand how a computer works , because rather than having a tiny chip in front of you , you've got to look at this humongous thing and say , " ah , i see the memory operating , i see the cpu operating , i hear it operating . i probably smell it operating . "	當它完成時 , 你會終於能夠理解電腦是如何運作的 , 因為 , 不需要在你面前裝一個小晶片 , 你得要看著這個巨大的東西 , 然後說: 「 啊 , 我看到記憶體在運作 , 我看到cpu在運作 , 我聽見它在運作 。 我聞起來可能在運作 。 」
but in between that we're going to do a simulation .	但在這之間 , 我們將會做一個模擬 。
babbage himself wrote , he said , as soon as the analytical engine exists , it will surely guide the future course of science .	babbage自己寫道:一旦分析引擎真的存在它一定會引導未來的科學發展
of course , he never built it , because he was always fiddling with new plans , but when it did get built , of course , in the 1940s , everything changed .	當然 , 他從來沒有把它做出來 , 因為他總是在微笑新計劃 , 但當它真的在1940年代被做出來時 , 一切都改變了 。
now , i'll just give you a little taste of what it looks like in motion with a video which shows just one part of the cpu mechanism working .	現在 , 我讓各位稍微了解一下它在動作時的樣子 , 這影片展示出的只是cpu的運作過程中的一部分 。
so this is just three sets of cogs , and it's going to add . this is the adding mechanism in action , so you imagine this gigantic machine .	所以這只是三組齒輪 , 它將會加上 。 這是加法的運作 , 所以 , 想像一下這台巨大的機器 。
so , give me five years .	所以 , 給我五年時間 。
before the 2030s happen , we'll have it .	在2030之前 , 我們將會有 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
in this imagefilled talk , yann arthusbertrand displays his three most recent projects on humanity and our habitat stunning aerial photographs in his series " the earth from above , " personal interviews from around the globe featured in his web project " 6 billion others , " and his soontobereleased movie , " home , " which documents human impact on the environment through breathtaking video .	在充滿影像的演說中 , 雅南•阿特伯特蘭展示了他最近三項關於人性的近期作品 , 我們的棲息地在他的系列《地之上》中播出了他的作品《地之上》 , 來自世界各地的個人訪談 , 標題是他的網路《六十億人》 , 及他剛出版的電影 , 《家》 , 將人類對於環境所產生的影響 , 藉由拍攝影像 。
art , climate change , environment , film , future , humanity , media , photography	藝術、氣候變化、環境、未來、人類、媒體、攝影技術等 。
yann arthusbertrand captures fragile earth in wideangle	雅南•亞瑟伯特用寬寬寬的角度捕捉脆弱的地球 。
i have a big impact on the planet to travel here by plane .	我對地球造成很大的影響 , 只要飛機過去 。
i emitted , in the atmosphere , nine tons of co2 ; that is the weight of two elephants .	我在大氣中排放了9噸二氧化碳 , 那是兩隻大象的重量 。
i came here to speak about ecology , and i emitted as much co2 as a frenchman in one year .	我來這裡談談生態學 , 以法國人一年的排放量來排放二氧化碳 。
so what do i have to do ?	所以 , 我該怎麼做 ?
i have to kill a frenchman when i come back at home ?	當我回到家時 , 我得要殺一個法國人 ?
i have to do my carbon offset in another way , like i do every time .	我必須用另一種方式來減碳 , 像我每次都做 。
in fact my work is to show our impact on our planet .	事實上 , 我的工作是展示出我們對地球的影響 。
i'm going to show you some examples of the last pictures i've done in the last year .	我要給你們看一些例子 , 關於我去年拍攝的最後一幅照片 。
alberta sand oil , a lot of pollution .	亞伯達省的油砂 , 很多的污染 。
you know the problem ; we don't want to believe what we know .	你知道問題的所在 ; 我們不想相信已知的事物 。
in alberta people work nonstop , 24 hours by seven to extract as much oil as they can .	在亞伯達省 , 人們一天24小時一班 , 七小時一班輪替 , 為的就是盡可能多抽取石油 。
we know about the end of oil .	我們知道石油終將衰竭
oil sand is not a longterm solution .	油砂不是一個長期解決方案 。
but we use three times more oil than we find every year .	但我們每年使用的石油量卻是三倍之多 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
coral reef in new caledonia .	新克里多尼亞的珊瑚礁 。
100 percent of the coral may be wiped out before 2050 because of global warming .	全部的珊瑚可能在2050年前就因為全球暖化而被消滅了 。
and you know how coral are very sensitive to temperature , and are very important for the biodiversity of the sea .	你知道珊瑚對溫度非常敏感 , 且對海洋的多樣性非常重要 。
north pole . i've done this picture last summer .	北極是我去年夏天拍攝的照片
it was impossible to do this picture 15 years ago .	15年前 , 做這張照片是不可能的 。
now there is a new way open between atlantic and pacific .	現在 , 大西洋和太平洋之間有了一條新路 。
the thickness of the arctic decreased more than 40 percent since 1960 .	自1960年起 , 北極的厚度就下降了超過40% 。
there is a new face of kilimanjaro without ice .	有一種新的面孔 , 沒有冰 。
it lost 80 percent of its ice .	它失去了80%的冰 。
according to scientists , in 100 years all the mountain glacier will be gone .	根據科學家估計 , 在一百年內 , 所有高山的冰河都會消失 。
glaciers are very important for the life on earth .	冰河對地球上的生命非常重要 。
like al gore told you , two billion people live on the water from the glacier of himalaya .	正如阿爾•高爾所說 , 二十億人住在水上是來自喜馬拉雅冰河的 。
return of fish men .	再回來談魚的男人 。
one fifth of human kind depend on fish to live .	五分之一的人類是依靠魚而活 。
today now 70 percent of the fish stock are overexploited .	現今有70%的魚庫被過度利用 。
according to fao , if we don't change our system of fishing the main sea resources will be gone in 2050 .	根據聯合國的資料 , 如果我們不改變捕魚的系統 , 2050年的主要海洋資源就會消失 。
we don't want to believe what we know .	我們不想相信我們所知道的 。
the beautiful picture , by [unclear] in africa .	這張美麗的照片 , 在非洲 。
one human of six have not enough to eat in the world .	世界上每六個人就有一個人沒有足夠的食物 。
one billion people have not enough to eat .	十億人沒有足夠的食物 。
in africa , corn is one of the main foods in many places .	在非洲 , 玉米是許多地方的主要食物之一 。
here in america , 90 percent of the corn cultivated is used to feed animals or to do oil .	在美國 , 培育出來的90%玉米都被用來餵養動物或石油 。
palm tree plantation in borneo .	在婆羅洲棕櫚樹種植園 。
every year we lose 50 thousand square miles in deforestation .	每一年 , 我們在森林砍伐上就損失了五萬平方英里 。
refugee camp in darfur .	達佛的難民營 。
today we have 20 million refugees in the world .	今天全球有兩千萬難民 。
according to the u . n . , we speak about 250 million refugees in 2050 .	根據聯合國 , 2050年我們談到2.5億名難民 。
i always show my pictures in the street .	我總是在街上展示我的照片 。
we have done already 100 exhibitions in the cities .	我們已經在城市裡舉辦了100場展覽 。

12th man: if i was to go back to iraq and speak to the people , i'd have to bow down and kiss their feet .	第十二個男人:如果我回到伊拉克 , 跟伊拉克人民說 , 我就得放下腳下 , 親吻他們的腳 。
just as that woman tried to kiss my feet when we were taking her sons .	就如同那個女人想親吻我的腳 , 我們帶著她的兒子 。
and i feel humbled by their strength .	我因為他們的力量而感到謙卑 。
and i will forever feel a need to make reparations to iraq .	我永遠覺得有必要向伊拉克做報復 。
second woman: dad , mom , i grew up .	第二個女人:爸爸 , 媽媽 , 我長大了 。
you shouldn't worry about me . dad doesn't need to go to work .	你不該擔心我 。 爸爸不需要上班 。
my family . . . what can i say ?	我的家人...我可以說什麼 ?
at the moment , my family is very poor , my life here in shenzhen is just about showing myself that i can earn more and to let my parents stay and have something to live on .	此刻 , 我的家人很窮 , 我在深圳的生活 , 就是要展現自己 , 我可以賺更多錢 , 讓父母去過生活 。

13th man: after seven years now of being in a wheelchair , i've done more in life being in a chair than out of a chair .	第十三個男人:我在輪椅上度過了七年 , 我在輪椅上所完成的人生 , 比坐在椅子外面時多了 。

the name of the movie is " home " " maison . "	這部電影的名字是 「 家 」 。
it is about the state of the planet .	重點是地球的狀況 。
it's a fantastic story of life on the earth .	這是個關於地球生命的奇妙故事 。

video: this earth is four and a half billion years old .	影片:地球已經有45億年的歷史了 。
these plants , several hundred million years old .	這些植物已經有數億年的歷史了 。
and we humans have been walking upright for only 200 thousand years .	我們人類直立行走僅20萬年 。
we've managed to adapt , and have conquered the whole planet .	我們成功地適應並征服了整個地球 。
for generations , we've been raising our children , not unlike millions of other species living beside us .	世世代以來 , 我們養育我們的孩子 , 和我們身邊其他數百萬種物種不同 。
for the past 30 years i've been closely watching the earth and its dwellers from high up in the sky .	過去30年來 , 我從高空中觀察地球和它的居民 。
our life is tied to the wellbeing of our planet .	我們的生活依賴於地球的福祉 。
we depend on water , forests , deserts , oceans .	我們依賴水、森林、沙漠、海洋 。
fishing , breeding , farming are still the world's foremost human occupations .	捕魚、繁殖、農業 , 仍然是世界上最重要的人類職業 。
and what binds us together is far greater than what divides us .	將我們連結在一起的程度遠大於區隔我們的力量 。
we all share the same need for the earth's gifts the same wish to rise above ourselves , and become better .	我們對地球的禮物都有同樣的需求 , 希望能超越我們自己 , 變得更好 。
and yet we carry on raising walls to keep us apart .	然而 , 我們卻繼續在牆壁上築牆 , 來讓我們保持距離 。
today our greatest battle is to protect the natural offerings of our planet .	今天 , 我們最大的戰役就是保護地球的天然資源 。
in less than 50 years we've altered it more thoroughly than in the entire history of mankind .	在不到50年的時間裡 , 我們已經徹底地改變了它 , 遠遠超過了人類的整個歷史 。
half of the world's forests have vanished .	世界上一半的森林已經消失 。
water resources are running low .	水資源的運輸很低 。
intensive farming is depleting soils .	集約農業正在耗盡土壤 。
our energy sources are not sustainable .	我們的能源來源不是永續的 。
the climate is changing .	氣候正在改變 。
we are endangering ourselves .	我們正在危害我們自己 。
we're only trying to improve our lives .	我們只在嘗試改善我們的生活 。
but the wealth gaps are growing wider .	但 , 財富差距越來越大 。
we haven't yet understood that we're going at a much faster pace than the planet can sustain .	我們還沒有意識到 , 我們正以比地球能夠承受的更快的速度前進 。
we know that solutions are available today .	我們知道 , 現今就有解決方案 。
we all have the power to change this trend for the better .	我們都有能力改變這個趨勢 , 變得更好 。
so what are we waiting for ?	所以 , 我們還在等什麼 ?
yab: luc besson is the producer of the movie .	伯特蘭:盧貝森是這部電影的製作人 。

in this accessible talk from tedxboston , richard resnick shows how cheap and fast genome sequencing is about to turn health care upside down .	在tedxboston的演講裡理查.瑞斯尼克揭示出原本和快速基因測序即將顛覆健康照護
dna , biotech , health care , science , technology	dna、生物科技、醫療保健、科學、科技、科技 。
richard resnick: welcome to the genomic revolution	理查德.雷斯尼克:歡迎來到基因組革命 。
ladies and gentlemen , i present to you the human genome .	各位先生女士 , 我為你們介紹人類基因組 。
chromosome one , top left .	染色體一 , 左上角 。
bottom right are the sex chromosomes .	右下角是性別染色體 。
women have two copies of that big x chromosome ; men have the x and , of course , that small copy of the y .	女人有兩份大的x染色體 ; 男人有一份x染色體 , 當然還有一份小的y染色體 。
sorry boys , but it's just a tiny little thing that makes you different .	很抱歉男孩 , 但這只是讓你與眾不同的小東西 。
so if you zoom in on this genome , then what you see , of course , is this double helix structure the code of life spelled out with these four biochemical letters , or we call them bases , right: a , c , g and t .	所以 , 如果你放大這個基因組 , 你會看到 , 當然 , 這個雙螺旋結構──生命的編碼是由四個生化字母所組成 , 我們稱它們為基對 , 右邊是a、c、g、t 。
how many are there in the human genome ? three billion .	人類基因組中有多少基因 ? 30億 。
is that a big number ?	這是一個很大的數字嗎 ?
well , everybody can throw around big numbers .	每個人都可以隨便亂丟大數字 。
but in fact , if i were to place one base on each pixel of this 1280 by 800 resolution screen , we would need 3 , 000 screens to take a look at the genome .	但 , 事實上 , 如果我把這1280年像素上每一個像素上一個基對 , 到800個解析度螢幕上 , 我們需要3000個螢幕來觀察基因組 。
so it's really quite big .	真的很大 。
and perhaps because of its size , a group of people all , by the way , with y chromosomes decided they would want to sequence it .	也許是因為它的大小 , 有一群人有y染色體 , 最後決定要將它排序 。
and so 15 years , actually , and about four billion dollars later , the genome was sequenced and published .	事實上 , 15年後 , 大約40億美金後 , 基因組定序並發表 。
in 2003 , the final version was published , and they keep working on it .	2003年 , 最終的版本出版了 , 還繼續寫下去 。
that was all done on a machine that looks like this .	這一切都是在像這樣的機器上完成的 。
it costs about a dollar for each base a very slow way of doing it .	每個基底都要花1美元這是很慢的做法
well folks , i'm here to tell you that the world has completely changed and none of you know about it .	各位 , 我來這裡是要告訴各位 , 世界已經完全改變了 , 你們都不知道 。
so now what we do is we take a genome , we make maybe 50 copies of it , we cut all those copies up into little 50base reads , and then we sequence them , massively parallel .	所以我們做的是將一個基因組複製50份然後把所有的複製品切成50基對然後我們對它們進行大規模的排序
and then we bring that into software , and we reassemble it and we tell you what the story is .	然後我們將它放入到軟體中 , 再次將它重組 , 我們會告訴你這個故事是什麼 。
and so just to give you a picture of what this looks like , the human genome project: 3 gigabases , right .	給各位看看這看起來是什麼樣子的人類基因組計畫:3gabas , 對吧 ?
one run on one of these machines: 200 gigabases in a week .	一台機器會跑一台:每週200gabas 。
and that 200 is going to change to 600 this summer , and there's no sign of this pace slowing .	那個夏天將會改變到6000年 , 這個步調不會減速 。
so the price of a base , to sequence a base , has fallen 100 million times .	所以要定序基礎的價格已經下跌了一億倍 。
that's the equivalent of you filling up your car with gas in 1998 , waiting until 2011 , and now you can drive to jupiter and back twice .	這就等同於你在1998年把車裝滿氣體 , 等到2011年 , 現在你可以開木星或木星兩次 。
world population , pc placements , the archive of all the medical literature , moore's law , the old way of sequencing , and here's all the new stuff .	世界人口、pc位置、所有醫學文獻的存檔、摩爾定律、舊定律 , 這些是新東西 。
guys , this is a log scale ; you don't typically see lines that go up like that .	各位 , 這是對數比例尺 , 你通常不會看到這些線條向上移動 。
so the worldwide capacity to sequence human genomes is something like 50 , 000 to 100 , 000 human genomes this year .	全世界的人類基因組序列能力今年約有5萬到10萬人 。
and we know this based on the machines that are being placed .	我們從已被放置的機器中知道這一點 。
this is expected to double , triple or maybe quadruple year over year for the foreseeable future .	預計未來會加倍、三倍 , 或四倍 , 年復一年 , 可預見的未來會加倍 。
in fact , there's one lab in particular that represents 20 percent of all that capacity .	事實上 , 有一個實驗室佔了所有能力的20% 。
it's called the beijing genomics institute .	它叫做 " 北京基因研究所 " 。
the chinese are absolutely winning this race to the new moon , by the way .	順道一提 , 中國在贏得這場新月球比賽 。
what does this mean for medicine ?	這對醫學意味著什麼 ?
so a woman is age 37 .	一個女人37歲 。
she presents with stage 2 estrogen receptorpositive breast cancer .	她會出現第二期雌激素受體陽性乳癌 。
she is treated with surgery , chemotherapy and radiation .	她接受了手術、化療和放射治療 。
two years later , she comes back with stage three c ovarian cancer .	兩年後 , 她又發現了三期的卵巢癌 。
unfortunately , treated again with surgery and chemotherapy .	不幸的是 , 再次用手術和化療治療 。
she comes back three years later at age 42 with more ovarian cancer , more chemotherapy .	三年後 , 她在42歲時 , 發現了更多卵巢癌 , 更多的化療 。
six months later , she comes back with acute myeloid leukemia .	六個月後 , 她又患上了急性骨髓性白血病 。
she goes into respiratory failure and dies eight days later .	八天後 , 她陷入呼吸衰竭 ,
so first , the way in which this woman was treated , in as little as 10 years , will look like bloodletting .	首先 , 這個女人被醫治的方式在短短的10年內 , 看起來就像在做血液檢查 。
and it's because of people like my colleague , rick wilson , at the genome institute at washington university , who decided to take a look at this woman postmortem .	因為像我在華盛頓大學基因研究所的同事rickwilson決定要研究這位女士後剖析
and he sequenced , he took skin cells , healthy skin , and cancerous bone marrow , and he sequenced the whole genomes of both of them in a couple of weeks , no big deal .	他進行了基因測序 , 取了皮膚細胞、健康的皮膚、和癌細胞的骨髓 , 並在幾週內完成了這兩組基因組的測序 , 沒什麼大不了 。
and then he compared those two genomes in software , and what he found , among other things , was a deletion , a 2 , 000base deletion across three billion bases in a particular gene called tp53 .	然後他在軟體中比較這兩個基因組 , 他發現 , 在其它事物中 , 有一處耗損 , 在三十億個基因中 , 有一個兩千個鹼基的廢墟 , 在一個叫做tp53的基因上 。
if you have this deleterious mutation in this gene , you're 90 percent likely to get cancer in your life .	如果你有這種基因遺傳變異 , 你一生中就有90%的可能性會得癌症 。
so unfortunately , this doesn't help this woman , but it does have severe , profound if you will , implications to her family .	不幸的是 , 這對女人沒有幫助 , 但這對她的家人來說是很嚴重、很深遠的 。
i mean , if they have the same mutation , and they get this genetic test , and they understand it , then they can go and get regular screens , and they can catch cancer early and potentially live a significantly longer life .	我的意思是 , 如果他們有相同的突變 , 且他們有基因測試 , 且他們能了解 , 那他們就能定期去做篩檢 , 能及早發現癌症 , 很有可能可以過更長的人生 。
let me introduce you now to the beery twins , diagnosed with cerebral palsy at the age of two .	現在讓我來介紹beery雙胞胎 , 在2歲的時候被診斷出腦性麻痺 。
their mom is a very brave woman who didn't believe that the symptoms weren't matching up , and through some heroic efforts and a lot of internet searching , she was able to convince the medical community that , in fact , they had something else .	他們的母親是個非常勇敢的女子 , 她不相信這些症狀與眾不同 , 透過一些英勇的努力和網際網路搜尋 , 她說服了醫療界 , 其實他們還有別的東西 。
what they had was doparesponsive dystonia .	他們的做法是肌張力不全的肌張力不全症 。
and so they were given ldopa , and their symptoms did improve , but they weren't totally asymptomatic .	因此 , 他們得到了左旋多巴 , 他們的症狀確實有改善 , 但他們沒有完全症狀 。
turns out the gentleman in this picture is a guy named joe beery , who was lucky enough to be the cio of a company called life technologies .	這張照片裡的這位先生是joebeery , 他很幸運能成為一家叫做生命科技的公司的執行長 。
they're one of the two companies that makes these massive whole genome sequencing tools .	他們是兩家製造大量基因定序工具的公司之一 。
and so what he did was he got his kids sequenced .	他所做的是讓他的孩子做基因測序 。
and what they found was a series of mutations in a gene called spr , which is responsible for producing serotonin , among other things .	他們發現在一個叫做spr的基因中有一系列突變 , 負責產生血清素和其他物質 。
so on top of ldopa , they gave these kids a serotonin precursor drug , and they're effectively normal now .	所以在左旋多巴的基礎上 , 他們給了這些孩子使用血清素的前身藥物 , 現在他們是正常的 。
guys , this would never have happened without whole genome sequencing .	沒有全部的基因定序 , 這種事不可能實現 。
and at the time this was a few years ago it cost $100 , 000 .	在幾年前 , 它要花10萬美金 。
today it's $10 , 000 . next year it's $1 , 000 .	今天是一萬元 。 明年是一千元 。
the year after it's $100 , give or take a year .	年後的價格是100元 , 或一年 。
that's how fast this is moving .	這是它移動的速度 。
so here's little nick likes batman and squirt guns .	像是蝙蝠俠和水槍 。
and it turns out nick shows up at the children's hospital with this distended belly like a famine victim .	結果發現 , 尼克在兒童醫院出現 , 腹部像饑荒受害者 。
and it's not that he's not eating , it's that when he eats , his intestine basically opens up and feces spill out into his gut .	並不是他不吃東西 , 而是當他吃東西的時候 , 他的腸道會打開然後排泄物外流進他的腸子裡 。
so a hundred surgeries later , he looks at his mom and says , " mom , please pray for me . i'm in so much pain . "	經過一百次手術 , 他看著他的媽媽說: 「 媽媽 , 請祈禱我 , 我很痛苦 。 」
his pediatrician happens to have a background in clinical genetics and he has no idea what's going on , but he says , " let's get this kid's genome sequenced . "	他的小兒科醫生剛好有臨床遺傳學的背景 , 他不知道發生什麼事 , 但他說: 「 我們把這個孩子的基因定序 。 」
and what they find is a singlepoint mutation in a gene responsible for controlling programmed cell death .	他們發現的是在一個控制細胞死亡的基因上 , 有一個單點突變 。
so the theory is that he's having some immunological reaction to what's going on to the food essentially , and that's a natural reaction , which causes some programmed cell death .	所以這個理論是 , 他對本質上發生的事情產生了一種免疫反應 , 這種反應很自然 , 會造成某些編程過的細胞死亡 。
but the gene that regulates that down is broken .	但是管制它的基因已經被破壞了 。
and so this informs , among other things , of course , a treatment for bone marrow transplant , which he undertakes .	這就顯示了其他事物的治療 , 當然是治療骨髓移植的治療 , 這是他所接受的 。
and after nine months of grueling recovery , he's now eating steak with a1 sauce .	他現在用a1醬汁吃牛排了 。
the prospect of using the genome as a universal diagnostic is upon us today .	使用基因組來作為普遍診斷的前景已經來到我們面前了 。
today , it's here .	今天 , 它在這裡 。
and what it means for all of us is that everybody in this room could live an extra five , 10 , 20 years just because of this one thing .	這對我們所有人的意義是這間房間裡的每個人都可以多活個五、十年、二十年 , 只因為這個東西 。
which is a fantastic story , unless you think about humanity's footprint on the planet and our ability to keep up food production .	這真是一個美妙的故事 , 除非你思考人類在地球上的足跡 , 以及我們保持糧食生產的能力 。
so it turns out that the very same technology is also being used to grow new lines of corn , wheat , soybean and other crops that are highly tolerant of drought , of flood , of pests and pesticides .	結果發現 , 同樣的技術也被用來種植新的玉米、小麥、黃豆 , 和其他極能忍受乾旱、洪水、害蟲和殺蟲劑 。
now look , as long as we continue to increase the population , we're going to have to continue to grow and eat genetically modified foods , and that's the only position that i'll take today .	只要我們繼續增加人口 , 我們就得繼續種植和吃基因改造的食物 , 這是我今天唯一要做的事 。

consumer applications for genomics , they will flourish .	基因組學的消費者應用會蓬勃發展

daniel kraft demos his marrow miner a new device that quickly harvests lifesaving bone marrow with minimal pain to the donor . he emphasizes that the adult stem cells found in bone marrow can be used to treat many terminal conditions , from parkinson's to heart disease .	丹尼爾克拉夫特的骨髓移除了骨髓的新設備 , 迅速移除捐贈者的骨髓 , 強調骨髓中發現的成人幹細胞能被用來治療很多絕症狀 , 從帕金森症到心臟疾病 。

so i am a pediatric cancer doctor and stemcell researcher at stanford university where my clinical focus has been bone marrow transplantation .	我是一個小兒科癌醫生 , 也是史丹佛大學的幹細胞研究員 , 我的臨床專注就是骨髓移植 。
now , inspired by jill bolte taylor last year , i didn't bring a human brain , but i did bring a liter of bone marrow .	去年jillboltetaylor給了我靈感 , 我沒有帶一個人腦 , 但我帶了一公升的骨髓 。
and bone marrow is actually what we use to save the lives of tens of thousands of patients , most of whom have advanced malignancies like leukemia and lymphoma and some other diseases .	而骨髓其實就是我們用來拯救數萬名病人的生命 , 當中大部分患有較先進的惡性腫瘤 , 如血癌、淋巴瘤和其他一些疾病 。

so actually how do we harvest this bone marrow ?	所以 , 我們要如何收集這些骨髓 ?
well we have a whole o . r . team , general anesthesia , nurses , and another doctor across from me .	我們有一整個o.r.團隊 , 麻醉醫師 , 護士 , 我對面還有另一位醫生 。
bob's on the table , and we take this sort of small needle , you know , not too big .	鮑勃在桌上 , 我們拿著這個小針 , 你知道的 , 不是太大 。
and the way we do this is we basically place this through the soft tissue , and kind of punch it into the hard bone , into the tuchus that's a technical term and aspirate about 10 mls of bone marrow out , each time , with a syringe .	基本上 , 我們的方法是將它放在軟組織上 , 將它包進硬骨裡 , 插入tuchus , 每次用針筒吸出大約10mls的骨髓 。
and hand it off to the nurse . she squirts it into a tin .	然後把針筒傳給護士 , 她把針筒注射到一個鐵桶裡 。
hands it back to me . and we do that again and again .	把它交還給我 。 我們不斷重複這個動作 。
about 200 times usually .	大約二百次 。
and by the end of this my arm is sore , i've got a callus on my hand , let alone bob , whose rear end looks something more like this , like swiss cheese .	我的手臂末端是sore , 我手上有通話器 , 更不用說bob了 , 他的屁股看起來像這樣 , 像瑞士起司 。
so i'm thinking , you know , this procedure hasn't changed in about 40 years .	所以我在想 , 你知道的 , 這個程序在40年沒有改變 。
and there is probably a better way to do this .	應該有更好的方法來做這件事 。
so i thought of a minimally invasive approach , and a new device that we call the marrow miner .	所以我想出了一個微不足道的新裝置 , 我們稱之為 「 骨髓採取器 」 。
and the marrow miner , the way it works is shown here .	而這個採礦者 , 它的運作方式在這裡 。
our standard seethrough patient .	我們的 「 看完病人 」 標準 。
instead of entering the bone dozens of times , we enter just once , into the front of the hip or the back of the hip .	與其進入骨頭數十次 , 我們只需要進入一次 , 在臀部前面或後面 。
and we have a flexible , powered catheter with a special wire loop tip that stays inside the crunchy part of the marrow and follows the contours of the hip , as it moves around .	我們有一個彈性的導管利用一個特殊的電線循環機針尖固定在骨髓裡隨着臀部的輪廓移動
so it enables you to very rapidly aspirate , or suck out , rich bone marrow very quickly through one hole .	它能讓你快速地渴望 , 或是快速地吸乾富有的骨髓 , 迅速穿過一個洞 。
we can do multiple passes through that same entry .	我們可以通過同一個入口多次進出 。
and , so , very quickly , bob can just get one puncture , local anesthesia , and do this harvest as an outpatient .	所以 , 很快地 , bob只需要一個穿刺 , 局部麻醉 , 並以病人的身分收割為門診 。
so i did a few prototypes . i got a small little grant at stanford .	所以我做了一些原型 。 我得到史丹佛大學的小額獎助 。
and played around with this a little bit .	稍微玩一下這個
and our team members developed this technology .	我們的團隊成員開發了這項技術 。
and eventually we got two large animals , and pig studies .	最後我們有兩個大型動物和豬的研究 。
and we found , to our surprise , that we not only got bone marrow out , but we got 10 times the stem cell activity in the marrow from the marrow miner , compared to the normal device .	令人驚訝的是 , 我們不但沒有得到骨髓 , 還從骨髓採取的幹細胞活性比正常裝置多出十倍 。
this device was just fda approved in the last year .	這個設備在去年才剛被美國食品及藥物管理局批准 。
here is a live patient . you can see it following the flexible curves around .	這是個活生的病患 , 你可以看到 , 它跟著一個柔軟的曲線移動 。
there will be two passes here , in the same patient , from the same hole .	在同一個病人 , 同一個洞裡會有兩條路線 。
this was done under local anesthesia , as an outpatient .	以局部麻醉為例 , 以門診病人的身分完成 。
and we got , again , about three to six times more stem cells than the standard approach done on the same patient .	比起標準方法 , 在同一個病人身上 , 我們得到了大約三到六倍的幹細胞 。
so why should you care ? bone marrow is a very rich source of adult stem cells .	所以 , 為什麼你要在乎 ? 骨髓是非常豐富的成人幹細胞 。
you all know about embryonic stem cells .	你們都知道胚胎幹細胞 。
they've got great potential but haven't yet entered clinical trials .	他們有很大的潛力 , 但還沒有進入臨床試驗 。
adult stem cells are throughout our body , including the bloodforming stem cells in our bone marrow , which we've been using as a form of stemcell therapy for over 40 years .	成體幹細胞遍佈我們身體各處 , 包括我們骨髓中血液循環的幹細胞 , 我們使用這種幹細胞療法已長達四十年 。
in the last decade there's been an explosion of use of bone marrow stem cells to treat the patient's other diseases such as heart disease , vascular disease , orthopedics , tissue engineering , even in neurology to treat parkinson's and diabetes .	在過去十年裡 , 利用骨髓幹細胞治療患者其他疾病如心臟病、血管疾病、組織工程甚至在神經學上治療帕金森氏症和糖尿病 。
we've just come out , we're commercializing , this year , generation 2 . 0 of the marrow miner .	今年 , 我們剛剛公佈 , 我們正在商業化 。 骨髓採取器的2.0 。
the hope is that this gets more stem cells out , which translates to better outcomes .	希望能得到更多幹細胞 , 讓它們翻譯成更好的結果 。
it may encourage more people to sign up to be potential livesaving bone marrow donors .	可能會鼓勵更多人登記成為能拯救生命的骨髓捐贈者 。
it may even enable you to bank your own marrow stem cells , when you're younger and healthier , to use in the future should you need it .	甚至可能讓你在未來儲存你自己的骨髓幹細胞 , 當你更年輕、更健康時 , 用在未來你需要它 。
and ultimately and here's a picture of our bone marrow transplant survivors , who come together for a reunion each year at stanford .	最後這是一張我們骨髓移植受害者的照片 , 他們每年都會在史丹佛聚會 。
hopefully this technology will let us have more of these survivors in the future .	希望這項技術能讓我們未來能有更多這些倖存者 。
physicist and surfer garrett lisi presents a controversial new model of the universe that just maybe answers all the big questions . if nothing else , it's the most beautiful 8dimensional model of elementary particles and forces you've ever seen .	物理學家和衝浪者garetlisi提出了一個對宇宙的爭議性的新模型 , 它可能會回答所有大問題 。 如果其他 , 它是你見過最美麗的基本粒子和力量的8維模型 。
physics , science , technology	物理、科學、科技 ,
garrett lisi on his theory of everything	伽利特•里西用他對萬物的理論所做的一切理論 。
whoa , dude . check out those killer equations . sweet .	喔 , 老兄 。 看看這些殺手級的方程式 。 甜點 。
actually , for the next 18 minutes i'm going to do the best i can to describe the beauty of particle physics without equations .	在接下來的18分鐘裡我要盡我所能描述粒子物理的美好而不用方程式
it turns out there's a lot we can learn from coral .	事實證明 , 我們能從珊瑚身上學到很多東西 。
coral is a very beautiful and unusual animal .	珊瑚是非常美麗又特別的動物 。
each coral head consists of thousand of individual polyps .	每個珊瑚都有成千上萬的珊瑚樣本 。
these polyps are continually budding and branching into genetically identical neighbors .	這些珊瑚會不斷地繁殖和分裂變成基因相同的鄰居 。
if we imagine this to be a hyperintelligent coral , we can single out an individual and ask him a reasonable question .	如果我們想像這珊瑚是超級聰明的珊瑚 , 我們可以找個人來問他一個合理的問題 。
we can ask how exactly he got to be in this particular location compared to his neighbors if it was just chance , or destiny , or what ?	我們可以問 , 相較於他的鄰居 , 他究竟是如何變成這樣 ? 如果只是機會 , 或者只是命運 , 或者是甚麼 ?
now , after admonishing us for turning the temperature up too high , he would tell us that our question was completely stupid .	在我們收到全球暖化的警告之後 , 他會告訴我們 , 我們的問題完全是愚蠢的 。
these corals can be quite kind of mean , you see , and i have surfing scars to prove that .	這些珊瑚可能是相當重要的 , 你看 , 而我有衝浪疤痕可以證明這一點 。
but this polyp would continue and tell us that his neighbors were quite clearly identical copies of him .	但這珊瑚會繼續告訴我們 , 他的鄰居和他一模一樣 。
that he was in all these other locations as well , but experiencing them as separate individuals .	他和其他地方一樣 , 都和別人一樣 , 但他們也體驗到是不同的人 。
for a coral , branching into different copies is the most natural thing in the world .	對珊瑚來說 , 分支成不同的複製品是世界上最自然的東西 。
unlike us , a hyperintelligent coral would be uniquely prepared to understand quantum mechanics .	和我們不同的是高智商的珊瑚已準備好要了解量子力學 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics very accurately describes how our universe works .	量子力學的數學方法非常準確地描述我們的宇宙如何運作 。
and it tells us our reality is continually branching into different possibilities , just like a coral .	它告訴我們現實世界和珊瑚一樣 , 不斷地分裂成不同的可能性 。
it's a weird thing for us humans to wrap our minds around , since we only ever get to experience one possibility .	對我們人類來說 , 把心思包起來是很奇怪的 , 因為我們只能體驗一種可能性 。
this quantum weirdness was first described by erwin schrödinger and his cat .	這種量子力學的奇特現象最早是由薛丁格和他的貓提出來的 。
the cat likes this version better .	貓更喜歡這個版本 。
in this setup , schrödinger is in a box with a radioactive sample that , by the laws of quantum mechanics , branches into a state in which it is radiated and a state in which it is not .	在這個裝置中 , 薛丁格處於一個放射性樣本的盒子中 , 根據量子力學的定律 , 將分支延伸到一個狀態 , 它是放射線的狀態 , 而這個狀態並不是這樣的 。
in the branch in which the sample radiates , it sets off a trigger that releases poison and schrödinger is dead .	在散布的枝幹中 , 釋放毒氣 , 薛丁格就死了 。
but in the other branch of reality , he remains alive .	但在現實的另一個分支裡 , 他仍然活著 。
these realities are experienced separately by each individual .	每個個體都會接觸到這些實相 。
as far as either can tell , the other one doesn't exist .	不管怎麼說 , 另一個都不存在 。
this seems weird to us , because each of us only experiences an individual existence , and we don't get to see other branches .	這對我們來說很奇怪 , 因為我們每個人的經驗都只是單獨的存在 , 而我們看不到其他的分支 。
it's as if each of us , like schrödinger here , are a kind of coral branching into different possibilities .	彷彿我們每一個人 , 像薛丁格一樣 , 都是珊瑚分裂成不同的可能性 。
the mathematics of quantum mechanics tells us this is how the world works at tiny scales .	量子力學的數學理論告訴我們這就是微小世界運作的方式 。
it can be summed up in a single sentence: everything that can happen , does .	可以用一句話來總結:所有可能發生的事 , 都會發生 。
but this does not mean everything happens .	但這並不表示所有事情都會發生 。
the rest of physics is about describing what can happen and what can't .	物理學的其他部分則是描述什麼會發生 , 什麼不會 。
what physics tells us is that everything comes down to geometry and the interactions of elementary particles .	物理學告訴我們一切都可用幾何學以及基本粒子的相互作用
and things can happen only if these interactions are perfectly balanced .	唯有這些互動是完全平衡的才能發生 。
now i'll go ahead and describe how we know about these particles , what they are and how this balance works .	現在我要描述一下我們對這些粒子的了解它們是什麼以及它們的平衡是如何運作的
in this machine , a beam of protons and antiprotons are accelerated to near the speed of light and brought together in a collision , producing a burst of pure energy .	在這個機器中質子和反質子被加速到接近光速的速度然後相撞產生出一股巨大的純能量
this energy is immediately converted into a spray of subatomic particles , with detectors and computers used to figure out their properties .	這種能量馬上被轉換成亞原子粒子的噴射 , 探測器和電腦曾經想出它們的性質 。
this enormous machine the large hadron collider at cern in geneva has a circumference of 17 miles and , when it's operating , draws five times as much power as the city of monterey .	這個在日內瓦歐洲核子研究中心的大型強子對撞機周長有17英里 , 當它在運作時 , 所產生的能量相當於蒙特雷市的5倍 。
we can't predict specifically what particles will be produced in any individual collision .	我們無法精確地預測哪些粒子會在每一次碰撞中產生 。
quantum mechanics tells us all possibilities are realized .	量子力學告訴我們所有可能性
but physics does tell us what particles can be produced .	但物理學告訴我們哪些粒子會被製造出來 。
these particles must have just as much mass and energy as is carried in by the proton and antiproton .	這些粒子的質子和能量一定都是由質子和反質子所帶的 。
any particles more massive than this energy limit aren't produced , and remain invisible to us .	任何的粒子都比這個能量極限所產生的質量都比這個能量極限所產生的質量都更大 , 且我們仍然是看不見的 。
this is why this new particle accelerator is so exciting .	這就是為什麼這種新的粒子加速器如此令人興奮 。
it's going to push this energy limit seven times beyond what's ever been done before , so we're going to get to see some new particles very soon .	它將超越過去七倍的能量極限於能量 , 所以我們很快就會看到新的粒子 。
but before talking about what we might see , let me describe the particles we already know of .	但在談我們可能看到什麼之前 , 先讓我描述一下我們已經知道的粒子 。
there's a whole zoo of subatomic particles .	亞原子的所有動物園都有 。
most of us are familiar with electrons .	我們大多對電子很熟悉
a lot of people in this room make a good living pushing them around .	在這房間裡的很多人過著良好的生活
but the electron also has a neutral partner called the neutrino , with no electric charge and a very tiny mass .	但電子有個中性夥伴叫做微中子 , 沒有電荷 , 質量很小 。
in contrast , the upanddown quarks have very large masses , and combine in threes to make the protons and neutrons inside atoms .	相較之下 , 上夸克有較大的質量 , 把三個夸克結合在一起 , 形成原子中的質子和中子 。
all of these matter particles come in left and righthanded varieties , and have antiparticle partners that carry opposite charges .	所有這些粒子都分成左右兩類 , 還有攜帶相反電荷的反粒子夥伴 。
these familiar particles also have less familiar second and third generations , which have the same charges as the first but have much higher masses .	這些熟悉的粒子還有比較不熟悉的第二代和第三代電量和第一代相同但質量較高
these matter particles all interact with the various force particles .	這些物質粒子都會和不同的力子產生交互作用 。
the electromagnetic force interacts with electrically charged matter via particles called photons .	透過光子 , 電磁力會和帶電粒子產生反應 。
there is also a very weak force called , rather unimaginatively , the weak force , that interacts only with lefthanded matter .	另外還有一種非常微弱的力量叫做微弱的力量只能和左旋的物質相互作用
the strong force acts between quarks which carry a different kind of charge , called color charge , and come in three different varieties: red , green and blue .	夸克之間的強力作用力 , 帶有不同的載荷 , 稱為顏色載荷 , 由三種類別組成紅色、綠色和藍色 。
you can blame murray gellmann for these names they're his fault .	你可以怪murraygellmann , 因為這些名字是他的錯 。
finally , there's the force of gravity , which interacts with matter via its mass and spin .	最後 , 還有重力 , 透過質量和旋轉 , 和物質產生交互作用 。
the most important thing to understand here is that there's a different kind of charge associated with each of these forces .	最重要的是每一種力都對應有不同的載荷 。
these four different forces interact with matter according to the corresponding charges that each particle has .	這四種力通過各自粒子所攜帶的載荷與物質相互作用
a particle that hasn't been seen yet , but we're pretty sure exists , is the higgs particle , which gives masses to all these other particles .	一種還沒被看見的粒子 , 但我們很確定存在的存在 , 是希格斯粒子 , 它給予所有其他粒子的質量 。
the main purpose of the large hadron collider is to see this higgs particle , and we're almost certain it will .	大型強子對撞機的主要目的是要看到希格斯粒子 , 我們幾乎可以確定會如此 。
but the greatest mystery is what else we might see .	但最大的奧秘在於我們還能看到什麼 。
and i'm going to show you one beautiful possibility towards the end of this talk .	我要向你們展示一個美麗的可能性來到演講的尾聲 。
now , if we count up all these different particles using their various spins and charges , there are 226 .	如果我們用不同的自旋和載荷計算出所有不同的粒子總共有226個
that's a lot of particles to keep track of .	可以追蹤的就是許多粒子 。
and it seems strange that nature would have so many elementary particles .	大自然擁有這麼多的基本粒子是很奇怪的 。
but if we plot them out according to their charges , some beautiful patterns emerge .	但如果我們依據他們的載荷把它們畫出來 , 一些美麗的圖案就會出現 。
the most familiar charge is electric charge .	最熟悉的載荷是電荷
electrons have an electric charge , a negative one , and quarks have electric charges in thirds .	電子有電荷 , 負電荷而夸克在三分之一就有電荷
so when two up quarks and a down quark are combined to make a proton , it has a total electric charge of plus one .	所以當兩個上夸克和一個下夸克結合在一起就產生了一個質子 , 它的電荷總共為一個質子 。
these particles also have antiparticles , which have opposite charges .	這些粒子還有反粒子 , 它們也有相反的載荷 。
now , it turns out the electric charge is actually a combination of two other charges: hypercharge and weak charge .	結果發現 , 電荷實際上是另兩種載荷的結合超荷和弱荷
if we spread out the hypercharge and weak charge and plot the charges of particles in this twodimensional charge space , the electric charge is where these particles sit along the vertical direction .	如果我們把超荷和弱荷分開在這個二度載荷空間中畫出粒子的載荷電荷就是這些粒子在垂直方向的位置
the electromagnetic and weak forces interact with matter according to their hypercharge and weak charge , which make this pattern .	電磁力和弱力通過超荷和弱荷與物質相互作用而形成這個模式
this is called the unified electroweak model , and it was put together back in 1967 .	這叫做電弱統一模型 , 於1967年提出 。
the reason most of us are only familiar with electric charge and not both of these is because of the higgs particle .	因為希格斯粒子的緣故我們只對電荷有瞭解卻不是因為希格斯粒子
the higgs , over here on the left , has a large mass and breaks the symmetry of this electroweak pattern .	左邊的希格斯粒子有很大的質量打破了電弱圖案的對稱性 。
it makes the weak force very weak by giving the weak particles a large mass .	它的弱力之所以脆弱 , 是因為它給予弱粒子一個大質量 。
since this massive higgs sits along the horizontal direction in this diagram , the photons of electromagnetism remain massless and interact with electric charge along the vertical direction in this charge space .	由於大量的希格斯粒子在水平方向分佈電磁力的光子仍然沒有質量而且在載荷空間中與電荷相互作用
so the electromagnetic and weak forces are described by this pattern of particle charges in twodimensional space .	所以電磁力和弱力在這個二度空間中通過粒子載荷的型式描述出來 。
we can include the strong force by spreading out its two charge directions and plotting the charges of the force particles in quarks along these directions .	我們可以把強力沿兩個載荷的方向表示出來然後將載荷用夸克形式沿這些方向畫出來
the charges of all known particles can be plotted in a fourdimensional charge space , and projected down to two dimensions like this so we can see them .	所有已知粒子的載荷可以在四度空間中畫出來然後投影到二度空間以便我們能看到
whenever particles interact , nature keeps things in a perfect balance along all four of these charge directions .	每當粒子相互作用 , 大自然就在四個載荷方向上保持完美的平衡 。
if a particle and an antiparticle collide , it creates a burst of energy and a total charge of zero in all four charge directions .	如果粒子和反粒子相撞 , 它會產生能量爆炸 , 四個電荷方向都是零電荷 。
at this point , anything can be created as long as it has the same energy and maintains a total charge of zero .	此時 , 任何東西都可以產生 , 只要能量相同 , 並且保持總載荷是零 。
for example , this weak force particle and its antiparticle can be created in a collision .	比如 , 這個弱子和它的反粒子可以在碰撞中產生 。
in further interactions , the charges must always balance .	進一步的相互作用中載荷必須保持平衡
one of the weak particles could decay into an electron and an antineutrino , and these three still add to zero total charge .	其中一個弱子可以衰退成一個電子和一個反中微子而這三個仍然是零電荷
nature always keeps a perfect balance .	大自然總是保持完美的平衡 。
so these patterns of charges are not just pretty .	所以這些電荷的型式不只漂亮 。
they tell us what interactions are allowed to happen .	它們告訴我們什麼樣的互動是允許的 。
and we can rotate this charge space in four dimensions to get a better look at the strong interaction , which has this nice hexagonal symmetry .	我們可以在四度空間中旋轉載荷空間得到更好的觀察強相互作用它有很好的對稱性
in a strong interaction , a strong force particle , such as this one , interacts with a colored quark , such as this green one , to give a quark with a different color charge this red one .	在強相互作用中 , 強力粒子 , 比如這個 , 會和有色夸克互動 , 比如這個綠色的 , 給夸克一個不同的顏色載荷這個紅色的夸克 。
and strong interactions are happening millions of times each second in every atom of our bodies , holding the atomic nuclei together .	強相互作用每秒鐘會在我們身體的每個原子中發生數百萬次 , 將原子核結合在一起 。
but these four charges corresponding to three forces are not the end of the story .	但和三種力量相對應的這四種載荷還不是終點 。
we can also include two more charges corresponding to the gravitational force .	我們還可以把多兩個載荷放進重力的相對位置 。
when we include these , each matter particle has two different spin charges , spinup and spindown .	當我們將它們納入時 , 每個粒子的旋轉載荷有兩個不同的旋轉載荷、旋轉和自旋向 。
so they all split , and give a nice pattern in sixdimensional charge space .	所以它們全都分開了 , 在六度載荷空間中形成一個很好的圖案 。
we can rotate this pattern in six dimensions , and see that it's quite pretty .	我們可以在六度空間中旋轉這個圖案 , 看看它是很漂亮的 。
right now , this pattern matches our best current knowledge of how nature is built at the tiny scales of these elementary particles .	目前 , 這個圖案符合我們目前對於大自然如何在小尺度下建構的最佳知識 。
this is what we know for certain .	這是我們很確定的事 。
some of these particles are at the very limit of what we've been able to reach with experiments .	其中的一些粒子在實驗中非常受限 。
from this pattern , we already know the particle physics of these tiny scales . the way the universe works with these tiny scales is very beautiful .	從這個模式中 , 我們已經知道這些微小尺度的粒子學 。 宇宙運作的方式是非常漂亮的 。
but now i'm going to discuss some new and old ideas about things we don't know yet .	但是現在我要來談一些關於我們還不知道的新舊觀念 。
we want to expand this pattern using mathematics alone , and see if we can get our hands on the whole enchilada .	我們想要只用數學方法來擴展這個模式 , 看看我們能否把我們的手放到全芝加拿大 。
we want to find all the particles and forces that make a complete picture of our universe .	我們想要找到構成宇宙的所有粒子和力量 。
and we want to use this picture to predict new particles that we'll see when experiments reach higher energies .	我們想用這張圖來預測新的粒子 , 當試驗達到高能量時 , 我們會看到的粒子 。
so there's an old idea in particle physics that this known pattern of charges , which is not very symmetric , could emerge from a more perfect pattern that gets broken similar to how the higgs particle breaks the electroweak pattern to give electromagnetism .	在粒子物理學中有一個古老的想法 , 就是這種不對稱的載荷圖案 , 可能會從一個更完美的圖案中產生出來 , 類似希格斯粒子如何打破了電弱圖案 , 以產生電磁力 。
in order to do this , we need to introduce new forces with new charge directions .	為了達成這個目的 , 我們需要引進新的載荷方向 。
when we introduce a new direction , we get to guess what charges the particles have along this direction , and then we can rotate it in with the others .	當我們導入一個新的方向時 , 我們要猜測在這個方向上粒子的載荷 , 接著我們就可以讓它和其他粒子一起旋轉 。
if we guess wisely , we can construct the standard charges in six charge dimensions as a broken symmetry of this more perfect pattern in seven charge dimensions .	若我們猜對的話 , 我們可以在六度載荷空間中建構標準載荷 , 作為七度載荷空間中最完美的對稱基礎 。
this particular choice corresponds to a grand unified theory introduced by pati and salam in 1973 .	在1973年 , 帕蒂和薩拉姆提出了這個統一理論 。
when we look at this new unified pattern , we can see a couple of gaps where particles seem to be missing .	當我們看到這個新的合成圖案 , 我們可以看到一些粒子似乎缺少的空隙 。
this is the way theories of unification work .	這就是統一理論的原理 。
a physicist looks for larger , more symmetric patterns that include the established pattern as a subset .	物理學家將已有的結構作為子集 , 尋找較大、較對稱的形狀 。
the larger pattern allows us to predict the existence of particles that have never been seen .	這個更大的結構 , 可以讓我們預測從未見過的粒子的存在 。
this unification model predicts the existence of these two new force particles , which should act a lot like the weak force , only weaker .	這種統一模型預測了這兩種新力粒子的存在 , 它應和弱力很相似 , 只是比較弱 。
now we can rotate this set of charges in seven dimensions and consider an odd fact about the matter particles: the second and third generations of matter have exactly the same charges in sixdimensional charge space as the first generation .	我們可以在七度空間中旋轉這個載荷集 , 考慮到關於粒子的奇怪現象:在六度載荷空間中 , 物質的第二代和第三代物質擁有和第一代物質擁有完全一樣的載荷 。
these particles are not uniquely identified by their six charges .	這些粒子的獨特性不是從它們的六個載荷來辨識出來的 。
they sit on top of one another in the standard charge space .	在標準載荷空間中 , 它們會彼此疊加 。
however , if we work in eightdimensional charge space , then we can assign unique new charges to each particle .	然而 , 如果我們在八度載荷空間中工作 , 我們就能對每個粒子分配出獨特的新載荷 。
then we can spin these in eight dimensions , and see what the whole pattern looks like .	然後在八度空間中旋轉看看整體的圖案是什麼樣子
here we can see the second and third generations of matter now related to the first generation by a symmetry called " triality . "	在這裡 , 我們可以看到物質的第二代和第三代通過一種稱作 「 三重性 」 的對稱關係 。
this particular pattern of charges in eight dimensions is actually part of the most beautiful geometric structure in mathematics .	在八度中的這個特殊的載荷圖案 , 其實是數學中最美麗的幾何結構之一 。
it's a pattern of the largest exceptional lie group , e8 .	這是最大的例外說謊團體e8的圖案
this lie group is a smooth , curved shape with 248 dimensions .	李群是光滑曲線形的248維度 。
each point in this pattern corresponds to a symmetry of this very complex and beautiful shape .	圖案的每一點都對應到這個複雜而美麗的形狀的對稱性 。
one small part of this e8 shape can be used to describe the curved spacetime of einstein's general relativity , explaining gravity .	e8的一小部分可以用來描述愛因斯坦廣義相對論中用來解釋重力的扭曲時空
together with quantum mechanics , the geometry of this shape could describe everything about how the universe works at the tiniest scales .	與量子力學一起 , 這個形狀的幾何形狀就能描述宇宙如何以最小的尺度運作 。
the pattern of this shape living in eightdimensional charge space is exquisitely beautiful , and it summarizes thousands of possible interactions between these elementary particles , each of which is just a facet of this complicated shape .	這種圖案存在於八度載荷空間中是如此精緻美麗 , 它可以總結成千上萬的基本粒子間的相互作用 , 每一個都只是這個複雜形狀的一個平面 。
as we spin it , we can see many of the other intricate patterns contained in this one .	當我們轉動它時 , 可以看到其中許多錯綜複雜的圖案 。
and with a particular rotation , we can look down through this pattern in eight dimensions along a symmetry axis and see all the particles at once .	有了特定的旋轉我們可以在八度空間沿一個對稱軸觀察這個圖案同時看到所有粒子
it's a very beautiful object , and as with any unification , we can see some holes where new particles are required by this pattern .	這是個非常美麗的物體 , 就像任何統一一樣 , 我們可以看到一些洞 , 那裡的新粒子是這個圖案所需要的 。
there are 20 gaps where new particles should be , two of which have been filled by the patisalam particles .	新粒子的空隙有20個空隙 , 其中兩個已經被帕翠西亞姆粒子填補過 。
from their location in this pattern , we know that these new particles should be scalar fields like the higgs particle , but have color charge and interact with the strong force .	從圖案的位置 , 我們知道這些新粒子應該是像希格斯粒子那樣的稀少場域 , 但它們有顏色載荷 , 和強力相互作用 。
filling in these new particles completes this pattern , giving us the full e8 .	在這些新粒子中填滿了這個圖案 , 讓我們得到完整的e8 。
this e8 pattern has very deep mathematical roots .	這個e8圖案有著深厚的數學根基 。
it's considered by many to be the most beautiful structure in mathematics .	它被許多人認為是數學界中最美麗的結構 。
it's a fantastic prospect that this object of great mathematical beauty could describe the truth of particle interactions at the smallest scales imaginable .	這個偉大的數學美學之物有個驚人的前景可以在最小的尺度下描述粒子互動的真相
and this idea that nature is described by mathematics is not at all new .	而這個被數學描述的概念 , 並不是新的 。
in 1623 , galileo wrote this: " nature's grand book , which stands continually open to our gaze , is written in the language of mathematics .	1623年 , 伽利略寫道: 「 大自然的孫子書 , 一直敞開我們的凝視 , 都是用數學的語言寫出來的 。
its characters are triangles , circles and other geometrical figures , without which it is humanly impossible to understand a single word of it ; without these , one is wandering around in a dark labyrinth . "	它的角色是三角形、圓形和其他幾何形狀 , 沒有了這些人在人力所能理解的單字 ; 沒有了這些 , 人會在黑暗的迷宮中四處遊蕩 。 」
i believe this to be true , and i've tried to follow galileo's guidance in describing the mathematics of particle physics using only triangles , circles and other geometrical figures .	我相信這是真的我曾試過按照伽利略的指引用三角形圓形和其他的幾何形狀來描述粒子物理學的數學性
of course , when other physicists and i actually work on this stuff , the mathematics can resemble a dark labyrinth .	當然 , 當我和其他物理學家在研究這些東西時數學就像一個黑暗的迷宮
but it's reassuring that at the heart of this mathematics is pure , beautiful geometry .	但確保數學的核心是純粹美麗的幾何學 。
joined with quantum mechanics , this mathematics describes our universe as a growing e8 coral , with particles interacting at every location in all possible ways according to a beautiful pattern .	與量子力學結合 , 這個數學把我們的宇宙描述成一個不斷成長的e8珊瑚 , 每個地方的粒子會根據美麗的圖案在各個地方產生交互作用 。
and as more of the pattern comes into view using new machines like the large hadron collider , we may be able to see whether nature uses this e8 pattern or a different one .	若用大型強子對撞機來觀察更多圖案 , 我們可能會看到 , 大自然使用這種e8圖案或另一種圖案 。
this process of discovery is a wonderful adventure to be involved in .	這個發現的過程是一個奇妙的探險 。
if the lhc finds particles that fit this e8 pattern , that will be very , very cool .	如果對撞機發現了符合e8圖案的粒子那就太酷了
if the lhc finds new particles , but they don't fit this pattern well , that will be very interesting , but bad for this e8 theory .	如果對撞機發現了新粒子 , 但不符合這個圖案 , 那會非常有趣 , 但對e8理論不利 。
and , of course , bad for me personally .	當然 , 對我個人來說也不好 。
now how bad would that be ?	那會多糟 ?
well , pretty bad .	嗯 , 非常糟糕 。
but predicting how nature works is a very risky game .	但預測大自然如何運作是很冒險的遊戲 。
this theory and others like it are long shots .	這個理論和其他類型的理論都是很長的點擊 。
one does a lot of hard work knowing that most of these ideas probably won't end up being true about nature .	一個做了很多辛苦的工作 , 知道大部份這些想法最終可能不會成真 。
that's what doing theoretical physics is like: there are a lot of wipeouts .	理論物理就是這樣子的:有很多的無花果 。
in this regard , new physics theories are a lot like startup companies .	這樣看來 , 新物理理論和新創公司很像 。
as with any large investment , it can be emotionally difficult to abandon a line of research when it isn't working out .	如同任何大型投資一樣 , 在失敗的情況下 , 在情感上很難放棄一系列的研究 。
but in science , if something isn't working , you have to toss it out and try something else .	但在科學上 , 如果沒有用 , 就得要丟掉它 , 嘗試其他東西 。
now , the only way to maintain sanity and achieve happiness in the midst of this uncertainty is to keep balance and perspective in life .	要維持理智並在不確定中獲得幸福 , 唯一的方法就是在人生中保持平衡和觀點 。
i've tried the best i can to live a balanced life .	我已經盡全力去過一個平衡的生活 。
i try to balance my life equally between physics , love and surfing my own three charge directions .	我試著在物理、愛、衝浪中找到平衡 , 用我自己的三個載荷方向 。
this way , even if the physics i work on comes to nothing , i still know i've lived a good life .	這樣一來 , 即使我研究的物理學一點都沒用 , 我仍然知道我過得很好 。
and i try to live in beautiful places .	我試著住在美麗的地方 。
for most of the past ten years i've lived on the island of maui , a very beautiful place .	過去十年我大部分時間都住在毛伊島一個非常美麗的地方
now it's one of the greatest mysteries in the universe to my parents how i managed to survive all that time without engaging in anything resembling fulltime employment .	現在 , 這是我父母最大的謎題之一 , 我是如何在沒有一個全職工作的情況下活下來的 。
i'm going to let you in on that secret .	我要告訴你們這個秘密 。
this was a view from my home office on maui .	這是我在毛伊島的家庭辦公室的照片 。
and you may have noticed that these beautiful views are similar , but in slightly different places .	你可能已經注意到 , 這些美麗的景觀是相似的 , 但在稍微不同的地方 。
that's because this used to be my home and office on maui .	因為這曾經是我在毛伊島的家和辦公室 。
i've chosen a very unusual life .	我選擇了一種很不尋常的人生 。
but not worrying about rent allowed me to spend my time doing what i love .	但不用擔心房租 , 讓我可以花時間做我愛的事 。
living a nomadic existence has been hard at times , but it's allowed me to live in beautiful places and keep a balance in my life that i've been happy with .	有時 , 過著流浪的生活很艱苦 , 但它讓我能住在美麗的地方 , 並在我的人生保持平衡 。
it allows me to spend a lot of my time hanging out with hyperintelligent coral .	它讓我可以花很多時間和超級聰明的珊瑚在一起 。
but i also greatly enjoy the company of hyperintelligent people .	但我也很享受超級聰明人的公司 。
so i'm very happy to have been invited here to ted .	我很高興能被邀請到這裡來ted 。
chris anderson: i probably understood two percent of that , but i still absolutely loved it . so i'm going to sound dumb .	克里斯•安德森:我大概明白其中2% , 但我還是很喜歡它 。 所以我要聽起來很笨 。
your theory of everything garrett lisi: i'm used to coral .	你的萬物理論:我很習慣珊瑚 。
ca: that's right . the reason it's got a few people at least excited is because , if you're right , it brings gravity and quantum theory together .	克:沒錯 。 至少有少數人感到興奮的原因是 , 如果你是對的 , 它會把重力和量子理論結合在一起 。
so are you saying that we should think of the universe , at its heart that the smallest things that there are , are somehow an e8 object of possibility ?	所以你是不是在說我們應該以宇宙為核心去想 , 最小的事物有可能就是e8物體 ?
i mean , is there a scale to it , at the smallest scale , or . . . ?	我的意思是 , 在最小的尺度下 , 會不會有一個尺寸 ?
gl: well , right now the pattern i showed you that corresponds to what we know about elementary particle physics that already corresponds to a very beautiful shape .	gl:嗯 , 我剛剛給你們看的圖案與我們所知的基本粒子物理學已經相對應到一個非常美麗的圖案
and that's the one that i said we knew for certain .	那個就是我說我們很肯定知道的 。
and that shape has remarkable similarities and the way it fits into this e8 pattern could be the rest of the picture .	這個形狀與e8圖案非常相似 , 其精密之處在於其餘的圖案 。
and these patterns of points that i've shown for you actually represent symmetries of this highdimensional object that would be warping and moving and dancing over the space time that we experience .	我給你們看的這些點圖案實際上代表了這個高維物體的對稱性這些圖案會在我們體驗的時空中扭曲、移動、舞蹈
and that would be what explains all these elementary particles that we see .	這就解釋了所有這些基本粒子 。
ca: but a string theorist , as i understand it , explains electrons in terms of much smaller strings vibrating i know you don't like string theory vibrating inside it .	克:但弦理論家 , 如我所知 , 用較小的弦波振動來解釋電子 , 我知道你不喜歡弦理論在它內部振動 。
how should we think of an electron in relation to e8 ?	我們該如何看待e8的電子 ?
gl: no , it would be one of the symmetries of this e8 shape .	不對 , 它會是這個e8圖形的對稱之一 。
so what's happening is , as the shape is moving over spacetime , it's twisting . and the direction it's twisting as it moves is what particle we see . so it would be ca: the size of the e8 shape , how does that relate to the electron ?	所以當這個形狀在時空中移動的時候它扭轉了方向它在移動的時候扭曲了我們看到的粒子 。 所以它是克里斯:e8的大小那跟電子有甚麼關係 ?
i kind of feel like i need that for my picture .	我覺得我需要那張照片 。
is it bigger ? is it smaller ?	會更大嗎 ? 會更小嗎 ?
gl: well , as far as we know electrons are point particles , so this would be going down to the smallest possible scales .	gl:據我們所知 , 電子是點粒子 , 所以會縮小到最小的尺度 。
so the way these things are explained in quantum field theory is , all possibilities are expanding and developing at once .	所以 , 在量子場理論中 , 這些東西的解釋方式是 , 所有的可能性都在同時展開和發展 。
and this is why i use the analogy to coral .	這就是為什麼我會使用珊瑚的比喻 。
and in this way , the way that e8 comes in is it will be as a shape that's attached at each point in spacetime .	如此一來 , e8的進入方式是 , 它就像每個時空點的形狀 。
and , as i said , the way the shape twists the directional along which way the shape is twisting as it moves over this curved surface is what the elementary particles are , themselves .	如我所說 , 形狀在經過這個曲線的表面時 , 扭曲的方向和它扭曲的方向是基本粒子它們自己 。
so through quantum field theory , they manifest themselves as points and interact that way .	通過量子場理論 , 他們以點和相互作用來展現他們自己 。
i don't know if i'll be able to make this any clearer .	我不知道我能不能把這張圖做得更清楚 。
ca: it doesn't really matter .	克:沒關係 。
it's evoking a kind of sense of wonder , and i certainly want to understand more of this .	它激起了我的興趣 , 我當然希望更了解這一點 。
but thank you so much for coming . that was absolutely fascinating .	但非常謝謝你來到這裡 。 這真是太吸引人了 。
the legendary chimpanzee researcher jane goodall talks about tacare and her other community projects , which help people in booming african towns live sidebyside with threatened animals .	很傳奇的黑猩猩研究員珍.古德爾談到塔卡爾和其它社區計畫 , 協助非洲快速發展的小鎮和受到威脅的動物一起住在旁邊 。
africa , animals , biodiversity , environment , global issues , pollution , primates , science	非洲、動物、生物多樣性、環境、全球議題、污染、靈長類、科學 。
jane goodall helps humans and animals live together	珍.古德幫助人類和動物一起生活 。
good afternoon , good evening , whatever .	午安 , 晚安
we can go , jambo , guten abend , bonsoir , but we can also ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh , ooh .	我們可以 , 晚安 , 晚安 , 晚安 , 晚安 , 但我們也可以--噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 , 噢 。
that is the call that chimpanzees make before they go to sleep in the evening .	這是黑猩猩在晚上睡覺前的叫聲 。
you hear it going from one side of the valley to the other , from one group of nests to the next .	你聽到的是從山谷的一端傳到另一端 , 從一群巢穴傳到下一批 。
and i want to pick up with my talk this evening from where zeray left off yesterday .	昨天晚上我想從我的演講中挑選這個 , 這是昨天zeray離開的地方 。
he was talking about this amazing , threeyearold australopithecine child , selam .	他談到這個了不起的三歲靈長類孩子selam
and we've also been hearing about the history , the family tree , of mankind through dna genetic profiling .	我們也曾聽過透過dna基因圖譜來說明人類的歷史、家族樹的人類歷史 。
and it was a paleontologist , the late louis leakey , who actually set me on the path for studying chimpanzees .	已故的古生物學家路易斯.李奇是他讓我走上研究黑猩猩的路徑 。
and it was pretty extraordinary , way back then .	在當時 , 情況挺不可思議的
it's kind of commonplace now , but his argument was because he'd been searching for the fossilized remains of early humans in africa .	現在已經有些常見了 , 但他的論點是 , 因為他一直在尋找非洲早期人類的化石 。
and you can tell an awful lot about what those beings looked like from the fossils , from the shape of the muscle attachments , something about the way they lived from the various artifacts found with them .	從化石 , 肌肉依附的形狀 , 可以大量地分辨出那些肌肉的外觀 , 關於他們如何與他們共存的各種人造物品 。
but what about how they behaved ? that's what he wanted to know .	但他們的行為呢 ? 他就是想知道 。
and of course , behavior doesn't fossilize .	當然 , 行為不會化石 。
he argued and it's now a fairly common theory that if we found behavior patterns similar or the same in our closest living relatives , the great apes , and humans today , then maybe those behaviors were present in the apelike , humanlike ancestor some seven million years ago .	他主張--這是個很普遍的理論如果我們在現存的近親大猩猩身上找到相似的行為模式 , 如今人類 , 也許這些行為在七百萬年前出現在人猿類的人類祖先身上 。
and therefore , perhaps we had brought those characteristics with us from that ancient , ancient past .	因此 , 也許我們把這些特性從古老的過去中帶到了這裡 。
well , if you look in textbooks today that deal with human evolution , you very often find people speculating about how early humans may have behaved , based on the behavior of chimpanzees .	嗯 , 如果你看一下今天在教科書中研究人類的進化你會經常發現人們根據黑猩猩的行為來猜測早期人類的行為模式
they are more like us than any other living creature , and we've heard about that during this ted conference .	牠們和我們相似多於其他生物在這場ted大會上我們也聽過
so it remains for me to comment on the ways in which chimpanzees are so like us , in certain aspects of their behavior .	所以對我來說 , 我仍然要評論在黑猩猩的某些方面 , 在牠們行為的某些方面 , 黑猩猩是如此地相似 。
every chimpanzee has his or her own personality .	每一隻黑猩猩都有他或她自己的個性 。
of course , i gave them names . they can live to be 60 years or more , although we think most of them probably don't make it to 60 in the wild .	當然 , 我給他們取名字 。 他們可以活到60歲以上 , 雖然我們認為大多數人在野外不會活到60歲 。
mr . wurzel . the female has her first baby when she's 11 or 12 .	烏爾茲先生 。 當雌性十一或十二歲時 , 她的第一個寶寶是女生 。
thereafter , she has one baby only every five or six years , a long period of childhood dependency when the child is nursing , sleeping with the mother at night , and riding on her back .	每五六年 , 她只生了一個小孩 , 童年依賴期很長一段 , 小時候要照顧母親 , 晚上和媽媽一起睡 , 騎在背上 。
and we believe that this long period of childhood is important for chimpanzees , just as it is for us , in relation to learning .	我們相信這段長時間的幼兒期對黑猩猩很重要 , 就跟我們人類一樣 , 與學習有關 。
as the brain becomes ever more complex during evolution in different forms of animals , so we find that learning plays an ever more important role in an individual's life history .	當大腦在不同動物的演化過程中變得更複雜時 , 我們發現學習在個體的生命歷史中扮演著越來越重要的角色 。
and young chimpanzees spend a lot of time watching what their elders do .	年輕的黑猩猩花很多時間觀察長輩的行為 。
we know now that they're capable of imitating behaviors that they see .	我們現在知道牠們有能力模仿他們看到的行為 。
and we believe that it's in this way that the different toolusing behaviors that have now been seen in all the different chimpanzee populations studied in africa how these are passed from one generation to the next , through observation , imitation and practice , so that we can describe these toolusing behaviors as primitive culture .	我們相信這是以這種方式 , 不同使用工具的方式 , 已經在非洲各個黑猩猩族群中觀察到這些行為是如何從一個世代傳到下一個世代 , 模仿和做法 , 如此一來 , 我們就能將這些使用工具的行為描述成原始文化 。
chimpanzees don't have a spoken language . we've talked about that .	黑猩猩們沒有口語的語言 。 我們已經談過了 。
they do have a very rich repertoire of postures and gestures , many of which are similar , or even identical , to ours and formed in the same context . greeting chimpanzees embracing .	牠們的確有很豐富的肢體和姿勢 , 當中有許多和我們相似 , 甚至與我們相同 , 在相同的情境中形成 。 相同的對比 , 和擁抱的黑猩猩 。
they also kiss , hold hands , pat one another on the back .	他們也會互相親吻對方、握手、拍對方背 。
and they swagger and they throw rocks .	它們會大吃一驚 , 會扔石頭 。
in chimpanzee society , we find many , many examples of compassion , precursors to love and true altruism .	在黑猩猩的社會 , 我們發現很多很多有同情心的例子 , 都是有愛的前兆 , 和真正的利他行為 。
unfortunately , they , like us , have a dark side to their nature .	不幸的是 , 就像我們人類一樣 , 牠們也有天生的黑暗面 。
they're capable of extreme brutality , even a kind of primitive war .	他們能夠極度殘暴 , 甚至有點原始的戰爭 。
and these really aggressive behaviors , for the most part , are directed against individuals of the neighboring social group .	而這些極具攻擊性的行為 , 大多時候都是針對鄰近社會群體的對象 。
they are very territorially aggressive .	他們非常激烈
chimpanzees , i believe , more than any other living creature , have helped us to understand that , after all , there is no sharp line between humans and the rest of the animal kingdom .	我相信黑猩猩 , 比起其它的生物 , 已經讓我們了解 , 人類和動物王國之間並沒有明顯的界線 。
it's a very blurry line , and it's getting more blurry all the time as we make even more observations .	這是一條非常模糊的線 , 隨著我們進行更多的觀察 , 它變得更加模糊 。
the study that i began in 1960 is still continuing to this day .	我在1960年開始的研究至今仍在進行中 。
and these chimpanzees , living their complex social lives in the wild , have helped more than anything else to make us realize we are part of , and not separated from , the amazing animals with whom we share the planet .	而這些生活在野外複雜的社會生活的黑猩猩們 , 幫助我們去認識到 , 比任何其他東西都還要多 , 我們也是這些令人驚奇的動物的一份子 , 卻沒有被分開 , 那些與我們共享這個星球的生物 。
so it's pretty sad to find that chimpanzees , like so many other creatures around the world , are losing their habitats .	所以發現黑猩猩 , 就像世界上其他生物一樣 , 正在失去牠們的棲息地 。
this is just one photograph from the air , and it shows you the forested highlands of gombe .	這是一張從空中拍攝的照片 , 它是哥倫比的森林高地 。
and it was when i flew over the whole area , about 16 years ago , and realized that outside the park , this forest , which in 1960 had stretched almost unbroken along the eastern shore of lake tanganyika , which is where the tiny , 30squaremile gombe national park lies , that a question came to my mind .	那時我飛越整個地區 , 大約16年前 , 那時我了解到 , 在這個公園之外的這片森林在1960年時幾乎完全沒有被破壞 , 沿著坦岡尼卡的東岸 , 也就是這個小小的 , 30平方公里的岡貝國家公園在此處 , 我突然想到一個問題 。
" how can we even try to save these famous chimpanzees , when the people living around the national park are struggling to survive ? "	「 我們要如何拯救這些知名的黑猩猩 , 當居住在國家公園附近的黑猩猩正掙扎求生 ? 」
more people are living there than the land could possibly support .	更多人居住在那裏 , 遠遠超過這塊土地所能獲得的支援 。
the numbers increased by refugees pouring in from burundi and over the lake from congo .	受難者的數量從蒲隆地湧入 , 剛果湖的難民數量也增加了 。
and very poor people they couldn't afford to buy food from elsewhere .	窮人買不起他們來自其他地方的食物 。
this led to a program , which we call tacare .	這導致了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為坦尚尼亞造林計劃 。
it's a very holistic way of improving the lives of the people living in the villages around the park .	這是個非常整體的方法來改善公園附近村民的生活 。
it started small with 12 villages . it's now in 24 .	從十二個村莊開始 , 現在是二十四個村莊 。
there isn't time to go into it , but it's including things like tree nurseries , methods of farming most suitable to this now very degraded , almost desertlike land up in these mountains .	時間不夠多 , 但它包含了一些東西 , 比如樹木的護士、農耕的方式 , 現今最適合這種被降解、幾乎像沙漠一樣的山上土地 。
ways of controlling , preventing soil erosion .	控制與預防土壤流失的方法 。
ways of reclaiming overused farmland , so that within two years they can again be productive .	收回過度使用的農地 , 這麼一來 , 兩年後 , 農地就會再有生產力了 。
working to help the villagers obtain fresh water from wells .	致力於幫助村民從井裡取得淡水 。
perhaps build some schoolrooms .	也許建造一些學校教室 。
most important of all , i believe , is working with small groups of women , providing them with opportunities for microcredit loans .	我相信 , 最重要的是 , 和一些婦女們合作 , 提供她們提供微型貸款的機會 。
and we've got , as is the case around the world , about 95 percent of all loans returned .	如同世界各地的情況 , 有95%的貸款回來了 。
empowering women , working with education , providing scholarships for girls so they can finish secondary school , in the clear understanding that , all around the world , as women's education improves , family size drops .	授權給婦女 , 與教育工作 , 提供獎學金給女孩們 , 這樣她們才能完成中學 , 並且清楚的知道 , 隨著女性的教育改善家庭規模下降 。
we provide information about family planning and about hiv/aids .	我們提供家庭規劃和愛滋病的資訊 。
and as a result of this program , something's happening for conservation .	由於這個計畫 , 有些事情發生在保育上 。
what's happening for conservation is that the farmers living in these 24 villages , instead of looking on us as a bunch of white people coming to study a whole bunch of monkeys and by the way , many of the staff are now tanzanian but when we began the tacare program , it was a tanzanian team going into the villages .	農民們生活在這24個村落裡 , 而不是把我們當成一群白人來研究一群猴子順便一提 , 很多工作人員現在已經是坦尚尼亞人了 , 但是當我們開始坦尚尼亞造林計劃時 , 坦尚尼亞的團隊屬於這個村莊 。
it was a tanzanian team talking to the villagers , asking what they were interested in .	那是一支坦尚尼亞的團隊和村民交流 , 詢問他們感興趣的 。
were they interested in conservation ? absolutely not .	他們對保育感興趣嗎 ? 絕對不是
they were interested in health ; they were interested in education .	他們對健康有興趣 , 他們對教育有興趣 。
and as time went on , and as their situation began to improve , they began to understand ever more about the need for conservation .	隨著時間過去 , 他們的情況開始改善 , 他們開始更了解保育的重要性 。
they began to understand that as the upper levels of the hills were denuded of trees , so you've got this terrible soil erosion and mudslides .	他們開始明白 , 隨著山丘的上層被推開樹木 , 所以土壤受到侵蝕和泥土流動 。
today , we are developing what we call the greater gombe ecosystem .	現今 , 我們正在開發一種叫做gombe的生態系統 。
this is an area way outside the national park , stretching out into all these very degraded lands .	這個區域遠在國家公園之外 , 向外延伸到所有被摧毀的土地中 。
and as these villages have a better standard of life , they are actually agreeing to put between 10 percent and 20 percent of their land in the highlands aside , so that once again , as the trees grow back , the chimpanzees will have leafy corridors through which they can travel to interact as they must for genetic viability with other remnant groups outside the national park .	當這些村落擁有更好的生活標準時 , 他們實際上同意將百分之十到二十的高地邊緣的土地放置在外面 , 如此一來 , 當樹木長回來的時候 , 黑猩猩就會有樹葉走廊 , 通過這些地方可以與國家公園外的遺傳物質進行互動 。
so tacare is a success .	坦尚尼亞造林計劃是成功的 。
we're replicating it in other parts of africa , around other wilderness areas which are faced with extreme population pressure .	我們在非洲的其他地方 , 用其他地方來複製 , 用在人口壓力極端的其他野外區域 。
the problems in africa , however , as we've been discussing for the whole of these first couple of days of ted , are major problems .	然而 , 在非洲的問題 , 正如我們在ted的前幾天討論的問題 , 都是很大的問題 。
there is a great deal of poverty .	貧窮的問題非常嚴重 。
and when you get large numbers of people living in land that is not that fertile , particularly when you cut down trees , and you leave the soil open to the wind for erosion , as desperate populations cut down more and more trees , so that they can try and grow food for themselves and their families , what's going to happen ? something's got to give .	當你有大量的居民住在不太肥沃的土地上 , 尤其是當你砍掉樹木 , 你把土壤打開 , 讓土壤被侵蝕 , 因為絕望的人口減少了越來越多的樹木 , 所以他們可以試著為自己和家人種食物 , 會發生什麼事 ? 一定要付出代價 。
and the other problems in not only africa , but the rest of the developing world and , indeed , everywhere what are we doing to our planet ?	還有另一個問題 , 不只是非洲 , 還有其他的開發中國家 , 到處都一樣 , 我們對地球做了什麼事 ?
you know , the famous scientist , e . o . wilson said that if every person on this planet attains the standard of living of the average european or american , we need three new planets .	你知道的 , 著名的科學家 , 愛德華.威爾森曾說過 , 如果地球上每一個人都能遵守標準生活 , 包括歐洲人或美國人 , 我們就需要三個新的星球 。
today , they are saying four . but we don't have them . we've got one .	現今 , 他們有四個說法 , 但我們沒有 , 我們只有一個 。
and what's happened ? i mean , the question here is , here we are , arguably the most intelligent being that's ever walked planet earth , with this extraordinary brain , capable of the kind of technology that is so well illustrated by these ted conferences , and yet we're destroying the only home we have .	到底發生了什麼事 ? 我的意思是 , 問題是 , 我們在這裡 , 可以說是最聰明的生物 , 也是走在地球上最有智慧的生物 , 擁有這種非凡的大腦 , 能夠說明這種技術的效果 , 被ted研討會給描繪出來 , 而我們卻在摧毀我們唯一的家園 。
the indigenous people around the world , before they made a major decision , used to sit around and ask themselves , " how does this decision affect our people seven generations ahead ? "	全世界的原住民 , 在他們做出重大決定之前 , 通常會坐下來問自己: 「 這個決定會如何影響我們七代之後的同胞 ? 」
today , major decisions and i'm not particularly talking about africa here , but the developed world major decisions involving millions of dollars , and millions of people , are often based on , " how will this affect the next shareholders' meeting ? "	今天 , 重大的決定 , 我指的不是非洲 , 而是世界上數百萬美元重大的決定 , 數百萬人 , 通常都是基於: 「 這會如何影響下一次的股東會議 ? 」
and these decisions affect africa .	這些決定會影響非洲 。
as i began traveling around africa talking about the problems faced by chimpanzees and their vanishing forests , i realized more and more how so many of africa's problems could be laid at the door of previous colonial exploitation .	當我開始在非洲各處旅行 , 談論黑猩猩面臨的問題 , 談到牠們消失的森林 , 我發現越來越多非洲面臨的問題 , 存在於過去殖民時代剝削的門上 。
so i began traveling outside africa , talking in europe , talking in the united states , going to asia .	所以我開始在非洲之外旅行 , 到歐洲演說 , 到美國演說 , 到亞洲去 。
and everywhere there were these terrible problems .	到處都有這些可怕的問題 。
and you know the kind i'm talking about . i'm talking about pollution .	你知道我說的那種 , 我指的是污染 。
the air that we breathe that often poisons us .	我們呼吸的空氣通常會毒害我們 。
the earth is poisoning our foods .	地球正在毒害著我們的食物 。
the water water is perhaps one of the most crucial issues that we're going to face in this century and everywhere water is being polluted by agricultural , industrial and household chemicals that still are being sprayed around the world , seemingly with the inability to profit from past experience .	水資源 , 水可能是這個世紀所面臨的最關鍵的議題之一 , 世界各地的水正在被污染 , 被農業、工業和家庭使用的化學物質污染 , 這些化學物質仍然被散播到全世界 , 似乎無法從經驗中獲取過去的利益 。
the mangroves are being cut down ; the effects of things like the tsunami get worse .	紅樹林被砍伐 ; 海嘯的影響更加惡化 。
we've talked about the soil erosion .	我們已經談過土壤流失 。
we have the reckless burning of fossil fuels along with other greenhouse gasses , so called , leading to climate change .	我們有不斷燃燒的石化燃料 , 還有其他溫室氣體 , 導致氣候變遷 。
finally , all around the world , people have begun to believe that there is something going on very wrong with our climate .	最後 , 在世界各地 , 人們開始相信我們的氣候出了問題 。
all around the world climates are mixed up .	全世界的氣候都混在一起了 。
and it's the poor people who are affected worse .	受影響的窮人更差 。
it's africa that already is affected .	非洲已經受到影響了 。
in many parts of subsaharan africa , the droughts are so much worse .	在撒哈拉以南非洲的許多地區 , 旱災愈來愈糟 。
and when the rain does come , it so often leads to flooding and added distress , and the cycle of poverty and hunger and disease .	當雨來了 , 它經常會導致洪水和更多的痛苦 , 還有貧窮、飢餓和疾病的惡性循環 。
and the numbers of people living in an area that the land cannot support , who are too poor to buy food , who can't move away because the whole land is degraded .	住在土地無法支援的地區 , 貧窮的人無法購買食物 , 也無法搬走 , 因為整個土地都已經退化了 。
and so you get desertification creeping , creeping , creeping as the last of the trees are cut down .	所以當最後一棵樹被砍掉時 , 你會看到沙漠化的現象 。
and this kind of thing is not just in africa . it's all over the world .	這種事情並不只是在非洲 , 在全世界都是如此 。
so it wasn't surprising to me that as i was traveling around the world i met so many young people who seemed to have lost hope .	所以 , 我並不意外 , 當我在世界各地旅行時 , 我遇到許多失去希望的年輕人 。
we seem to have lost wisdom , the wisdom of the indigenous people .	我們似乎失去了智慧 , 失去了原住民的智慧 。
i asked a question . " why ? "	我問了一個問題: 「 為什麼 ? 」
well , do you think there could be some kind of disconnect between this extraordinarily clever brain , the kind of brain that the ted technologies exemplify , and the human heart ? talking about it in the nonscientific term , in terms of love and compassion . is there some disconnect ?	嗯 , 你認為在這聰明的大腦之間 , 可能有某種隔閡 , 那種ted科技會向我們展示 , 而人類的心臟 ? 用非科學的術語來說吧 , 愛和同情心 , 是否存在某種斷層 ?
and these young people , when i talk to them , basically they were either depressed or apathetic , or bitter and angry . and they said more or less the same thing , " we feel this way because we feel you've compromised our future and there's nothing we can do about it . "	這些年輕人 , 當我和他們談話時 , 他們基本上是憂鬱症、冷漠 , 或苦難和憤怒 。 他們多或少說了同樣的話 , 「 我們會有這種感覺 , 因為我們覺得你已經妥協了我們的未來 , 而我們對它卻無能為力 。 」
we have compromised their future .	我們已經妥協了他們的未來 。
i've got three little grandchildren , and every time i look at them and i think how we've harmed this beautiful planet since i was their age , i feel this desperation .	我有三個小孫子 , 每當我看著他們時 , 我就會想到在我還小的時候 , 我們如何傷害這個美麗的星球 , 我會感到絕望 。
and that led to this program we call roots and shoots , which began right here in tanzania and has now spread to 97 countries around the world .	這就帶到了我們稱為根與芽的計畫 , 這個計畫從坦尚尼亞開始 , 目前已經擴散到全球九十七個國家 。
it's symbolic . roots make a firm foundation .	它有象徵性的意義 。 根有堅定的基礎 。
shoots seem tiny ; to reach the sun they can break through a brick wall .	芽看似微小 ; 要到達陽光 , 它們能穿過磚牆 。
see the brick wall as all these problems we've inflicted on the planet , environmental and social . it's a message of hope .	把磚牆視為地球上所有的問題 , 像是環境和社會問題 。 這是希望的訊息 。
hundreds and thousands of young people around the world can break through and can make this a better world for all living things .	全世界有成千上萬的年輕人能夠突破身邊 , 為所有生物創造一個更美好的世界 。
the most important message of roots and shoots: every single one of us makes a difference , every single day .	根與芽的最重要的信息是:我們每一個人每天都會做出改變 。
we have a choice . every one of us in this room , we have a choice as to what kind of difference we want to make .	我們有選擇 。 在這房間裡的每一個人 , 我們都有一個選擇 , 來決定我們想要做什麼樣的改變 。
the very poor have no choice . it's up to us to change things so that the poor have choice as well .	貧窮的人沒有選擇 。 這取決於我們要改變現狀 , 窮人也有選擇權 。
the roots and shoots groups all choose three projects .	根與芽的小組全都選了三個計劃 。
it depends on how old they are , and which country , whether they're in a city or rural , as to what kinds of projects .	這取決於他們年齡多大 , 不管在哪個國家 , 不管在哪個城市或鄉村 , 哪種計畫 。
but basically , we have programs now from preschool right through university , with more and more adults starting their own roots and shoots groups .	但基本上 , 我們有從幼兒園到大學的專案計畫 , 越來越多的成年人開始著手進行他們自己的根與芽的計劃 。
and every group chooses , between them , three different kinds of project to make this a better world , recognizing that all these different problems are interconnected and impinge on each other .	每個團體在他們之間做選擇 , 三個不同的計畫 , 讓這個更美好的世界 , 承認這些不同的問題彼此連結 , 並互相影響 。
so one of their projects will be to help their own human community .	所以 , 他們的其中一個計畫就是協助他們自己的人類社群 。
and then , if they're able , they may raise money to help communities in other parts of the world .	接著 , 如果他們能做到 , 他們就能籌集資金來協助世界上其他地方的社區 。
one of their projects will be to help animals not just wildlife , domestic animals as well .	他們的其中一個計畫是要幫助動物 , 不僅是野生動物、家養動物 。
and one of their projects will be to help the environment that we all share .	其中一個計畫是幫助我們共有的環境 。
and woven throughout all of this is a message of learning to live in peace and harmony within ourselves , in our families , in our communities , between nations , between cultures , between religions and between us and the natural world .	整體來說 , 編織就是一個學習如何在我們自己、我們的家庭、我們的社區、國家、文化、宗教與自然之間生活的訊息 。
we need the natural world . we cannot go on destroying it at the rate we are .	我們需要自然世界 。 我們不能再以現有的速度破壞自然 。
we not do have more than this one planet .	我們沒有超過這個星球 。
just picking one or two of the projects right here in africa that the roots and shoots groups are doing , one or two projects only in tanzania , in uganda , kenya , south africa , congobrazzaville , sierra leone , cameroon and other groups . and as i say , it's in 97 countries around the world .	在非洲這裡舉出一兩個計畫根與芽的團體正在進行一兩項計畫在坦尚尼亞 , 在烏干達 , 肯亞 , 南非 , 剛果 , 獅子山共和國 , 喀麥隆和其他團體 。 如我說的 , 目前有97個國家正在進行 。
of course , they're planting trees . they're growing organic vegetables .	當然 , 他們種植樹木 , 他們種植有機蔬菜
they're working in the refugee camps , with chickens and selling the eggs for a little amount of money , or just using them to feed their families , and feeling a sense of pride and empowerment , because they're no longer helpless and depending on others with their vegetables and their chickens .	他們在難民營工作 , 他們帶著雞隻賣雞蛋 , 只為了一點點錢 , 或只是用它們來餵飽他們的家人 , 讓他們感到自豪和自主 , 因為他們不再無助 , 不再依靠人們的蔬菜和雞隻 。
it's being used in uganda to give some psychological help to exchild soldiers .	它被用在烏干達 , 給童兵一些心理上的幫助 。
doing projects like this is bringing them out of themselves .	做這樣的計畫是把他們帶出自己 。
once again , they're useful members of society .	再一次地 , 他們是有用的社會成員 。
we have this program in prisons as well .	我們在監獄也有這個計畫 。
so , there's no time for more roots and shoots now .	所以 , 現在沒有更多根與芽的時刻了 。
but oh , they're also working on hiv/aids .	但 , 喔 , 他們也在研究愛滋病 。
that's a very important component of roots and shoots , with older kids talking to younger ones .	那是根與芽的重要要素 , 讓年長的孩子和年紀較小的孩子溝通 。
and unwanted pregnancies and things like that , which young people listen to better from other youth , rather than adults .	不想要懷孕 , 諸如此類的 , 年輕人會傾聽其他年輕人的心聲 , 而非成年人 。
hope . that's the question i get asked as i'm going around the world: " jane , you've seen so many terrible things , you've seen your chimpanzees decrease in number from about one million , at the turn of the century , to no more than 150 , 000 now , and the same with so many other animals .	希望 。 我在世界各地都會被問到這個問題: 「 珍 , 你看過很多糟糕的事情 , 你看過你的黑猩猩數量減少了大約一百萬隻 , 在本世紀初 , 到現在不超過十五萬隻 , 許多其他動物也一樣 。
forests disappearing , deserts where once there was forest .	森林不斷消失 , 曾經有森林的地方也消失 。
do you really have hope ? " well , yes .	你真的有希望嗎 ? " 嗯 , 是的 。
you can't come to a conference like ted and not have hope , can you ?	你不能來參加像ted這樣的研討會 , 沒有希望 , 可以嗎 ?
and of course , there's hope . one is this amazing human brain .	當然 , 還有希望 。 其中之一是人的大腦 。
and i mean , think of the technologies .	我的意思是 , 想想看科技 。
and i've just been so thrilled , finally , to come to people talking about compost latrines .	我最後非常興奮 , 能夠來談談堆肥式公廁 。
it's one of my hobbyhorses .	這是我其中一個嗜好 。
we just flush all this water down the lavatory , it's terrible .	我們只是把所有的水往馬桶裡沖 , 真是糟糕 。
and then talking about renewable energy desperately important .	再談到極度重要的可再生能源 。
do we care about the planet for our children ?	我們是否在乎孩子們的星球 ?
how many of us have children or grandchildren , nieces , nephews ?	有多少人有小孩、孫子、姪子、姪子 ?
do we care about their future ?	我們在乎他們的未來嗎 ?
and if we care about their future , we , as the elite around the world , we can do something about it . we can make choices as to how we live each day .	如果我們在乎他們的未來 , 我們身為世界上精英份子 , 我們可以做點什麼 。 我們可以選擇如何過日子 。
what we buy . what we wear .	我們買什麼 。 我們穿什麼 。
and choose to make these choices with the question , how will this affect the environment around me ?	選擇用問題來做這些選擇 , 這對我周圍的環境會有什麼影響 ?
how will it affect the life of my child when he or she grows up ?	當他或她長大後 , 它會如何影響我的孩子的生活 ?
or my grandchild , or whatever it is .	或我的孫子 , 等等 。
