so the human brain , coupled with the human heart , and we join hands around the world .	所以 , 人類的腦 , 再加上人類的心 , 然後我們就加入世界各地的手 。
and that's what ted is helping so well with , and google who help us , and esri are helping us with mapping in gombe national park .	這就是ted在幫助我們 , google也幫助我們 , esri也在幫助我們繪製國家公園地圖 。
all of these technologies we can use .	所有這些我們能使用的科技
now let's link them , and it's beginning to happen , isn't it ?	現在讓我們來把它們連結起來 , 它已經開始發生了 , 不是嗎 ?
you've heard about it this afternoon . it's beginning to happen .	今天下午你已經聽說了 , 它已經開始發生了 。
this change , this change . to see change that we must have if we care about the future .	這種改變 , 這種改變 。 如果我們關心未來 , 我們必須看到這些改變 。
and the next reason for hope nature is amazingly resilient .	下一個原因是希望大自然有驚人的韌性 。
you can take an area that's absolutely destroyed , with time and perhaps some help it can regenerate .	你可以把一塊完全被摧毀的區域 , 只要有時間 , 或許還能有幫助 , 就能再生 。
and an example is the tacare program .	而坦尚尼亞造林計劃就是其中一個例子
i told you , where a seemingly dead tree stump if you stop hacking them for firewood , which you don't need to because you have wood lots , then in five years you can have a 30foot tree .	我告訴你 , 如果你停止砍伐木柴 , 那看似已死去的樹木 , 那你就不用因為你有很多木材 , 然後在五年內 , 你可以砍掉一棵三十英呎的樹 。
and animals , almost on the brink of extinction , can be given a second chance . that's my next book .	幾乎在絕種的邊緣上動物可以給第二次機會這就是我的下一本書
it's inspiring . and it brings me to my last category of hope , and we've heard about this so much in the last two days: this indomitable human spirit . this determination of people , the resilience of the human spirit , so that people who you would think would be battered by poverty , or disease , or whatever , can pull themselves up out of it , sometimes with a helping hand , and take their part in society , and take their part in changing the world .	這很鼓舞人心 。 這也帶到了我最後一類希望 , 在過去的兩天中 , 我們已經聽到了很多這樣的事:這種不屈不撓的人類精神 。 人們堅韌的決心 , 人類精神的韌性 , 所以那些你認為會被貧窮、疾病所擊垮的人 , 有時 , 他們自己會被迫離開這個世界 , 讓他們成為改變世界的一份子 。
and just to think of one or two people out of africa who are just really inspiring .	想想那些激勵人心的非洲人 。
we could make a very long list , but obviously nelson mandela , emerging from 17 years of hard physical labor , 23 years of imprisonment , with this amazing ability to forgive , so that he could lead his nation out the evil regime of apartheid without a bloodbath .	我們可以列出一個很長的清單 , 但很顯然的 , 納爾遜•曼德拉出現於17年的實體勞工身上 , 23年的監禁 , 帶著這不可思議的寬恕去原諒他的國家 , 讓他在沒有血戰的情況下 , 走出了種族隔離的邪惡政權 。
ken sarowiwa , in nigeria , who took on the giant oil companies , and although people around the world tried their best , was executed .	奈及利亞的沙羅維瓦對抗巨大的石油公司 , 雖然全世界的人盡力而為 , 卻被處決了 。
people like this are so inspirational .	像這樣的人是非常鼓舞人心的 。
people like this are the role models we need for young africans .	像這樣的人 , 是我們需要年輕非洲人的典範 。
and we need some environmental role models as well , and i've been hearing some of them today .	我們也需要一些環境角色模範 , 今天我已經聽過其中一些 。
so i'm really grateful for this opportunity to share this message again , with everyone at ted .	所以我很感謝這個機會再次分享這個訊息 , 給ted的每個人 。
and i hope that some of us can get together and talk about some of these things , especially the roots and shoots program .	我希望我們中的一些人可以聚在一起討論這些事 , 特別是根與芽的計畫 。
and just a last word on that the young woman who's running this entire conference center , i met her today .	最後我要說的 , 是那位管理這整個會議的年輕女子 , 我今天遇到了她 。
she came up so excited , with her certificate . she was [in] roots and shoots .	她拿著證書變得很興奮 。 她是根與芽的證書 。
she was in the leadership in dar es salaam .	她在dressalaam的領導階層 。
she said it's helped her to do what she's doing .	她說這能協助她做她在做的事 。
and it was very , very exciting for me to meet her and see just one example of how young people , when they are empowered , given the opportunity to take action , to make the world a better place , truly are our hope for tomorrow .	對我來說 , 非常興奮能夠見到她 , 並看到一個例子 , 當年輕人被賦權時 , 能夠採取行動的機會 , 讓這個世界變得更美好 , 真正成為明天的希望 。
artist dianna cohen shares some tough truths about plastic pollution in the ocean and in our lives and some thoughts on how to free ourselves from the plastic gyre .	藝術家黛安娜•柯恩有一些關於海洋污染的困難事實 , 和我們生活中的一些想法 , 關於如何將我們從塑膠漩渦中解放出來 。
consumerism , global issues , green , mission blue , oceans , plastic	消費主義、全球議題、綠色、任務藍色、海洋、塑膠 。
dianna cohen: tough truths about plastic pollution	黛安娜.柯恩:關於塑膠污染的棘手真相 。
i'm a visual artist , and i'm also one of the cofounders of the plastic pollution coalition .	我是個視覺藝術家 , 我也是塑膠污染聯盟的共同創辦人之一 。
i've been working with plastic bags , which i cut up and sew back together as my primary material for my artwork for the last 20 years .	我一直在跟塑膠袋合作 , 我把塑膠袋剪下來 , 縫合成我作品的主要材料 , 已經有二十年了 。
i turn them into two and threedimensional pieces and sculptures and installations .	我把它們變成二、三維的部分 , 雕塑和裝置藝術 。
upon working with the plastic , after about the first eight years , some of my work started to fissure and break down into smaller little bits of plastic .	大約八年後 , 我和塑膠一起工作 , 我有些工作開始裂解 , 分解成更小的塑膠塊 。
and i thought , " great .	我心想: 「 太好了 。
it's ephemeral just like us . "	跟我們一樣 , 那是短暫的 。 」
upon educating myself a little further about plastics , i actually realized this was a bad thing .	一旦我對塑膠更進一步的教育我意識到這是一件壞事
it's a bad thing that plastic breaks down into smaller little bits , because it's always still plastic .	塑膠分解成小塊是壞事 , 因為總是塑膠分解成小塊 。
and what we're finding is that a lot of it is in the marine environment .	我們發現很多的物質都存在於海洋環境中 。
i then , in the last few years , learned about the pacific garbage patch and the gyre .	接著 , 在過去幾年 , 我了解到太平洋垃圾帶和垃圾漩渦 。
and my initial reaction and i think this is a lot of people's first reaction to learning about it is , " oh my god !	我最初的反應是許多人對此的第一反應: 「 天哪 !
we've got to go out there and clean this thing up . "	我們得走出去清理這個東西 。 」
so i actually developed a proposal to go out with a cargo ship and two decommissioned fishing trawlers , a crane , a chipping machine and a coldmolding machine .	所以我真的提出了一個計劃 , 跟一艘貨物船及兩艘退休的拖網漁船、一座起重機、一台磨碎機和一台冷模機出海 。
and my intention was to go out to the gyre , raise awareness about this issue and begin to pick up the plastic , chip it into little bits and cold mold it into bricks that could potentially be used as building materials in underdeveloped communities .	而我的意圖是要出發到垃圾漩渦 , 提高人們對這個議題的認知 , 然後開始把塑膠拿出來 , 把它做成一點碎片 , 把它壓縮成磚塊 , 讓它們可以被用來當作發展中社區的材料 。
i began talking with people who actually had been out to the gyre and were studying the plastic problem in the marine environment and upon doing so , i realized actually that cleaning it up would be a very small drop in the bucket relative to how much is being generated every day around the world , and that actually i needed to back up and look at the bigger picture .	我開始和實際去過垃圾漩渦的人聊天 , 研究海洋環境中的塑膠問題 , 在做這件事時 , 我了解到 , 要把塑膠清理乾淨 , 和全世界每天產生的垃圾比起來 , 是非常小的比例 , 且我得要退一步 , 看看更大的狀況 。
and the bigger picture is: we need to find a way to turn off the faucet .	更重要的是:我們需要找到方法去關掉水面 。
we need to cut the spigot of singleuse and disposable plastics , which are entering the marine environment every day on a global scale .	我們需要削減一塊一塊使用即丟棄的塑膠 , 它們每天都以全球的規模進入海洋環境 。
so in looking at that , i also realized that i was really angry .	看到這一點 , 我也了解到我很生氣 。
i wasn't just concerned about plastic that you're trying to imagine out in the middle of the pacific ocean of which i have learned there are now 11 gyres , potentially , of plastic in five major oceans in the world .	我不只在乎塑膠 , 你還在試著想像在太平洋中間的海洋 , 我現在知道有11個塑膠垃圾漩渦遍及世界上五個主要海洋 。
it's not just that gyre of plastic that i'm concerned about it's the gyre of plastic in the supermarket .	我關心的不只是這些塑膠垃圾漩渦還有這些超市的塑膠漩渦
i'd go to the supermarket and all of my food is packaged in plastic .	我會去超市 , 所有的食物都是塑膠包裝 。
all of my beverages are packaged in plastic , even at the health food market .	我所有的飲料都是塑膠包裝的即使在健康食品市場也是如此
i'm also concerned about the plastic in the refrigerator , and i'm concerned about the plastic and the toxins that leach from plastic into us and into our bodies .	我也很擔心冰箱裡的塑膠還有從塑膠中滲出的有毒物 , 滲出到我們的身體裡 。
so i came together with a group of other people who were all looking at this issue , and we created the plastic pollution coalition .	所以我和一群其他人一起研究這個問題 , 我們也創造了塑膠污染聯盟 。
we have many initiatives that we're working on , but some of them are very basic .	我們有很多計畫正在進行 , 但有些計畫很基本 。
one is: if 80 to 90 percent of what we're finding in the ocean of the marine debris that we're finding in the ocean is plastic , then why don't we call it what it is .	第一:如果我們在海洋中發現的海洋中有80% ~ 90%的物質是塑膠 , 那為什麼我們不把它稱為是塑膠 。
recycling everybody kind of ends their books about being sustainable and greening with the idea of recycling .	回收 , 每本書的結尾都是關於永續經營和綠色回收這個點子 。
you put something in a bin and you don't have to think about it again .	你只要在垃圾桶裡裝點東西 , 你就不用再想了 。
what is the reality of that ?	事實是什麼 ?
in the united states , less than seven percent of our plastics are recycled .	在美國 , 塑膠回收的比率不到7% 。
and if you really look into it , particularly when it comes to plastic bottles , most of it is only downcycled , or incinerated , or shipped to china .	如果你仔細觀察 , 特別是塑膠瓶大部分只能降級回收 , 或是燒掉 , 或是運到中國去 。
it is downcycled and turned into lesser things , while a glass bottle can be a glass bottle again or can be used again a plastic bottle can never be a plastic bottle again .	它是被降級回收 , 然後變成更少的東西 , 而玻璃瓶可以是玻璃瓶再次使用 , 或者再次使用塑膠瓶 , 永遠不會再是塑膠瓶 。
so this is a big issue for us .	所以這對我們來說是一個大問題 。
another thing that we're looking at and asking people to think about is we've added a fourth r onto the front of the " reduce , reuse , recycle , " three r's , and that is refuse .	另一件我們正在看和要求人們思考的事是我們在 「 減量、再利用、回收 」 前面加上第四個r , 那就是拒絕 。
whenever possible , refuse singleuse and disposable plastics .	總之 , 盡量拒絕用過即丟的塑膠 。
alternatives exist ; some of them are very oldschool .	替代方案是有的 , 有些是非常老派的 。
i myself am now collecting these cool pyrex containers and using those instead of glad and tupperware containers to store food in .	現在我在收集這些很酷的畢氏容器 , 用那些取代掉掉的保鮮盒和保鮮盒 , 來儲存食物 。
and i know that i am doing a service to myself and my family .	我知道我正在為自己和我的家人服務 。
it's very easy to pick up a stainlesssteel bottle or a glass bottle , if you're traveling and you've forgotten to bring your stainlesssteel bottle and fill that up with water or filtered water , versus purchasing plastic bottled water .	要找到一個不銹鋼瓶或玻璃瓶是很容易的 , 如果你要去旅行 , 而你忘了帶個不銹鋼瓶裝水 , 和採用過濾過的塑膠瓶裝水相比 , 要買塑膠瓶裝水 。
i guess what i want to say to everybody here and i know that you guys know a lot about this issue is that this is a huge problem in the oceans , but this is a problem that we've created as consumers and we can solve .	我想對在座的各位說──我知道你們對這件事很了解──這對海洋是很大的問題 , 但這是身為消費者所造成的問題 , 我們可以解決 。
we can solve this by raising awareness of the issue and teaching people to choose alternatives .	我們可以藉由提高對這個問題的認知和教導人們去選擇替代方案來解決這個問題 。
so whenever possible , to choose alternatives to singleuse plastics .	所以 , 盡可能地選擇用過的塑膠替代品 。
we can cut the stem tide the stem of this into our oceans and in doing so , save our oceans , save our planet , save ourselves .	我們可以把這些流向海洋的莖切開 , 如此一來 , 拯救我們的海洋、拯救我們的地球、拯救我們自己 。
this demo from pattie maes' lab at mit , spearheaded by pranav mistry was the buzz of ted . it's a wearable device with a projector that paves the way for profound interaction with our environment . imagine " minority report " and then some .	這張圖是來自麻省理工學院的pattiemaes的實驗室 , 由pranvmgory帶領的 , 是ted的buz 。 它是一個可以穿戴的裝置 , 上面裝有深度的互動效果 。 想像一下 , 「 關鍵報告 」 和一些 。
demo , design , interface design , technology	展示、設計、介面設計、科技、科技 。
pattie maes and pranav mistry demo sixthsense	pattimaes和panavemes是第六感的演示
i've been intrigued by this question of whether we could evolve or develop a sixth sense a sense that would give us seamless access and easy access to metainformation or information that may exist somewhere that may be relevant to help us make the right decision about whatever it is that we're coming across .	我一直對這個問題很感興趣 , 即我們能否進化或發展出第六感──一種能夠讓我們無縫接觸、容易取得代碼或現存的資訊 , 能夠協助我們做出正確的決定 , 決定我們遇到了什麼 。
and some of you may argue , well , don't today's cell phones do that already ?	有些人可能會說 , 現今的手機已經不是已經在做這件事了嗎 ?
but i would say no .	但我會說 , 不 。
when you meet someone here at ted and this is the top networking place , of course , of the year you don't shake somebody's hand and then say , " can you hold on for a moment while i take out my phone and google you ? "	當你在ted與某人見面──當然 , 這是今年最佳的社交場所──你不會和某人握手然後說: 「 你能等一下嗎 ? 我拿出我的手機和谷歌嗎 ? 」
or when you go to the supermarket and you're standing there in that huge aisle of different types of toilet papers , you don't take out your cell phone , and open a browser , and go to a website to try to decide which of these different toilet papers is the most ecologically responsible purchase to make .	或者 , 當你去超市站在那裡 , 用很大的不同型式的衛生紙走道 , 你不會拿出手機 , 打開瀏覽器 , 去一個網站 , 來決定這些不同的衛生紙是最環保的購買方式 。
so we don't really have easy access to all this relevant information that can just help us make optimal decisions about what to do next and what actions to take .	所以 , 我們無法很容易取得所有相關的資訊 , 來協助我們做出最佳決策 , 決定下一步要做什麼 , 要採取什麼行動 。
and so my research group at the media lab has been developing a series of inventions to give us access to this information in a sort of easy way , without requiring that the user changes any of their behavior .	所以我在媒體實驗室的研究小組正在研發一系列的發明 , 以某種簡單的方式取得這些資訊 , 並且不需要使用者改變他們的行為 。
and i'm here to unveil our latest effort , and most successful effort so far , which is still very much a work in process .	我來這裡是要揭開我們最新的努力 , 也是最成功的努力 , 到目前為止 , 這仍然是一個過程 。
i'm actually wearing the device right now and we've sort of cobbled it together with components that are off the shelf and that , by the way , only cost 350 dollars at this point in time .	其實我身上正戴著這個裝置 , 我們已經用現成的零件將它組合起來 。 順道一提 , 現在這個裝置的成本是350美元 。
i'm wearing a camera , just a simple webcam , a portable , batterypowered projection system with a little mirror .	我帶著一台攝影機 , 一個簡單的網路攝影機 , 一個可攜式的電池動力投影系統 , 還有鏡子 。
these components communicate to my cell phone in my pocket which acts as the communication and computation device .	這些元件在口袋裡跟我的手機溝通 , 作為溝通和計算機的功能 。
and in the video here we see my student pranav mistry , who's really the genius who's been implementing and designing this whole system .	在影片中 , 我們看到我的學生 , 帕納•密斯 , 他真的是執行和設計整個系統的天才 。
and we see how this system lets him walk up to any surface and start using his hands to interact with the information that is projected in front of him .	我們看到這個系統讓他走到任何平面上 , 開始用他的手和投影在他面前的資訊進行互動 。
the system tracks the four significant fingers .	系統追蹤這四隻重要手指 。
in this case , he's wearing simple marker caps that you may recognize .	在這個例子中 , 你可能認得到 , 他戴著簡單的標記蓋子 。
but if you want a more stylish version you could also paint your nails in different colors .	但如果你想要比較時髦的版本 , 你也可以把指甲塗上不同顏色 。
and the camera basically tracks these four fingers and recognizes any gestures that he's making so he can just go to , for example , a map of long beach , zoom in and out , etc .	攝影機基本上能追蹤這四隻手指並且辨識出他正在做的任何動作例如 , 他可以直接移動 , 舉例來說 , 長灘的地圖 , 放大和縮小等等
the system also recognizes iconic gestures such as the " take a picture " gesture , and then takes a picture of whatever is in front of you .	這個系統還能辨識出具象徵性的手勢 , 例如拍照的動作 , 然後拍一張你面前的事物 。
and when he then walks back to the media lab , he can just go up to any wall and project all the pictures that he's taken , sort through them and organize them , and resize them , etc . , again using all natural gestures .	當他走回媒體實驗室後 , 他可以走到任何一面牆上 , 將他拍下的所有照片投影出來 , 分析並組織它們 , 將它們放大 , 以此類推 。 同樣地 , 使用自然的手勢 。
so , some of you most likely were here two years ago and saw the demo by jeff han or some of you may think , " well , doesn't this look like the microsoft surface table ? "	有人兩年前可能就在這裡 , 看到jeffhan的示範 , 或者你們有些人可能會想: 「 這不是看起來像微軟的平面電腦嗎 ? 」
and yes , you also interact using natural gestures , both hands , etc .	沒錯 , 你也用自然的手勢互動 , 雙手等等 。
but the difference here is that you can use any surface , you can walk to up to any surface , including your hand if nothing else is available and interact with this projected data .	差別在於你可以用任何表面 , 你可以走到任何平面上 , 包括你的手 , 如果沒有其他表面可以用的話 , 就可以和這些投影出來的資料進行互動 。
the device is completely portable , and can be . . .	這個裝置是可以隨身攜帶的 , 也可以是...
so one important difference is that it's totally mobile .	其中一個重要不同點是它是完全流動的 。
another even more important difference is that in mass production this would not cost more tomorrow than today's cell phones and would actually not sort of be a bigger packaging could look a lot more stylish than this version that i'm wearing around my neck .	另一項更重要的不同點在於 , 量產後的成本明天 , 比現有的手機要貴 , 且設計出來的包裝設計本來可以比我脖子上掛的版本還要時髦很多 。
but other than letting some of you live out your fantasy of looking as cool as tom cruise in " minority report , " the reason why we're really excited about this device is that it really can act as one of these sixthsense devices that gives you relevant information about whatever is in front of you .	除此之外 , 讓你們其中一些人活在 「 關鍵報告 」 裡看起來像湯姆克魯斯的幻想世界裡一樣酷的幻想世界 , 我們對這裝置感到很興奮的原因 , 是因為它可以作為第六感裝置的其中之一 , 讓你知道在你面前有什麼資訊 。
so we see pranav here going into the supermarket and he's shopping for some paper towels .	所以我們看到帕納進入超市他要買一些紙巾
and , as he picks up a product the system can recognize the product that he's picking up , using either image recognition or marker technology , and give him the green light or an orange light .	當他拿起一個產品 , 這個系統可以辨識出他正在採集的產品 , 使用影像辨識或標記技術 , 給他綠燈或橘燈 。
he can ask for additional information .	他能尋求額外的資訊 。
so this particular choice here is a particularly good choice , given his personal criteria .	所以這個選擇在他個人的標準下 , 是特別好的選擇 。
some of you may want the toilet paper with the most bleach in it rather than the most ecologicallyresponsible choice .	有些人可能想買加入最多漂白劑的衛生紙而不是最環保的選擇 。
if he picks up a book in the bookstore , he can get an amazon rating it gets projected right on the cover of the book .	如果他在書店裡拿起一本書 , 他能取得亞馬遜書局的評分 , 就直接投影在書的封面上 。
this is juan's book , our previous speaker , which gets a great rating , by the way , at amazon .	這是juan的書 , 我們之前的演講者 , 順道一提 , 在亞馬遜得到很好的評分 。
and so , pranav turns the page of the book and can then see additional information about the book reader comments , maybe sort of information by his favorite critic , etc .	所以 , 帕納翻開書頁 , 看得到更多關於這本書的資訊 , 像是讀者評論的資訊 , 可能是讀者最喜歡的評論家的評論 , 等等 。
if he turns to a particular page he finds an annotation by maybe an expert of a friend of ours that gives him a little bit of additional information about whatever is on that particular page .	如果他翻到特定的一頁 , 他會找到我們朋友的註解 , 讓他能得到更多關於那一頁內容的資訊 。
reading the newspaper it never has to be outdated .	閱讀報紙 , 它永遠不會過時 。
you can get video annotations of the event that you're reading about you can get the latest sports scores etc .	你可以用影片來說明你正在讀的事件內容你可以得到最新的運動分數等等 。
this is a more controversial one .	這是一個更有爭議性的議題 。
as you interact with someone at ted , maybe you can see a word cloud of the tags , the words that are associated with that person in their blog and personal web pages .	當你在ted與某人互動時 , 也許你可以看見一團團的標籤 , 和那人相關的單字在他們的部落格和個人網頁上 。
in this case , the student is interested in cameras , etc .	在這個例子中 , 學生對攝影機感興趣 ,
on your way to the airport , if you pick up your boarding pass , it can tell you that your flight is delayed , that the gate has changed , etc .	在你去機場的路上 , 如果你拿起你的登機證 , 它可以告訴你 , 你的航班延遲了 , 登機門也改變了 , 等等 。
and , if you need to know what the current time is it's as simple as drawing a watch on your arm .	如果你需要知道現在的時間 , 就如同在手臂上畫一個手錶一樣簡單 。
so that's where we're at so far in developing this sixth sense that would give us seamless access to all this relevant information about the things that we may come across .	這就是我們目前正在開發第六感能夠讓我們無縫地取得關於我們可能遇到的事物的相關資訊 。
my student pranav , who's really , like i said , the genius behind this .	我的學生帕納 , 就像我說的 , 他是這背後的天才 。
he does deserve a lot of applause because i don't think he's slept much in the last three months , actually .	他的確應該得到很多掌聲 , 因為我認為過去三個月來他沒睡多少 。
and his girlfriend is probably not very happy about him either .	他的女朋友可能也對他不太滿意 。
but it's not perfect yet , it's very much a work in progress .	但它尚未完美 , 它還在進步中 。
and who knows , maybe in another 10 years we'll be here with the ultimate sixth sense brain implant .	誰知道呢 , 也許十年後我們會帶著植入腦的終極第六感來到這裡 。
phyllis rodriguez and aicha elwafi have a powerful friendship born of unthinkable loss . rodriguez' son was killed in the world trade center attacks on september 11 , 2001 ; elwafi's son zacarias moussaoui was convicted of a role in those attacks and is serving a life sentence . in hoping to find peace , these two moms have come to understand and respect one another .	phyllisrodriguez和aichaelwafi有力的友誼是出生於難以想像的損失 。 rodriguez的兒子在2001年9月11日 , 在世界貿易中心攻擊上被殺害 ; elwafi的兒子zaussaoui被定罪於襲擊中扮演一個角色 , 並為一個終身找到和平的終生 。
culture , global issues , politics	文化、全球議題、政治、政治 。
9/11 healing: the mothers who found forgiveness , friendship	911修復:找到寬恕的母親、友誼的母親 。
phyllis rodriguez: we are here today because of the fact that we have what most people consider an unusual friendship .	phyllisrodriguez:我們今天來到這裡 , 是因為我們有大多數人認為不尋常的友誼 。
and yet , it feels natural to us now .	但 , 現在我們覺得很自然 。
i first learned that my son had been in the world trade center on the morning of september 11th , 2001 .	我第一次發現我的兒子在世界貿易中心 , 那是在2001年9月11日的早上 。
we didn't know if he had perished yet until 36 hours later .	我們不知道他是否死了 , 直到36小時後 。
at the time , we knew that it was political .	當時 , 我們知道那是政治的 。
we were afraid of what our country was going to do in the name of our son my husband , orlando , and i and our family .	我們害怕我們的國家將會做些什麼事以我們兒子之名--我的丈夫 , 奧蘭多 , 我和我的家人 。
and when i saw it and yet , through the shock , the terrible shock , and the terrible explosion in our lives , literally , we were not vengeful .	當我看到---雖然 , 很震驚 , 很恐怖的震驚 , 我們生活中可怕的爆炸 , 真的 , 我們沒有復仇 。
and a couple of weeks later when zacarias moussaoui was indicted on six counts of conspiracy to commit terrorism , and the u . s . government called for a death penalty for him , if convicted , my husband and i spoke out in opposition to that , publicly .	幾個星期後當zacariasmoussaoui被指控六項恐怖主義的陰謀時 , 美國政府要求對他判處死刑如果罪名是 , 我和我丈夫公開反對這個說法 。
through that and through human rights groups , we were brought together with several other victims' families .	透過這些以及透過人權團體 , 我們和其他受害者家屬團結在一起 。
when i saw aicha in the media , coming over when her son was indicted , and i thought , " what a brave woman .	當我在媒體上看到aicha , 當她的兒子被起訴時 , 她走過來 , 我心想: 「 多麼勇敢的女人 。
someday i want to meet that woman when i'm stronger . "	有一天 , 當我更強壯時 , 我想和那位女士見面 。 」
i was still in deep grief ; i knew i didn't have the strength .	我還在深深的悲慟中 ; 我知道我沒有力量 。
i knew i would find her someday , or we would find each other .	我知道有一天我會找到她 , 或我們會找到彼此 。
because , when people heard that my son was a victim , i got immediate sympathy .	因為 , 當人們聽到我的兒子是受害者 , 我馬上就得到同情 。
but when people learned what her son was accused of , she didn't get that sympathy .	但當人們知道她兒子被指控的事 , 她沒有得到那種同情 。
but her suffering is equal to mine .	但她的痛苦和我是平等的 。
so we met in november 2002 , and aicha will now tell you how that came about .	我們在2002年11月相遇 , 現在aicha會告訴你這一切是如何發生的 。
aicha elwafi: good afternoon , ladies and gentlemen .	aichael-wafi:午安 , 各位先生女士 。
i am the mother of zacarias moussaoui .	我是zacariasmoussaoui之母
and i asked the organization of human rights to put me in touch with the parents of the victims .	我要求人權組織讓我去接觸那些受害者的父母 。
so they introduced me to five families .	所以他們介紹我給五個家庭認識 。
and i saw phyllis , and i watched her .	我看到phyllis , 我看著她 。
she was the only mother in the group .	她是這群人中唯一的母親 。
the others were brothers , sisters .	其他都是兄弟姊妹
and i saw in her eyes that she was a mother , just like me .	我看到在她的眼裡 , 她是母親 , 跟我一樣 。
i suffered a lot as a mother .	身為母親 , 我常受苦 。
i was married when i was 14 .	我十四歲時結了婚 。
i lost a child when i was 15 , a second child when i was 16 .	我十五歲時失去了一個孩子 , 我十六歲時失去了第二個孩子 。
so the story with zacarias was too much really .	所以 , zacarias的故事實在太過分了 。
and i still suffer , because my son is like he's buried alive .	我仍然很痛苦 , 因為我兒子就像被埋了一樣 。
i know she really cried for her son .	我知道她真的為她的兒子哭了 。
but she knows where he is .	但她知道他在哪裡 。
my son , i don't know where he is .	我的兒子 , 我不知道他在哪裡 。
i don't know if he's alive . i don't know if he's tortured .	我不知道他是否還活著 , 我不知道他是否受到折磨 。
i don't know what happened to him .	我不知道他發生了什麼事 。
so that's why i decided to tell my story , so that my suffering is something positive for other women .	這就是為什麼我決定要說我的故事 , 這樣我的苦難對其他女性來說是正面的 。
for all the women , all the mothers that give life , you can give back , you can change .	所有婦女 , 所有賦予生命的母親 , 你可以回饋 , 你可以改變 。
it's up to us women , because we are women , because we love our children .	這取決於我們女人 , 因為我們是女人 , 因為我們愛我們的孩子 。
we must be handinhand and do something together .	我們一定要手牽手一起做些事情 。
it's not against women , it's for us , for us women , for our children .	這不是反對女性 , 而是為了我們 , 為我們女人 , 為了我們的孩子 。
i talk against violence , against terrorism .	我反對暴力 , 反對恐怖主義 。
i go to schools to talk to young , muslim girls so they don't accept to be married against their will very young .	我去學校跟年輕的穆斯林女孩說話 , 這樣他們才不會接受結婚 , 不符合他們的意願 。
so if i can save one of the young girls , and avoid that they get married and suffer as much as i did , well this is something good .	所以 , 如果我能拯救其中一位年輕女孩 , 盡量避免她們結婚、受苦 , 嗯 , 這是件好事 。
this is why i'm here in front of you .	這就是為什麼我會站在你們面前 。
pr: i would like to say that i have learned so much from aicha , starting with that day we had our very first meeting with other family members which was a very private meeting with security , because it was november 2002 , and , frankly , we were afraid of the superpatriotism of that time in the country those of us family members .	pr:我想說我從aicha身上學到很多 , 從那天開始 , 我們第一次和其他家庭成員見面是非常私人的 , 安全是2002年11月 , 老實說 , 我們害怕當時國家裡的超級愛國主義者 。
but we were all so nervous .	但我們都好緊張 。
" why does she want to meet us ? "	「 她為什麼想和我們見面 ? 」
and then she was nervous .	然後她就緊張了 。
" why did we want to meet her ? "	「 為什麼我們要和她見面 ? 」
what did we want from each other ?	我們希望對方得到什麼 ?
before we knew each others' names , or anything , we had embraced and wept .	在我們知道彼此的名字或其他東西之前 , 我們已經擁抱和哭泣 。
then we sat in a circle with support , with help , from people experienced in this kind of reconciliation .	然後我們就圍成一圈 , 帶著支持和幫助 , 人們體驗到了這種和解 。
and aicha started , and she said , " i don't know if my son is guilty or innocent , but i want to tell you how sorry i am for what happened to your families .	aicha從頭開始 , 她說: 「 我不知道我的兒子是有罪還是無罪 , 但我想告訴你們 , 我對你們家人的遭遇有多麼不好意思 。
i know what it is to suffer , and i feel that if there is a crime , a person should be tried fairly and punished . "	我知道痛苦是什麼 , 且我覺得 , 如果犯罪發生 , 應該要被公平對待、被懲罰 。 」
but she reached out to us in that way , and it was , i'd like to say , it was an icebreaker .	但她以那種方式接觸我們 , 我想說 , 那是個破冰的人 。
and what happened then is we all told our stories , and we all connected as human beings .	接下來發生的是 , 我們都說了自己的故事 , 我們都以人類的身分來連結 。
by the end of the afternoon it was about three hours after lunch we'd felt as if we'd known each other forever .	下午完結的時候 , 大概是午餐後的三小時 , 我們覺得好像彼此認識了很久 。
now what i learned from her , is a woman , not only who could be so generous under these present circumstances and what it was then , and what was being done to her son , but the life she's had .	我從她身上學到的是 , 一個女人 , 不單止是她可以如此的寬容即使在當時的處境和當時的處境 , 和正在對她兒子做的事 , 甚至她的生活 。
i never had met someone with such a hard life , from such a totally different culture and environment from my own .	我從來沒有遇過這麼艱苦的人生 , 從一個完全不同的文化和環境 。
and i feel that we have a special connection , which i value very much .	我覺得我們有一種特殊的連結 , 我很重視它 。
and i think it's all about being afraid of the other , but making that step and then realizing , " hey , this wasn't so hard .	我認為這一切都是關於害怕對方 , 但踏出這一步 , 然後了解到: 「 嘿 , 這不是很困難 。
who else can i meet that i don't know , or that i'm so different from ? "	還有誰能跟我見面 , 我不知道 , 或跟我很不一樣 ? 」
so , aicha , do you have a couple of words for conclusion ?	所以 , aicha , 你有幾個字可以得出結論嗎 ?
because our time is up .	因為我們的時間到了 。
aw: i wanted to say that we have to try to know other people , the other .	aw:我想說我們得要試著去認識其他人 , 其他人 。
you have to be generous , and your hearts must be generous , your mind must be generous .	你要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 , 你的心也要寬容 。
you must be tolerant .	你一定要寬容 。
you have to fight against violence .	你必須對抗暴力 。
and i hope that someday we'll all live together in peace and respecting each other .	我希望有一天我們都能和平地生活在一起 , 互相尊重 。
this is what i wanted to say .	這就是我想說的 。
too much of the world lacks access to clean drinking water . engineer michael pritchard did something about it inventing the portable lifesaver filter , which can make the most revolting water drinkable in seconds . an amazing demo from tedglobal 2009 .	世界上太多地方無法取得乾淨的飲用水了 。 工程師麥可.普立查對此採取一些行動 , 發明了可攜式的生命保護過濾器 , 在幾秒鐘之內 , 就能讓最令人振奮的水源喝水 。 2009年tedglobal的演示是非常驚人的 。
business , demo , design , global issues , invention , technology , water	商業、展示設計、全球議題、發明、科技、水資源 。
michael pritchard's water filter turns filthy water drinkable	michaelprichard的水過濾器讓骯髒的水變成可以飲用的 。
i'd like to talk about a couple of things today .	今天我想談幾件事 。
the first thing is water .	第一是水 。
now i see you've all been enjoying the water that's been provided for you here at the conference , over the past couple of days .	現在我看到你們都在享受著會議中的水 , 在過去幾天 , 在會議中提供給你們的水 。
and i'm sure you'll feel that it's from a safe source .	我相信你們會覺得它的來源是安全的 。
but what if it wasn't ?	但如果它不是呢 ?
what if it was from a source like this ?	如果它是來自這樣的來源呢 ?
then statistics would actually say that half of you would now be suffering with diarrhea .	然後統計數字會說你們之中有一半的人現在都在腹瀉中受苦 。
i talked a lot in the past about statistics , and the provision of safe drinking water for all .	我在過去談了很多關於統計和提供所有人安全的飲用水 。
but they just don't seem to get through .	但它們似乎沒能熬過 。
and i think i've worked out why .	我想我找出原因了 。
it's because , using current thinking , the scale of the problem just seems too huge to contemplate solving .	因為 , 用當前的想法 , 這個問題的規模似乎太大了 , 無法想像要解決 。
so we just switch off: us , governments and aid agencies .	所以我們就放棄:我們、政府 , 和援助機構 。
well , today , i'd like to show you that through thinking differently , the problem has been solved .	今天 , 我想告訴各位 , 透過不同的思考方式 , 問題已經被解決了 。
by the way , since i've been speaking , another 13 , 000 people around the world are suffering now with diarrhea .	順道一提 , 從我開始演講到現在 , 全世界還有1萬3千人正在腹瀉中受苦 。
and four children have just died .	四個孩子剛剛死去 。
i invented lifesaver bottle because i got angry .	我發明了lifesaver濾水瓶是因為我很憤怒 。
i , like most of you , was sitting down , the day after christmas in 2004 , when i was watching the devastating news of the asian tsunami as it rolled in , playing out on tv .	我和大部分人一樣 , 就是坐下 , 2004年聖誕節的隔天 , 我看著電視不斷報導亞洲海嘯摧毀性的新聞 , 當時我正在電視上播放 。
the days and weeks that followed , people fleeing to the hills , being forced to drink contaminated water or face death .	接下來的幾週 , 人們逃到山丘上 , 被迫喝被污染的水 , 或面臨死亡 。
that really stuck with me .	這一直困擾著我 。
then , a few months later , hurricane katrina slammed into the side of america .	幾個月後 , 卡崔娜颶風往美國衝刺了 。
" okay , " i thought , " here's a first world country , let's see what they can do . "	「 好吧 , 」 我心想: 「 這是第一個世界國家 , 我們來看看他們能做什麼 。 」
do you know it took five days to get water to the superdome ?	你知道要花五天才能把水送到超級主體嗎 ?
people were shooting each other on the streets for tv sets and water .	人們在街上互相開槍 , 只為了電視機和水 。
that's when i decided i had to do something .	那時 , 我決定我得要做點什麼 。
now i spent a lot of time in my garage , over the next weeks and months , and also in my kitchen much to the dismay of my wife .	接下來的數個月 , 我在車庫裡待了很多時間 , 廚房裡令我妻子感到很沮喪 。
however , after a few failed prototypes , i finally came up with this , the lifesaver bottle .	然而 , 經過一些失敗的原型之後 , 我終於做出了這個 , 生命安全瓶 。
okay , now for the science bit .	好 , 現在來談談科學 。
before lifesaver , the best hand filters were only capable of filtering down to about 200 nanometers .	在lifesaver濾水瓶之前 , 最好的手動過濾器只能過濾小至200奈米 。
the smallest bacteria is about 200 nanometers .	最小的細菌大約200奈米 。
so a 200nanometer bacteria is going to get through a 200nanometer hole .	所以一個200奈米的細菌將會穿過一個200奈米大的洞 。
the smallest virus , on the other hand , is about 25 nanometers .	另一方面 , 最小的病毒大約是25奈米 。
so that's definitely going to get through those 200 nanometer holes .	這絕對會穿過那些200奈米大的洞 。
lifesaver pores are 15 nanometers .	救生員的氣孔是15奈米 。
so nothing is getting through .	所以沒有任何東西走完了 。
okay , i'm going to give you a bit of a demonstration .	好 , 我來示範一下 。
would you like to see that ?	你想看到這個嗎 ?
i spent all the time setting this up , so i guess i should .	我花了很多時間準備它 , 所以我猜我應該試試看 。
we're in the fine city of oxford .	我們住在美好的牛津城裡 。
so someone's done that up .	有人就這麼做了 。
fine city of oxford , so what i've done is i've gone and got some water from the river cherwell , and the river thames , that flow through here . and this is the water .	美好的牛津城 , 我做的是從河裡的陳列帶了一些水 , 還有河流的泰姆斯 , 流過這裡 。 這就是水 。
but i got to thinking , you know , if we were in the middle of a flood zone in bangladesh , the water wouldn't look like this .	但我必須去想 , 你知道嗎 , 如果我們身在孟加拉一帶洪水區的中間 , 水不會像這樣 。
so i've gone and got some stuff to add into it .	所以我拿了一些東西來加進去 。
and this is from my pond .	這是從我池塘拿來的 。
have a smell of that , mister cameraman .	聞一下吧 , 攝影師先生 。
we're just going to pour that in there .	我們就把它倒進去 。
michael pritchard: okay . we've got some runoff from a sewage plant farm .	麥可.普立查:好的 , 我們還有一些從污水處理場流出的 。

put that in there . there we go .	把它放進去 。 就是這樣 。
and some other bits and pieces , chuck that in there .	還有其它的位元和碎片 , 把它放進去 。
and i've got a gift here from a friend of mine's rabbit .	我這裡有一位朋友的兔子送的禮物 。
so we're just going to put that in there as well .	所以我們也把它放進去 。
the lifesaver bottle works really simply .	lifesaver濾水瓶的運作非常簡單 。
you just scoop the water up .	你只要把水往上爬 。
today i'm going to use a jug just to show you all . let's get a bit of that poo in there .	今天我要用一個水壺來展示給大家看 。 讓我們來一點點大便 。
that's not dirty enough . let's just stir that up a little bit .	這還不夠髒 。 我們稍微攪拌一下 。
okay , so i'm going to take this really filthy water , and put it in here . do you want a drink yet ?	好 , 現在我要把這個很骯髒的水放進這個水裡 。 你要喝嗎 ?
okay . there we go .	好了 , 來吧 。
give it a few pumps . okay ?	給它一些泵 。 好嗎 ?
that's all that's necessary .	這些就是必要的 。
now as soon as i pop the teat , sterile drinking water is going to come out .	一旦我把茶拉出來 , 無菌的飲用水就會流出來 。
i've got to be quick . okay , ready ?	準備好了嗎 ?
there we go . mind the electrics .	好了 , 小心電器 。
that is safe , sterile drinking water .	這樣很安全 , 無菌的飲用水 。
there you go chris .	來吧克里斯 。
what's it taste of ?	它的味道是什麼 ?
let's see chris's program throughout the rest of the show . okay ?	我們來看看克里斯在接下來的節目裡的節目 。 好嗎 ?
okay . lifesaver bottle is used by thousands of people around the world .	世界各地有數千人使用lifesaver濾水瓶
it'll last for 6 , 000 liters .	可以維持6000公升
and when it's expired , using failsafe technology , the system will shut off , protecting the user .	當它過期時 , 使用故障安全的技術 , 系統就會關閉 , 保護使用者 。
pop the cartridge out . pop a new one in .	將內筒取出 , 換一個新的進去 。
it's good for another 6 , 000 liters .	可以再增加6 , 000公升 。
so let's look at the applications .	咱們來看看這些應用 。
traditionally , in a crisis , what do we do ?	傳統上 , 在危機中 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
then , after a few weeks , we set up camps .	幾個禮拜後 , 我們建立營地 。
and people are forced to come into the camps to get their safe drinking water .	人們被迫來到難民營取得安全的飲用水 。
what happens when 20 , 000 people congregate in a camp ?	當兩萬人聚集在營地時會發生什麼事 ?
diseases spread . more resources are required .	疾病傳播 , 需要更多的資源
the problem just becomes selfperpetuating .	問題只在於自行複製 。
but by thinking differently , and shipping these , people can stay put .	但換種方式思考 , 運送這些資訊 , 人們就可以留在原地 。
they can make their own sterile drinking water , and start to get on with rebuilding their homes and their lives .	他們可以自行製造無菌飲用水 , 並開始重建他們的家園和生活 。
now , it doesn't require a natural disaster for this to work .	這並不需要天然災害才可行 。
using the old thinking , of national infrastructure and pipe work , is too expensive .	用舊的想法 , 國家基礎建設和管道工程的費用實太昂貴了
when you run the numbers on a calculator , you run out of noughts .	當你計算機運算時 , 你的運算能力不夠 。
so here is the " thinking different " bit .	這就是 「 用不同想法 」 的部份 。
instead of shipping water , and using manmade processes to do it , let's use mother nature . she's got a fantastic system .	與其運送水和使用人造過程來運送 , 讓我們使用大自然 。 她有一個很棒的系統 。
she picks the water up from there , desalinates it , for free , transports it over there , and dumps it onto the mountains , rivers , and streams .	她從上面取水 , 免費淡化水 , 運送到那裡 , 把水傾倒在山上、河流和溪流上 。
and where do people live ? near water .	人們住在哪裡 ? 鄰近水源的地方 。
all we've go to do is make it sterile . how do we do that ?	我們要做的就是讓它消毒 。 我們要怎麼做呢 ?
well , we could use the lifesaver bottle .	我們可以使用lifesaver濾水瓶 。
or we could use one of these .	或者我們也可以用這一種 。
the same technology , in a jerry can .	同樣的技術 , 裝在五加侖罐子裡 。
this will process 25 , 000 liters of water ; that's good enough for a family of four , for three years .	這會處理二萬五千公升的水 , 這足夠一個四人家庭使用三年 。
and how much does it cost ?	要花多少錢 ?
about half a cent a day to run .	每天大約只需半分錢 。
so , by thinking differently , and processing water at the point of use , mothers and children no longer have to walk four hours a day to collect their water .	所以 , 用不同的方式思考 , 在用水時處理水 , 母親和孩子們不再需要每天走四小時來取得他們的用水 。
they can get it from a source nearby .	他們可以從附近的資源取得它 。
so with just eight billion dollars , we can hit the millennium goal's target of halving the number of people without access to safe drinking water .	只要花八十億美元 , 我們就能達到千禧目標的目標 , 讓無法取得安全飲用水的人數減半 。
to put that into context , the u . k . government spends about 12 billion pounds a year on foreign aid .	具體而言 , 英國政府每年花大約120億英鎊在國外援助上 。
but why stop there ?	但 , 為什麼會停在這裡 ?
with 20 billion dollars , everyone can have access to safe drinking water .	有了200億美元 , 每個人都能取得安全的飲用水 。
so the threeandahalf billion people that suffer every year as a result , and the two million kids that die every year , will live .	結果是每年因此受苦的三十五億人 , 每年死亡的兩百萬名孩童會活下來 。
paddy ashdown claims that we are living in a moment in history where power is changing in ways it never has before . in a spellbinding talk at tedxbrussels he outlines the three major global shifts that he sees coming .	paddyashown聲稱我們活在歷史的某個時刻 , 權力正以前所未有的方式變化 。 在tedxbrusel的演講中 , 他發表了他為期三大全球性變化 。
foreign policy , global issues , politics , world cultures	外交政策、全球議題、政治、世界文化 ,
paddy ashdown: the global power shift	paddyashown:全球權力轉移 。
there's a poem written by a very famous english poet at the end of the 19th century .	有首詩是十九世紀末由一位非常有名的英國詩人所寫的
it was said to echo in churchill's brain in the 1930s .	它在1930年代被告知要在教堂的腦中迴盪 。
and the poem goes: " on the idle hill of summer , lazy with the flow of streams , hark i hear a distant drummer , drumming like a sound in dreams , far and near and low and louder on the roads of earth go by , dear to friend and food to powder , soldiers marching , soon to die . "	這首詩是這麼寫的: 「 夏日的山丘上 , 躺在潮流之中 , 我聽見遠方的鼓聲 , 像夢裡的聲音一樣 , 遠、近、低沉、大聲說出來 , 在地球的道路上 , 親愛的朋友、食物 , 走到粉末的路上 , 很快就要死 。 」
those who are interested in poetry , the poem is " a shropshire lad " written by a . e . housman .	那些對詩很感興趣的人 , 這首詩的作者是一位shropshirelad的作家 , 由一位e.e.豪斯曼所寫 。
but what housman understood , and you hear it in the symphonies of nielsen too , was that the long , hot , silvan summers of stability of the 19th century were coming to a close , and that we were about to move into one of those terrifying periods of history when power changes .	但是 , 豪斯曼所領悟到的 , 你也在尼爾森交響曲中聽過 , 那是十九世紀那漫長 , 炎熱的夏天 , 卻是近距離的 , 我們即將進入歷史上最恐怖的時期之一 , 那時的權力正在改變 。
and these are always periods , ladies and gentlemen , accompanied by turbulence , and all too often by blood .	各位先生女士這些日子總是伴隨著騷動偶爾也會有血
and my message for you is that i believe we are condemned , if you like , to live at just one of those moments in history when the gimbals upon which the established order of power is beginning to change and the new look of the world , the new powers that exist in the world , are beginning to take form .	我給你們的訊息是 , 我相信我們被譴責 , 若你們願意 , 只活在歷史上的那些時刻 , 當那些已經建立的權力秩序發生改變的時刻 , 以及這個世界的新樣貌 , 那些存在於世界上的新權力開始成形 。
and these are and we see it very clearly today nearly always highly turbulent times , highly difficult times , and all too often very bloody times .	那些是--我們今天很清楚的看到--幾乎每次都非常混亂 , 非常艱難--而且經常是非常血腥的時代 。
by the way , it happens about once every century .	順便一提 , 這種事每個世紀都會發生一次 。
you might argue that the last time it happened and that's what housman felt coming and what churchill felt too was that when power passed from the old nations , the old powers of europe , across the atlantic to the new emerging power of the united states of america the beginning of the american century .	你也許會說 , 上一次發生的狀況 , 那就是霍斯曼的感受 , 和邱吉爾的感受 , 當權力從原住民傳過來 , 歐洲的舊勢力 , 橫跨大西洋到美國的新興勢力──這就是本世紀初的開始 。
and of course , into the vacuum where the tooold european powers used to be were played the two bloody catastrophes of the last century the one in the first part and the one in the second part: the two great world wars .	當然 , 在那個時候歐洲人過時的權力被用來扮演兩場血腥的災難就在上個世紀第一部份第二部份:兩次世界大戰
mao zedong used to refer to them as the european civil wars , and it's probably a more accurate way of describing them .	毛澤東曾經說過他們是歐洲內戰 , 這可能是更正確的描述方式 。
well , ladies and gentlemen , we live at one of those times .	各位先生女士 , 我們生活的次數之一 。
but for us , i want to talk about three factors today .	但對我們來說 , 我今天要談三個因素 。
and the first of these , the first two of these , is about a shift in power .	第一種是權力移轉 。
and the second is about some new dimension which i want to refer to , which has never quite happened in the way it's happening now .	第二個層面是我想指出的一些新的層面在現今從來沒有像現在這樣發生過
but let's talk about the shifts of power that are occurring to the world .	但讓我們來談談世界上發生的權力移轉 。
and what is happening today is , in one sense , frightening because it's never happened before .	現今正在發生的是 , 在某種意義上 , 可怕 , 因為以前從來沒有發生過 。
we have seen lateral shifts of power the power of greece passed to rome and the power shifts that occurred during the european civilizations but we are seeing something slightly different .	我們見過橫向的權力轉移──希臘的力量被轉移到羅馬 , 在歐洲文明中發生的權力轉移──但我們看到的稍微不同 。
for power is not just moving laterally from nation to nation .	因為權力不只是國與國之間的橫向移轉 。
it's also moving vertically .	它還直向運動 。
what's happening today is that the power that was encased , held to accountability , held to the rule of law , within the institution of the nation state has now migrated in very large measure onto the global stage .	現今所發生的是 , 被推廣的權力 , 被責任的權力 , 受到法律的牽制 , 到了國家的機構內 , 已經大幅遷移到全球的舞台上 。
the globalization of power we talk about the globalization of markets , but actually it's the globalization of real power .	全球化的權力雖然我們說是全球化市場但實際上卻是全球化權力
and where , at the nation state level that power is held to accountability subject to the rule of law , on the international stage it is not .	從國家的角度來看 , 權力掌握在法律的掌控權 , 在國際舞台上 , 並非如此 。
the international stage and the global stage where power now resides: the power of the internet , the power of the satellite broadcasters , the power of the money changers this vast moneygoround that circulates now 32 times the amount of money necessary for the trade it's supposed to be there to finance the money changers , if you like , the financial speculators that have brought us all to our knees quite recently , the power of the multinational corporations now developing budgets often bigger than mediumsized countries .	現在的國際舞台和全球舞台 , 即網路的力量、衛星廣播的力量、金錢轉移的力量、流通的金錢財富比交易所需的金錢還要高32倍 , 如果你願意 , 金融的推測者 , 近期已經把我們都帶到我們的膝蓋上了 , 數量的預算增加了32倍 。
these live in a global space which is largely unregulated , not subject to the rule of law , and in which people may act free of constraint .	這些生活在一個全球化的空間 , 大多是沒有規範的 , 而非受到法律的限制 , 人們可能不受約束 。
now that suits the powerful up to a moment .	現在這套方法很強而有力地結合了這個時刻 。
it's always suitable for those who have the most power to operate in spaces without constraint , but the lesson of history is that , sooner or later , unregulated space space not subject to the rule of law becomes populated , not just by the things you wanted international trade , the internet , etc . but also by the things you don't want international criminality , international terrorism .	那些在沒有限制的情況下最有權力的人在沒有制約的環境中運行 , 但歷史的教訓是 , 遲早 , 沒有管制的空間 , 不會受到法律的規則所牽涉 , 不僅僅是你想要的國際貿易、網路、等等 。 還包括你不希望國際犯罪、國際恐怖主義 。
the revelation of 9/11 is that even if you are the most powerful nation on earth , nevertheless , those who inhabit that space can attack you even in your most iconic of cities one bright september morning .	911的真相是 , 即使你是地球上最強大的國家 , 然而 , 那些生活在太空中的國家 , 卻能夠攻擊你 , 即使是在九月的一個早晨當中 , 最具代表性的象徵 。
it's said that something like 60 percent of the four million dollars that was taken to fund 9/11 actually passed through the institutions of the twin towers which 9/11 destroyed .	有人說四百萬美金中大約有百分之六十用來資助911恐怖攻擊的錢是從雙子星大樓的機構通過911摧毀的
you see , our enemies also use this space the space of mass travel , the internet , satellite broadcasters to be able to get around their poison , which is about destroying our systems and our ways .	我們的敵人也使用這樣的空間大眾旅遊、網路、衛星廣播人員有能力購買毒藥 , 也就是摧毀我們的系統和路線 。
sooner or later , sooner or later , the rule of history is that where power goes governance must follow .	遲早 , 早晚或晚 , 歷史的規則就是權力在哪裡被治理 。
and if it is therefore the case , as i believe it is , that one of the phenomenon of our time is the globalization of power , then it follows that one of the challenges of our time is to bring governance to the global space .	因此 , 如我所相信的 , 如果發生了這種狀況 , 我們這個時代的一個現象就是權力全球化 , 那麼我們這個時代所面臨的挑戰就是把統治者帶到國際舞台上 。
and i believe that the decades ahead of us now will be to a greater or lesser extent turbulent the more or less we are able to achieve that aim: to bring governance to the global space .	我相信在未來的數十年 , 將會是越來越多或更少的亂流 , 我們有能力達到那個目標:把統治者帶到全球空間 。
now notice , i'm not talking about government .	請注意 , 我不是在說政府 。
i'm not talking about setting up some global democratic institution .	我不是在說要建立一些全球民主制度 。
my own view , by the way , ladies and gentlemen , is that this is unlikely to be done by spawning more u . n . institutions .	對了 , 我自己的看法是 , 女士們先生們 , 我不太可能會有更多聯合國機構的幫助 。
if we didn't have the u . n . , we'd have to invent it .	如果我們沒有聯合國 , 我們就要把它發明出來 。
the world needs an international forum .	這個世界需要一個國際論壇 。
it needs a means by which you can legitimize international action .	它需要一個可以合法化國際行動的手段
but when it comes to governance of the global space , my guess is this won't happen through the creation of more u . n . institutions .	但當涉及國際舞台的管理我認為這不會發生在建立更多的聯合國機構
it will actually happen by the powerful coming together and making treatybased systems , treatybased agreements , to govern that global space .	會發生在強權聚集在一起 , 以條約為基礎的系統 , 以協定為基礎的協定 , 來統治這個全球空間 。
and if you look , you can see them happening , already beginning to emerge .	如果你仔細看 , 你可以看到這些正在發生的事情 , 已經開始發生了 。
the world trade organization: treatybased organization , entirely treatybased , and yet , powerful enough to hold even the most powerful , the united states , to account if necessary .	世界貿易組織:合約為底的組織 , 完全以合約為基礎的組織 , 然而 , 強大到足以維持最強勢的組織 , 即便是美國 , 還是得要考量的 。
kyoto: the beginnings of struggling to create a treatybased organization .	京都議定書:掙扎著想要建立一套合約為底的組織 。
the g20: we know now that we have to put together an institution which is capable of bringing governance to that financial space for financial speculation .	二十國集團現在我們知道我們必須組建一個能夠把統治權帶到金融空間的機構去做金融猜測 。
and that's what the g20 is , a treatybased institution .	這就是二十國集團在做的 , 一個以條約為基礎的機構
now there's a problem there , and we'll come back to it in a minute , which is that if you bring the most powerful together to make the rules in treatybased institutions , to fill that governance space , then what happens to the weak who are left out ?	現在有一個問題 , 我們等下會再回到這個問題 , 就是如果你把最有權力的人集合起來 , 在條約制式的制度上制定出一套規則 , 來填補統治空間 , 那麼弱國又會怎麼樣 ?
and that's a big problem , and we'll return to it in just a second .	這是個大問題 , 我們很快就會回到這問題上 。
so there's my first message , that if you are to pass through these turbulent times more or less turbulently , then our success in doing that will in large measure depend on our capacity to bring sensible governance to the global space .	所以 , 我的第一條訊息就是 , 如果你經由這些動亂次數或更少動盪 , 那麼我們的成功將大量依據我們的能力 , 把合理的管理帶到全球空間 。
and watch that beginning to happen .	看這一開始發生 。
my second point is , and i know i don't have to talk to an audience like this about such a thing , but power is not just shifting vertically , it's also shifting horizontally .	我的第二點是 , 我知道我不需要和像這樣的觀眾談這件事 , 但權力不只是直向移轉 , 還會橫向移轉 。
you might argue that the story , the history of civilizations , has been civilizations gathered around seas with the first ones around the mediterranean , the more recent ones in the ascendents of western power around the atlantic .	你也許會說 , 文明的故事 , 人類文明的歷史 , 已經聚集在海洋上 , 最先到達地中海的文明 , 近期西方後大西洋後裔的後裔 ,
well it seems to me that we're now seeing a fundamental shift of power , broadly speaking , away from nations gathered around the atlantic [seaboard] to the nations gathered around the pacific rim .	在我看來 , 我們現在看到的是更根本的權力移轉 , 廣泛來說 , 遠離大西洋岸周圍的國家 , 到太平洋岸邊的國家 。
now that begins with economic power , but that's the way it always begins .	這要從經濟實力開始 , 但總是這樣開始的 。
you already begin to see the development of foreign policies , the augmentation of military budgets occurring in the other growing powers in the world .	你已經開始看見外交政策的發展 , 軍事預算的增強 , 發生在世界上其他正在成長的政策中 。
i think actually this is not so much a shift from the west to the east ; something different is happening .	我認為 , 這其實不算是從西方移轉到東邊 , 不同的事情正在發生 。
my guess is , for what it's worth , is that the united states will remain the most powerful nation on earth for the next 10 years , 15 , but the context in which she holds her power has now radically altered ; it has radically changed .	我想 , 值得一提的是美國會永遠是地球上最強大的國家在接下來的十年 , 十五年 , 她掌握她的權力的情境已經徹底改變 , 已經徹底改變了 。
we are coming out of 50 years , most unusual years , of history in which we have had a totally monopolar world , in which every compass needle for or against has to be referenced by its position to washington a world bestrode by a single colossus .	我們正走出過去的50年 , 最不尋常的時代 , 在這個時代 , 我們有一個完全獨立的世界 , 在這個世界中 , 每個指控與否都需要依據它的位置來指出華盛頓這個世界 , 一個巨大的世界是最好的 。
but that's not a usual case in history .	但這在歷史上卻不常見 。
in fact , what's now emerging is the much more normal case of history .	事實上 , 現在所發生的事 , 是歷史上更正常的事 。
you're beginning to see the emergence of a multipolar world .	你開始看到一個多極化的世界出現 。
up until now , the united states has been the dominant feature of our world .	到目前為止 , 美國一直是世界的主導特徵 。
they will remain the most powerful nation , but they will be the most powerful nation in an increasingly multipolar world .	他們會保持最強大的國家 , 但他們會是這個日益擴大的多極世界中最強大的國家 。
and you begin to see the alternative centers of power building up in china , of course , though my own guess is that china's ascent to greatness is not smooth .	你會開始看到在中國建立權力的替代中心 , 當然 , 我個人猜測 , 中國要邁向偉大 , 並不是光滑的 。
it's going to be quite grumpy as china begins to democratize her society after liberalizing her economy .	因為中國在自由經濟之後 , 會開始民主化她的社會 。
but that's a subject of a different discussion .	但那是另一個主題 。
you see india , you see brazil .	你看到的是印度、巴西 。
you see increasingly that the world now looks actually , for us europeans , much more like europe in the 19th century .	事實上 , 對我們歐洲人來說 , 世界看起來越來越像十九世紀的歐洲 。
europe in the 19th century: a great british foreign secretary , lord canning , used to describe it as the " european concert of powers . "	在十九世紀 , 英國的外交大臣坎寧將歐洲描述為 「 歐洲的權力協調 」
there was a balance , a fivesided balance .	有一種平衡 , 一種五面向的平衡 。
britain always played to the balance .	英國人總是在玩平衡 。
if paris got together with berlin , britain got together with vienna and rome to provide a counterbalance .	如果巴黎和柏林合作 , 英國就和維也納和羅馬合作 , 來維也納和羅馬取得平衡 。
now notice , in a period which is dominated by a monopolar world , you have fixed alliances nato , the warsaw pact .	請注意 , 在這個由獨立世界主宰的時期 , 你有著固定的北約組織 , 華沙區聯盟 。
a fixed polarity of power means fixed alliances .	一個固定的權力兩極性意味著結盟 。
but a multiple polarity of power means shifting and changing alliances .	但 , 權力的多極性 , 意味著改變和改變盟友 。
and that's the world we're coming into , in which we will increasingly see that our alliances are not fixed .	這就是我們即將進入的世界 , 我們將會看到越來越多的同盟國沒有被修復 。
canning , the great british foreign secretary once said , " britain has a common interest , but no common allies . "	傑出的英國外交大臣坎寧曾說過: 「 英國有一個共同的興趣 , 但沒有普通的盟友 。 」
and we will see increasingly that even we in the west will reach out , have to reach out , beyond the cozy circle of the atlantic powers to make alliances with others if we want to get things done in the world .	我們也會逐漸看到 , 即使在西方世界我們也需要向外伸出援手 , 超越大西洋的舒適圈 , 和他人結盟 , 只要我們想要在世界上做事 。
note , that when we went into libya , it was not good enough for the west to do it alone ; we had to bring others in .	請注意 , 當我們進入利比亞時 , 西方是不夠的 , 我們必須讓其他人參與 。
we had to bring , in this case , the arab league in .	在這個例子中 , 我們得要把阿拉伯聯盟帶進來 。
my guess is iraq and afghanistan are the last times when the west has tried to do it themselves , and we haven't succeeded .	我猜伊拉克和阿富汗是西方國家嘗試自己做事的最後幾次 , 但我們還沒有成功 。
my guess is that we're reaching the beginning of the end of 400 years i say 400 years because it's the end of the ottoman empire of the hegemony of western power , western institutions and western values .	我想我們快要到400年底的開始了我說四百年後才終止因為這是西方國家權力、西方國家制度和西方價值觀的最終帝國的終點
you know , up until now , if the west got its act together , it could propose and dispose in every corner of the world .	你知道嗎 , 到目前為止 , 如果西方國家能攜手合作 , 它能在世界的每個角落提出並丟棄 。
but that's no longer true .	但這已經不是事實了 。
take the last financial crisis after the second world war .	以上次世界大戰後的金融危機為例 。
the west got together the bretton woods institution , world bank , international monetary fund the problem solved .	西方世界銀行 , 國際貨幣基金組織問題解決了 。
now we have to call in others .	現在我們必須在別人身上打電話 。
now we have to create the g20 .	現在我們必須建立一個g20集團
now we have to reach beyond the cozy circle of our western friends .	現在我們必須超越西方朋友的舒適圈 。
let me make a prediction for you , which is probably even more startling .	讓我來做個預測 , 這可能會更嚇人 。
i suspect we are now reaching the end of 400 years when western power was enough .	我猜想西方國家有400年的力量足夠了 , 已經到了西方國家了 。
people say to me , " the chinese , of course , they'll never get themselves involved in peacemaking , multilateral peacemaking around the world . "	人們對我說: 「 中國絕對不會參與什麼在世界上建立和平的活動 。 」
oh yes ? why not ?	沒錯吧 ? 為什麼不呢 ?
how many chinese troops are serving under the blue beret , serving under the blue flag , serving under the u . n . command in the world today ?	有多少中國軍隊在藍色貝雷特的背後服務 , 在藍色旗幟下工作 , 在聯合國的指令下服務 ?
how many americans ? 11 .	有多少美國人 ? 十一歲 。
what is the largest naval contingent tackling the issue of somali pirates ?	對於索馬利亞海盜 , 最大的海軍艦隊到底是什麼 ?
the chinese naval contingent .	中國的海軍憲法
of course they are , they are a mercantilist nation .	當然 , 他們是重商的國家 。
they want to keep the sea lanes open .	他們想要保持航道的開放
increasingly , we are going to have to do business with people with whom we do not share values , but with whom , for the moment , we share common interests .	漸漸地 , 我們得要和我們沒有共享價值觀的人做生意 , 但 , 目前 , 我們共同共同利益 。
it's a whole new different way of looking at the world that is now emerging .	這是個全新的角度來看這世界正在發展
and here's the third factor , which is totally different .	第三個因素 , 完全不同 。
today in our modern world , because of the internet , because of the kinds of things people have been talking about here , everything is connected to everything .	今天 , 在我們的現代世界 , 由於網際網路 , 因為人們在此談論的人們 , 每件事都和一切息息相關 。
we are now interdependent .	我們是互相依賴的 。
we are now interlocked , as nations , as individuals , in a way which has never been the case before , never been the case before .	我們現在的關係 , 以國家和個人的關係 , 在以前從未如此過 , 從未如此過過 。
the interrelationship of nations , well it's always existed .	國與國之間的相關關係一直都存在 。
diplomacy is about managing the interrelationship of nations .	外交就是管理國家之間的相互關係 。
but now we are intimately locked together .	但現在我們被緊密地鎖在一起了 。
you get swine flu in mexico , it's a problem for charles de gaulle airport 24 hours later .	你在墨西哥得到豬流感 , 24小時後 , 查爾斯•高爾機場出了問題 。
lehman brothers goes down , the whole lot collapses .	雷曼兄弟倒閉了 , 整個崩潰了 。
there are fires in the steppes of russia , food riots in africa .	俄羅斯的大草原發生火災非洲的食物暴動
we are all now deeply , deeply , deeply interconnected .	我們彼此之間有著深深的關聯 。
and what that means is the idea of a nation state acting alone , not connected with others , not working with others , is no longer a viable proposition .	也就是說 , 一個國家獨自行動 , 而不是與其他人聯繫 , 不再與其他人合作 , 不再是個可行的論點 。
because the actions of a nation state are neither confined to itself , nor is it sufficient for the nation state itself to control its own territory , because the effects outside the nation state are now beginning to affect what happens inside them .	因為一個國家的行動並不侷限於自己 , 也不夠讓國家能夠去控制它自己的領土 , 因為國外的影響已經開始影響著他們內在的一切 。
i was a young soldier in the last of the small empire wars of britain .	我當時還是個年輕的軍人 , 住在英國最後一場小型帝國戰爭中 。
at that time , the defense of my country was about one thing and one thing only: how strong was our army , how strong was our air force , how strong was our navy and how strong were our allies .	那時 , 我的國家要防禦一件事 , 只有一點:我們的軍隊有多堅強 , 我們的空軍有多堅強 , 我們的海軍有多堅強 , 我們的盟友有多堅強 。
that was when the enemy was outside the walls .	敵人就在城牆外
now the enemy is inside the walls .	現在敵人就在城牆內
now if i want to talk about the defense of my country , i have to speak to the minister of health because pandemic disease is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of agriculture because food security is a threat to my security , i have to speak to the minister of industry because the fragility of our hitech infrastructure is now a point of attack for our enemies as we see from cyber warfare i have to speak to the minister of home affairs because who has entered my country , who lives in that terraced house in that inner city has a direct effect on what happens in my country as we in london saw in the 7/7 bombings .	現在如果我想談談我國家的辯護 , 我必須和衛生部長談 , 因為傳染病對我們的安全是威脅 , 我必須和農業部談談 , 因為糧食安全對我們的安全造成威脅 , 我必須和產業的部長談談 , 因為高科技基礎設施的脆弱 , 現在對敵人的攻擊 , 如同我們從網路戰火上看到的那樣 , 和在我們國家的房子裡發生了什麽樣的影響 。
it's no longer the case that the security of a country is simply a matter for its soldiers and its ministry of defense .	一個國家的安全不再只和軍人和國防有關
it's its capacity to lock together its institutions .	它的能力是把制度鎖在一起的能力 。
and this tells you something very important .	這告訴你們一件很重要的事 。
it tells you that , in fact , our governments , vertically constructed , constructed on the economic model of the industrial revolution vertical hierarchy , specialization of tasks , command structures have got the wrong structures completely .	它告訴我們 , 事實上 , 我們的政府 , 縱向建造 , 建立在工業革命的經濟模式上 , 縱向層級制度 , 分工作任務 , 指揮結構 , 完全錯了結構 。
you in business know that the paradigm structure of our time , ladies and gentlemen , is the network .	在座的各位 , 商人都知道 , 我們時代的典範結構 , 各位 , 先生女士 , 就是網路 。
it's your capacity to network that matters , both within your governments and externally .	你的網路能力是重要的 , 無論在你的政府還是外部 。
so here is ashdown's third law .	這是ashdown的第三定律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順道一提 , 不要問我第一個法則和第二個法則 , 因為我還沒發明出來 ; 第三法則總是比較好聽 , 對吧 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	接下來的第三個法則是 , 在現代 , 每件事都有關連最重要的是 , 你能和別人做什麼 ,
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	無論你是政府 , 還是軍人 , 還是企業 , 還是你的連接點 , 你的連接點 , 你與他人的連結能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解在工業上 , 政府不了解這一點 。
but now one final thing .	但最後一件事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果是這樣的 , 女士們先生們 , 那就是我們現在以過去從來沒有發生過的緊緊相連 , 那麼 , 也是因為我們和彼此有著相同命運 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 也是第一次 , 集體防禦 , 將我們視為國家安全的概念 , 已經不夠了 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	過去 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我很安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家強大 , 我很安全 ; 我的聯盟 , 比如北約組織 , 比他們的聯盟更強大 , 我也很安全 。
it is no longer the case .	這已經不是事實了 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	大規模毀滅性武器的相互關聯性 , 和大規模毀滅性武器的出現越來越多 , 我和我的敵人有著同樣的命運 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	1970年代日內瓦的蘇聯公會議時 , 我當外交官時 , 和蘇聯一起協商時 , 我們成功了 , 因為我們知道我們和他們有共同的命運 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全是不夠的 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	和平來到北愛爾蘭 , 因為雙方都知道零和遊戲是行不通的 。
they shared a destiny with their enemies .	他們和敵人有著相同的命運
one of the great barriers to peace in the middle east is that both sides , both israel and , i think , the palestinians , do not understand that they share a collective destiny .	阻礙著中東和平的其中一項要素是以色列和巴勒斯坦人都不了解他們和我們有著共同的命運
and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以 , 各位先生女士 , 在過去的願景家和詩人們 , 成為我們必須認真看待的公共政策 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 最後就以一首詩結束 。
the great poem of john donne's .	偉大的約翰•多恩的詩
" send not for whom the bell tolls . "	「 不用寄鐘聲給誰 。 」
the poem is called " no man is an island . "	這首詩叫做 " 沒有人是孤島 "
and it goes: " every man's death affected me , for i am involved in mankind , send not to ask for whom the bell tolls , it tolls for thee . "	這句話是: 「 每一個人的死亡都影響著我 , 因為我和人類有關係 , 不要去問鐘聲是什麼人 , 它代表了我 。 」
for john donne , a recommendation of morality .	多恩是道德的建議
for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	我認為 , 對我們而言 , 等式的一部分是生存的 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了找到長壽和健康的路 , 丹•巴特納和團隊研究世界的 「 藍寶地 」 , 這些長老和活力在tedxtc上共享9個常見的飲食習慣 , 和維持一百歲以上的飲食習慣 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物、文化、探索、食物、食物、生命、科學 ,
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	danbuetner:如何活出100+ ?
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	有個丹麥雙胞胎的研究證實 , 在某些生物限制下 , 平均人平均壽命只有百分之十 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外百分之九十是由生活方式決定 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍寶地的前提是:如果我們能找到長壽的最佳生活方式 , 我們就能找出一個實際的長壽公式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一般美國人 , 長壽的最佳公式是什麼 ? 他們大概不會告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽說過南灘減肥法或阿金減肥法
you have the usda food pyramid .	你有美國農業部糧食金字塔
there is what oprah tells us .	歐普拉告訴我們的是:
there is what doctor oz tells us .	oz醫生告訴我們的是:
the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	事實是有很多混淆了真正幫助我們活得更久的東西 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該跑馬拉松還是做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該吃有機肉還是豆腐 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	至於營養品 , 你該吃嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	荷爾蒙或白斑魚呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	故意在其中演奏嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神上 ? 那我們如何社交 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	我們研究長壽的方法是與國家地理雜誌和國家老化研究所合作 , 找出四個人口確定地理界線的確認區域 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後請一組專家帶進去 , 有條理地介紹這些人的所作所為 , 來提煉跨文化的精華 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	演講最後我會告訴你們精華是什麼
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想破除一些常見的迷思長壽的迷思 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個迷思是 , 如果你真的很努力 , 你可以活到一百歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 在美國 , 五千人中只有一個人能活到一百歲 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	雖然它是美國成長最快的族群 , 但很難達到一百人 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是為長壽而設計的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被設計為一種叫做成功繁衍的產品 。
i love that word .	我愛這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	這讓我想起大學日子 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家把這個詞當作成功 , 指的是你有孩子時的年齡 , 接著下一代 , 當你的孩子有了孩子時的年齡 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	演化的影響完全消失後
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是哺乳類 , 如果你是老鼠、大象、或人 , 在這兩者之間 , 都是一樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	要活到一百歲 , 你不僅要有很好的生活方式 , 你還得拿到基因彩票 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個迷思是 , 有些治療可以減緩 , 反轉 , 甚至停止老化 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	仔細想想 , 有99件事情可以讓我們老化 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	只要幾分鐘的時間 , 那些腦細胞就會死亡 , 它們就不會再回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	打網球太激烈 , 膝蓋也擦掉了你的軟骨 , 軟骨從來沒有回來過 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的動脈會堵塞 。 我們的大腦會用斑塊堵塞 , 我們可以得到阿茲海默症 。
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多事情會出錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有三十五兆個細胞 , 上兆個 「 t 」 。 我們在談的是國債數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	那些細胞每八年轉一次 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每次他們調動就會產生一些傷害 , 傷害就會累積起來 。
and it builds up exponentially .	成倍增長 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像以前我們都有披頭四或老鷹專輯我們會把它複製到一個錄音帶上然後讓朋友複製那錄音帶很快地 , 世代代代相傳錄音會聽起來像垃圾
well , the same things happen to our cells .	同樣的事也發生在我們的細胞上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一個六十五歲的人老化的速度比一個十二歲的人快一百二十五倍
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果不能阻止老化或者停止老化 , 我在這裡幹嘛 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	事實上 , 最好的科學告訴我們 , 人體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 對女性來說 , 多了一點 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但在這個國家 , 平均壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以 , 在某個時點 , 我們會在那條線上留下12年美好的光景 。
these are years that we could get .	這些是我們能得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示多年來大部分都免於慢性病、心臟病、癌症和糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為 , 若要消除這些消失光陰最好的方法就是看看世界各地的文化 , 那些實際上正在經歷它們的文化 , 那些地方的人們可以活到一百歲 , 比我們活到更高十倍的比例 , 那些預期壽命多了十二年 , 中年死亡率 , 只是這個國家中年死亡率的一小部分 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現的第一個藍寶地是在義大利海岸附近的125英里處在沙丁尼亞島上
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	不是整座島 , 整座島約有一百四十萬人 , 卻只在高地 , 一個叫努奧羅省的地方 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡是男人最長壽的地區 , 大約百歲人瑞的數目是美國人的十倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這裡的居民不僅活到一百歲 , 他們還活得很好 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	一百零二歲的老人仍然騎腳踏車去工作 , 砍柴 , 還能打敗比自己年輕六十歲的小夥子 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史實際上可以追溯到基督的時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	它其實是一個孤立的青銅器文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地非常貧瘠 , 它們大多是牧羊人 , 牧羊人有規律、低密度的體能活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食主要是以植物為主 , 以可帶到田裡的食物為中心 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們想出一種未發酵的全麥麵包叫做cata音樂 , 用小麥製作 , 一種來自青草餵養的動物的乳酪 , 這種乳酪富含omega-3脂肪酸而非omega-6脂肪酸 , 來自玉米餵養的動物 , 還有一種葡萄酒 , 比世界上任何酒都多出三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但我認為真正的秘密是他們組織社會的方式 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	薩丁尼亞社會最突出的元素之一 , 就是他們對待老人的方式 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你有沒有注意到在美國 , 社會平等似乎在24歲達到高峰 ?
just look at the advertisements .	只要看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在薩丁尼亞 , 你越老越公平 , 你的讚頌就越多智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	走進薩丁尼亞的酒吧你看不到運動畫刊的泳裝日曆而是看到百歲人瑞的月曆
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	事實證明 , 這不只讓老邁的父母跟家人更親近還增加預期壽命四到六年研究顯示那些家庭的小孩也有較低死亡率和較低疾病率
that's called the grandmother effect .	這叫做祖母效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們在地球的另一端發現了第二個藍色區域 , 位在東京的南方800英里 , 在okinawa的阿基戈 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	琉球其實是161個小島
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	主島的北部是世界長壽的原點
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是發現最老的女性居住的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這裡的人有世界上最長而無障礙的預期壽命 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	牠們活很久 , 通常在牠們的睡眠中死亡 , 非常快 , 我可以告訴你們 , 牠們在做愛後 ,
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們比一般美國人多活七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	在美國 , 百歲人瑞的人數是五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	結腸癌和乳癌的機率是五分之一 , 在美國這裡是大殺手 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	心血管疾病的比例是六分之一 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這個文化能產生這些數字 , 很明顯地 , 他們能教導我們一些東西 。
what do they do ?	他們怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	同樣地 , 植物為主的飲食富含許多顏色的蔬菜
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃大約八倍的豆腐 , 和美國人一樣 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比起吃什麼 , 吃什麼就更重要 。
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各式各樣的小策略可以避免過食 , 如你所知 , 這在美國是一個大問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察到的一些策略:它們吃飯時的盤子比較小 , 所以每次吃的卡路里也比較少 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	與其供應家庭風格 , 在這裡你可以無意識地吃東西 , 他們在櫃台上提供食物 , 把食物帶走 , 帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們還有一個三千年的格言我認為是有史以來最好的飲食建議
it was invented by confucius .	它是由孔子所發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這種飲食被稱為 「 嗜鹽、嗜鹽 」 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是一個小小的說法 , 讓人們在用餐前提醒他們不要再吃東西的時候 , 八分一飽就好 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	飽足感要花上半小時才能從肚子傳到腦袋
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	藉由記住 , 到達80% , 它可以幫助你避免這麼做 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 和薩丁尼亞一樣 , 琉球人有少數的社會結構可以讓我們聯想到長壽 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道隔離會導致死亡 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	十五年前美國人平均有三個好朋友
we're down to one and half right now .	現在我們只剩下一個半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你夠幸運生在琉球你會生在一個自動擁有半打朋友的系統
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱之為模合 。 如果你碰到運氣 , 你會被期待分享假如不好的孩子生病、父母去世 , 你總會有人支持你 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這個特別的moai , 這五位女士已經在一起九十七年了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均年齡是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國我們會把成人生活分成兩個部分 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	我們的工作是有生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 砰 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這指的就是要退出去輕鬆的椅子 , 或是去亞利桑那州打高爾夫 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在琉球語中甚至沒有退休這個詞
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反而是有個詞會打動你整個人生 , 這個詞是 「 ikigai 」 。
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	粗略的翻譯是 " 早上起床的理由 "
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	對於這位一百零二歲的空手道師父來說 , 他的生存價值就是這項武術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這位一百歲的漁夫來說 , 牠一週持續捕魚三次 ,
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是一個問題國家老化研究院給了我們一個問卷給這些百歲人瑞
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	其中一個問題 , 他們非常有文化觀 , 提出問卷的人 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的生存價值是什麼 ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們馬上就知道他們早上起床的理由 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	對這位一百零二歲的老太來說她的生存價值只是她的曾曾曾孫女
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	有兩個女孩 , 年齡在101歲半時分開了 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	我問她感覺如何抱著一個曾曾孫女 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她回過頭說: 「 感覺好像飛躍上天堂 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我覺得那是個很棒的想法 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我在地理的編輯要我去找美國的藍寶地 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	有一陣子我們看了明尼蘇達的草原那裡的百歲人瑞的比例非常高
but that's because all the young people left .	但是因為年輕人都離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再次轉向資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現 , 美國最長壽的民眾 , 來自七天前的教友集中在加州的羅馬林達市 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	基督復臨派是保守的衛理學家 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們在星期五日落後慶祝安息日 , 到星期六日出為止 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	他們稱之為 「 二十四小時的庇護 」 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	它們遵循了五個小習慣 , 相對來說 , 它們的長壽相對是很長的 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 平均女性的預期壽命是80 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一個基督復臨派的女士來說 , 他們的預期壽命是89 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	男性之間的差異更為明顯他們預期壽命比美國同伴多11年
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這個研究追蹤了大約七萬人三十年 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史特林研究 。 我認為它最能說明這個藍寶地計畫的基礎 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是一個多種族的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	白人、黑人、西班牙裔、亞洲人 。
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一的共通點就是一套非常小的生活習慣 , 幾乎一輩子都遵守儀式 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們直接從聖經中採取飲食 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	創世紀第一章第二十九章上帝談到豆子和種子另一節則是談到綠色植物很明顯少了肉
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們非常認真地看待這個庇護時間 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週24小時 , 無論他們多忙 , 工作壓力多大 , 孩子需要被駕駛 , 停止一切 , 專注於他們的上帝 , 他們的社交網路 , 接著 , 宗教信仰的天性 , 就是走進大自然 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	強大之處不在於偶爾完成 , 權力是每週完成一輩子的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	一點都不困難 , 一點都不花錢
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	基督復臨派教徒往往和其他基督教徒混在一起
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一個基督復臨派的會議 , 你不會看到有人在揮舞吉姆貝姆或揮舞著關節 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	相反地 , 他們在談下一次的自然步行交換食譜 , 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但它們會用很深刻、可量化的方式影響彼此 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這個文化讓埃爾斯沃•偉倫這樣的文化出現了 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	埃爾斯沃•偉倫九十七歲 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是百萬富翁 , 但當承包商想要六千美金來建立隱私圍籬時 , 他說: 「 為了這類錢 , 我自己自己做吧 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天他都在外頭鏟水泥把欄杆拖來拖去
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	可以預測 , 也許到了第四天他被送進手術室
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是手術台上這個人 , 而是開心手術的那個人 。
at 97 he still does 20 openheart surgeries every month .	九十七歲的他一個月仍動二十次開心手術 。
ed rawlings , 103 years old now , an active cowboy , starts his morning with a swim .	艾德•羅林斯 , 現在一百零三歲 , 是個活躍的牛仔 , 早上就開始游泳 。
and on weekends he likes to put on the boards , throw up rooster tails .	在週末 , 他喜歡踏上衝浪板 , 放棄公雞尾巴 。
her grandson actually lives in the twin cities here .	她的孫子其實就住在雙子城這裡 。
she starts her day with lifting weights .	她每天從舉重開始 。
