she rides her bicycle .	她騎腳踏車 。
and then she gets in her rootbeer colored 1994 cadillac seville , and tears down the san bernardino freeway , where she still volunteers for seven different organizations .	再來是1994年的塞維利亞凱迪拉克 , 她在聖貝納迪諾高速公路上揮手 , 到現在她仍是七個不同組織的志工 。
i've been on 19 hardcore expeditions .	我曾經參加過19次深奧的探險 。
i'm probably the only person you'll ever meet who rode his bicycle across the sahara desert without sunscreen .	我大概是你見過的唯一一個人他騎著腳踏車橫越撒哈拉沙漠卻沒有防曬霜
but i'll tell you , there is no adventure more harrowing than riding shotgun with marge deton .	但我要告訴各位 , 沒有任何探險比坐上瑪莉奇•戴頓的槍擊事件更恐怖 。
" a stranger is a friend i haven't met yet ! " she'd say to me .	「 陌生人是我還沒見過的朋友 ! 」 她對我說 。
so , what are the common denominators in these three cultures ?	所以 , 這三個文化中的共通點是什麼 ?
what are the things that they all do ?	什麼是他們全部都在做的事 ?
and we managed to boil it down to nine .	我們試著歸納出九項
in fact we've done two more blue zone expeditions since this and these common denominators hold true .	事實上我們已經多做了兩次藍寶地探險 , 和這些常見的探險家所持的關係 。
and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	第一項我即將要說一項悖論他們都不運動至少是我們所認為的運動
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	取而代之 , 他們建立起自己的生活 , 使他們不斷地進入身體的活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些百歲的琉球女人女人坐在地板上 , 每天30到40次 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	薩丁尼亞人住在垂直的房子裡 , 上下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次去商店、教堂、或朋友家都要走路 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們一點都不方便 。
there is not a button to push to do yard work or house work .	沒有按鈕可以達到院子工作或家庭工作 。
if they want to mix up a cake , they're doing it by hand .	如果他們想混合蛋糕 , 他們就用手做蛋糕 。
that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	就像跑步機一樣能燃燒卡路里
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們有意圖做身體活動時 , 這是他們喜歡做的事 。 他們會走路 , 唯一證明能否保持認知衰退的方法 , 而且他們都傾向有菜園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何用正確的方式生活所以他們有正確的人生觀 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每個文化都要花時間來轉變 。
the sardinians pray . the seventhday adventists pray .	薩丁尼亞人祈禱 , 第七天的教導教徒祈禱 。
the okinawans have this ancestor veneration .	琉球人有這種祖先的復原
but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你匆匆促或焦慮不安會引發一種發炎反應這反應和阿茲海默症到心血管疾病相關
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你一天放慢15分鐘 , 你就把那發炎狀態轉變成更加抗炎的狀態 。
they have vocabulary for sense of purpose , ikigai , like the okinawans .	他們有詞彙來表達刻意的意義 , 像琉球人 ,
you know the two most dangerous years in your life are the year you're born , because of infant mortality , and the year you retire .	你知道你生命中最危險的兩年就是你出生的那一年 , 因為嬰兒死亡率 , 以及退休那年 。
these people know their sense of purpose , and they activate in their life , that's worth about seven years of extra life expectancy .	這些人知道他們的使命感 , 他們在生活中活躍起來 , 這價值大約是七年的預期壽命 。
there's no longevity diet .	沒有長壽飲食 。
instead , these people drink a little bit every day , not a hard sell to the american population .	相反的 , 這些人每天都少喝點酒 , 對美國人來說不難賣 。
they tend to eat a plantbased diet .	他們傾向於吃植物肉 。
doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不是說他們不吃肉 , 而是很多豆子和堅果 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來避免過食一些小東西 , 在適當的時間點讓他們遠離餐桌
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	這一切的基礎是他們如何建立關係 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把家人放在第一 , 照顧他們的孩子和年邁的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們全都屬於一個以信仰為基礎的社群 , 一個月可以多增加4 ~ 14年的預期壽命 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	最重要的是他們也屬於對的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們不是生來就遇到對的人就是他們積極和平共處
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從佛明罕研究中得知 , 如果你三個最好的朋友都過胖你有一半的機率會超重 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和不健康的人混在一起 , 隨著時間 , 會有明顯的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反地 , 如果你的朋友對休閒活動的想法是體力活動 , 保齡球或打曲棍球騎腳踏車或園藝如果你的朋友喝點酒 , 但不是過量 , 他們會吃對的 , 他們會很投入 , 而且信任和信任 , 隨著時間 , 會有最大的影響 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	減肥是行不通的 。 飲食在世界歷史上從來沒有人為超過百分之二的人口工作過
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	運動計劃通常一月開始十月就結束
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	關於長壽並沒有短期的解決方案 , 不管是藥丸或其他的 ,
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你仔細想想 , 你的朋友是長期的冒險 , 因此 , 也許你能做的最重要的事情是增加年歲 , 增加年歲 。 謝謝你 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	傳導電流的墨水一扇從明顯轉變為不透明的窗戶一旦轉換成了音樂 , 所有東西都存在 , 而catanamota就說了:該是時候讓我們玩樂了 。 mota帶領我們參觀一個驚喜和酷炫的新材料然後他提醒了我們該如何做實驗 , 要嘗試 , tker , 要有樂趣
creativity , design , technology	創意、設計、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:玩玩玩聰明的材料 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我在葡萄牙有位朋友 , 他的祖父用腳踏車和洗衣機造了一台車 , 讓他能夠運送家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他負擔不起車子 , 也是因為他知道如何蓋車 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	曾幾何時 , 我們了解事物是如何運作的 , 如何被製造出來 , 我們就能建造、修復它們 , 至少能根據購買來做出明確的決策 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在二十世紀的後半 , 許多diy的做法在二十世紀的後半就消失了 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 自造者社群和開放原始碼的模式正在將這類知識帶回我們的生活中 , 我相信我們需要把這些知識帶到下一個階段 , 由零件組成 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	大部分的時候 , 我們仍然知道紙和紡織品等傳統材料是由什麼製造的 , 以及它們的生產方式 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有了這些奇妙、未來化的複合材料 , 可以改變形狀、可以導電的顏料、可以改變顏色的顏料、會發光的布料 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我給你們看一些例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	導電油墨讓我們不用傳統印刷電路或電線來繪畫電路 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在我手上拿著的這個小例子中 , 我們用它來製造一個觸控感應器 , 通過打開這個小光線 , 針對我的皮膚做出反應 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	藝術家早已在用導電油墨 , 但近期的開發顯示 , 我們很快就能把它用在雷射印表機和筆上 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這塊丙烯酸纖維附滿了無色的散光粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這意味著 , 雖然普通的丙烯酸纖維只會在邊緣散光 , 但當我打開燈時 , 它會在整個表面上發光 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	這類材質的應用 , 包括室內設計和多點觸控系統 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	熱變色的顏料在特定溫度下會改變顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把這個放到熱板上 , 把這個溫度設定在比環境高一點點的地方 , 大家可以看到會發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	這項材料主要的應用是在嬰兒奶瓶上它能顯示內容物是否涼了可以喝了
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	這些只是一些常被稱為智慧型材料的例子 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	再過幾年 , 它們就會成為我們日常生活中常用物品和技術的一部分 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒辦法擁有科幻小說中會出現的飛天車科幻小說裡會有改變顏色的牆壁 , 依溫度而改變顏色的鍵盤捲起來的鍵盤 , 開關就會變得不透明的窗戶 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是社會科學家 , 所以 , 我為什麼要在這裡談論智慧型材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個製造家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我對事物的運作感到好奇 , 它們是如何被製造出來的 , 也因為我相信 , 我們應該要更深入了解建構出我們世界的元素 , 而現在 , 我們對於這些高科技結合物的未來還不夠了解 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧型材料難以在少量下取得 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	幾乎沒有任何關於如何使用它們的資訊 , 很少人說它們是如何被製造出來的 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	目前 , 它們主要存在於商業機密和專利中 , 只有大學和企業能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	大約三年前 , 我和克絲蒂•波爾開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為 「 公開材料 」 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	在這個網站中 , 我們和任何想要加入的人都可以分享實驗成果 , 發表資訊鼓勵其他人隨時隨地做出貢獻並收集像我們一樣的研究報告和導資料
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它能變成一個大型、集體生成的 , 用智慧型材料來發送自己的信息庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但 , 為什麼我們要在乎智慧型材料的運作方式以及它們的組成方式 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法形塑我們不了解的東西 , 而我們不了解且使用的東西最後會形塑我們 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們用的物品 , 我們穿的衣服 , 我們住的房子 , 都對我們的行為、健康和生活品質有著深遠的影響 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們要活在一個由智慧型材料構成的世界 , 我們應該要知道且了解它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二點 , 同樣重要的是 , 創新總是由改造者推動的 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 業餘人士 , 不是專家 , 是發明家和改進者 , 從山腳踏車到半導體、個人電腦、飛機等都有 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是材料科學很複雜 , 需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但事實並非全然如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	伊利諾大學有兩位科學家 , 當時發表了一篇論文 , 用較簡單的方法製作導電油墨 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	jordanbunker在讀這篇論文後完全沒有化學經驗他在他的造物空間中只靠現成的物質和工具重現了這個實驗
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他用烤箱甚至根據其他科學家的說明書自製試管混合器
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	喬登接著在網路上發佈了他的結果 , 包括他試過、不成功的所有試驗結果 , 讓其他人可以學習並進行複製 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	喬登創新的主要形式就是在設備精良的大學實驗室裡進行一項由設備精密的實驗在芝加哥的車庫裡只用便宜的材料和工具他自己製作
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在 , 他發表了這項研究 , 其他人可以接續並設計更簡單的處理程序和改善 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另外一個例子 , 我想提到她的專案計畫的目標 , 是要強調材料的表達性質 , 同時要強調建材的創意和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子組件非常強大 , 它們教導我們事情的運作方式 , 但限制本身就影響了我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	漢娜的辦法 , 另一方面 , 是發想出一系列的技術來創造特別的物體 , 讓我們能不受限於設計的限制 , 來教導我們有關材料本身的知識 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	在漢娜眾多令人印象深刻的實驗中 , 這是我最喜歡的一個 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[紙喇叭]我們現在看到的只是一張紙上面貼了一些銅線 , 連到mp3和磁鐵上
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	根據麻省理工科爾荷州理工學院的研究 , 漢娜用一系列的紙喇叭 , 從簡單的銅膠帶到導電布和油墨 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約旦和許多其它的製造者漢娜把食譜公開讓任何人都能複製和繁殖
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙電子是物質科學中最理想的分支之一 , 它讓我們能創造出較便宜且有彈性的電子 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	漢娜的手工藝成品和她分享發現的事實 , 讓一系列美感與創新的新可能性開啟了她的大門 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	製造者有趣的地方在於 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 我們並不害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從非傳統角度解決問題 , 最後發現替代方案 , 甚至更好的方式來做事 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以越多人在材料上實驗越多研究人員願意分享他們的研究生產者他們的知識我們就有越好的機會創造出服務所有人的科技
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	我覺得我應該有點像泰德尼爾森在1970年代早期寫下 " 你現在應該要了解電腦 "
back then , computers were these large mainframes only scientists cared about , and no one dreamed of even having one at home .	當時 , 電腦是只有科學家在關心的大型計算機甚至沒有人想過要在家裝一個
so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以 , 我站在這裡說 , 有點奇怪 , 「 你現在必須要了解智慧型材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	請記住 , 取得新興科技的先驅知識是確保我們能對自己的未來有發言權的最佳方式 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們會進入一個玻璃氣泡 , 鎖定門和按下加速器 , 靠著我們的眼睛引導我們儘管我們只能看到前面和後面幾個車子 。 但如果車子能和彼此分享資料 , 關於它們的位置和速度 , 用預測模型來計算在路上每個人的安全路線 ? 珍妮•嘿 , 不意外地想像一個沒有意外的世界 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮佛•喜利:如果車子能說話 , 意外可能可以避免發生事故 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	承認吧開車是危險的
it's one of the things that we don't like to think about , but the fact that religious icons and good luck charms show up on dashboards around the world betrays the fact that we know this to be true .	這是我們不喜歡去思考的事情之一 , 但事實是 , 宗教圖像和好運迷圖出現在世界各地的儀表板上 , 背叛了我們所知道的事實 。
car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	車禍是美國16至19歲死亡的主因車禍是死亡的主因而當中百分之七十五的車禍跟毒品或酒精無關
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能肯定說 , 但我記得我的第一次意外 。
i was a young driver out on the highway , and the car in front of me , i saw the brake lights go on .	當時我還年輕在高速公路上 , 前面的車子 , 我看到煞車燈亮了 。
i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 這傢伙慢了 , 我也會慢下來 。 」
i step on the brake .	我踩煞車 。
but no , this guy isn't slowing down .	但 , 不 , 這傢伙並沒有慢下來 。
this guy is stopping , dead stop , dead stop on the highway .	這傢伙在高速公路上停車 , 停車 , 死路段 。
it was just going 65 to zero ?	只能飛65到0嗎 ?
i slammed on the brakes .	我踩煞車 。
i felt the abs kick in , and the car is still going , and it's not going to stop , and i know it's not going to stop , and the air bag deploys , the car is totaled , and fortunately , no one was hurt .	我感覺到abs啟動了 , 車子還在 , 它不會停下來 , 我知道車子不會停下來 , 空氣袋子開了 , 車子完全安裝了 , 幸運的是 , 沒人會受傷 。
but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我完全沒想到那輛車會停我認為我們可以做得更好
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變駕駛經驗 , 做法是讓車子彼此交談 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我希望各位能思考一下這種開車的體驗 , 現在的情況 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	上車 。 關上門 。 你在一個玻璃泡泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你無法直接感受周遭的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個延伸的身體裡 。
you're tasked with navigating it down partiallyseen roadways , in and amongst other metal giants , at superhuman speeds .	你的任務是要引導它 , 讓它在部份看不見的道路上 , 和其他巨大的金屬巨人之間 , 以超人的速度前進 。
okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 你只需要指引你是你的兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好的 , 這就是你所有的眼睛不是為了這個任務而設計的然後人們要求你做這樣的事例如 , 你要換條車道第一件要做的事是什麼 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛從路面上移下來 , 沒錯 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	不要再看你要去哪裡 , 轉過身來 , 檢查你的盲點 , 不看你要去哪裡 。
you and everyone else . this is the safe way to drive .	你和所有其他人 。 這是安全駕駛 。
why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須選擇 , 我們要看這裡 , 還是看這裡 ?
and usually we do a fantastic job picking and choosing what we attend to on the road .	通常我們在路上採取了不起的工作 。
but occasionally we miss something .	但偶爾我們會錯失一些東西 。
occasionally we sense something wrong or too late .	偶爾我們會感覺到不對或太遲的感覺 。
in countless accidents , the driver says , " i didn't see it coming . "	無數的意外 , 司機說: 「 我沒看到它要來 。 」
and i believe that . i believe that .	我相信這一點 。 我相信 。
we can only watch so much .	我們只能看到這麼多東西 。
but the technology exists now that can help us improve that .	但現存的科技 , 能協助我們改善它 。
in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 有了車輛互相交換資料 , 我們不只能看到前面三輛車 , 後面三輛車 , 右邊和左邊全都看到 , 同時 , 鳥類的視野 , 我們確實能看到那些車子的視野 。
we will be able to see the velocity of the car in front of us , to see how fast that guy's going or stopping .	我們可以看見前面車輛的速度 , 看看他能走得多快或不停 。
if that guy's going down to zero , i'll know .	如果那個人要降到零 , 我會知道 。
and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	有了計算、演算法和預測模型 , 我們就能看到未來 。
you may think that's impossible .	你可能認為這不可能 。
how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 這真的很困難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	實際上 , 不對 , 車子不是不可能的
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車是三維立體的物體 , 有固定的位置和速度 。
they travel down roads .	它們沿著道路行走 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	他們經常旅行到已出版的路線上 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	要合理地預測車子在不久的將來會變成什麼樣子並不困難
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即便如此 , 當你坐在車子裡 , 遇到一些摩托車騎士 , 以時速85英里降下 , 車道我知道你有過這種經歷 , 有人沒有 「 無中生有 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個人在路上可能已經走了半小時了 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對吧 ? 我的意思是 , 有人見過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	10 , ~ 20 , 30英里前 , 有人看到那個人 , 一旦有車看到那個人 , 將他放在地圖上 , 他就在地圖上位置 , 速度 , 估計他會以每小時85英哩的速度繼續前進 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你會知道 , 因為你的車會知道 , 因為其他車也會在他的耳邊小聲說一些話 , 比如: 「 順道一提 , 五分鐘 , 摩托車騎士 , 請小心 。 」
you can make reasonable predictions about how cars behave .	你可以合理的預測車的行為
i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 它們是牛頓的物體 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說是很棒的 。
so how do we get there ?	那我們要如何做到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以開始分享我們車子間的位置資料就只是分享gps
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我的車上有gps和照相機 , 我就能精確地知道我在哪裡 , 及我走得多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	用電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車子在哪裡 , 以及他們要往哪裡去 。
and same with the other cars .	其他車也一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	車子的位置可以準確的知道其他車子在哪
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩部車子能分享資料 , 如果它們能彼此交談 , 會發生什麼事 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生了什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	bobwang教授和他的團隊做了電腦模擬模擬 , 估計會發生什麼事 , 甚至在輕量車輛上進行 , 讓車子可以共用gps資料 , 我們將這個研究帶出電腦模擬 , 送到裝有感應器的機器人床上 , 裝有實在的感應器 , 裝在機器人上:立體攝影機、gps , 以及2d雷射雷射測距儀 , 這些都是常用的系統 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們還裝上一台短距的無線電機 , 讓機器人彼此對話 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人彼此碰撞時 , 它們會精確地追蹤彼此的位置 , 它們能夠避開彼此 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	我們現在在這個組合中加入越來越多的機器人 , 我們遇到了一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	其中一個問題是 , 當你太過聊天 , 很難去處理所有的封包 , 所以你得把重點放在第一 , 這就是預測模型幫助你的所在 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人車子在追蹤預測軌跡 , 你不會把注意力放在那些資訊封包上 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	首先你對這個稍微偏離軌道的傢伙進行排序 。
that guy could be a problem .	那個人可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌跡 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以你不只知道他要偏離航道 , 知道如何 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	而且你知道哪些司機需要提醒才能離開 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想做的是 , 我們要如何警告大家 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些車要怎麼小聲地說: 「 你得趕緊離開這裡 ? 」
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 這取決於兩件事:一 , 車子的性能 , 第二是駕駛的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果有人有一輛很棒的車 , 但他們在手機上 , 或者做些什麼 , 他們可能就無法在緊急情況下做出最佳反應 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了分離的研究 , 做關於駕駛者狀態的模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 用三台攝影機 , 我們可以偵測到駕駛人是否會期待前進、看遠、看手機 , 或喝杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預知事故我們可以預測是誰 , 哪些車子最好離開路線去計算每個人最安全的路線
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術現今就存在了 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨的最大問題是我們自己的意願去分享我們的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我想這是個很讓人不安的概念 , 我們的車子會看著我們 , 和其他車子聊天 , 我們將在八卦大海上行駛 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信 , 它能被做成保護我們的隱私的方式 , 就像現在 , 當我從外面看你的車時 , 我真的不了解你 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看著你的牌照號碼 , 我真的不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信 , 我們的車子可以在我們的背後談我們 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我覺得這將會是件好事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我希望你們能考慮一下如果你真的不希望那煩人的青少年在你背後知道你在煞車 , 知道你要停下來 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	藉由自願地分享我們的數據 , 我們可以為每個人做最好的事 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以讓你的車子跟你說話吧
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路更安全 。
x prize founder peter diamandis talks about how he helped stephen hawking fulfill his dream of going to space by flying together into the upper atmosphere and experiencing weightlessness at zero g .	x獎得主彼得•戴曼迪斯談到他如何協助史蒂芬•霍金完成了他的夢想 , 讓他能一起飛上大氣 , 並體驗到在0g時的無重力 。
business , flight , science , short talk , space , technology , universe	商業、飛行、科學、短暫的談話、空間、科技、宇宙等 ,
peter diamandis on stephen hawking in zero g	彼得•戴曼迪斯在史蒂芬•霍金斯 , 00萬得主導一切 。
those of you who know me know how passionate i am about opening the space frontier .	認識我的人都知道我對打開太空新領域有多熱情 。
so when i had the chance to give the world's expert in gravity the experience of zero gravity , it was incredible .	所以當我有機會給這位世界重力專家無重力的經驗時 , 那真是不可思議 。
and i want to tell you that story .	我想告訴你們那個故事 。
i first met him through the archon x prize for genomics .	我第一次見到他是基因學的archonxprize 。
it's a competition we're holding , the second x prize , for the first team to sequence 100 human genomes in 10 days .	這是我們舉辦的競賽 , 第二個xprize , 讓第一組在10天內完成100個人類基因組測序 。
we have something called the genome 100 100 individuals we're sequencing as part of that .	我們有我們稱之為基因組100個個個體的定序 。
craig venter chairs that event .	克萊格•凡特那件事的椅子 。
and i met professor hawking , and he said his dream was to travel into space .	我和霍金教授見面 , 他說他的夢想是上太空旅行 。
and i said , " i can't take you there , but i can take you into weightlessness into zerog .	我說: 「 我不能帶你上去 , 但我可以帶你進入無重力場 , 進入零度 。
and he said , on the spot , " absolutely , yes . "	他說: 「 絕對是的 。 」
well , the only way to experience zerog on earth is actually with parabolic flight , weightless flight .	嗯 , 唯一能體驗世上無重力飛行的方法 , 其實是有拋物線飛行、無重力飛行 。
you take an airplane , you fly over the top , you're weightless for 25 seconds .	你搭飛機 , 飛到頂端 , 你有25秒無重力 。
come back down , you weigh twice as much .	再下來 , 你的體重是兩倍 。
you do it again and again .	你不斷重複這個動作 。
you can get eight , 10 minutes of weightlessness how nasa's trained their astronauts for so long .	你可以有8到10分鐘的無重力經驗 , 美國太空總署訓練他們的太空人太久了 。
we set out to do this .	我們打算這麼做 。
it took us 11 years to become operational .	我們花了11年才開始營運 。
and we announced that we were going to fly stephen hawking .	我們宣布要飛史蒂芬•霍金 。
we had one government agency and one company aircraft operator say , you're crazy , don't do that , you're going kill the guy .	我們有一家政府機關和一家公司的操作員說 , 你瘋了 , 不要這樣做 , 你就會殺了那傢伙 。
and he wanted to go .	他想要去 。
we worked hard to get all the permissions .	我們很努力取得所有的同意 。
and six months later , we sat down at kennedy space center .	六個月後 , 我們在甘迺迪太空中心坐下 。
we had a press conference , we announced our intent to do one zerog parabola , give him 25 seconds of zerog .	我們開了一場記者會 , 我們宣布我們打算要做一個無重力拋物面鏡 , 給他25秒的零 。
and if it went really well , we might do three parabolas .	如果一切順利 , 我們可能會做三個拋物線飛行 。
well , we asked him why he wanted to go up and do this .	嗯 , 我們問他 , 為什麼他要上台來做這件事 ?
and what he said , for me , was very moving .	他對我說的話非常感人 。
he said , " life on earth is at an everincreasing risk of being wiped out by disaster . . .	他說: 「 地球上的生命有不斷增加的風險被災難摧毀......
i think the human race doesn't have a future if it doesn't go into space .	我認為如果人類不上太空 , 就沒有未來 。
i therefore want to encourage public interest in space . "	所以我想鼓勵大眾對太空的興趣 。 」
we took him out to the kennedy space center , up inside the nasa vehicle , into the back of the zerog airplane .	我們帶他到甘迺迪太空中心 , 飛到nasa的車上 , 飛機的後面 。
we had about 20 people who made donations we raised $150 , 000 in donations for children's charities who flew with us .	我們有大約二十個人捐款我們捐十五萬美金給那些跟我們一起飛的兒童慈善機構 。
a few tedsters here .	這裡有幾位tedster 。
we set up a whole er .	我們成立了全急診室 。
we had four emergency room doctors and two nurses on board the airplane .	我們有四個急診醫生和兩位護士在飛機上
we were monitoring his po2 of his blood , his heart rate , his blood pressure .	我們監測他的血液、他的心跳、他的血壓 。
we had everything all set in case of an emergency ; god knows , you don't want to hurt this worldrenowned expert .	萬一發生緊急事故 , 我們都準備好了 ; 天知道 , 你並不想要傷害這位世界知名的專家 。
we took off from the shuttle landing facility , where the shuttle takes off and lands .	我們從太空梭降落場起飛 , 太空梭起降 。
and my partner byron lichtenberg and i carefully suspended him into zerog .	我和我的夥伴byronlichtenberg小心翼翼的讓他停止到零 。
once he was there , [we] let him go to experience what weightlessness was truly like .	一旦他抵達那裡 , 我們就讓他去體驗無重力的真正感覺 。
and after that first parabola , you know , the doc said everything is great . he was smiling , and we said go .	在第一個拋物線飛行過後 , 你知道 , 醫生說一切都很棒 。 他在笑 , 我們說要開始 。
so we did a second parabola .	所以我們做了第二個拋物線飛行 。
we actually floated an apple in homage to sir isaac newton because professor hawking holds the same chair at cambridge that isaac newton did .	我們其實是在艾薩克牛頓博士的致敬下漂浮的蘋果 , 因為霍金教授在劍橋大學擔任和牛頓相同的椅子 。
and we did a fourth , and a fifth and a sixth .	我們做了第四、五、第六次 。
and a seventh and an eighth .	第七和第八次 。
and this man does not look like a 65yearold wheelchairbound man .	這個人看起來不像一個65歲的輪椅男子 。
he was so happy .	他很開心 。
we are living on a precious jewel , and it's during our lifetime that we're moving off this planet .	我們生活在一個珍貴的珠寶中 , 我們正在離開這個星球 。
please join us in this epic adventure .	請加入我們這趟史詩般的探險 。
medical animator david bolinsky presents 3 minutes of stunning animation that show the bustling life inside a cell .	醫學動畫家大衛波林斯基在一個細胞內展現了3分鐘讓人驚訝的生命 。
design , entertainment , film , health , medicine , science , technology , visualizations	設計、娛樂、電影、健康、藥物、科學、科技、視覺化 。
david bolinsky animates a cell	大衛波林斯基對一個細胞進行動畫 ,
i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是醫學繪圖師 , 我從稍微不同的角度看事情 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	自從我長大以來 , 我就一直在觀察著藝術、真與美的表現 , 以及科學中真與美的表現 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是他們自身的美妙事物 , 他們都有非常美妙的事物 , 能讓他們看到真與美 , 能被科學和數學給審視 , 就像理想中完美的連體雙胞胎 , 一個科學家想要約會 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些是對 「 真 」 表示敬畏的表現 , 意思是 , 它們是你可以崇拜的事物 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	它們是強大的理想 。 它們是不可思議的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	它們是獨一無二的 , 有時是有用的 , 通常是很久之後才會發現的 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	現在你就可以開始播放一些照片了 , 因為我不想在螢幕上看到我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	對非科學領域的人來說 , 真與美通常都不太可能 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	它們描述了美麗事物 , 通常只有在你了解一個人的語言和語法中 , 才能夠理解這個主題的人所使用的真與美 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看看數學 , e=mc平方 , 如果你看看宇宙的常數 , 那裡有一個人類的理想 , 你可以看到生命是從描述宇宙的數字進化出來的 。 這些是非常難理解的事物 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	自從我被醫學插圖師教導我的動畫 , 他是雕塑家兼我的視覺導師 , 我想找到一個方法 , 幫助人們理解生物科學中的真與美 , 利用動畫 , 說故事 , 說出故事 , 這樣人們不見得能得到的東西 , 也能被教導 , 能被理解 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	今日的學生常常沉浸在一種環境中 , 他們所學到的 , 是有真與美的主題 , 但他們被教導的方式是片面的 , 而它深深吸引到 , 真與美並不總是顯而易見的 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	就像你煮雞湯的古老食譜 , 直到香味消失為止 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想這樣對學生做 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會真正開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	幾年前 , 我接到哈佛大學分子與細胞生物學系的robertlue打來的電話 。 他問我我跟我的團隊有沒有興趣 , 願意改變哈佛醫學和科學教育的做法 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們開始進行一個探索細胞的計畫 , 這個計畫可以探索分子和細胞生物學中固有的真與美 , 這樣學生才能了解所有這些事實背後的更大圖像 。
they could have a mental image of the cell as a large , bustling , hugely complicated city that's occupied by micromachines .	他們腦海中會出現一個細胞的圖像 , 是個繁忙、非常複雜的城市 , 由微機械佔據 。
and these micromachines really are at the heart of life .	而這些微機械確實位於生命的中心 。
these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微機械 , 能讓世界各地的奈米工程師嫉妒 , 它們是自我引導、強大、精確的裝置 , 由胺基酸鏈所組成 。
and these micromachines power how a cell moves .	這些微機械讓細胞移動 。
they power how a cell replicates . they power our hearts .	它們驅動細胞複製 , 驅動我們的心臟 。
they power our minds .	它們影響了我們的心智 。
and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 找出一個方法把這個故事變成一個動畫 , 會是哈佛大學bivisions的核心 , 一個哈佛大學為分子和細胞生物學學生所設立的網站 , 除了所有的文字資料外 , 這些學生將能視覺化 , 將細胞內的真相與美 , 能夠研究這些觀點 , 以此為目標 , 他們將能發揮他們的想像力 , 使得以發揮他們的想像力 , 使得他們能夠發現生命能夠被使用 。
so we set out by looking at how these molecules are put together .	所以我們開始研究這些分子如何被組合在一起 。
we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們想出了一個主題 , 那就是 , 巨噬細胞正在沿著微血管噴流 , 它們會接觸到微血管壁的表面 , 它們會從微血管壁中提取資訊 , 它們會得到外面某處有發炎反應的資訊 , 在外面 , 看不見和感覺 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但它們得到的資訊會讓它們停止 , 讓它們內化 , 得要做出各式各樣的部分 , 才能讓它們改變形狀 , 試著從微血管中跳脫出來 , 找出發生了什麼事 。
so these molecular motors we had to work with the harvard scientists and databank models of the atomically accurate molecules and figure out how they moved , and figure out what they did .	所以這些分子馬達我們必須和哈佛的科學家合作 , 研究原子上精確的分子模型 , 並弄清楚它們是如何移動的 , 並弄清楚它們是怎麼做到的 。
and figure out how to do this in a way that was truthful in that it imparted what was going on , but not so truthful that the compact crowding in a cell would prevent the vista from happening .	並且弄清楚如何做到這一點 , 以確切的方式呈現發生了什麼事 , 但不說實話 , 一個細胞內極端擁擠的情況 , 就能避免視覺的發生 。
and so what i'm going to show you is a threeminute reader's digest version of the first aspect of this film that we produced . it's an ongoing project that's going to go another four or five years .	接下來我要讓各位看一段我們製作的影片第一部份的讀者消化版本 。 這是一個持續進行的專案計畫 , 會延續四到五年 。
and i want you to look at this and see the paths that the cell manufactures these little walking machines , they're called kinesins that take these huge loads that would challenge an ant in relative size .	請大家看這段影片 , 看到細胞製造的路 , 這些會走動的小機械 , 它們是驅動蛋白 , 負責大量使用 , 大量的貨物相對大小的工蟻 。
run the movie , please .	請播放這部電影 。
but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些驅動著細胞內部的機器真的很不可思議 , 它們真的是所有生命的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器彼此間的互動 。
they pass information to each other .	它們彼此傳遞信息 。
they cause different things to happen inside the cell .	它們造成細胞內不同現象的發生 。
and the cell will actually manufacture the parts that it needs on the fly , from information that's brought from the nucleus by molecules that read the genes .	細胞會利用讀取基因的分子從細胞核中取出它所需的零件 。
no life , from the smallest life to everybody here , would be possible without these little micromachines .	沒有生命 , 從最小的生命到這裡的每一個人 , 如果沒有這些微機械 , 就有可能實現 。
in fact , it would really , in the absence of these machines , have made the attendance here , chris , really quite sparse .	事實上 , 在沒有這些機器的情況下 , 克里斯 , 這裡的出席率真的很低 。
this is the fedex delivery guy of the cell .	這是細胞中的fedex快遞人員 。
this little guy is called the kinesin , and he pulls a sack that's full of brand new manufactured proteins to wherever it's needed in the cell whether it's to a membrane , whether it's to an organelle , whether it's to build something or repair something .	這個小傢伙叫做驅動蛋白 , 他拉著滿是全新的蛋白質到細胞所需的任何地方 , 不論是到細胞膜、細胞膜、器官 , 不論是用來製造或修復東西 。
and each of us has about 100 , 000 of these things running around , right now , inside each one of your 100 trillion cells .	而我們每個人體內都有大約10萬個這種小東西正在跑來跑去 , 而我們體內的每一百兆個細胞都有 。
so no matter how lazy you feel , you're not really intrinsically doing nothing .	所以 , 不論你感覺有多懶惰 , 本質上 , 你並沒有在做任何事 。
so what i want you to do when you go home is think about this , and think about how powerful our cells are .	所以 , 當你回家之後 , 我要你想想這一點 , 並想想我們的細胞有多強大 。
and think about some of the things that we're learning about cellular mechanics .	想想我們正在學習關於細胞機械的一些事情 。
once we figure out all that's going on and believe me , we know almost a percent of what's going on once we figure out what's going on , we're really going to be able to have a lot of control over what we do with our health , with what we do with future generations , and how long we're going to live .	一旦我們搞懂了一切 , 相信我 , 我們幾乎知道發生了什麼事 , 一旦我們搞清楚發生了什麼事 , 我們將能夠掌控我們對健康的掌控 , 掌握我們對未來世代的操作 , 以及我們能活多久 。
and hopefully we'll be able to use this to discover more truth , and more beauty .	希望我們能用這技術來發現更多的真與美 。
but it's really quite amazing that these cells , these micromachines , are aware enough of what the cell needs that they do their bidding .	但這些細胞 , 這些微機械 , 真的很不可思議 , 它們足以察覺細胞需要它們做它們的命令 。
they work together . they make the cell do what it needs to do .	它們合作 。 它們使細胞能做到它需要做的事 。
and their working together helps our bodies huge entities that they will never see function properly .	它們的合作協助我們身體一個巨大的實體 , 它們永遠不會看到正常的實體 。
enjoy the rest of the show . thank you .	請好好享受接下來的表演 。 謝謝 。
becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝琪•布蘭頓打算在她的車上住一年 , 看看這個國家 , 但 , 當憂鬱症發作時 , 她的露營工作結束了 , 她的旅程變成了無家可歸 。 在這個親密的演講中 , 她描述了她成為美國工作無家可歸的經歷 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、快樂、人生、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、說故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	beckyblanton:那一年我無家可歸 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是作家和記者 , 我也是個異性好奇的人 , 所以 , 身為記者 , 在22年內 , 我學會了很多新東西 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到的其中一件事就是要變成隱形的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成了工作無家可歸者之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我辭掉了報紙編輯的工作就在我父親同年二月去世之後 , 我決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死讓我十分痛苦 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	當我在做這件事的時候 , 我想要感受並處理很多事情 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我一生都在露營 。 我決定住在旅行車裡一整年 , 要做這件事 , 就像一趟漫長的露營旅行 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以我打包了我的貓 , 我的洛威爾和我的露營裝備 , 送到1975年雪佛蘭 , 開車去日落 , 完全沒能意識到三件重要的事 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:社會等同於永恆的結構 , 甚至是一個小屋 , 身為人的價值 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我沒有意識到 , 很快地 , 其他人的負面感受 , 會影響到我們的現實 , 只要我們放手 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我沒有意識到 , 無家可歸是一種態度 , 而非生活方式 。
at first , living in the van was great .	一開始 , 住在旅行車很棒 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在營地洗澡、定期吃飯 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我還有時間休息和哀悼悲痛 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但接著 , 我父親死去的憤怒和沮喪出現了 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我得要有全職的工作來支付帳單 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	本來輕微的彈簧變成了一個極度炎熱的夏天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	到處都看不見我有一隻貓跟狗這實在是太燙了
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓從車窗來回地跑
the doggy went into doggy day care .	這隻狗接受了日光照顧
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	每當我能在辦公大樓和卡車停靠時 , 我都會用淋浴設備 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或在公眾衛生間洗身 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	夜間的車廂中很少在華氏80度以下讓人幾乎無法入睡
food rotted in the heat .	食物在熱氣中腐壞
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	冰箱裡的冰巢會在幾小時之內融化 , 當時還蠻悲慘的 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我找不到一間公寓 , 或買不起一間公寓 , 可以讓我找到一隻腐爛的貓和貓 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕放棄他們 , 所以我待在旅行車上 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當夜間的高溫讓我連走50英尺到公共洗手間時 , 我用桶和垃圾袋當廁所 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天來臨時 , 溫度在冰點以下的狀態下降 。 他們待在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面臨全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	每天晚上我都停車 , 以避免被警察察察發現且惹來爭執 。
i didn't always succeed .	我不是每次都成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我覺得我無法掌控我的人生 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道何時或如何發生 , 但我從一個有才華的作家和記者轉變成一個住在車裡的無家者 , 把我的呼吸帶走 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒變 。 我的智商沒掉 。
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的才能、正直、價值觀 , 所有關於我的一切都是一樣的 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我有些改變了 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我在沮喪時旋轉得更深、更深 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終 , 有人提醒我去一間無家可歸的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 。 我三天沒洗澡了 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我和排隊中的人一樣濃厚和沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我只是沒喝醉或喝醉過 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當一些無家者發現 , 包括一位前任大學教授 , 他們說: 「 你不是無家可歸的人 。 你為什麼在這裡 ? 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家者不認為我是無家可歸者 , 但我還是認為我是無家可歸的人 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	那位教授聽了我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有工作 , 你有希望 。
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的無家者沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	診所給我的憂鬱症 , 讓我有自殺傾向 。 我記得當時在想: 「 如果我自殺 , 沒有人會注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	不久之後 , 有一位朋友告訴我她聽說提姆•羅斯一個知名記者在全國廣播的電視節目上談到我
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我曾寫過一篇關於我父親的文章在他死前一年寫在提姆的新書上
and he was doing the talk show circuit . and he was talking about my writing .	他當時正在演說節目電路上演說我的作品
and when i realized that tim russert , former moderator of " meet the press , " was talking about my writing , while i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , i started laughing .	當我發現提姆羅斯 , 《與媒體會面》的前主持人 , 正在談論我的寫作 , 那時我還住在一輛在沃爾瑪停車場的旅行車上 , 我開始大笑 。
i started laughing because it got to the point where , was i a writer , or was i a homeless woman ?	我開始笑了 , 因為接觸到那個時候 , 我是作家 , 還是無家可歸的女人 ?
so i went in the bookstore . and i found tim's book .	於是我走進書店 。 我找到提姆的書 。
and i stood there . and i reread my essay .	我站在那裡 。 我重新讀了我的論文 。
because i was a writer .	因為我是個作家 。
i was a writer .	我是個作家 。
shortly after that i moved back to tennessee .	在那之後不久我搬回了田納西
i alternated between living in a van and couch surfing with friends .	我和朋友住在旅行車裡 , 和沙發衝浪 。
and i started writing again .	我又開始寫作了 。
by the summer of the following year i was a working journalist .	接下來的夏天 , 我成了一名記者 。
i was winning awards . i was living in my own apartment .	我正在贏得獎項 。 我住在我自己的公寓 。
i was no longer homeless .	我不再無家可歸了 。
and i was no longer invisible .	我不再隱形了 。
thousands of people work full and parttime jobs , and live in their cars .	數以千計的人全職工作 , 兼職工作 , 住在他們的車上 。
but society continues to stigmatize and criminalize living in your vehicle or on the streets .	但社會持續歧視並將生活在車上或街頭的犯罪化 。
so the homeless , the working homeless , primarily remain invisible .	所以 , 無家者、工作無家者 , 大部份仍然是隱形的 。
but if you ever meet one , engage them , encourage them , and offer them hope .	但如果你遇到他們 , 加入他們 , 鼓勵他們 , 並給他們希望 。
the human spirit can overcome anything if it has hope .	人類的精神可以克服任何事物 , 如果它有希望的話 。
and i'm not here to be the poster girl for the homeless .	我不是來這裡做無家可歸的海報 。
i'm not here to encourage you to give money to the next panhandler you meet .	我不是來這裡鼓勵你們捐錢給下一個乞討者 。
but i am here to tell you that , based on my experience , people are not where they live , where they sleep , or what their life situation is at any given time .	但我在這裡要告訴各位 , 根據我的經驗 , 人們不是住在他們住的地方 , 他們在哪裡睡覺 , 或者他們的人生狀況在任何時間點 。
three years ago i was living in a van in a walmart parking lot , and today i'm speaking at ted .	三年前我住在旅行車裡 , 在沃爾瑪停車場 , 今天我在ted演講 。
hope always , always finds a way . thank you .	希望總是能找到路 。 謝謝 。
at tedxchange , thailand's " mr . condom , " mechai viravaidya , walks us through the country's bold plan to raise its standard of living , starting in the 1970s . first step: population control . and that means a lot of frank , funny and very effective talk about condoms .	在tedxange , 泰國的 「 保險套先生 」 , mechaiviravaidya , 帶領我們走過全國大膽的計劃 , 以提升其生活水準 , 從1970年開始 。 首先是人口控制 。 這意味著有很多法蘭克、滑稽 , 和有效的討論保險套 。
culture , global issues , health , population , science	文化、全球議題、健康、人口、科學、科學 。
mechai viravaidya: how mr . condom made thailand a better place	技工:保險套讓泰國成為更好的地方 。
now , when i was a young man 40 years ago , the country was very , very poor with lots and lots and lots of people living in poverty .	四十年前 , 當我還是個年輕人時 , 這個國家非常、非常貧窮 , 許多人生活在貧窮的環境中 。
we decided to do something about it , but we didn't begin with a welfare program or a poverty reduction program .	我們決定要做點什麼 , 但我們不是從福利計畫開始 , 或從貧窮減少計畫開始 。
but we began with a familyplanning program , following a very successful maternal child health activity , sets of activities .	但我們從一個家族的育兒健康活動開始 , 接下來是非常成功的產婦健康活動 , 一系列活動 。
so basically , no one would accept family planning if their children didn't survive .	所以 , 基本上沒有人會接受如果他們的孩子無法生存的計劃 。
so the first step: get to the children , get to the mothers , and then follow up with family planning .	所以 , 第一步:先找孩子 , 找母親 , 然後再做家庭規劃 。
not just child mortality alone , you need also family planning .	不只是兒童死亡率 , 還需要節育計畫 。
now let me take you back as to why we needed to do it .	現在讓我帶各位回顧一下 , 為何我們需要這麼做 。
in my country , that was the case in 1974 .	在我的國家 , 那是1974年的案例 。
seven children per family tremendous growth at 3 . 3 percent .	每個家庭平均有七個小孩 , 成長率是極高的3.3% 。
there was just no future .	沒有未來 。
we needed to reduce the population growth rate .	我們需要降低人口成長率 。
so we said , " let's do it . "	所以我們說: 「 我們來做吧 。 」
the women said , " we agree . we'll use pills , but we need a doctor to prescribe the pills , " and we had very , very few doctors .	婦女說: 「 我們同意 , 我們會用避孕藥 , 但我們需要醫生來開藥 。 」 而且只有非常少數的醫生 。
we didn't take no as an answer ; we took no as a question .	我們沒有接納答案 ; 我們接納 「 不 」 是個問題 。
we went to the nurses and the midwives , who were also women , and did a fantastic job at explaining how to use the pill .	我們去找同樣是女性的護士和助產士 , 對於如何使用藥丸做了很棒的工作 。
that was wonderful , but it covered only 20 percent of the country .	那很棒 , 但只覆蓋了全國20%的地區 。
what do we do for the other 80 percent leave them alone and say , " well , they're not medical personnel . "	我們給其他80%的人做的是讓他們獨自對他們說: 「 他們不是醫療人員 。 」
no , we decided to do a bit more .	不 , 我們決定要多做一點 。
so we went to the ordinary people that you saw .	所以我們去見了你看到的平凡人物 。
actually , below that yellow sign i wish they hadn't wiped that , because there was " cocacola " there .	其實 , 在那個黃色標誌下 , 我希望他們還沒毀於那個標誌 , 因為那裡有可口可樂 。
we were so much bigger than cocacola in those days .	當時我們比可口可樂還要大很多 。
and no difference , the people they chose were the people we chose .	沒差別 , 他們所選的人就是我們選的人 。
they were wellknown in the community , they knew that customers were always right , and they were terrific , and they practiced their family planning themselves .	他們在社區中很有名 , 他們知道顧客永遠是對的 , 且他們很棒 , 他們自己會做節育計畫 。
so they could supply pills and condoms throughout the country , in every village of the country .	所以他們可以在全國各個村落提供避孕藥和保險套 。
so there we are . we went to the people who were seen as the cause of the problem to be the solution .	所以我們去了 。 我們去了被視為問題的根源 , 去成為解決方案 。
wherever there were people and you can see boats with the women , selling things here's the floating market selling bananas and crabs and also contraceptives wherever you find people , you'll find contraceptives in thailand .	不論人們在哪裡 , 你都能看到船上有女性 , 賣的是水上市場 , 賣香蕉和螃蟹 , 還有避孕用品 , 不論你在泰國哪裡找到人 , 你都能在泰國找到避孕用品 。
and then we decided , why not get to religion because in the philippines , the catholic church was pretty strong , and thai people were buddhist .	然後我們決定 , 何不去宗教 , 因為在菲律賓 , 天主教會相當堅強 , 泰國人是佛教徒 。
we went to them and they said , " look , could you help us ? "	我們去找他們 , 他們說: 「 你能幫我們嗎 ? 」
i'm there the one in blue , not the yellow holding a bowl of holy water for the monk to sprinkle holy water on pills and condoms for the sanctity of the family .	我就在那裡 , 藍色的 , 不是黃色的 , 拿著一碗聖水 , 讓僧侶把聖水灑在藥丸和保險套上 , 為了家人的神聖 。
and this picture was sent throughout the country .	這張照片在全國各地傳送 。
so some of the monks in the villages were doing the same thing themselves .	所以有些村莊的僧侶也做了同樣的事 。
and the women were saying , " no wonder we have no sideeffects .	婦女說: 「 難怪我們沒有副作用 。
it's been blessed . "	得到了祝福 。 」
that was their perception .	那是他們的感知 。
and then we went to teachers .	然後我們找上了老師 。
you need everybody to be involved in trying to provide whatever it is that make humanity a better place .	你需要每個人去試著提供任何能讓人類成為更好的地方的地方 。
so we went to the teachers .	所以我們去找老師 。
over a quarter of a million were taught about family planning with a new alphabet a , b for birth , c for condom , i for iud , v for vasectomy .	有超過25萬人被教導用新的字母來教導家庭規劃--a , b是生育 , c是保險套 , i是子宮切除術 。
and then we had a snakes and ladders game , where you throw dice .	然後我們有一個蛇和梯子遊戲 , 你扔骰子去看 。
if you land on anything profamily planning , you move ahead .	如果你著陸在一個很有希望的計畫上 , 你就往前走 。
like , " mother takes the pill every night .	比如: 「 媽媽每天晚上都吃藥 。
very good , mother . move ahead .	很好 , 媽媽 , 往前走 。
uncle buys a condom . very good , uncle . move ahead .	叔叔買了保險套 。 很好 , 叔叔 。 往前走 。
uncle gets drunk , doesn't use condom . come back , start again . "	叔叔喝醉了 , 不用保險套 。 回來 , 再重新開始 。 」
again , education , class entertainment .	同樣地 , 教育和娛樂 。
and the kids were doing it in school too .	孩子們在學校也這樣做 。
we had relay races with condoms , we had children's condomblowing championship .	我們和保險套有接力賽 , 我們有兒童保險套的冠軍 。
and before long , the condom was know as the girl's best friend .	過不久 , 保險套就成了女孩最好的朋友 。
in thailand , for poor people , diamonds don't make it so the condom is the girl's best friend .	在泰國 , 對窮人而言 , 鑽石不是為了保險套而是女孩的好朋友 。
we introduced our first microcredit program in 1975 , and the women who organized it said , " we only want to lend to women who practice family planning .	我們在1975年推出了第一個小額貸款計畫 , 主辦這計畫的女性說: 「 我們只想借錢給那些實施家庭計畫的女性 。
if you're pregnant , take care of your pregnancy .	如果你懷孕了 , 照顧你的懷孕
if you're not pregnant , you can take a loan out from us . "	如果你沒有懷孕 , 你可以從我們這裡借出借款 。 」
and that was run by them .	那是由他們來管理的 。
and after 35/36 years , it's still going on .	在35/36年後 , 它仍然在進行中 。
it's a part of the village development bank ; it's not a real bank , but it's a fund microcredit .	這是鄉村發展銀行的一部分 , 不是真的銀行 , 而是一筆基金 。
and we didn't need a big organization to run it it was run by the villagers themselves .	我們不需要一個大型組織來運作 , 而是靠村民自己來運作 。
and you probably hardly see a thai man there , it's always women , women , women , women .	你幾乎看不到泰國男人在那裡 , 永遠都是女人、女人、女人 。
and then we thought we'd help america , because america's been helping everyone , whether they want help or not .	接著 , 我們認為我們會協助美國 , 因為美國一直在協助每個人 , 不論他們是否想要協助 。
and this is on the fourth of july .	這是7月4日 。
we decided to provide vasectomy to all men , but in particular , american men to the front of the queue , right up to the ambassador's residence during his [unclear] .	我們決定為所有男人提供輸精管切除術 , 特別是 , 排隊前面的美國人 , 排隊時排在大使館 。
and the hotel gave us the ballroom for it very appropriate room .	飯店給了我們一間交響間 , 非常適合的場所 。
and since it was near lunch time , they said , " all right , we'll give you some lunch .	他們說: 「 好 , 我們會給你一些午餐時間 。
of course , it must be american cola .	當然 , 它一定是美國的可樂 。
you get two brands , coke and pepsi .	有兩種品牌 , 可口可樂和百事可樂 。
and then the food is either hamburger or hotdog . "	食物要不是漢堡或熱狗 。 」

it made a lot of news in america , and it angered some people also .	美國有很多新聞 , 也讓一些人很生氣 。

then aids came along and hit thailand , and we had to stop doing a lot of good things to fight aids .	接著 , 愛滋病襲擊泰國 , 我們不得不停止對抗愛滋病 ,

so i thought , " well , if you can't go to the government , go to the military . "	所以我想: 「 嗯 , 如果你不能去政府 , 去軍隊 。 」

and after i gave them statistics , they said , " yes . okay . you can use all the radio stations , television stations . "	在我做完統計後 , 他們說: 「 是的 。 你可以使用所有的電台、電視站 。 」

every ministry , even judges , had to be involved in aids education everyone and we said the public , institutions , religious institutions , schools everyone was involved .	每個部長 , 甚至法官 , 都必須接受愛滋病的教育 。 每一個人 , 我們說 , 公共機構、宗教機構、學校--每個人都參與 。

these are primary school kids third , fourth grade going to every household in the village , every household in the whole of thailand , giving aids information and a condom to every household , given by these young kids .	這些是小學三年級、四年級的孩子 , 拜訪了村子裡的每個家庭 , 全泰國的每個家庭 , 提供愛滋病的資訊和保險套 , 給這些孩子們提供 。

because poor people are business people who lack business skills and access to credit .	因為窮人是商人 , 他們缺乏商業技能 , 無法取得信用 。

so , that was done .	所以 , 完成了 。
the money goes from the company into the village via treeplanting .	該公司的資金從村莊移植到村莊 。

and before you can borrow the money , you need to be trained .	在貸款之前 , 你需要接受訓練 。
and we believe if you want to help the poor , those who are living in poverty , access to credit must be a human right .	我們相信 , 如果你想幫助窮人 , 住在貧窮中的人 , 信用能力就必須要成為一種人權 。

your smartphone may feel like a friend but a true friend would give you a smile once in a while . at ted2013 , keller rinaudo demos romo , the smartphonepowered mini robot who can motor along with you on a walk , slide you a cup of coffee across the table , and react to you with programmable expressions .	你的智慧型手機可能會像個朋友 , 但真正的朋友會給你一次笑容 。 在2013年 , 在ted2013年 , 凱勒•里納多•羅摩 , 他是智慧型手機的迷你 , 他可以和你一起散步行走 , 滑動地通過桌子喝咖啡 , 並對你做出反應 , 做出可編程表情 。
keller rinaudo: a mini robot powered by your phone	kellerrinaudo:一個迷你機器人是由你的手機所驅動 。
so just by a show of hands , how many of you all have a robot at home ?	舉個手 , 你們當中有多少人家裡有機器人 ?
not very many of you .	不太多人 。
okay . and actually of those hands , if you don't include roomba how many of you have a robot at home ?	好的 。 請舉手 , 如果你不包含掃描室-在家中有多少人有機器人 ?
that's the problem that we're trying to solve at romotive that i and the other 20 nerds at romotive are obsessed with solving .	這是我們在romotive努力解決的問題romotive我和其他20位怪胎都著迷於解決 。
so we really want to build a robot that anyone can use , whether you're eight or 80 .	所以我們真的想要打造一個 , 任何人都可以用的機器人 , 不論你是八歲或八十歲 。
and as it turns out , that's a really hard problem , because you have to build a small , portable robot that's not only really affordable , but it has to be something that people actually want to take home and have around their kids .	事實證明 , 這是個非常困難的問題 , 因為你要打造一個小型、可攜式的機器人 , 它不僅要能負擔得起 , 它也要能成為一個家家戶都想要帶著孩子到家裡去的機器人 。
this robot can't be creepy or uncanny .	這種機器人並不會讓人毛骨悚然或不討喜 。
he should be friendly and cute .	他應該要友善又可愛 。
romo's a robot that uses a device you already know and love your iphone as his brain .	romo這個機器人 , 使用一個你已經知道且喜愛你的iphone , 做為他的大腦 。
and by leveraging the power of the iphone's processor , we can create a robot that is wifi enabled and computer visioncapable for 150 bucks , which is about one percent of what these kinds of robots have cost in the past .	藉由iphone處理器的力量我們可以創造一個可以wi-fi無線網路運作的機器人同時擁有電腦視覺能力的150塊美金這大約是過去那種機器人所花費的百分之一

if i duck down , he'll follow me .	如果我蹲下 , 他會跟著我 。
