so there are all of you through romo's eyes .	透過romo的眼睛 , 你們全部都在那裡 。
and finally , because romo is an extension of me , i can express myself through his emotions .	最後 , 因為romo是我的延伸 , 我可以透過他的情緒來表達我自己 。
so i can go in and i can say let's make romo excited .	所以我可以進去 , 說咱們來讓romo興奮一下 。
but the most important thing about romo is that we wanted to create something that was literally completely intuitive .	但關於romo最重要的事是 , 我們想要創造完全直覺的事物 。
you do not have to teach someone how to drive romo .	你不需要教別人如何駕駛romo 。
in fact , who would like to drive a robot ?	事實上 , 有誰想要駕駛機器人 ?
thank you , scott .	謝謝你 , 史考特
and even cooler , you actually don't have to be in the same geographic location as the robot to control him .	更酷的是 , 你其實不需要和機器人在同一個地理位置來控制它 。
so he actually streams twoway audio and video between any two smart devices .	所以他其實是在用任何兩個智慧型設備之間的雙向音訊和視訊串流 。
so you can log in through the browser , and it's kind of like skype on wheels .	你可以從瀏覽器登入 , 它有點像輪子上的skype 。
so we were talking before about telepresence , and this is a really cool example .	我們先前談到遠端臨場 , 這是一個很酷的例子 。
you can imagine an eightyearold girl , for example , who has an iphone , and her mom buys her a robot .	舉例來說 , 你可以想像一個八歲大的女孩 , 她有一支iphone , 而她媽媽買了一個機器人 。
that girl can take her iphone , put it on the robot , send an email to grandma , who lives on the other side of the country .	那個女孩可以拿著她的iphone , 放在機器人上 , 寄一封電子郵件給住在國家另一端的奶奶們 。
grandma can log into that robot and play hideandgoseek with her granddaughter for fifteen minutes every single night , when otherwise she might only be able to get to see her granddaughter once or twice a year .	奶奶可以登入那個機器人 , 和她的孫女一起玩捉迷藏 。 每晚十五分鐘 , 否則她一年可能只能見到她孫女一兩次 。
so those are a couple of the really cool things that romo can do today .	所以這些是romo今天能做的一些很酷的事 。
but i just want to finish by talking about something that we're working on in the future .	但最後我想談談我們未來要努力的方向 。
this is actually something that one of our engineers , dom , built in a weekend .	這實際上是我們的一個工程師 , dom , 在一個週末完成的 。
it's built on top of a google open framework called blockly .	它是建立在google一個叫做blockly的開放框架上的 。
this allows you to drag and drop these blocks of semantic code and create any behavior for this robot you want .	這可以讓你拖拉這些區塊的語義編碼 , 為這個機器人創造任何你想要的行為 。
you do not have to know how to code to create a behavior for romo .	你不需要知道如何寫程式 , 才能創造出romo的行為 。
and you can actually simulate that behavior in the browser , which is what you see romo doing on the left .	實際上 , 你可以在瀏覽器中看到romo在左邊的行為 。
and then if you have something you like , you can download it onto your robot and execute it in real life , run the program in real life .	如果你有你喜歡的東西 , 你可以下載它到你的機器人 , 並在現實生活中執行它 , 即時執行這個程式 。
and then if you have something you're proud of , you can share it with every other person who owns a robot in the world .	如果你能得到你自豪的事物 , 你就能和世界上所有擁有機器人的人分享它 。
so all of these wifi–enabled robots actually learn from each other .	所有這些wi-fi無線網路的機器人 , 都能互相學習 。
the reason we're so focused on building robots that everyone can train is that we think the most compelling use cases in personal robotics are personal .	我們之所以著重在建造一個每個人都可以訓練的機器人 , 是因為我們認為在個人機器人中 , 最能引人注目的使用方式 , 是個人的 。
they change from person to person .	它們會從人變成人 。
so we think that if you're going to have a robot in your home , that robot ought to be a manifestation of your own imagination .	所以 , 我們認為 , 如果你要在家裡裝一個機器人 , 那機器人應該是你想像力的表現 。
so i wish that i could tell you what the future of personal robotics looks like .	我希望我能告訴你個人機器人的未來是什麼樣子 。
to be honest , i have no idea .	老實說 , 我不知道 。
but what we do know is that it isn't 10 years or 10 billion dollars or a large humanoid robot away .	但我們知道的是 , 這不是十年或一百億美金 , 或一個大型的類人形機器人 。
the future of personal robotics is happening today , and it's going to depend on small , agile robots like romo and the creativity of people like yourselves .	個人機器人的未來正在發生 , 它取決於小型、敏捷的機器人 , 如romo , 以及像你們一樣的人的創造力 。
so we can't wait to get you all robots , and we can't wait to see what you build .	我們等不及把機器人送到你們全部 , 我們等不及要看看你們建造了什麼 。
author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	作家和活動家伊莎貝•阿言德討論了女性、創意、女權主義的定義 , 當然 , 還有這場演說的熱情 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、為人父母、講故事、女人、世界文化...
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾•阿言德講述充滿熱情的故事 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝謝你 。 來到這裡真的是最聰明的一員 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我來這裡是要告訴各位一些關於熱情的故事 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	我很愛這句猶太諺語 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	比事實更真誠的是什麼 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是說故事的人 。 我想傳達一些比事實更真實的東西 , 和我們共同的人性相比 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	我對所有故事都感興趣 , 有些甚至令我不安 , 直到我最後寫完它們 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	有些主題不斷出現正義、忠誠、暴力、死亡、政治和社會議題、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我知道我們身邊的謎題 , 所以我寫下巧合、預兆、情緒、夢想、大自然的力量、魔法 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去的20年裡 , 我出版了幾本書 , 但我一直活在匿名中 , 直到2006年2月 , 當我帶著在義大利冬季奧運的奧運旗幟時 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我成為了名人 。 現在大家在macy's中發現我 , 我的孫子認為我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴你我四分鐘的名氣 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	一名籌辦奧運開幕式的籌辦人打電話通知我被選為旗手之一
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我回答 , 這是個錯誤認同的案例因為我是從運動員的最遠處取得的
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不知道在不用助行器的情況下 , 我可以走動體育場 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我被告知這不是開玩笑的事 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運國旗 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五位女性代表五大洲 , 三位奧運金牌得主 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	很自然地 , 我的第一個問題是:我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說穿制服 , 要求我的測量指標 。
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有個景象 , 彷彿自己處在富裕的主流之中 , 看起來像米其林的老人 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	到了二月中期 , 我到了杜林 , 熱情的群眾歡呼時 , 八十個奧運隊都在街上 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些運動員為了競爭而犧牲了一切 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都值得勝利 , 但還是要靠點運氣 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	雪上的小缺口 , 冰層的一英吋 , 風的力量 , 可以決定比賽的結果 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 訓練或運氣之外 , 最重要的是心 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有無懼且堅定的心才能得到金牌 。
it is all about passion .	這一切都與熱情有關 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	杜林街上滿是紅色海報 , 宣佈奧運的標語 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情就在這裡 , 不是一直都是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心 , 驅使我們並決定我們的命運 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我在書中角色所需要的:熱情的心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要突破、異議、冒險精神、外來者、叛軍 , 他們提出問題、修改規則 , 和冒險 。
people like all of you in this room .	就像在座各位
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	有常識的好人不會畫有趣的角色 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只會交配好的前夫 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在體育場的綠色房間裡 , 我見到其他旗手三位運動員 , 女演員蘇珊莎蘭登和蘇菲雅羅蘭 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	還有兩位心中充滿熱情的女人:來自肯亞的諾貝爾獎得主 , 她種了三千萬棵樹 。 透過這麼做 , 她改變了土壤、氣候 , 在非洲的某些地方 , 當然也改變了許多村落的經濟狀況 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	柬埔寨行動主義者索瑪利•瑪曼 , 極力反抗兒童賣淫 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她十四歲時 , 她的祖父將她賣到妓院 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們 , 小女孩被男人強暴 , 她們相信和非常年輕的處女做愛 , 會治癒愛滋病 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	還有那些逼孩子們每天被迫接收五、十五個客戶的妓院 , 如果他們反抗 , 他們會被電擊折磨 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我拿到制服 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我平常穿的服裝 , 但那不是米其林穿的服裝 , 其實也不是我預期的 , 不是很差 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像個冰箱 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但也有大部分的旗幟 , 除了蘇菲雅羅蘭 , 普遍的美麗與熱情的象徵 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	蘇菲雅七十多歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她很性感、很瘦、很高 , 帶著很深的棕色 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	那麼 , 你要如何有一根深色的皮膚 , 沒有皺紋 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當電視記者問: 「 她怎麼能看起來這麼棒 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她回答: 「 保持姿勢 。 我總是挺直的 , 我不會製造老人的噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 這裡你有一些免費的建議來自地球上最美麗的女人之一 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不屈不撓、不咳嗽、不呼吸、不跟自己說話、不放屁 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她並沒有說真的 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在午夜時分 , 我們被叫到體育場的機翼 , 擴音器負責宣佈奧運的旗幟 , 首先音樂是從這裡開始的 , 艾達遊行 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	蘇菲雅羅蘭就在我面前 , 她比我高一呎 , 數不清頭髮 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她優雅地走著 , 就像非洲草原上的長頸鹿將旗子舉在肩上 。 我在後面慢跑跑 , 手伸上旗子 , 頭其實在那該死的旗子下 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	所有的攝影機 , 當然都是蘇菲雅 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	這對我來說是幸運的 , 因為在大部分媒體照片中我看起來也一樣 , 儘管常常在蘇菲雅的雙腿之間 。
a place where most men would love to be .	一個大部分男人都想待的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我一生中最棒的四分鐘是奧林匹克體育館員 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我老公很冒犯我這麼說 , 雖然我跟他解釋說 , 我們私下需要花不到四分鐘 , 所以他不該把我當做自己 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有這四分鐘的所有剪報 , 因為我不想在老年時將它們忘記 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想要永遠記住奧運的關鍵字 。
so here's a tale of passion .	以下是一個充滿熱情的故事 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	時間是1998年 , 剛果的圖西族難民營是座監獄 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順道一提 , 世界上80%的難民和流離失所者都是女人和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以把這個地方命名為剛果的死亡營 , 因為沒有被殺的人 , 會死於疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	故事的主角是一位年輕女性蘿絲•瑪班多和她的孩子
she's pregnant and a widow .	她是懷孕的寡婦 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵迫使她眼睜睜看著她的丈夫被虐待和殺害 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	不知何故 , 她讓她七個孩子活了下來 , 幾個月後 , 她生出早產的雙胞胎 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她用棍子剪斷臍帶然後用頭髮綁起來
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她用營地指揮官的名字命名雙胞胎 , 以取得他們的喜好 , 並用黑色茶餵他們 , 因為她的牛奶無法維持下去 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當軍人闖進她的牢房 , 強暴她大女兒時 , 她不想放手 , 即使他們手上拿著槍 ,
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	不知怎麼的 , 這個家庭存活了十六個月然後 , 靠著不凡的運氣和熱情的美國人沙夏•查諾夫他成功將她送上美國救援機 , 蘿絲•瑪班多和九個孩子最後到了亞利桑那州鳳凰城在那裡生活、茁壯成長
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	瑪班多 , 在斯瓦希里 , 意味著偉大的愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我書中的主角是堅強且充滿熱情的女性 , 像是蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不編造它們 , 不需要它們 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我環顧四周 , 到處都能看見 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我一生都在為女性、為女性工作 。
i know them well .	我對他們很熟悉 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生在很久以前 , 在很遠的時代 , 在一個父系天主教和保守家庭中 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	難怪我五歲就已經是個憤怒的女權主義者 , 雖然還沒達到智利 , 所以沒人知道我到底是怎麼回事 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就發現 , 為了讓我的自由付出很高的代價 , 以及質疑父權制度 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但是我很高興能付出代價 , 因為每當我被擊中的一擊 , 我就能夠分出兩次 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	有一次 , 當我的女兒寶拉二十多歲時 , 她告訴我女權運動過時了 , 我應該繼續走下去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們打了一場記住的仗 。 女權主義是約會嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對於我女兒和在座各位一樣有特權的女性 , 但對其他國家的姊妹來說 , 她們仍然被迫提早婚姻、妓女、強迫勞工 , 她們的孩子不想要或無法餵飽她們 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們無法掌控自己的身體或生活 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育 , 沒有自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴、毆打 , 有時因受罰被殺 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對於現今大部分西方女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者是一種侮辱 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女權主義從來就不性感 , 但讓我跟各位保證 , 它從來沒有阻止我調情 , 我很少有缺乏男人的苦惱 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女權已經死去 , 絕非死 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已進化 。 如果你不喜歡這個名詞 , 改變它 , 為了女神的天啊 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為 「 愛芙洛蒂 」 、 「 維納斯 」 、 「 花香 」 , 隨便你叫什麼名字 「 不重要 」 , 只要我們了解它是什麼 , 我們就支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個關於熱情的故事 , 一個悲傷的故事 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	在孟加拉的一個村莊裡 , 一間婦女診所
the year is 2005 .	時間是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國牙醫 , 在她三週假期間 , 她去診所當義工 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好要乾淨的牙齒 , 但當她到那裡時 , 她發現沒有醫生、沒有牙醫 , 診所就只是一間蒼蠅屋子 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	在外面 , 有一排女子等了幾個小時才被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人痛苦難當 , 因為她有數個腐敗的明星 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮明白唯一的解決方案就是拔掉牙齒不好 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她沒有執照 , 也從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她很常冒險 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至沒有合適的樂器 , 但幸運的是 , 她帶來了一些非vocaine 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有顆勇敢且熱情的心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她在一旁祈禱 , 然後開始行動 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 病患鬆了口氣 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , 衛生學家抽出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她再次來到所謂的診所時 , 她的第一位病人和她的丈夫在等她 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	這位女士的臉看起來像西瓜 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	腫到看不見眼睛
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫氣極了 , 威脅要殺了美國人 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮被自己造成的後果嚇壞了 , 但翻譯解釋說病人的狀況和手術沒有關係 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	前一天 , 她丈夫因為在家準備晚餐不足而毆打她 。
millions of women live like this today .	今天有數百萬的女性過著這樣的生活 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是最貧窮的人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然女性分擔世界上三分之二的勞動力 , 但她們擁有的卻不到世界資產的百分之一 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們的薪水比男性低 , 如果他們有薪水 , 他們仍然是脆弱的 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立 , 而且他們經常受到剝削、暴力和虐待的威脅 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	事實上 , 給予婦女教育、工作、控制自己收入的能力、繼承和財產的能力 , 讓社會受益 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果女人有力量 , 她的孩子和她的家人會變得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家屬能繁榮 , 村落能繁榮 , 最終整個國家也是如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	旺加里•馬塔伊到肯亞的一個村落 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人談 , 解釋說土地很貧瘠 , 因為他們砍樹並賣掉了 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她讓婦女們種植新樹並澆水 , 一滴接著一滴 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五六年或六年內 , 森林充斥著土壤 , 村落被拯救了 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮和最落後的社會往往就是那些壓抑女性的社會 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這個顯而易見的事實卻被政府以及慈善機構忽略 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	女性的專案每得到1美元 , 男性的專案就有20美元 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性佔人類人口的51% 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	給予他們能力 , 不僅是科技、設計和娛樂 , 更能改變一切 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以保證 , 女性可以一起合作連結、有知識、受教育 , 能為這個可憐的星球帶來和平與繁榮 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在今天的任何一場戰爭中 , 許多傷亡者是平民 , 主要是婦女和兒童 。 他們是附屬傷害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人掌控世界 , 看看我們有什麼麻煩 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼樣的世界 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是大部分人所問的根本問題 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	參與現有的世界秩序是合理的嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們要一個保存生命的世界一個生活品質才會讓所有人豐富而不僅僅是特權
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	一月份時 , 我看到費南多•巴特羅在加州大學伯克萊圖書館的畫作展出 。
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	在美國 , 沒有博物館或畫廊只有紐約畫廊有波特羅的作品 , 才敢展示這幅畫因為主題是阿布格萊布監獄
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	它們是巨大的畫作 , 充滿了酷刑和權力濫用 , 以大量的巴特羅風格呈現 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我無法將那些影像從我的腦海或心中得到出來 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最擔心的是無罪的權力 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕濫用權力 , 以及濫用權力 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們這個族群中 , 雄性領袖定義現實 , 強迫其他成員接受現實並遵守規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則隨時在改變 , 但總是受惠 , 這種情況下 , 下滲經濟失敗的效果 , 在經濟學上是行不通的 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從上到下 , 一層層的欺壓濫用 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和小孩 , 尤其是窮人 , 都在最底層 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使是最陰鬱的男人也有人可以虐待女人或孩子 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我受夠了少數人操縱多數人的權力 , 透過性別、收入、種族和階級 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我想該是時候成熟了 , 徹底地改變我們的文明 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但若要真正改變 , 我們需要讓女性的能量在世界的管理中成為可能 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要讓女性掌握權力我們需要培養男性心中的女性能量
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	當然 , 我指的是有年輕心智的男人 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老傢伙是絕望的 ; 我們得等他們死光 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我想要有蘇菲雅羅蘭的長腿和著名的胸部 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但 , 若能選擇 , 我寧願有勇敢的心 , 像旺加里•瑪太、索瑪利•曼、珍妮 , 和蘿絲•瑪班多 。
i want to make this world good .	我希望這個世界變得更好 。
not better , but to make it good .	不是更好 , 而是讓它變好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 這是有可能的 。 看看在座的四周 , 所有的知識、精力、才華和技術 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	讓我們擺脫冷氣 , 捲起袖子 , 激情地工作 , 創造一個近乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦這麼大的城市中 , 有三千萬份餐是供應的 。 但 , 所有食物是從哪裡來的 ? 建築師卡洛琳鋼鐵討論每日供應一座城市的奇蹟 , 顯示出古老的食物路線如何塑造了現代世界 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡洛琳鋼:食物如何形塑我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	要如何供應食物給一座城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們這個時代的一個大問題 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但很少被提出來 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們視為理所當然 , 如果我們去商店或餐廳 , 或在一個小時內進入劇院大廳 , 那裡將會有食物等待著我們 , 神奇的是從某個地方來的 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你想到 , 倫敦這麼大的城市每天要有足夠的食物被製造、運輸、購買、賣菜、吃、處置同樣的事 , 每天都發生在每個城市 , 都市被餵食是很了不起的 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們住在這樣的地方 , 如同他們是世界上最自然的地方 , 忘記我們是動物 , 我們也需要進食 , 事實上 , 我們也要仰賴自然世界 , 就像我們古老的祖先一樣 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著更多人搬到城市裡 , 更多的大自然被轉變為非凡的景觀 , 就像我身後的景觀──在巴西馬托格羅索的大豆田 , 以供應食物給我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是非凡的景觀 , 但很少人看到它們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	越來越多這些景觀也不僅僅是用來餵飽我們 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們越往城市居住越多人吃肉 , 全球就有三分之一的穀物被餵給動物 , 而不是餵給我們人類 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	由於它需要三倍的穀物實際上是十倍的穀物如果用動物首先通過的話 , 餵飽人類的糧食不是個非常有效的方法
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是個日漸增加的問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到2050年 , 估計將是我們居住的城市人數的兩倍 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	據估計 , 肉類和乳製品會消耗兩倍之多 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 肉類和城市化的力量正逐漸增加 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將是個巨大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	到2050年 , 六十億個肉食性動物 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 。 如果我們不做改變 , 那我們就不太可能解決這個問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	每年有一千九百萬公頃的熱帶雨林消失被開發成新的耕地 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時我們也失去同樣數量的可耕地 , 可耕種鹽化和侵蝕 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們也很渴望化石燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	西方每消費一卡路里的食物要耗去十卡路里的能量 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	雖然我們所生產的成本很高 , 我們卻不重視它 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	半數在美國生產的食物都被丟掉了 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	在這一切的最後 , 在這個漫長的過程中 , 我們甚至無法妥善地供應食物給地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	十億人過胖 , 卻有十億人挨餓 。
none of it makes very much sense .	這一切都不合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	試想全球百分之八十的食物交易只掌握在五家跨國企業的手上 , 這真是個可怕的局面 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們進入城市時 , 世界也接受了西方的飲食習慣 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看向未來 , 它是一種不可持續的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	我們是怎麼走到這一步的 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們該怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	首先 , 回答一個稍微容易一點的問題 , 大約一萬年前 , 我會說 , 是這個過程的開端 , 在古老的東邊 , 稱為新月沃土 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 它是月亮的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	而且還很肥沃 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	大約在一萬年前 , 在這裡有兩項非凡的發明農業和城市的產生大約在同一個地方同時發生
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市是結合在一起的 。 他們彼此需要 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為它是第一次由我們的古老祖先發現穀物 , 產生足夠大、穩定的食物來源 , 足以支撐永久聚落 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些聚落是什麼樣子的 , 我們可以看到它們是緊密的 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	它們被生產的農地包圍 , 主要是像這個在烏爾這樣的神殿 , 事實上 , 精神分配中心是中央食物分配中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因爲是神殿安排收割收集穀物獻給諸神再把諸神沒吃的穀物歸還給人們
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 這些城市的精神和實體生活是由他們賴以維生的穀物和收穫所主導 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 每座古老的城市都是如此 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是全部這麼小 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	眾所皆知 , 在西元一世紀時 , 羅馬就有大約一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	那麼 , 像這樣的城市是如何滿足自己的呢 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古老食物里程 」 。
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬得以接近海 , 這讓海水可以從很遠很遠的地方運來進食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是唯一能做這件事的方式 , 在古代 , 因為要把食物運送到馬路上是很困難的 , 這很艱難 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物很快就消失了 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以羅馬有效地在某些地方發動戰爭 , 像是大屠殺和埃及 , 僅僅為了取得他們的穀物儲備量 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說這個帝國的擴張其實是一場漫長的軍事化購物中心 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我很喜歡這個事實 , 我只需要提到:羅馬還曾經從倫敦進口牡蠣我覺得這很不可思議 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬就在它的胃口塑造它的內陸 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是另一件事也發生在工業化前的世界 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看一下十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 穀物是來自泰姆斯 , 在這張圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以穀物市場就在城市的南方 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	道路從它們走到便宜的道路 , 也就是主要的市場 , 也是穀物市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看那些街道的名字 , 麵包街 , 你可以看出三百年前的狀況 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	魚也是如此
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚也是從河裡來的 。 同樣的事情 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 比林斯門是倫敦的魚市場一直到1980年代中期才開始運作
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	仔細想想 , 這真的很不可思議 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他每個人都在附近徘徊 , 帶著看起來像磚塊的行動電話 , 有點像在港口的臭魚 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	城市裡食物的另一件事是:一旦它的根部被建立起來 , 它們就幾乎不會動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	肉類是另外一個故事 , 因為 , 當然 , 動物可以走進這個城市 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦大部分的肉品是從西北方向來的 , 從蘇格蘭和威爾斯 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以它來到倫敦西北方 , 這就是為什麼史密斯菲爾德 , 倫敦著名的肉市場 , 位在那裏 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	家禽類從東安格利亞進來 , 一直到東北方 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像氣象女人在做這件事 。 總之 , 鳥類也以小小的帆布保護著進來 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	當他們到達便宜的東邊時 , 他們就在那裡被賣掉了 , 這就是為什麼被稱為 「 家禽 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	實際上 , 如果你看看任何城市的地圖在工業時代之前建成你可以追蹤食物的進程
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它實際上是如何被食物所塑造 , 無論是閱讀街道的名字 , 讓你有很多線索 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街 , 在以前是你星期五去買魚的地方 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但你也要想像它滿是食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間是唯一購買食物的地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年史密斯菲爾德的照片 , 你可以看到很難住在這樣一個城市 , 且不知你的食物從哪裡來 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐 , 你有可能會在三天前在你的窗外面帶著氣或出血 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	所以這顯然是一個有機城市 , 是有機循環的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年大西部的照片 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 最早的鐵路旅客當中有一些是豬和羊 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被殺害 , 被視覺和思想所取代 , 在鄉間的某處 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們用鐵路來到城市裡 。
and this changes everything .	這改變了一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它使得它第一次能夠在任何地方成長城市 , 真正的大小和形狀都有可能實現 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	過去城市受限於地理條件 ; 過去城市得要透過艱難的物理手段來取得食物 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 它們就從地理釋放了 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	從倫敦的地圖上可以看出在火車經過的九十年後倫敦的地圖從一個很容易餵飽的小點由動物走進來的小點到一個很大的小點 , 很難跟任何人步行 , 不管是動物還是人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然這只是開端 。 在火車來襲之後 , 汽車真的是這過程的終點 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是城市中最終的解放 , 從大自然的任何明顯的關係中解放 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這類城市完全沒有氣味 , 更沒有混亂 , 當然也沒有人 , 因為沒有人會夢到能走在那樣的景色中 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們的做法是開車到郊區的某處一個箱子 , 帶回一週的購物 , 然後想著要怎麼處理這些問題 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	此時此刻 , 我們與食物及城市的關係已完全改變 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	這裡有食物 , 以前是市中心 , 城市的社交中心 , 位在邊緣 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	它曾經是一個社交活動 , 買賣食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前會做菜 , 現在只要加水 , 或加一點點雞蛋 , 如果你要做蛋糕的話 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不會聞到食物 , 看看它有沒有吃的 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們只是閱讀包裝背後的標籤 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們不珍視食物 , 我們不信任它
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以 , 我們不再信任它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	我們不再珍視它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代飲食習慣其中一個最諷刺的就是他們讓自己答應的目標變得更容易 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由使城市在任何地方、任何地方都有可能發展出來 , 它們確實把我們與最重要的關係保持距離 , 那就是我們和大自然 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	這也使得我們必須依賴他們所能傳遞的系統 , 如同我們所見 , 他們無法永續經營 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	所以 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是個新問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	五百年前托馬斯.摩爾就在問他自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的著作《烏托邦》的前面 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列的半自給自足的城邦 , 如果聽起來很熟悉 , 一天走在一起 , 每個人都基本上是種植農作物 , 在自家的後院種蔬菜 , 一起享用餐點等等 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為 , 你可以說食物是烏托邦的根本原則即便摩爾最初不是這樣設想
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這裡還有另外一個著名的烏托邦的視覺 , ebenezerhoward的 " 花園城市 " 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的想法:一系列的半自給自足的城邦、小型的都會區 , 周圍有耕地 , 由鐵路連接在一起 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以是他視覺的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	甚至完成了 , 但與默斯克韋茲的願景無關 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這些烏托邦理念的問題 , 就是他們是烏托邦人 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是湯瑪斯•摩爾刻意用的詞 。
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	開個玩笑 , 因為希臘語裡它有雙重主導權 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	可以是指好地方 , 或沒有地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為它是理想的 。 它是想像出來的 。 我們無法擁有它 。
and i think , as a conceptual tool for thinking about the very deep problem of human dwelling , that makes it not much use .	我認為 , 用概念來思考人類居住的深層問題 , 這樣就沒什麼用了 。
so i've come up with an alternative , which is sitopia , from the ancient greek , " sitos " for food , and " topos " for place .	所以我想出了一個替代方案 , 就是希托邦 , 來自古希臘文 , 「 希托 」 指的是食物 , 「 屁股 」 , 指定的地方 。
i believe we already live in sitopia .	我相信我們已經住在希托邦 。
we live in a world shaped by food , and if we realize that , we can use food as a really powerful tool a conceptual tool , design tool , to shape the world differently .	我們生活在由食物塑造的世界 , 如果我們意識到 , 我們就可以用食物當作非常強大的工具 , 一個概念性工具 , 設計工具 , 用不同的方式塑造世界 。
so if we were to do that , what might sitopia look like ?	如果我們這樣做 , 希托邦會長什麼樣子 ?
well i think it looks a bit like this .	嗯 , 我覺得看起來有點像這樣 。
i have to use this slide . it's just the look on the face of the dog .	我必須用這張投影片 。 這只是狗的臉上的情形 。
but anyway , this is it's food at the center of life , at the center of family life , being celebrated , being enjoyed , people taking time for it .	總之 , 這是生活的中心 , 在家庭生活的中心 , 被讚頌 , 被享受 , 人們花時間在上面 。
this is where food should be in our society .	這就是食物在我們社會中應有的位置 。
but you can't have scenes like this unless you have people like this .	但你不能有這樣的場景 , 除非你有這種人 。
by the way , these can be men as well .	順便一提 , 這也可以是男人 。
it's people who think about food , who think ahead , who plan , who can stare at a pile of raw vegetables and actually recognize them .	人們會想到食物 , 他們會預先思考 , 計畫 , 他們會盯著一堆生菜 , 實際認可它們 。
we need these people . we're part of a network .	我們需要這些人 , 我們是網絡的一部分 。
because without these kinds of people we can't have places like this .	因為如果沒有這些人 , 我們就沒有這些地方 。
here , i deliberately chose this because it is a man buying a vegetable .	我故意選這張是因為這是男人在買蔬菜
but networks , markets where food is being grown locally .	但網路、市場 , 讓食物在當地生長 。
it's common . it's fresh .	很普遍 , 新鮮 。
it's part of the social life of the city .	它是社交生活的一部分 。
because without that , you can't have this kind of place , food that is grown locally and also is part of the landscape , and is not just a zerosum commodity off in some unseen hellhole .	因為沒有了這些 , 你就不可能有這種地方 , 當地種植的食物 , 也是風景的一部分 , 而且不只是某種看不見的地獄商品 。
cows with a view .	牛則有自己的視野 。
steaming piles of humus .	蒸汽堆積如山
this is basically bringing the whole thing together .	這基本上是把所有東西結合在一起 。
and this is a community project i visited recently in toronto .	這是我最近在多倫多探訪的一個社區計畫 。
it's a greenhouse , where kids get told all about food and growing their own food .	這是一間溫室 , 孩子們會全部講述食物和種植自己的食物 。
here is a plant called kevin , or maybe it's a plant belonging to a kid called kevin . i don't know .	這裡有一株叫做凱文的植物 , 或是它屬於凱文的孩子 , 我不知道 。
but anyway , these kinds of projects that are trying to reconnect us with nature is extremely important .	總之 , 這類計畫正試圖將我們與大自然重新連結 , 是非常重要的 。
so sitopia , for me , is really a way of seeing .	所以 , 希托邦 , 對我來說 , 其實是一種看待的方式 。
it's basically recognizing that sitopia already exists in little pockets everywhere .	基本上 , 意識到希托邦已經存在於每個地方的小口袋裡 。
the trick is to join them up , to use food as a way of seeing .	訣竅是要把它們連接起來 , 用食物當作是一種看見的方式 。
and if we do that , we're going to stop seeing cities as big , metropolitan , unproductive blobs , like this .	如果我們這樣做 , 我們就不會再把城市視為大型、都市化、無生產力的區塊了 。
we're going to see them more like this , as part of the productive , organic framework of which they are inevitably a part , symbiotically connected .	我們會把它們看成是有生產力有機架構的一部分 , 它們無可避免地被連結著 。
but of course , that's not a great image either , because we need not to be producing food like this anymore .	當然 , 這也不是一張很棒的圖片 , 因為我們需要不再生產像這樣的食物 。
we need to be thinking more about permaculture , which is why i think this image just sums up for me the kind of thinking we need to be doing .	我們需要多想想永續農業 , 這就是為什麼我認為這張圖可以總結出我們該做的事 。
it's a reconceptualization of the way food shapes our lives .	這概念化了食物如何形塑我們的生活 。
the best image i know of this is from 650 years ago .	我所知道的最好的圖片是650年前的 。
it's ambrogio lorenzetti's " allegory of good government . "	安布洛吉歐•羅倫澤蒂的 " 良好政府的寓言 "
it's about the relationship between the city and the countryside .	而是城市與鄉間的關係 。
and i think the message of this is very clear .	我認為這件事的訊息非常清楚 。
if the city looks after the country , the country will look after the city .	如果城市照顧這個國家 , 這個國家會照顧這個城市 。
and i want us to ask now , what would ambrogio lorenzetti paint if he painted this image today ?	我現在想問大家安布洛吉歐.羅倫澤蒂會怎麼畫 ? 如果他今天畫了這張圖 ?
what would an allegory of good government look like today ?	今天 , 好的政府的寓言會是什麼樣子的 ?
because i think it's an urgent question .	因為我認為這是一個迫切的問題 。
it's one we have to ask , and we have to start answering .	這是我們必須問的問題 , 我們必須開始回答 。
we know we are what we eat .	我們知道我們吃什麼 。
we need to realize that the world is also what we eat .	我們需要了解 , 世界是我們吃的東西 。
but if we take that idea , we can use food as a really powerful tool to shape the world better .	但如果我們能採取這個想法 , 我們可以使用食物作為一個強大的工具 , 來改善這個世界 。
weeks from the charter for compassion launch , karen armstrong looks at religion's role in the 21st century: will its dogmas divide us ? or will it unite us for common good ? she reviews the catalysts that can drive the world's faiths to rediscover the golden rule .	同情憲章的幾個星期後 , 凱倫•阿姆斯壯觀察了21世紀的宗教角色:教條會將我們分割嗎 ? 還是會讓我們團結一致 ? 她檢視能促使世界的信仰重新發現黃金法則的催化劑 。
god , ted prize , global issues , politics , religion , tedglobal2009 , violence	上帝、ted大獎、全球議題、政治、宗教、tedglobal2009年的暴力事件 。
karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karenarmstrong:讓我們重新審視黃金法則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	多年來我一直感到挫折 , 因為身為宗教歷史學家 , 我敏銳地意識到同情心在世界上的主要宗教信仰中扮演的核心角色 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	他們每一個人都發展出他們自己所謂的 「 黃金法則 」 的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時會出現一個正面的版本 「 向其他人對待自己 」 。
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面的版本 「 不要對其他人做你不想對你做的事 。 」
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你自己的內心 , 發現是什麼讓你感到痛苦 , 接著拒絕 , 在任何情況下 , 去讓別人感到痛苦 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們也強調同情的重要性 , 不是因為它聽起來很棒 , 而是因為它很有效 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們實施了黃金法則 , 就像孔子說: 「 一整天、每一天 」 , 不只是做好事 , 接著又回到貪婪、自我主義的人生 , 但若要做一整天 , 你就要脫離你世界的中心 , 另外一個你會超越自己 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	它會引領你到一個名為 「 神 」 、 「 涅盤 」 、 「 道 」 的境界 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	超越我們對存在的認知 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你從來不知道很多時候 , 這對於宗教生活是如此重要 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為和一些很棒的例外 , 當宗教人士結合在一起時 , 宗教領袖會聚在一起 , 他們爭論的是深奧的教義 , 或是說出一連串的仇恨指南 , 或是一連串的仇恨 , 來對抗同性戀或類似的事 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	人們往往不想變得慈悲
i sometimes see when i'm speaking to a congregation of religious people a sort of mutinous expression crossing their faces because people often want to be right instead .	有時我會看到 , 當我和一群宗教人士談話時 , 有點不太可能表達出他們臉上的表情 , 因為人們通常會希望他們是對的 。
and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	這當然會打敗運動的對象 。
now why was i so grateful to ted ?	為什麼我對ted這麼感激 ?
because they took me very gently from my booklined study and brought me into the 21st century , enabling me to speak to a much , much wider audience than i could have ever conceived .	因為他們溫和地把我從我的書架研究帶到21世紀 , 讓我能對更廣泛的觀眾說話 , 遠比我想像的還要廣 。
because i feel an urgency about this .	因為我覺得這件事很急迫 。
if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不想辦法在全球實施黃金法則 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 不論在哪裡 , 我懷疑我們會有一個可實現的世界 , 把下一代傳遞給下一代 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	我們這個時代的任務 , 我們這個時代最大的任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球性社會 , 如我所說 , 讓人們可以和平共處 。
and the religions that should be making a major contribution are instead seen as part of the problem .	而應該對宗教做出重大貢獻的宗教反而被視為問題的一部分 。
and of course it's not just religious people who believe in the golden rule .	當然 , 不只是宗教人士 , 他們相信黃金法則 。
this is the source of all morality , this imaginative act of empathy , putting yourself in the place of another .	這是所有道德的來源 , 這種富有想像力的同理心行為 , 讓自己置身於他人之處 。
and so we have a choice , it seems to me .	所以我們有一個選擇 , 這對我來說 。
we can either go on bringing out or emphasizing the dogmatic and intolerant aspects of our faith , or we can go back to the rabbis . rabbi hillel , the older contemporary of jesus , who , when asked by a pagan to sum up the whole of jewish teaching while he stood on one leg , said , " that which is hateful to you , do not do to your neighbor .	我們可以繼續宣揚或強調宗教的教條或是不寬容的面向 , 或者我們可以回到拉比希勒 , 和耶穌的大老同一代 , 當他站在一條腿上的時候 , 去總結猶太教義 , 他說: 「 你不願意做的事 , 不要對你的鄰居做任何事 。
that is the torah and everything else is only commentary . "	「 這就是教義 , 其他都只是評論 。 」
and the rabbis and the early fathers of the church who said that any interpretation of scripture that bred hatred and disdain was illegitimate .	猶太教中早期的父親們 , 他們說任何對聖經的詮釋 , 任何對聖經的詮釋都是違法的 。
and we need to revive that spirit .	我們需要復興那份精神 。
and it's not just going to happen because a spirit of love wafts us down .	這不只發生 , 因為愛的精神會讓我們失望 。
we have to make this happen , and we can do it with the modern communications that ted has introduced .	我們必須讓它實現 , 我們可以實現ted介紹的現代傳媒介 。
already i've been tremendously heartened at the response of all our partners .	我已經對所有伴侶的回應都心存激動了 。
in singapore , we have a group going to use the charter to heal divisions recently that have sprung up in singaporean society , and some members of the parliament want to implement it politically .	在新加坡 , 我們有個團體要用 「 憲章 」 來治癒新加坡社會最近出現的憲法 ; 議會的一些成員要在政治上實施它 。
in malaysia , there is going to be an art exhibition in which leading artists are going to be taking people , young people , and showing them that compassion also lies at the root of all art .	在馬來西亞 , 將來會有一場藝術展覽 , 主導藝術家會帶領人們 , 年輕人 , 向他們展示 , 同情也是所有藝術的根源 。
throughout europe , the muslim communities are holding events and discussions , are discussing the centrality of compassion in islam and in all faiths .	在歐洲各地 , 穆斯林團體舉辦事件和討論 , 討論同情心在伊斯蘭和所有信仰的核心 。
but it can't stop there . it can't stop with the launch .	但它不能就此停止 , 它不能就這樣就停止發射 。
religious teaching , this is where we've gone so wrong , concentrating solely on believing abstruse doctrines .	宗教教導 , 這也是我們如此走錯的地方 , 非常專注於相信深奧的教義 。
religious teaching must always lead to action .	宗教教誨一定要付諸行動 。
and i intend to work on this till my dying day .	我打算在這條路上直到臨終那一天為止工作 。
and i want to continue with our partners to do two things educate and stimulate compassionate thinking .	我還想繼續跟我們的夥伴繼續做兩件事 , 教育並激發同情心思維 。
education because we've so dropped out of compassion .	教育因為我們已經失去了同情心 。
people often think it simply means feeling sorry for somebody .	人們通常認為這只是對某些人感到遺憾
but of course you don't understand compassion if you're just going to think about it .	但想一想 , 你就是不了解同情心 。
you also have to do it .	你也必須這樣做 。
i want them to get the media involved because the media are crucial in helping to dissolve some of the stereotypical views we have of other people , which are dividing us from one another .	我希望媒體參與其中 , 是因為媒體是幫助人們破除我們對其他人的刻板印象的關鍵 , 使我們彼此隔離 。
the same applies to educators .	教育家也一樣 。
i'd like youth to get a sense of the dynamism , the dynamic and challenge of a compassionate lifestyle .	我希望年輕人能體會到一種充滿活力、有同情心的生活方式的動態和挑戰 。
and also see that it demands acute intelligence , not just a gooey feeling .	還有 , 它需要有急性智慧 , 不只是糟糕的感覺 。
i'd like to call upon scholars to explore the compassionate theme in their own and in other people's traditions .	我想請求學者來探索他們自己的同情心主題 , 以及他們自己的傳統中 。
and perhaps above all , to encourage a sensitivity about uncompassionate speaking , so that because people have this charter , whatever their beliefs or lack of them , they feel empowered to challenge uncompassionate speech , disdainful remarks from their religious leaders , their political leaders , from the captains of industry .	最重要的是 , 鼓勵人們對於沒有同情心的言論 , 這麼一來 , 因為人們有這個憲章 , 不論他們的信仰 , 不論他們的信仰 , 或他們缺少什麼 , 他們就會覺得有能力去挑戰不夠熱情的言論 , 不確定性的言論來自於他們的信仰領袖 , 他們的政治領袖 , 來自工業界的首領 。
because we can change the world , we have the ability .	因為我們能改變世界 , 我們有能力 。
i would never have thought of putting the charter online .	我從來不會想把憲章放上網 。
i was still stuck in the old world of a whole bunch of boffins sitting together in a room and issuing yet another arcane statement .	我還被困在一個老世界裡 , 一大堆的波芬斯坐在房間裡 , 發表了一個神秘的聲明 。
and ted introduced me to a whole new way of thinking and presenting ideas .	ted介紹我一種全新的思考和呈現想法的方式 。
because that is what is so wonderful about ted .	因為那就是ted美妙的地方 。

and of course the problems sometimes seem insuperable .	當然 , 有些時候 , 這些問題似乎很棘手 。
but i'd just like to quote , finish at the end with a reference to a british author , an oxford author whom i don't quote very often , c . s . lewis .	但我想引用一句話來結束 , 一位英國作家 , 牛津作家 , 我不太常提到他 , c.s.路易斯 。

it's in his book " the four loves . "	這是他《四項愛》的書 。
he said that he distinguished between erotic love , when two people gaze , spellbound , into each other's eyes .	他說 , 他區分性愛 , 當兩個人凝視 , 拼字 , 看彼此的眼睛 。
and then he compared that to friendship , when two people stand side by side , as it were , shoulder to shoulder , with their eyes fixed on a common goal .	然後他把這和友誼比較 , 當兩個人站在一邊 , 肩並肩 , 視力固定在共同的目標上 。
we don't have to fall in love with each other , but we can become friends .	我們不需要愛上彼此 , 但我們可以成為朋友 。
and i am convinced .	我深信不疑 。
i felt it very strongly during our little deliberations at vevey , that when people of all different persuasions come together , working side by side for a common goal , differences melt away .	在我們對薇薇的小小考慮期間 , 我覺得它非常強烈 , 當不同說服的人集合在一起 , 一面為共同的目標努力 , 差異會融化 。
and we learn amity .	我們會學習到 「 性 」 。

the text here is right side and upside down so that you are forced to turn the book around , and you can see it from ground point of view and from her point of view looking in the hole , getting a different kind of perspective , moving you around the space . particularly appropriate in a building that can contain perfectly a sphere dimensions of the diameter being the same as the distance from the center of the floor to the center of the oculus .	這裡的文字是對的 , 上下顛倒 , 所以你被迫將書本翻過來 , 從地面看 , 從她的角度看進去 , 用不同的觀點看待書 , 帶著不同的觀點 , 讓你繞著空間移動 。 特別是適合建築物的空間 , 直徑是直徑的直徑和從地面向到章魚的中心的距離是一樣的 。
unfortunately for her , the anchor line gets tangled around the feet of some boy scouts who are visiting the pantheon , and they are immediately yanked out and given an extraordinary but terrifying tour of some of the domes of rome , which would , from their point of view , naturally be hanging upside down .	不幸的是 , 對她來說 , 這條架線纏住了一些正在參觀萬神殿的男孩們 , 他們馬上就被傾出去 , 進行一段非凡但又恐怖的巡迴演出 , 從他們的角度來看 , 很自然的就上下擺了 。
they bail out as soon as they get to the top of saint ivo , that little spiral structure you see there .	他們一到達聖伊沃的頂峰就保釋出來了 , 就看到那個螺旋狀的結構 。
she continues on her way over piazza navona .	她繼續前往那佛那廣場 。
notices a lot of activity at the tre scalini restaurant , is reminded that it is lunchtime and she's hungry .	注意到在trespalini餐廳有很大的活動這提醒她要吃午餐了 , 她餓了
they keep on motoring towards the campo de' fiori , which they soon reach . ajax the dog is put in a basket and lowered with a list of food into the marketplace , which flourishes there until about one in the afternoon , and then is completely removed and doesn't appear again until six or seven the following morning .	他們繼續向鮮花廣場行駛很快就到了 。 小狗阿賈克斯被放在籃子裡 , 把一份食物放到市場上 , 一直到下午一點 , 才會繁衍出去 , 一直到隔天六、七點都不會再出現 , 直到第二天早上 。
anyway , the pooch gets back to the dirigible with the stuff .	總之 , 小狗回到飛船上 ,
unfortunately , when she goes to unwrap the prosciutto , ajax makes a lunge for it .	不幸的是 , 當她要解開這個針筒時 , 阿賈克斯為它做了一頓午餐 。
she's managed to save the prosciutto , but in the process she loses the tablecloth , which you can see flying away in the upper lefthand corner .	她成功救了這條桌布 , 但在過程中 , 她失去了桌布 , 你可以看到在左上角飛走的桌布 。
they continue without their tablecloth , looking for a place to land this thing so that they can actually have lunch .	他們沒有桌布 , 持續找個地方降落 , 這樣他們就可以吃午餐 。
they eventually discover a huge wall that's filled with small holes , ideal for docking a dirigible because you've got a place to tie up .	他們最終發現了一面巨大的牆 , 裡面都是小洞 , 用來做繞土 , 理想的做法 , 因為你有地方可以連結在一起 。
turns out to be the exterior wall that part of it that remains of the coliseum , so they park themselves there and have a terrific lunch and have a spectacular view .	結果那面牆是羅馬競技場殘留下來的外牆 , 所以他們停在那裡 , 吃很棒的午餐 , 景色壯觀 。
at the end of lunch , they untie the anchor , they set off through the baths of caracalla and over the walls of the city and then an abandoned gatehouse and decide to take one more look at the pyramid of cestius , which has this lightning rod on top .	吃完午餐後 , 他們解開錨出發 , 穿過卡拉卡拉浴場 , 飛過城市的牆面 , 然後一個廢棄的門廊 , 決定再看一眼賽斯提烏斯金字塔的金字塔 , 頂部有燈棒 。
unfortunately , that's a problem: they get a little too close , and when you're in a dirigible you have to be very careful about spikes .	不幸的是 , 問題來了:他們有點太靠近了 , 而當你在飛船上時 , 你得要非常小心滑鼠 。
so that sort of brings her little story to a conclusion .	這讓她的故事得以總結 。
marcello , on the other hand , is sort of a lazy guy , but he's not due at work until about noon .	另一方面 , 馬爾切洛有點懶惰 , 但他中午才下班 。

he gets up , leaps onto his scooter , races through the city past the church of santa maria della pace , down the alleys , through the streets that tourists may be wandering through , disturbing the quiet backstreet life of rome at every turn .	他站起來 , 躍上他的摩托車 , 越過城市的聖母堂 , 越過小巷 , 穿越小巷 , 觀光遊走的街道 , 時時刻刻都在迴盪著 , 每次都會打擾羅馬的安靜後台生活 。
that speed with which he is moving , i hope i have suggested in this little image , which , again , can be turned around and read from both sides because there's text on the bottom and text on the top , one of which is upside down in this image .	他在移動的速度 , 我希望我在這張圖上提出 , 同樣地 , 可以反過來看 , 從兩側讀出來 , 因為下面有字母 , 上面有文字 , 上面的字是上下顛倒的影像 。
so , he keeps on moving , approaching an unsuspecting waiter who is trying to deliver two plates of linguine in a delicate white wine clam sauce to diners who are sitting at a table just outside of a restaurant in the street .	所以 , 他繼續前進 , 接近一間毫不知情的服務生 , 他試圖在精緻的白葡萄酒蛤蚌蛤醬上遞送兩塊義肢給坐在街邊餐廳外的客人 。
waiter catches on , but it's too late .	服務員追上來了 , 但已經太遲了 。
and marcello keeps moving in his scooter .	馬爾切洛還在他的摩托車上前進 。
everything he sees from this point on is slightly affected by the linguine , but keeps on moving because this guy's got a job to do .	從這個時點 , 他看到的所有東西都有點被語言所影響 , 但仍然繼續前進 , 因為這個人有工作要做 。
removes some scaffolding . one of the reasons rome remains the extraordinary place it is that because of scaffolding and the determination to maintain the fabric , it is a city that continues to grow and adapt to the needs of the particular time in which it finds itself , or we find it .	移除一些支架 。 羅馬仍是個不可思議的地方 , 因為架構和維持結構的決心 , 這個城市持續成長 , 並適應特定時間的需求 , 或我們找到了它 。
right through the piazza della rotonda , in front of the pantheon again wreaking havoc and finally getting to work .	就在廣場 , 羅通達廣場 , 在萬神殿前 , 又會再次破壞大屠殺 , 終於成功了 。
marcello , as it turns out , is the driver of the number 64 bus , and if you've been on the number 64 bus , you know that it's driven with the same kind of exuberance as marcello demonstrated on his scooter .	結果發現 , 馬爾切洛是64路巴士的司機 , 如果你坐過64路巴士 , 你知道這巴士開得跟馬爾切洛的摩托車展示的一樣精彩 。
and finally carletto . you see his apartment in the upper lefthand corner .	最後是carletto , 你可以看到他在左上角的公寓
he's looking at his table ; he's planning to propose this evening to his girlfriend of 40 years , and he wants it to be perfect .	他正盯著桌子看桌子 , 今晚打算向他的女友求婚40年 , 他希望一切都是完美的 。
he's got candles out , he's got flowers in the middle and he's trying to figure out where to put the plates and the glasses .	他把蠟燭拿出來 , 中間有鮮花他正想著要把板子和玻璃放在哪裡
but he's not happy ; something's wrong .	但他不高興 , 不對勁 。
the phone rings anyway , he's called to the palazzo .	電話響了 , 叫他去palazzo 。
he saunters he saunters at a good clip , but as compared to all the traveling we've just seen , he's sauntering .	他在一段不錯的短片偷跑 , 但和我們剛剛看到的那些旅行比起來 , 他簡直嚇人了 。
everybody knows carletto , because he's in entertainment , actually ; he's in television .	大家都知道carletto , 因為他在娛樂界 , 其實他在電視界 。
he's actually in television repair , which is why people know him .	他真的在電視維修 , 這就是為什麼大家會知道他 。
so they all have his number .	所以他們都有他的電話號碼 。
he arrives at the palazzo , arrives at the big front door .	他抵達了大門 , 抵達大門 。
enters the courtyard and talks to the custodian , who tells him that there's been a disaster in the palazzo ; nobody's tvs are working and there's a big soccer game coming up , and the crowd is getting a little restless and a little nervous .	走進院子 , 和看門人聊天 , 他告訴他 , 宮殿裡有一場災難 。 沒有人有電視業 , 即將有一場大足球比賽 , 人群變得有點緊張和緊張 。
he goes down to the basement and starts to check the wiring , and then gradually works his way up to the top of the building , apartment by apartment , checking every television , checking every connection , hoping to find out what this problem is .	他下到地下室 , 開始檢查電線 , 然後慢慢地爬到樓頂 , 每間公寓都經過檢查 , 檢查每一台電視機 , 想找出問題的所在 。
he works his way up , finally , the grand staircase and then a smaller staircase until he reaches the attic .	他一直往上爬 , 終於到了大樓梯然後上了一個小一點的樓梯直到他到了閣樓
he opens the window of the attic , of course , and there's a tablecloth wrapped around the building's television antenna .	他打開閣樓的窗戶 , 當然 , 還有一張桌布掛在建築物的電視天線上 。
he removes it , the problems are solved , everybody in the palazzo is happy .	他除去它 , 問題就解決了 , 宮殿中的所有人都很開心 。
and of course , he also solves his own problem .	當然 , 他也解決了自己的問題 。
all he has to do now , with a perfect table , is wait for her to arrive .	他現在只需要用一個完美的桌子 , 就等著她抵達 。
that was the first attempt , but it didn't seem substantial enough to convey whatever it was i wanted to convey about rome .	那是第一次嘗試 , 但看起來還不夠實在 , 傳達我想表達的對羅馬的看法 。
so i thought , well , i'll just do piazzas , and i'll get inside and underneath and i'll show these things growing and show why they're shaped the way they are and so on .	所以我想 , 好吧 , 我就來做廣場 , 我會進進去和下面 , 展示這些東西的成長 , 並且展示它們的形成方式等等 。
and then i thought , that's too complicated . no , i'll just take my favorite bits and pieces and i'll put them inside the pantheon but keep the scale , so you can see the top of sant'ivo and the pyramid of cestius and the tempietto of bramante all side by side in this amazing space .	然後我想 , 這太複雜了 。 不對 , 我拿我最喜歡的位元和碎片 , 把它們放到萬神廟內 , 保持這個尺度 , 你可以看到聖誕節的頂端 , 還有賽斯提烏斯的金字塔 , 還有布拉曼特的小禮拜堂 , 都在這片神奇的空間中 。
now that's one drawing , so i thought maybe it's time for piranesi to meet escher .	這是一幅畫 , 所以我想也許是時候讓皮拉內西與埃舍見面了 。
you see that i'm beginning to really lose control here and also hope .	你可以看到我開始失去了控制權 , 也失去了希望 。
there's a very thin blue line of exhaust that sort of runs through this thing that would be kind of the trail that holds it all together .	有一條非常薄的藍色線條 , 貫穿了這些線條 , 讓整座城市團結在一起 。
then i thought , " wait a minute , what am i doing ? "	然後我想: 「 等等 , 我在做什麼 ? 」
a book is not only a neat way of collecting and storing information , it's a series of layers .	書不光是收集和儲存資訊的便捷方法 , 它還是一系列的層次 。
i mean , you always peel one layer off another ; we think of them as pages , doing it a certain way .	我的意思是 , 你總是把一層一層剝離另一層 ; 我們認為他們是頁面 , 某種程度上 。
but think of them as layers . i mean , rome is a place of layers horizontal layers , vertical layers and i thought , well just peeling off a page would allow me to if i got you thinking about it the right way would allow me to sort of show you the depth of layers .	但把它們想成層次 。 我的意思是 , 羅馬是個有層次地層次的地方 , 垂直地層次 , 我心想 , 剝去書本就能讓我用正確的方式來呈現層次 。
the stucco on the walls of most of the buildings in rome covers the scars ; the scars of centuries of change as these structures have been adapted rather than being torn down .	羅馬大樓的泥土牆上覆蓋了許多疤痕 ; 數世紀以來的疤痕一直在改變 , 而不是被拆除 。
if i do a foldout page on the lefthand side and let you just unfold it , you see behind it what i mean by scar tissue .	如果我在左邊畫一個摺疊頁 , 你把它打開 , 就可以看到傷疤組織的背後 。
you can see that in 1635 , it became essential to make smaller windows because the bad guys were coming or whatever .	你可以看到 , 在1635年 , 製造小窗戶是很重要的 , 因為壞人要來了 , 諸如此類 。
adaptations all get buried under the stucco .	各式各樣的適應作用都被埋在了這個黏液之下 。
i could peel out a page of this palazzo to show you what's going on inside of it .	我可以把這張palazzo的頁面給你們看看裡面發生了什麼事 。
but more importantly , i could also show you what it looks like at the corner of one of those magnificent buildings with all the massive stone blocks , or the fake stone blocks done with brick and stucco , which is more often the case .	但 , 更重要的是 , 我也可以向各位展示 , 在這些雄偉建築的角落裡 , 那些巨大的石塊 , 或用磚頭和灰泥做成的假石塊 , 情況更加常見 。
so it becomes slightly threedimensional .	所以它有點立體 。
i could take you down one of those narrow little streets into one of those surprising piazzas by using a double gate fold double foldout page which , if you were like me reading a popup book as a child , you hopefully stick your head into .	我可以帶你走下一條狹窄的街道 , 進入一個令人驚訝的廣場 , 使用雙扇摺疊頁 , 如果你和我小時候一樣 , 正在讀一本彈出書 , 希望你把你的頭伸進去 。
you wrap the pages around your head and are in that piazza for that brief period of time .	你把你頭上的頁面 , 就在廣場那邊 , 就為了那個短暫的時間 。
and i've really not done anything much more complicated than make foldout pages .	我其實沒有做任何更複雜的摺疊頁 。
but then i thought , maybe i could be simpler here .	但接著我想 , 也許我可以簡單一點 。
let's look at the pantheon and the piazza della rotonda in front of it .	我們來看看萬神殿和前面的羅通達廣場 。
here's a book completely wide open .	這本書完全打開了 。
ok , if i don't open the book the whole way , if i just open it 90 degrees , we're looking down the front of the pantheon , and we're looking sort of at the top , more or less down on the square .	如果我不打開這本書 , 如果我只打開90度 , 我們就在俯視萬神廟的正面 , 而在圖片的最上方 , 或多或少是從平面往下看 。
and if i turn the book the other way , we're looking across the square at the front of the pantheon .	如果我把書換個角度 , 我們就在萬神廟的正面看著廣場 。
no foldouts , no tricks just a book that isn't open the whole way .	沒有摺疊 , 沒有把戲只是本沒有打開的書 。
that seemed promising . i thought , maybe i'll do it inside and i can even combine the foldouts with the only partially opened book .	這似乎很有希望 。 我想 , 也許我可以在裡面做 , 甚至可以把摺疊文字和唯一開放的書結合 。
so we get inside the pantheon and it grows and so on and so forth .	我們進入萬神廟內部 , 它會一直擴張下去 。
and i thought , maybe i'm on the right track , but it sort of lost its human quality .	我心想 , 也許我正走對路 , 但它似乎失去了人類的特質 。
so i went back to the notion of story , which is always a good thing to have if you're trying to get people to pay attention to a book and pick up information along the way .	所以 , 我回到故事的概念 , 它總是一件好事 , 如果你想要讓人注意讀書 , 並在過程中取得資訊 。
" pigeon's progress " struck me as a catchy title .	「 鴿子的進展 」 震撼了我 。
if it was a homing pigeon , it would be called " homer's odyssey . "	如果這是一隻同鴿子 , 它會被稱為 「 荷馬的奧德賽 」 。
but it was the journey of the . . .	但它是這趟旅程......
i mean , if a title works , use it . but it would be a journey that went through rome and showed all the things that i like about rome .	我的意思是 , 如果書名行得通 , 用它 。 但它會是一趟穿越羅馬的旅程 , 並展示我喜歡羅馬的一切 。
it's a pigeon sitting on top of a church .	這是教堂頂上的鴿子 。
goes off during the day and does normal pigeon stuff . comes back , the whole place is covered with scaffolding and green netting and there's no way this pigeon can get home .	白天飛走 , 做鴿子該做的事 。 回來了 , 整個地方被鷹架和綠色網路覆蓋 , 而這種鴿子無法回家 。
so it's a homeless pigeon now and it's going to have to find another place to live , and that allows me to go through my catalog of favorite things , and we start with the tall ones and so on .	所以這是一隻無家可歸的鴿子 , 它必須找另一個居住地 , 這使我能走過我喜愛的目錄 , 我們從較高的 , 以此類推 。
maybe it has to go back and live with family members ; that's not always a good thing , but it does sort of bring pigeons together again .	也許它必須回去和家人住在一起 ; 那不一定是好事 , 但會讓鴿子再聚在一起 。
and i thought , that's sort of interesting , but maybe there's a person who should be involved in this in some way .	我就想 , 這很有趣 , 但也許有一個人該以某種方式參與其中 。
so i kind of came up with this old guy who spends his life looking after sick pigeons .	所以我想出了一個老傢伙一輩子都在照顧生病的鴿子
he'll go anywhere to get them dangerous places and whatnot and they become really friends with this guy , and learn to do tricks for him and entertain him at lunchtime and stuff like that .	他會去任何地方幫他們找危險的地方 , 然後他們會和這個傢伙交朋友 , 學會了在午餐時間幫他玩耍 , 諸如此類的事情 。
there's a real bond that develops between this old man and these pigeons .	這種老人和這些鴿子之間確實有著真實的連結 。
but unfortunately he gets sick . he gets really sick at the end of the story .	但不幸的是 , 他生病了 , 病的很重 。
he's taught them to spell his name , which is aldo .	他教他們拼他的名字 , aldo 。
they show up one day after three or four days of not seeing him he lives in this little garret and they spell his name and fly around .	他們在一個三四天沒見到他之後的一天 , 他就住在一個小小的車庫裡 , 然後他們把他的名字吐出來 。
and he finally gets enough strength together to climb up the ladder onto the roof , and all the pigeons , a la red balloon , are there waiting for him and they carry him off over the walls of the city .	最後他得到了足夠的力量 , 爬上梯子到屋頂上 , 所有的鴿子 , 像是紅氣球 , 都在等著他 , 然後他們把他帶走 , 帶到城市的牆上 。
and i forgot to mention this: whenever he lost a pigeon , he would take that pigeon out beyond the walls of the city .	我忘了提到:只要他失去一隻鴿子 , 他就會把那隻鴿子帶到城市外面去 。
in the old roman custom , the dead were never buried within the walls .	在羅馬的傳統里 , 去世的人從來沒有被埋在牆壁中 。
and i thought that's a really cheery story .	我覺得這個故事真的很令人開心 。
. that's really going to go a long way .	這將會有很長的路要走 。
so anyway , i went through . . . and again , if packaging doesn't work and if the stories aren't going anywhere , i just come up with titles and hope that a title will sort of kick me off in the right direction .	總之 , 我經歷了...再一次 , 如果包裝不成功 , 如果故事不在哪裡 , 我只是想出了頭銜 , 希望頭銜會向正確的方向把我踢下去 。
and sometimes it does focus me enough and i'll even do a title page .	有時候它確實讓我花了夠多的精力 , 我甚至會寫一頁 。
so , these are all title pages that eventually led me to the solution i settled on , which is the story of a young woman who sends a message on a homing pigeon she lives outside the walls of the city of rome to someone in the city .	這些全部都是書名最終把我帶到解決方案上 , 這是一位年輕女子的故事 , 她在羅馬城外的羅馬城外送了一封信給在市區的某個人 。
and the pigeon is flying down above the appian way here .	而鴿子就在阿基安的上方向下飛
you can see the tombs and pines and so on and so forth along the way .	你可以看見墳墓、松果等等 。
if you see the red line , you are seeing the trail of the pigeon ; if you don't see the red line , you are the pigeon .	如果你看到紅線 , 你看到的是鴿子的軌跡 ; 如果你看不到紅線 , 你就是那隻鴿子 。
and it becomes necessary and possible , at this point , to try to convey what that sense would be like of flying over the city without actually moving .	在這個時點 , 飛越城市是必要和可行的 , 在這個時點 , 試著傳達出那種飛越城市的感覺 , 卻不用移動 。
past the pyramid of cestius these will seem very familiar to you , even if you haven't been to rome recently past the gatehouse .	過了賽斯提烏斯金字塔--你可能覺得很熟悉 , 即使你最近沒有去過羅馬 , 過了大門 。
this is something that's a little bit unusual .	這有點不尋常 。
this pigeon does something that most homing pigeons do not do: it takes the scenic route , which was a device that i felt was necessary to actually extend this book beyond about four pages .	這隻鴿子做了一件其它鴿子不做的事:它選擇了一條景觀路線 , 我覺得這個儀器是必須把這本書延伸到四頁以外的地方 。
so , we circle around the coliseum , past the church of santa maria in cosmedin and the temple of hercules towards the river .	所以 , 我們圍繞著哥倫斯周圍 , 超越了在宇宙中聖母堂和海克力士的教堂 , 朝著河流前進 。
we almost collide with the cornice of the palazzo farnese designed by michelangelo , built of stone taken from the coliseum narrow escape .	我們差點撞上了由米開朗基羅設計的帕拉索場角 , 用的石頭是從羅馬競技場拆下來的 。
we swoop down over the campo de' fiori .	我們俯瞰鮮花廣場
this is one of those things i show to my students because it's a complete bastardization a denial of any rules of perspective .	這是我給學生看的其中一件事 , 因為這是完全違背所有觀點的規則 。
the only rule of perspective that i think matters is if it looks believable , you've succeeded .	我認為唯一重要的透視法是 , 如果它看起來很可信 , 你就成功了 。
but you try and figure out where the vanishing points meet here ; a couple are on mars and a couple of others in cremona .	但你試著去找出哪個消失點相加 ; 火星上有些地方是火星上 , 另外一些是在克雷莫納 。
but into the piazza in front of santa maria della pace , where invariably a soccer game is going on , and we're hit by a soccer ball .	但在廣場上 , 在聖母堂前面 , 和平常差不多 , 總是有一場足球賽正在進行 , 我們被一顆足球擊中 。
now this is a terrible illustration of being hit by a soccer ball .	這是一個很糟糕的插圖 , 被足球擊中 。
i have all the pieces: there's santa maria della pace , there's a soccer ball , there's a little bit of a bird's wing nothing's happening , so i had to rethink it .	我有所有的作品:有聖誕老人賽跑步 , 有足球 , 有一點點鳥翅膀 , 什麼都沒有 , 所以我得要重新思考它 。
and if you do want to see santa maria della pace , these books are really flexible , incredibly interactive just turn it around and look at it the other way .	假如你想看到聖母瑪莉亞•德拉的步調 , 這些書是很有彈性的 , 交互作用的--只要把它反過來看 。
through the alley , we can see the impact is captured in the red line .	穿過巷子 , 我們可以看到它的影響以紅線表示 。
and then bird manages to pull itself together past this medieval tower one of the few remaining medieval towers towards the church of sant'agnese and around the dome looking down into piazza navona which we've already mentioned and seen and flown over a couple of times ; there's the bernini statue of the four rivers and then past the wonderful borromini sant'ivo , stopping just long enough on the 26foot diameter oculus of the pantheon to catch our breath .	接著 , 鳥類能夠拉過這座中世紀的塔樓 , 剩下的中世紀塔樓之一 , 前往聖阿凡尼斯教堂的中世紀塔樓 , 附近的大樓 , 往下看 , 我們已經提到過、看見、飛過數次了 ; 還有伯利尼雕像 , 在這四條河流的四條河流之中 , 然後經過神奇的博羅米諾休斯聖安諾司修道 , 已經足夠長達26英尺 。
and then we can swoop inside and around ; and because we're flying , we don't really have to worry about gravity at this particular moment in time , so this drawing can be oriented in any way on the page .	然後我們可以在裡面到處亂跑 , 因為我們在飛 , 我們不用在這個特定時刻擔心重力 , 讓這幅圖在任何時候都有方向 。
we get a little exuberant as we pass gesu ; it's not surprising to sort of mimic the architecture in this way .	飛過耶穌堂的時候 , 我們會變得很興奮 ; 用這種方式來模仿這個建築並不讓人意外 。
past the wonderful wall filled with the juxtaposition that i was talking about ; beautiful carvings set into the walls above the neon " ristorante " sign , and so on .	一面牆上填滿了我剛剛談到的 " 和 " 暴風雨 " 的 " 暴風雪 " 招牌上方的 " 美麗雕刻 " 牆壁...等等
and eventually , we arrive at the courtyard of the palazzo , which is our destination .	最終 , 我們抵達了palazzo的院子 , 那是我們的目的地 。
straight up through the courtyard into a little window into the attic , where somebody is working at the drawing board .	直接穿過庭院 , 進入一扇小窗戶 , 進入閣樓 , 有人在畫板上工作 。
he removes the message from the leg of the bird ; this is what it says .	他從鳥的腿上除去訊息 ; 這就是它說的 。
as we look at the drawing board , we see what he's working on is , in fact , a map of the journey that the pigeon has just taken , and the red line extends through all the sights .	當我們看著設計圖的板子時 , 我們看到他正在努力的 , 事實上 , 這是一隻鴿子踏上旅程的地圖 , 紅線穿過所有景象 。
and if you want the information , so that we complete this cycle of understanding , all you have to do is read these paragraphs .	如果你想要這些資訊 , 所以我們完成了這個理解的循環 , 你所要做的就是讀這些段落 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院的騎士們自行組裝這個想法:與其建造一些東西 , 我們可以創造出一些材料 , 像是dna鏈接自行組合的方式 。 這是一個在初期很大的概念 ; tibbits告訴我們三個項目 , 它暗示著一個自我組裝的未來會是什麼樣子 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	高空的tibbit:我們能否做出會自己的東西 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天 , 我想向各位展示我們未來製造東西的方式 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築物和機器很快就會變成自我組裝、複製和修復 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以 , 我將展示我相信是目前的製造業狀態 , 然後比較一些自然生態系統 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	在目前的製造業狀態 , 我們有摩天大樓--兩年半的時間 , 50萬至一百萬個部分 , 相當複雜、嶄新、令人興奮的技術 , 鋼鐵、混凝土、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們有令人興奮的機器 , 能帶我們進入太空-250萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你觀察自然生態系統 , 我們有兩百萬類型的蛋白質 , 可以在一萬納秒中摺疊 , 或dna有三十億個鹼基對 , 我們可以在大約一個小時複製 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 我們的自然生態系統有著複雜性 , 但它們非常有效率 , 遠比任何我們能建立的東西都更有效率 。 遠比任何我們能建立的任何東西都複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	在能源方面 , 它們的效率更高 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不會犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	它們可以修復自己長壽 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以自然生態系統有一個超級有趣的東西 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們可以將它轉化為我們的建築環境 , 那我們就有了令人興奮的潛力 , 可以用來建設東西 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組裝 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要利用我們的物理環境中的自組裝 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	第一 , 我們需要解碼所有我們想建造的複雜性 , 這樣我們的建築物和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要解碼成簡單的序列基本上就是我們建築物的運作方式的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要可編程的部分 , 可以把序列拿起來 , 再用它來折疊 , 或重新配置 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能源 , 讓它能夠活化 , 讓我們的部分能夠折疊程式 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要某種類型的修正冗餘 , 來保證我們已經成功地建造出我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要向你們展示一些項目 , 是我在麻省理工學院的同事和我正在努力實現這個自我組裝的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先是macrobot和decibot 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	這些項目都是大型的可重組的機器人--8英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	它們與機電設備 , 傳感器嵌入 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	解碼你想要摺疊什麼 , 形成一連串的角度--負120 , 負120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , 負120--類似的東西 ; 所以一連串的角度 , 或者是轉動 , 你將這個序列透過弦發送出去 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都需要它的消息--負120 。 它會旋轉 , 檢查它是否到了那裡 , 然後把它傳遞給它的鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些傑出的科學家 , 工程師 , 設計師 , 在這個項目上工作 。
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為它真正的帶出了光線:這真的很可擴展嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 數以千計時數製造這8英尺的機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們真的能把這個規模做大嗎 ? 我們真的能把機器人嵌入每個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 關注的是被動天性 , 或被動試圖重新配置可編程 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但這又更進一步 , 並嘗試實際的計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上是最根本的計算 , 數位邏輯 , 直接嵌入到你的零件中 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是一個nand邏輯閘口 。
