you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一個正四面體 , 就是門 , 它會做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入的正四面體 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中一個是使用者的輸入 , 當你在做磚塊時 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是從以前被放置的磚 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	它會讓你在三維空間中得到輸出 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	這意味著用戶可以開始連接他們想要的磚塊 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算它以前的行為 , 你說你想要它做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動--向上或向下 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	在左邊 , [1 , 1]輸入等於輸出0 , 結果會下降 。
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , [0 , 0]輸入1輸出 , 它就會上升 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	這意味著我們的結構現在包含了我們要建造的藍圖 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	他們擁有所有這些建構出來的資訊
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	這意味著我們可以有某種形式的自我複製 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個案例中 , 我稱它為自我導向的複製 , 因為你的結構包含著確切的藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有錯誤 , 你可以更換零件 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有局部的訊息都嵌入在告訴你們如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以擁有攀登的東西 , 讀取它 , 然後在一對一輸出 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	它直接嵌入 ; 沒有任何外部的指令 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	我將展示的最後一個項目叫做偏見鏈 , 它可能是我們現在被動自組裝系統中最令人興奮的例子 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	需要重新配置和可編程 , 並讓它成為一個完全被動的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	基本上你有一個元素鏈 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 偏見也相同 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一條鏈、每一個元素 , 都想要向右或左轉 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你組裝鏈時 , 你基本上是在編程 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你告訴每個單位是否應該向左轉或向左轉 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	當你搖晃鏈 , 它會折疊成任何你編程的配置--在這個案例中 , 一個螺旋 , 或這個例子中 , 兩個彼此相鄰的立方體 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	基本上你可以設計任何立體形狀 , 或單面的 , 二維 , 完全被動地進入這條鏈 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們什麼是未來的意義 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我想這告訴我們有新的自我組裝、複製、修復我們實體結構、建築物、機器的新可能性 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些地區有新的可編程 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從而有新的計算可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們將有空間計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的建築物、橋樑、機器 , 所有磚塊都能計算出來 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這是驚人的並行和分散式的計算能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以這是令人興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為我所展示的這些項目 , 只是通往未來的一小步 , 如果我們實施這些新的自組裝世界的技術 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們去過月球 , 繪製了大陸地圖 , 我們甚至去過兩次海底最深的地點 。 下一代我們要探討的是什麼 ? 生物學家和內森•沃爾夫提出這個答案:幾乎所有 。 我們可以開始 , 他說 , 和那些不可思議的小世界 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性、探索、微生物學、科學 ,
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	內森•沃爾夫:還有什麼要探索 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我去了威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市 。
and i was there to honor a great 20th century explorer , roy chapman andrews .	目的是為了表揚一位偉大的20世紀探險家羅伊.查普曼安德魯斯
during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	安德魯斯在美國自然歷史博物館 , 帶領一系列的考察隊伍 , 前往未知的區域 , 像是這裏的戈壁沙漠 。
he was quite a figure .	他是個不錯的人物 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	後來有人說是印第安那瓊斯這個角色的基礎 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市時 , 我給一群中學生公開演說 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡告訴各位 , 如果有比ted這裡演講更嚇人的話 , 它會試著把一千個12歲孩子的注意力集中在45分鐘的演講中 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	在演講尾聲時 , 他們問了幾個問題 , 但從那之後 , 有一個問題深深地困擾著我 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一個年輕女孩站起來 , 她問了這個問題: 「 我們要去哪裡探索 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我想有很多人覺得偉大的地球探索年代已經結束了 , 對下一代來說 , 他們將必須去外太空或深海 , 才能找到重要的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但真的是這樣嗎 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	地球上真的沒有剩下的重要地方可以讓我們探索嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這有點讓我回想起生物史上我最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是個未知世界的探險家 , martinusbeijerinck 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	beijerinck一開始要找出菸草鑲嵌疾病的成因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是取出菸草植物的受感染汁液 , 再用更小的過濾器過濾 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他感覺到一定有什麼東西比當時所知的最小型的生命形式還要小 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他為他神秘的媒介命了一個名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱之為 「 毒藥 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在揭露病毒的過程中 , beijerinck為我們開啟了一個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	我們現在知道病毒構成地球上絕大部分的基因信息 , 遠超過所有其他形式的生命體的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	很明顯地 , 這個世界有著巨大的實際應用──像是天花的消滅 , 預防子宮頸癌疫苗的出現 , 我們現在知道主要是由人類乳突病毒所引起的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	而beijerinck的發現不是500年前發生的
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	beijerinck在100多年前發現了病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	基本上 , 我們已經有了汽車 , 但我們還沒有意識到我們星球上大多數基因信息的生命形式 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些驚人的工具 , 讓我們可以探索未知的世界--像是深度定序 , 讓我們可以做得比只看到表面還要多 , 還多 , 看看個別的物種的基因組 , 看看整個宏基因組 , 包含微生物群落的群落 , 在我們周圍 , 以及記錄這些物種中所有的基因信息 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以將這些技術應用在從土壤到皮膚之間的所有東西上 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們定期做這種事情 , 找出疫情爆發的成因 , 正是造成疫情的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了讓你們更了解這如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們取了你們每個人的鼻腔標本 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	我們通常會去尋找呼吸道疾病的病毒 , 像是流感病毒 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	首先我們會看到非常大量的基因信息 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這些基因信息 , 當然 , 我們會看到一些普通的嫌疑犯 , 當然 , 很多的人類基因信息 , 還有細菌和病毒信息 , 大部分是來自你鼻子中完全無害的東西 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到了令人非常驚訝的事 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這些資訊時 , 我們會發現 , 你鼻子裡大約有20%的基因信息與我們以前從未見過的東西完全吻合 , 不管是植物、動物、真菌、病毒 , 或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上我們不知道這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對於我們這些研究這種數據的小組 , 實際上我們當中有些人開始稱之為 「 資訊生物暗物質 」 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道它不是任何我們以前見過的東西 ; 它有點像是我們基因信息中未知的大陸 。
and there's a lot of it .	而且還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為你鼻子中20%的基因信息是很多的生物暗物質 , 如果我們觀察你的腸子 , 高達40%到50%的信息是生物暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使是在相對比較下無菌的血液中 , 大約有1%到2%的信息是暗物質無法被分類 , 無法與我們所見的任何東西配對或配對 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	一開始 , 我們以為這也許是人工製品 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深度排序的技術還相當新 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當他們愈來愈準確 , 我們已經確定這種信息是生命的一種形式 , 至少是生命的一種形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然解釋生物暗物質存在的假設都還在初期階段 , 還是有一個非常令人興奮的可能性存在:那就是埋藏在生命裡 , 基因資訊是還未被辨識出生命的特徵 。
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索一連串的a、t、c、g時 , 我們可能會發現一種全新的生命類型 , 像beijerinck一樣 , 它會從根本改變我們對生物學本質的看法 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	那或許能讓我們找出折磨我們的癌症的原因 , 或是找出我們不熟悉的爆發病源頭 , 或是在分子生物學中創造出新的工具 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很高興地宣布 , 和史丹佛大學、加州理工學院和加州大學舊金山分校的同事一起 , 我們目前正開始著手探索生物暗物質 , 以尋求新生命形式的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	大約一百多年前 , 人們還沒有意識到病毒 , 這種生命形式就是我們星球上大部分基因信息的生物 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年後 , 人們可能會驚訝於我們完全不知道一種新的生命類型 , 真的就在我們的眼前 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	的確 , 我們可能記錄了地球上所有的大陸 , 我們可能已經發現了所有的哺乳類動物 , 但這並不表示地球上沒有其它可探索的地方 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	beijerinck和他的同類提供了重要的啟示給下一代來自威斯康辛州的貝洛伊特市的探險家 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	如果我們要說出這個啟示 , 應該是像這樣子的:不要假設我們目前認為的全部都是這樣 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	追求你選擇要探索的領域中的暗物質 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們周圍有未知的事物 , 它們只是等待被發現 。
legendary scientist david deutsch puts theoretical physics on the back burner to discuss a more urgent matter: the survival of our species . the first step toward solving global warming , he says , is to admit that we have a problem .	傳說中的科學家大衛•德•德施將理論物理放在柱子上 , 討論一個更急迫的問題:我們人類的生存 。 解決全球暖化的第一步 , 他說 , 是承認我們有問題 。
climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、宇宙、文化、環境、全球議題、物理、科學、科技、宇宙等 。
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛•狄尤斯在我們所在的宇宙中 , 擺在我們在宇宙中的位置 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	有人叫我們踏上肢體 , 說出令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	我會試著這麼做 , 但我想要從大家都知道的兩件事開始 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	第一 , 事實上 , 是有史以來被記錄下來最多的事件 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	那就是 , 地球、太陽系、太陽系 , 或環境等等 , 都是獨一無二的適合人類演化或創造 , 因為它曾經是我們現在的思想和現在的存在 , 最重要的是我們未來的生存 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	如今這個想法有個戲劇化的名字:太空船地球 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	這裡的概念是 , 在太空船之外 , 宇宙是很有敵意的 , 內部是我們唯一依賴的 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只有一個機會:如果我們搞砸我們的太空船 , 我們別無選擇 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	第二件大家都知道的事 , 與人類歷史上大多數人所相信的相反 , 人類其實並不是存在的中心 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	正如史蒂芬•霍金說過的 , 我們只是一個典型的星球表面的化學污垢 , 它繞著一個典型的恆星運行 , 位於一個典型的銀河系的邊緣等等 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	第一件大家都知道的事 , 就是說我們正處於一個非常不典型的地方 , 獨一無二的適合等等 。 第二件事是說我們正處於一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你把這兩件事當作生命中深刻的真理 , 並以此作為生命決策的依據 , 那麼它們似乎會互相矛盾 。
but that doesn't prevent them from both being completely false .	但這並不能阻止他們兩者都是完全錯誤的 。
and they are . so let me start with the second one: typical . well is this a typical place ? well , let's look around , you know , and look in a random direction , and we see a wall , and chemical scum and that's not typical of the universe at all .	這些是的 。 讓我從第二個故事開始:典型的 , 這是典型的嗎 ? 嗯 , 讓我們看看四周 , 隨機的方向 , 我們看到一面牆 , 化學污垢 , 這一點也不典型的宇宙 。
all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你只要朝同一個方向走幾百英里 , 然後往回看 , 你完全看不到任何牆或化學污垢 。 如果你走得更遠 , 你會看到太陽、太陽系 , 和恆星等等 。
but that's still not typical of the universe , because stars come in galaxies .	但這仍然不是宇宙的典型 , 因為恆星是銀河系的 。
and most places in the universe , a typical place in the universe , is nowhere near any galaxies .	宇宙中的大部份地方 , 宇宙中一個典型的地方 , 都不在任何一個星系附近 。
so let's go out further , till we're outside the galaxy , and look back , and yeah , there's the huge galaxy with spiral arms laid out in front of us .	讓我們再往外走 , 直到我們到了外面的銀河 , 然後再往回看 , 巨大的銀河系 , 螺旋手臂就在我們面前 。
and at this point we've come 100 , 000 light years from here .	到目前為止 , 我們已經從這裡走了十萬光年 。
but we're still nowhere near a typical place in the universe .	但我們離宇宙中典型的地方還很遠 。
to get to a typical place , you've got to go 1 , 000 times as far as that into intergalactic space .	要到達典型的星系間空間 , 就要再走一千倍的距離 。
and so what does that look like ? typical .	那會是什麼樣子 ? 典型的 。
what does a typical place in the universe look like ?	宇宙中典型的地方長什麼樣子 ?
well , at enormous expense , ted has arranged a highresolution immersion virtual reality rendering of intergalactic space the view from intergalactic space .	ted大費的排列出一個高清晰的星系間空間的虛擬實境呈現──星系間空間的影像 。
so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	我們能把燈關掉嗎 ? 拜託 , 我們看得到嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	其實 , 不太完美--星系間空間--星系間空間是完全黑暗的 , 漆黑的 , 漆黑的 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	它是如此的黑暗 , 如果你看著離你最近的恆星 , 那顆恆星爆炸成超新星 , 當光線接觸到你時 , 你要直視它 , 你仍然無法看到明亮的光芒 。
that's how big and how dark the universe is .	宇宙就是如此的巨大和黑暗 。
and that's despite the fact that a supernova is so bright , so brilliant an event , that it would kill you stone dead at a range of several light years .	儘管事實上超新星是如此的明亮 , 如此的傑出 , 它會在數光年的範圍內殺死你 。
and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從星系間的空間來看 , 它是如此的遙遠 , 你甚至無法看到它 。
it's also very cold out there less than three degrees above absolute zero .	那裡也非常冷 , 溫度低於絕對零度三度 。
and it's very empty . the vacuum there is one million times less dense than the highest vacuum that our best technology on earth can currently create . so that's how different a typical place is from this place .	那裡空無一物 。 真空的密度比我們現在地球上最好的科技所能創造出來的密度要少一百萬倍 。 這就是一個典型的地方 。
and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方的不典型 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能把燈光打回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們怎麼知道離我們這麼遠的環境 ? 如此不同 , 如此陌生 , 和我們習以為常的環境 ?
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	地球──我們的環境 , 以我們形式來創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	那是什麼意思呢 ? 看看遠比我們剛才所說的更遠--從這裡開始 , 利用望遠鏡--你會看到像恆星的東西 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	它們被稱為 「 類星體 」 , 原始的意思是類星體 。
which means things that look a bit like stars . but they're not stars .	這意味著那些看起來有點像恆星的東西 , 但不是恆星 。
and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道它們是什麼 。 數十億年前 , 數十億光年之外 , 銀河系中心的物質朝著超大質量的黑洞倒塌 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	然後強烈的磁場引導了重力崩潰的一些能量 。 其中的一些物質 , 以極大的噴射流形成我認為是萬億個太陽的光輝 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	人類大腦的物理現象可能和噴射流的物理相差甚遠 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們無法在那瞬間存活下來 。 當語言試圖描述噴射流中的狀況時 , 語言會崩塌 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	會有點像經歷一次超新星的爆炸 , 但在近距離發生了數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 這種噴射流發生得如此精確 , 以至於數十億年後 , 在宇宙的另一邊 , 一些化學污垢可以準確地描述和模型 , 和預測 , 和解釋 , 最重要的是 , 在現實中 , 你的參考是你的認知 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個物理系統 , 大腦 , 包含了另外一個模型的準確工作模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不只是表面的圖像 , 雖然它也包含這個圖像 , 還有一個解釋性的模型 , 具體呈現出相同的數學關係和相同的因果結構 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識 。 如果這還不夠神奇 , 一個結構相似 , 另一條的信念就會隨著時間增加 。 這就是知識的增長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	物理定律有這種特殊的特性 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	這個實體物體 , 儘可能彼此不同 , 但卻仍然可以體現相同的數學和因果結構 , 隨著時間越來越多 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以我們是一種不一樣的化學污垢 。 這種化學污垢有普遍性 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它的結構有著持續精準的增長 , 一切的結構 。 這個地方 , 而非宇宙的其它地方 , 是包含在內的一個中心 , 包含著整個物理實體的結構與因果關係 。 所以 , 與物理定律的不微不足道 , 物理定律允許這個定律 , 甚至行使它發生的 , 是物理世界中最重要的事情之一 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和環境是如何形成的呢 ? 以我們人類的形式獲得這個與宇宙其他部分的特殊關係 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	史蒂芬•霍金的評論中 , 有一點是正確的 , 但那是錯誤的強調 。 有一點是正確的 。 它沒有任何特殊的物理原理 。 沒有特殊的放寬 , 沒有奇蹟涉入 。 它有三件我們現今擁有的事物 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中一個是物質 , 因為知識的增長是資訊處理的一種形式 。 信息處理就是計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 根本不知道如何讓電腦沒有物質來製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們還需要能量來製造電腦 , 最重要的是要讓媒體能夠對我們所發現的知識進行影響 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 較不可能實現 , 但對於開放式知識和解釋的創造 , 也是必要的 , 就是證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境中充滿了證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們碰巧要測試的時候 , 比如 , 牛頓的重力定律大約在三百年前 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但 , 我們過去做得到的證據 , 在地球上數十億年前 , 已經落下了每平方公尺的面積 , 之後還會再繼續下去數十億年 。 其他的科學也一樣 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	據我們所知 , 發掘所有科學中最根本的真理的證據就在我們星球上 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們所在之處充滿了證據 , 也充滿了物質和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在星系間空間中 , 這三個創造開放式知識的前題是他們最低的供應量 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	就像我說的 , 那裡是空的 , 那裡是冷的 , 那裡是暗的 , 還是 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個狹義的誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	想像在星系間空間中的一個立方體 , 和我們的房子大小一樣 , 太陽系 。 現在這個立方體是以人類的標準來看是非常空的 , 但那仍然意味著它含有超過一百萬噸的物質 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸足夠建造一個自給自足的太空站在那裡有一群科學家致力於創造開放式的知識流之類的
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在的科技甚至連從星系間空間收集氫氣和將其轉化成其他元素等等都遠不夠 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但問題是 , 在一個可以理解的宇宙中 , 如果某個東西不被物理定律禁止 , 那麽 , 除了知道如何之外 , 還能阻止我們去做呢 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是關於知識的問題 , 而不是資源的問題 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能自動獲得能源供給 , 因為轉變會是核融合反應爐和證據嗎 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	嗯 , 再次強調 , 這對人類感官來說是很黑暗的 。 但你只需要拿一個望遠鏡 , 甚至是現今的設計 , 看看外面的銀河系 , 就像我們從這裡看到的一樣 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	用一個更強大的望遠鏡 , 你將能夠看見恆星和行星 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些星系中 , 你可以做天體物理學 , 學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	定位在那裡 , 你可以建造粒子加速器 , 學習初級粒子物理學 , 化學等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	最難做的可能是生物學實地考察 , 因為要花數百萬年才能到達最近的有生命的星球 , 再回來 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但是我必須告訴你--對不起 , 理查--但我從來不喜歡生物學實地考察 , 我想我們可以每隔幾億年就完成一次 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 星系間空間確實包含所有創造開放式知識的前提條件 。 任何這樣的立方體 , 在宇宙的任何地方 , 都可以成為同樣的樞紐 , 只要我們知道如何實現它的話 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以 , 我們並沒有處在一個特別友善的地點 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果銀河系間空間能夠創造出一串開放式的解釋 , 那麼幾乎所有其他的環境都是如此 。 這就是地球 。 污染的地球也是如此 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	而限制性因素 , 就在這裡 , 不是資源 , 因為資源很充足 , 但知識是稀少的 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	這種以宇宙知識為基礎的觀點也許──我認為這應該會讓我們感覺非常特別 。 但也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為若沒有具體的知識能夠在宇宙中存活下去 , 我們就無法存活下去 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	僅僅是幾光年外的超新星爆炸 , 我們全都會死掉 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁.雷斯最近寫了一本書 , 內容是關於我們對於各種事物的脆弱性 , 從天體物理學 , 到科學實驗都出錯了 , 最重要的是對於大規模殺傷性武器的恐怖主義 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為人類文明只有50%的機率能在這個世紀存活 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他晚點會在研討會上討論這個主題 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	我不認為機率是正確的類別 , 可以討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我同意他的看法 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們可以失敗的存活 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但這不取決於機率 , 而是我們是否能及時創造出相關的知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	這種危險完全不是前所未有的物種會絕種
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明就這樣結束了 。 絕大多數的物種和所有的文明都是現在的歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想成為例外的話 , 那麼邏輯上我們唯一的希望就是使用區別我們族類和文明的一個特徵 , 與其他所有其他的特徵--也就是 , 我們與物理定律的特殊關係 , 我們創造新的解釋能力 , 新的知識成為存在的中心 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	讓我把這套系統用在當前的爭議上 , 不是因為我想要提議任何特定的解決方案 , 而只是要說明我的意思 。
and the controversy is global warming .	爭議就是全球暖化 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	我是物理學家 , 但我不是個對的物理學家 。 以全球暖化來說 , 我只是個分層人 。 作為一個分層人 , 理性的做法是認真看待科學理論 。 根據那個理論 , 避免災難已經太遲了 。
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果這是正確的 , 我們目前最好的選擇就是防止二氧化碳排放 , 像是京都議定書、它在經濟活動上的限制 , 以及它巨大的成本 , 不論是什麼 , 那都只是不合理的衡量方式 。
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	倡議的行動甚至都不是為了解決問題 , 僅僅稍微延遲這個問題 。 所以要避免它太遲 , 可能已經太遲了 , 在任何人意識到它之前就已經太遲了 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	在1970年代時已經太晚了 , 當時最好的科學理論告訴我們工業排放將要降低數十億人的死亡冰河時期 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	這件事對我來說是很清楚的 , 我也不知道為什麼它不會告知大眾辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們不可能總是知道 。 當我們知道即將發生的災難 , 以及如何解決災難成本低於災難本身的成本 , 那麼就沒有太多的爭論了 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有任何預防措施 , 沒有任何預防措施 , 可以避免我們尚未預見的問題 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	因此 , 我們需要一個能解決問題的立場 , 而不僅僅是能解決問題 。
and it's true that an ounce of prevention equals a pound of cure , but that's only if we know what to prevent .	的確 , 一盎司的預防等於一盎司的解藥 , 但這只是因為我們知道預防什麼 。
if you've been punched on the nose , then the science of medicine does not consist of teaching you how to avoid punches .	如果你已經在鼻子上打了一拳 , 那麼醫學的科學並不是在教你如何避免打針 。
if medical science stopped seeking cures and concentrated on prevention only , then it would achieve very little of either .	如果醫學不再研究治病的方法 , 只專注於預防 , 那它也幾乎無法完成 。
the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界在這時此刻正忙著想方案 , 要盡可能地減少氣體排放 。
it ought to be buzzing with plans to reduce the temperature , and with plans to live at the higher temperature and not at all costs , but efficiently and cheaply . and some such plans exist , things like swarms of mirrors in space to deflect the sunlight away , and encouraging aquatic organisms to eat more carbon dioxide .	可以大幅降低溫度 , 規劃可以大幅降低溫度 , 規劃可以降低溫度 , 不計代價地降低溫度 , 但是效率又便宜 。 有些規劃會存在 , 比如在太空中一大群鏡子 , 來將陽光偏移 , 並鼓勵水族有機體來吃更多二氧化碳 。
at the moment , these things are fringe research .	此時此刻 , 這些都是邊緣的研究 。
they're not central to the human effort to face this problem , or problems in general .	他們不是人類努力解決這個問題的核心 , 也不是一般性的問題 。
and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	帶著我們還沒意識到的問題 , 我們有能力正確的做法 , 不是無限期地避開好運 , 是我們唯一的希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 還包括生存 。
so take two stone tablets , and carve on them .	拿兩個石板 , 刻在上面 。
on one of them , carve: " problems are soluble . "	其中一塊刻上 " 問題是可以解決的 "
and on the other one carve: " problems are inevitable . "	另外一塊刻上 " 問題是不可避免的 "
how can a struggling country break out of poverty if it's trapped in a system of bad rules ? economist paul romer unveils a bold idea: " charter cities , " cityscale administrative zones governed by a coalition of nations .	一個掙扎的國家如何擺脫貧窮 , 如果它被困在不良規則的體制中 ? 經濟學家保羅•羅默發出一個大膽的想法: 「 特區城市 」 、 「 城市 」 的行政區 , 是由國家聯盟統治的 。
business , culture , economics , global issues , politics	商業、文化、經濟、全球議題、政治、政治 ,
paul romer's radical idea: charter cities	保羅•羅默極端的想法:特區城市 。
take a look at this picture .	看看這張照片 。
it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	它為我們帶來了一個非常迷人的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生在做功課在首都機場的路燈下因為他們家裡沒有電
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	我還沒見過這些特別的學生 , 但我見過像他們一樣的學生 。
let's just pick one for example , the one in the green shirt .	讓我們挑個例子 , 綠襯衫裡的那個 。
let's give him a name , too: nelson .	我們給他一個名字:尼爾森 。
i'll bet nelson has a cellphone .	我打賭nelson有支手機 。
so here is the puzzle .	所以謎題來了 。
why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼尼爾森可以使用像手機這樣尖端的科技但在家中卻無法使用一百年的科技來產生電燈 ?
now , in a word , the answer is " rules . "	簡單來說 , 答案是 「 規則 」 。
bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	不良的規則可以防止雙贏解決方案的產生 , 只要人們可以把新科技帶進像尼爾森這樣的人就可以使用 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼樣的規則 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	這個國家的電力公司遵循一條規則 , 它必須以非常低、補貼的價格銷售電力 , 事實上 , 它的價格非常低 , 賣掉的每一單位都要付出很低 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它既沒有資源 , 也沒有動機去幫許多用戶配電 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看到 , 有可能有不同的規則、規則 , 讓企業獲利不大 , 所以他們有動機去註冊更多客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這是尼爾森為他的電信公司購買的那種規則 , 從操作的下面 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統知道這些規則如何運作得很好 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電價制定的規則 , 但卻陷入了來自企業和消費者的抗議當中 , 他們想保存既有的補助制度 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他所遵守的規則 , 阻止了他讓雙贏解決方案幫助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在路燈下讀書 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰在於 , 我們要想出如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	我們能發展出一些規則來改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我認為有一種抽象的見解可以使實用化 , 那就是 , 如果我們能給人民更多的選擇 , 對許多國家的領導者 , 更多的選擇也是人 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但展示出這兩者之間的對立是很有用的 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導者的那種選擇 , 像是給總統提高電價的選擇 , 讓經濟的人民想要的這個選擇離開了 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望選擇繼續使用補貼的電力 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你只給一邊或另一邊 , 你會有張力或摩擦力 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能想辦法給雙方更多的選擇 , 那就給予我們一套規則 , 來改變那些使我們脫離陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	尼爾森也能接觸到網路 。
and he says that if you want to see the damaging effects of rules , the ways that rules can keep people in the dark , look at the pictures from nasa of the earth at night .	他說如果你想看到規則所造成的損害 , 規則可以讓人們待在黑暗中 , 看看美國太空總署拍的照片 ,
in particular check out asia .	特別是亞洲 。
if you zoom in here , you can see north korea , in outline here , which is like a black hole compared to its neighbors .	如果你放大這裡 , 你可以看到北韓 , 在這塊線上 , 和旁邊的黑洞相比 , 它就像是個黑洞 。
now , you won't be surprised to learn that the rules in north korea keep people there in the dark .	現在 , 你不會驚訝地發現北韓的規則總是把人放在黑暗中 。
but it is important to recognize that north korea and south korea started out with identical sets of rules in both the sense of laws and regulations , but also in the deeper senses of understandings , norms , culture , values and beliefs .	但值得注意的是 , 北韓和南韓開始時用的是同一套規則 , 不論是法律或法規 , 更深層的方面要了解、規範、文化、價值觀和信念 。
when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做了一些決定 , 導致他們一些規則上的分歧道路 。
so we can change we as humans can change the rules that we use to interact with each other , for better , or for worse .	我們可以改變身為人類的我們 , 可以改變彼此互動的規則 , 不論是好是壞 。
now let's look at another region , the caribbean .	現在我們來看看另一個加勒比海地區 。
zoom in on haiti , in outline here .	放大海地的畫面 , 在這裡 。
haiti is also dark , compared to its neighbor here , the dominican republic , which has about the same number of residents .	海地也很黑 , 相較於這裡的鄰居多明尼加共和國數量也差不多
both of these countries are dark compared to puerto rico , which has half as many residents as either haiti or the dominican republic .	這兩個國家 , 相較於波多黎各 , 波多黎各有一半的居民是像海地或多明尼加共和國 。
what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地警告我們的是 , 規則可能很糟 , 因為政府很軟弱 。
it's not just that the rules are bad because the government is too strong and oppressive , as in north korea .	不光是這些規則不好 , 因為政府的強勢和壓迫性太強 , 就像北韓的情況一樣 。
so that if we want to create environments with good rules , we can't just tear down .	所以如果我們想要創造有良好規則的環境 , 我們不能只是破壞 。
we've got to find ways to build up , as well .	我們也必須想辦法建設 ,
now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	如今 , 中國戲劇性地展現出運用規則所帶來的潛力和挑戰 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到剛開始的資料 , 中國是世界上的高科技領袖 。
chinese had pioneered technologies like steel , printing , gunpowder .	中國人的科技像煉鋼、印刷、火藥等都是先驅
but the chinese never adopted , at least in that period , effective rules for encouraging the spread of those ideas a profit motive that could have encouraged the spread .	但中國人從來沒有採用 , 至少在那個時期 , 有效的規則中 , 鼓勵那些想法散播出去 , 這是一個利潤動機 , 可以鼓勵傳播出去 。
and they soon adopted rules which slowed down innovation and cut china off from the rest of the world .	他們很快就採用了規則 , 放慢了創新 , 阻斷了中國和世界其他地方 。
so as other countries in the world innovated , in the sense both of developing newer technologies , but also developing newer rules , the chinese were cut off from those advances .	所以 , 隨著世界上其他國家的創新 , 在發展新科技的同時 , 也發展出更新的規則 , 中國也被這些進展阻斷了 。
income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	收入停滯不前 , 因為它放大了世界的另一端 。
this next chart looks at more recent data .	下一張圖表是比較近期的資料 。
it plots income , average income in china as a percentage of average income in the united states .	顯示的是中國的平均所得佔美國平均所得的百分比
in the '50s and '60s you can see that it was hovering at about three percent .	在50、60年代 , 你可以看到這個數字大約在百分之三左右 。
but then in the late '70s something changed .	但到了70年代末期 , 情況改變了 。
growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	中國經濟開始起飛中國人開始迎頭趕上美國
if you go back to the map at night , you can get a clue to the process that lead to the dramatic change in rules in china .	如果你回到夜裡的地圖你會發現這個過程導致中國體制的巨大改變
the brightest spot in china , which you can see on the edge of the outline here , is hong kong .	中國最亮的點你們可以在輪廓邊上看到 , 就是香港 。
hong kong was a small bit of china that , for most of the 20th century , operated under a very different set of rules than the rest of mainland china rules that were copied from working market economies of the time , and administered by the british .	香港是中國少數的點子 , 在20世紀大部份的時候 , 都採用非常不同的規則 , 相較於當時其他的中國大陸規則 , 其制度是來自當時的勞動市場經濟 , 由英國政府行政 。
in the 1950s , hong kong was a place where millions of people could go , from the mainland , to start in jobs like sewing shirts , making toys .	在1950年代 , 香港是一個數百萬人可以去的地方 , 從大陸開始 , 像是縫衣服 , 做玩具 。
but , to get on a process of increasing income , increasing skills led to very rapid growth there .	但 , 為了能進一步增加收入 , 增加技能 , 導致非常快速的成長 。
hong kong was also the model which leaders like deng xiaoping could copy , when they decided to move all of the mainland towards the market model .	香港當時也是一個模式讓像鄧小平這樣的領導者能夠複製 , 當他們決定將整個大陸推向市場模式時 。
but deng xiaoping instinctively understood the importance of offering choices to his people .	但鄧小平直覺地了解到提供人民選擇的重要性 。
so instead of forcing everyone in china to shift immediately to the market model , they proceeded by creating some special zones that could do , in a sense , what britain did: make the opportunity to go work with the market rules available to the people who wanted to opt in there .	所以 , 與其強迫所有人立刻轉換到市場模式 , 他們採取的做法是設立一些特區 , 從某種意義上來說 , 創造出可以實現的 , 讓英國人有機會和市場體制合作 , 讓那些想要選手的人有機會進入市場規則 。
so they created four special economic zones around hong kong: zones where chinese could come and work , and cities grew up very rapidly there ; also zones where foreign firms could come in and make things .	所以他們在香港周圍建立了四個經濟特區 , 讓中國能夠前往工作的地方 , 城市也在那裡快速成長 ; 外國企業也可以進來 , 製造東西 。
one of the zones next to hong kong has a city called shenzhen .	香港旁邊的一個區域有個叫深圳的城市 。
in that city there is a taiwanese firm that made the iphone that many of you have , and they made it with labor from chinese who moved there to shenzhen .	在那座城市中 , 有一間台灣企業 , 製造了你們很多人都擁有的iphone , 他們是靠中國人的勞力來建造的 , 搬到深圳 。
so after the four special zones , there were 14 coastal cites that were open in the same sense , and eventually demonstrated successes in these places that people could opt in to , that they flocked to because of the advantages they offered .	四個特區之後 , 有14個沿海城市 , 以相同的方式開放 , 最後在這些地方展示出成功 , 人民可以選擇去的地方 , 他們聚在一起 , 因為有利於提供的 。
demonstrated successes there led to a consensus for a move toward the market model for the entire economy .	那裡成功促成了全體經濟向市場模式邁進的共識 。
now the chinese example shows us several points .	中國的例子顯示了好幾點
one is: preserve choices for people .	第一 , 保存人民的選擇 。
two: operate on the right scale .	第二:運作的規模是對的 。
if you try to change the rules in a village , you could do that , but a village would be too small to get the kinds of benefits you can get if you have millions of people all working under good rules .	如果你試著改變一個村落的規則 , 你可以做到 , 但村落會太小 , 無法得到你所能得到的好處 , 如果你有數百萬人都在制度良好的規則下工作 。
on the other hand , the nation is too big .	另一方面 , 國家太大了 。
if you try to change the rules in the nation , you can't give some people a chance to hold back , see how things turn out , and let others zoom ahead and try the new rules .	如果你試著改變國家的規則 , 你就不能給一些人一個機會 , 看看事情的結果如何 , 讓其他人放大再試試新規則 。
but cities give you this opportunity to create new places , with new rules that people can opt in to .	但城市讓你有機會創造新地方 , 用人們可以遵守的新規則 。
and they're large enough to get all of the benefits that we can have when millions of us work together under good rules .	當數百萬人依靠良好的規則一起工作時 , 他們已經夠大了 , 可以取得所有我們能獲得的益處了 。
so the proposal is that we conceive of something called a charter city .	提議的是我們構思了所謂的特區城市 。
we start with a charter that specifies all the rules required to attract the people who we'll need to build the city .	一開始 , 我們規劃了各項規則 , 來吸引那些需要建造城市的人 。
we'll need to attract the investors who will build out the infrastructure the power system , the roads , the port , the airport , the buildings .	我們需要吸引投資者來建造電力系統、道路、港口、機場、建築 。
you'll need to attract firms , who will come hire the people who move there first .	首先你需要吸引公司的參與者 。
and you'll need to attract families , the residents who will come and live there permanently , raise their children , get an education for their children , and get their first job .	你需要吸引家庭 , 居民願意來永久住在那裡 , 養育他們的孩子 , 讓他們的孩子接受教育 , 取得他們的第一份工作 。
with that charter , people will move there .	隨著這一章節 , 人們會搬到那裡 。
the city can be built .	城市可以被建造起來 。
and we can scale this model .	我們可以擴大這個模式 。
we can go do it over and over again .	我們可以一遍又一遍地這樣做 。
to make it work , we need good rules . we've already discussed that .	要讓它成功 , 我們需要良好的規則 。 我們已經討論過了 。
those are captured in the charter .	那些是在憲章中被抓到的 。
we also need the choices for people .	我們也需要為人做出選擇 。
that's really built into the model if we allow for the possibility of building cities on uninhabited land .	這其實是建立在模型中 , 如果我們允許在無人居住的土地上建造城市的可能性 。
you start from uninhabited territory .	你從無人居住的領域開始 。
people can come live under the new charter , but no one is forced to live under it .	人們可以在新的憲章底下生活 , 但沒有人會被迫在它底下生活 。
the final thing we need are choices for leaders .	最後我們需要的是給領導者選擇 。
and , to achieve the kind of choices we want for leaders we need to allow for the potential for partnerships between nations: cases where nations work together , in effect , de facto , the way china and britain worked together to build , first a little enclave of the market model , and then scale it throughout china .	為了達成我們期望領導人的選擇我們需要讓國與國之間的合作可能性成為國與國之間的合作的可能例如 , 實質上 , 中國和英國的合作方式 , 首先是市場模式的一個小小的奴隸然後擴展到整個中國 。
in a sense , britain , inadvertently , through its actions in hong kong , did more to reduce world poverty than all the aid programs that we've undertaken in the last century .	在某種意義上 , 英國在不經意的 , 通過香港的行動 , 減少了世界貧窮的數量 , 比上個世紀所有援助計畫還要多 。
so if we allow for these kind of partnerships to replicate this again , we can get those kinds of benefits scaled throughout the world .	所以如果我們讓這樣的合作模式再度重現我們可以使全世界都受惠
in some cases this will involve a delegation of responsibility , a delegation of control from one country to another to take over certain kinds of administrative responsibilities .	在某些情況下 , 這會影響到負責任 , 權力由一個國家授權到另一個國家 , 來接管一些特定的行政權 。
now , when i say that , some of you are starting to think , " well , is this just bringing back colonialism ? "	現在 , 當我說這句話時 , 有些人開始想: 「 嗯 , 這只是讓殖民主義恢復嗎 ? 」
it's not . but it's important to recognize that the kind of emotions that come up when we start to think about these things , can get in the way , can make us pull back , can shut down our ability , and our interest in trying to explore new ideas .	不是的 , 但很重要的是要意識到當我們開始思考這些事情時產生的那種情緒可能會阻礙我們撤退 , 終結我們的能力和探索新想法的興趣
why is this not like colonialism ?	為什麼這和殖民主義不同 ?
the thing that was bad about colonialism , and the thing which is residually bad in some of our aid programs , is that it involved elements of coercion and condescension .	殖民主義不好的地方在於 , 在我們的一些援助計畫中 , 還剩下一個問題 , 那就是它和強制和優越的元素有關 。
this model is all about choices , both for leaders and for the people who will live in these new places .	這種模式的重點在於選擇 , 包括在這些新地方的領袖和人民 。
and , choice is the antidote to coercion and condescension .	而 「 選擇 」 是強制和優越的解藥 。
so let's talk about how this could play out in practice .	咱們來談談 , 要如何實現它 。
let's take a particular leader , raul castro , who is the leader of cuba .	咱們來看看特定的領袖raulcastro , 他是古巴的領袖 。
it must have occurred to castro that he has the chance to do for cuba what deng xiaoping did for china , but he doesn't have a hong kong there on the island in cuba .	卡斯楚一定也想過他有機會為古巴做到像鄧小平為中國所做的事但他在古巴沒有香港
he does , though , have a little bit of light down in the south that has a very special status .	不過他在南方的燈光很亮 , 它的地位很特別 。
there is a zone there , around guantanamo bay , where a treaty gives the united states administrative responsibility for a piece of land that's about twice the size of manhattan .	在關塔那摩灣周圍有一區 , 在那裡有條約為美國政府負責一塊土地 , 大約是曼哈頓的兩倍大 。
castro goes to the prime minister of canada and says , " look , the yankees have a terrible pr problem .	卡斯楚跑去找加拿大總理對他說: 「 看 , 南基斯有個嚴重的公關問題 。
they want to get out .	他們想要逃離 。
why don't you , canada , take over ?	你為什麼不 , 加拿大接管呢 ?
build run a special administrative zone .	建立一個特殊行政區 。
allow a new city to be built up there .	在那裡建造一座新城市 。
allow many people to come in .	讓許多人進來 。
let us have a hong kong nearby .	讓我們附近有一個香港 。
some of my citizens will move into that city as well .	我的一些市民也會搬進那個城市 。
others will hold back . but this will be the gateway that will connect the modern economy and the modern world to my country . "	其他人會退一步 , 但這將會是一座通往現代經濟和世界的通往我的國家的大道 。 」
now , where else might this model be tried ?	這個模型還能在哪裡試呢 ?
well , africa . i've talked with leaders in africa .	非洲 , 我和非洲的領導人談過 。
many of them totally get the notion of a special zone that people can opt into as a rule .	當中許多人完全了解特區的想法 , 讓大家可以選擇成一條規則 。
it's a rule for changing rules .	它是改變規則的規則 。
it's a way to create new rules , and let people optin without coercion , and the opposition that coercion can force .	它是一種創造新規則的方法 , 讓人民選擇沒有強制性 , 和強制性的反對力量也能引起強制作用 。
they also totally get the idea that in some instances they can make more credible promises to longterm investors the kind of investors who will come build the port , build the roads , in a new city they can make more credible promises if they do it along with a partner nation .	他們也完全了解 , 在某些情況下 , 他們可以對長期投資者做出更有保障的承諾 , 就像投資者會來蓋港口、建造道路、在新城市中 , 如果他們能和國家合作 , 做出更有保障的承諾 。
perhaps even in some arrangement that's a little bit like an escrow account , where you put land in the escrow account and the partner nation takes responsibility for it .	也許在某些安排有點像信託管理帳戶你把土地放在信託管理帳戶裡而合夥的國家也為此負責
there is also lots of land in africa where new cities could be built .	非洲還有很多的土地可以建造新城市 。
this is a picture i took when i was flying along the coast .	這是我沿著海岸飛行時照的照片 。
there are immense stretches of land like this land where hundreds of millions of people could live .	像這樣一大片延伸出去的土地上千萬人可以住在那裡 。
now , if we generalize this and think about not just one or two charter cites , but dozens cities that will help create places for the many hundreds of millions , perhaps billions of people who will move to cities in the coming century is there enough land for them ?	現在 , 如果我們簡化一下 , 不要只考慮一兩個特區的城市 , 而是數十個城市 , 能為數億人創造空間 , 也許未來的數十億人會住進都市 , 有足夠的土地容納他們嗎 ?
well , throughout the world , if we look at the lights at night , the one thing that's misleading is that , visually , it looks like most of the world is already built out .	在全世界 , 如果我們看夜裡的燈光 , 唯一誤導人的是 , 視覺上來看 , 世界上大部分的地區都已經被建造出來了 。
so let me show you why that's wrong .	讓我告訴你為什麼那是錯的 。
take this representation of all of the land .	以這塊地為例 。
turn it into a square that stands for all the arable land on earth .	把它變成一個方塊代表地球上所有的可耕地
and let these dots represent the land that's already taken up by the cities that three billion people now live in .	這些點代表的是有三十億人口居住的城市已經佔據了土地 。
if you move the dots down to the bottom of the rectangle you can see that the cities for the existing three billion urban residents take up only three percent of the arable land on earth .	如果你把這些點移到這個長方形的底部你會發現有30億人口的城市只佔了地球上可耕地面積的3%
so if we wanted to build cities for another billion people , they would be dots like this .	所以如果我們想再為數十億人建造城市 , 會是像這樣的點 。
we'd go from three percent of the arable land , to four percent .	我們從百分之三的可耕地發展到百分之四
we'd dramatically reduce the human footprint on earth by building more cities that people can move to .	我們會大大地減少地球上的人類足跡 , 做法是建立更多人們可以移動的城市 。
and if these are cities governed by good rules , they can be cities where people are safe from crime , safe from disease and bad sanitation , where people have a chance to get a job .	如果這些城市遵守良好的規則 , 它們可以是城市的居民安全 , 不受犯罪、疾病和衛生條件影響 , 人們就有機會找到工作 。
they can get basic utilities like electricity .	像是電力這種基本公共事業
their kids can get an education .	他們的孩子可以接受教育 。
so what will it take to get started building the first charter cities , scaling this so we build many more ?	所以 , 要建造第一個特區城市 , 要如何擴大規模 , 才能建造出更多這樣的城市 ?
it would help to have a manual .	一本手冊就更好了 。
what university professors could do is write some details that might go into this manual .	大學教授們能做的是為這本手冊撰寫一些細節 。
you wouldn't want to let us run the cities , go out and design them .	你不會想讓我們管理城市 , 到外面設計它們 。
you wouldn't let academics out in the wild .	你不會把學者趕出野外 。
but , you could set us to work thinking about questions like , suppose it isn't just canada that does the deal with raul castro .	但 , 你可以讓我們去思考一些問題 , 比如 , 不光是加拿大的問題 , 就能解決卡斯楚的問題 。
perhaps brazil comes in as a participant , and spain as well . and perhaps cuba wants to be one of the partners in a fourway joint venture .	也許巴西也加入參與者和西班牙 。 也許古巴也想成為四邊合作的一員 。
how would we write the treaty to do that ?	我們要如何寫條約來做到這一點 ?
there is less precedent for that , but that could easily be worked out .	沒有什麼先例可以解決 , 但那很容易就會被解決 。
how would we finance this ?	我們該如何去籌錢 ?
turns out singapore and hong kong are cities that made huge gains on the value of the land that they owned when they got started .	事實證明 , 新加坡和香港是在一開始就靠他們自己的土地獲得了巨大收益的城市 。
you could use the gains on the value of the land to pay for things like the police , the courts , but the school system and the health care system too , which make this a more attractive place to live , makes this a place where people have higher incomes which , incidentally , makes the land more valuable .	你可以用得到的錢來支付像警察、法庭等費用的費用 , 但學校體系和健康照護體系 , 這使得居住環境更吸引人 , 使居民的收入更高 , 更加珍貴 。
so the incentives for the people helping to construct this zone and build it , and set up the basic rules , go very much in the right direction .	所以 , 對於協助建造這塊區域的人的獎勵 , 建立它 , 並建立基礎規則 , 非常能走向正確的方向 。
so there are many other details like this .	還有很多其他的細節
how could we have buildings that are low cost and affordable for people who work in a first job , assembling something like an iphone , but make those buildings energy efficient , and make sure that they are safe , so they don't fall down in an earthquake or a hurricane .	我們如何讓一開始工作的人 , 擁有低成本且負擔得起的建築 , 例如iphone , 卻能讓建築節能 , 確保它們安全 , 不會落在地震或颶風中 。
many technical details to be worked out , but those of us who are already starting to pursue these things can already tell that there is no roadblock , there's no impediment , other than a failure of imagination , that will keep us from delivering on a truly global winwin solution .	許多技術細節尚待處理但我們這些已經開始追求這些事的人早已發現除了缺點想像沒有其他東西可以阻礙我們傳播一個真正的全球雙贏解決方案
let me conclude with this picture .	讓我用這張照片作結 。
the reason we can be so well off , even though there is so many people on earth , is because of the power of ideas .	儘管地球上有這麼多人 , 我們之所以能這麼幸福 , 是因為想法的力量 。
we can share ideas with other people , and when they discover them , they share with us .	我們可以和別人分享想法 , 當他們發現他們時 , 他們會和我們分享 。
it's not like scarce objects , where sharing means we each get less .	它不像稀有物品 , 分享意味著我們每個人都會變少 。
when we share ideas we all get more .	當我們分享想法時 , 我們都會得到更多 。
when we think about ideas in that way , we usually think about technologies .	當我們以這種方式思考想法時 , 我們通常想到的是科技 。
but there is another class of ideas: the rules that govern how we interact with each other ; rules like , let's have a tax system that supports a research university that gives away certain kinds of knowledge for free .	但還有另一類想法:主導我們彼此如何互動的規則 ; 規則像是:我們有稅制系統 , 支撐研究大學 , 免費提供某種知識 。
let's have a system where we have ownership of land that is registered in a government office , that people can pledge as collateral .	讓我們有一個土地制度 , 在政府辦公室註冊的土地 , 人民可以承諾為抵押抵押品 。
if we can keep innovating on our space of rules , and particularly innovate in the sense of coming up with rules for changing rules , so we don't get stuck with bad rules , then we can keep moving progress forward and truly make the world a better place , so that people like nelson and his friends don't have to study any longer under the streetlights . thank you .	如果我們能不斷創新我們的規則 , 尤其是在創造改變規則的基礎上 , 這樣我們就不會卡在不良的規則中 , 那麼我們就能不斷進步 , 真正讓世界變得更好 , 像尼爾森和他的朋友不再需要在路燈下學習 。 謝謝 。
genomics pioneer craig venter takes a break from his epic roundtheworld expedition to talk about the millions of genes his team has discovered so far in its quest to map the ocean’s biodiversity .	克雷格.凡特 , 基因學先驅者從他的史詩般的圓環探險中休息了一會兒 , 探討他的團隊目前發現的數百萬個基因 , 來繪製海洋的生物多樣性 。
dna , biosphere , biotech , entrepreneur , genetics , invention , oceans , science , technology	dna、生物圈、企業家、遺傳學、發明、海洋、科技、科技、科技、
craig venter on dna and the sea	克萊格•凡特在dna和海洋上 ,
at the break , i was asked by several people about my comments about the aging debate .	演講結束前 , 有幾個人問我對老化辯論的看法 。
and this will be my only comment on it .	而這是我唯一對此的評論 。
and that is , i understand that optimists greatly outlive pessimists .	那就是 , 我了解樂觀的人比悲觀者活得更久 。
what i'm going to tell you about in my 18 minutes is how we're about to switch from reading the genetic code to the first stages of beginning to write the code ourselves .	我在18分鐘內要告訴你們的是我們如何從閱讀基因編碼轉換到開始自己寫程式的第一階段
it's only 10 years ago this month when we published the first sequence of a freeliving organism , that of haemophilus influenzae .	僅僅是10年前的一個月 , 我們發表了第一組免費生存有機體的序列 , 即嗜血桿菌 。
that took a genome project from 13 years down to four months .	這項計畫花了13年才完成 , 才四個月 。
we can now do that same genome project in the order of two to eight hours .	我們現在可以在兩到八小時內完成同樣的基因計畫 。
so in the last decade , a large number of genomes have been added: most human pathogens , a couple of plants , several insects and several mammals , including the human genome .	所以 , 在過去十年間 , 大量的基因組被加上:大部分的人類病原體 , 幾種植物 , 幾隻昆蟲和幾種哺乳類動物 , 包括人類基因組 。
genomics at this stage of the thinking from a little over 10 years ago was , by the end of this year , we might have between three and five genomes sequenced ; it's on the order of several hundred .	十年前 , 在這個階段的基因組學就已經到了今年底 , 我們可能已經完成了三到五組基因組的測序 , 已經完成了數百組 。
we just got a grant from the gordon and betty moore foundation to sequence 130 genomes this year , as a side project from environmental organisms .	我們剛從grdon和bettymoore基金會獲得一項補助 , 今年我們已經完成了130組基因組的測序 , 做為環境生物的附屬計畫 。
so the rate of reading the genetic code has changed .	所以 , 閱讀基因編碼的速度已經改變了 。
but as we look , what's out there , we've barely scratched the surface on what is available on this planet .	但 , 根據我們的觀察 , 外面有什麼 , 我們幾乎沒有找到地球上能找到的物體表面 。
most people don't realize it , because they're invisible , but microbes make up about a half of the earth's biomass , whereas all animals only make up about one onethousandth of all the biomass .	大部分人不知道 , 因為它們是看不見的 , 但微生物佔地球生物總量的一半 , 所有的動物只占所有生物總量的1/0 。
and maybe it's something that people in oxford don't do very often , but if you ever make it to the sea , and you swallow a mouthful of seawater , keep in mind that each milliliter has about a million bacteria and on the order of 10 million viruses .	也許在牛津的人們通常不會這樣做 , 但如果你去海邊 , 吞一口海水 , 請記住每一毫升的海水中都有大約一百萬個細菌和大約一千萬個病毒 。
less than 5 , 000 microbial species have been characterized as of two years ago , and so we decided to do something about it .	到兩年前 , 只有少於5000種微生物已被定型 , 所以我們決定採取行動 。
and we started the sorcerer ii expedition , where we were , as with great oceanographic expeditions , trying to sample the ocean every 200 miles .	我們開始了第二次的飛行探險 , 就像偉大的海洋探險 , 試圖每200英里就取樣海洋 。
we started in bermuda for our test project , then moved up to halifax , working down the u . s . east coast , the caribbean sea , the panama canal , through to the galapagos , then across the pacific , and we're in the process now of working our way across the indian ocean .	我們從百慕達開始進行我們的考試計畫 , 接著移到哈利法克斯 , 沿著美國東岸 , 加勒比海 , 巴拿馬運河 , 穿過加拉巴哥群島 , 橫跨太平洋 , 現在我們正在橫越印度洋的途中 。
it's very tough duty ; we're doing this on a sailing vessel , in part to help excite young people about going into science .	這是很艱難的任務 ; 我們在帆船上這麼做 , 有一部分原因是要讓年輕人興奮進入科學領域 。
the experiments are incredibly simple .	實驗非常簡單 。
we just take seawater and we filter it , and we collect different size organisms on different filters , and then take their dna back to our lab in rockville , where we can sequence a hundred million letters of the genetic code every 24 hours .	我們只是把海水和過濾器拿起來 , 用不同的濾器收集不同的大小生物 , 接著 , 將它們的dna帶回我們在洛克維爾的實驗室 , 在那裡 , 我們可以每24小時完成一億個字母的基因編碼 。
and with doing this , we've made some amazing discoveries .	通過這樣做 , 我們有了驚人的發現 。
for example , it was thought that the visual pigments that are in our eyes there was only one or two organisms in the environment that had these same pigments .	例如 , 人們認為我們眼中的視覺色素環境中只有一兩種有機體擁有相同的色素
it turns out , almost every species in the upper parts of the ocean in warm parts of the world have these same photoreceptors , and use sunlight as the source of their energy and communication .	結果發現 , 世界上溫暖區域的所有物種 , 都有相同的光感接收器 , 以太陽為能源和溝通來源 。
from one site , from one barrel of seawater , we discovered 1 . 3 million new genes and as many as 50 , 000 new species .	從一個地方 , 從一桶海水中 , 我們發現了130萬種新基因 , 多達5萬種新物種 。
we've extended this to the air now with a grant from the sloan foundation .	我們已經從史隆基金會的補助金 , 將它延伸到空氣中 。
we're measuring how many viruses and bacteria all of us are breathing in and out every day , particularly on airplanes or closed auditoriums .	我們正在測量我們每天所呼吸的病毒和細菌數量 , 特別是在飛機上或密閉的會堂中 。
we filter through some simple apparatuses ; we collect on the order of a billion microbes from just a day filtering on top of a building in new york city .	我們透過一些簡單的儀器過濾 ; 我們僅僅在紐約市的一棟大樓頂層蒐集十億微生物的數量 。
and we're in the process of sequencing all that at the present time .	而我們正處於目前所有定序的過程中 。
just on the data collection side , just where we are through the galapagos , we're finding that almost every 200 miles , we see tremendous diversity in the samples in the ocean .	在收集資料方面 , 我們穿過加拉巴哥群島的地方 , 我們發現幾乎每隔200英里 , 我們在海裡看到巨大的多樣性 。
some of these make logical sense , in terms of different temperature gradients .	其中有些是合乎邏輯的 , 不同溫度差異的 。
so this is a satellite photograph based on temperatures red being warm , blue being cold and we found there's a tremendous difference between the warm water samples and the cold water samples , in terms of abundant species .	這是一張以溫度為基礎的衛星照片-紅色是溫暖的 , 藍色則是冷的-我們發現溫暖的水樣本和冰冷的水樣本有很大的差別 , 就豐富物種而言 。
the other thing that surprised us quite a bit is these photoreceptors detect different wavelengths of light , and we can predict that based on their amino acid sequence .	另一件令人驚訝的是這些色素細胞偵測不同波長的光線 , 我們可以根據它們的氨基酸序列預測出來 。
and these vary tremendously from region to region .	這些變化從地區到地區都極為不同 。
maybe not surprisingly , in the deep ocean , where it's mostly blue , the photoreceptors tend to see blue light .	或許不意外 , 在深海裡 , 大部分是藍色的光接受器 , 會看見藍色的光線 。
when there's a lot of chlorophyll around , they see a lot of green light .	當周圍有大量葉綠素時 , 它們會看到很多綠光 。
but they vary even more , possibly moving towards infrared and ultraviolet in the extremes .	但它們的變化可能更大 , 朝向紅外線和紫外線的狀況邁進 。
just to try and get an assessment of what our gene repertoire was , we assembled all the data including all of ours thus far from the expedition , which represents more than half of all the gene data on the planet and it totaled around 29 million genes .	為了評估我們的基因序列 , 我們集合了目前所有的資料 , 包括我們地球上一半以上的基因資料 , 總共包含了2億9千萬個基因 。
and we tried to put these into gene families to see what these discoveries are: are we just discovering new members of known families , or are we discovering new families ?	我們試著把這些放到基因家庭中 , 看看這些發現是什麼:我們發現了已知家庭的新成員 , 還是我們發現了新的家庭 ?
and it turns out we have about 50 , 000 major gene families , but every new sample we take in the environment adds in a linear fashion to these new families .	結果發現 , 我們有大約五萬個主要的基因族群 , 但我們在環境中所採集的每一個新樣本 , 都是以線性的方式 , 為這些新家庭所提供的 。
so we're at the earliest stages of discovery about basic genes , components and life on this planet .	所以 , 我們正處於發現基礎基因的最初階段 , 在這個星球上組成和生命的階段 。
when we look at the socalled evolutionary tree , we're up on the upper righthand corner with the animals .	當我們看到所謂的演化樹 , 我們就在右上角 , 和動物一起 。
of those roughly 29 million genes , we only have around 24 , 000 in our genome .	在大約兩億九千萬個基因中 , 我們的基因只有大約兩萬四千個 。
and if you take all animals together , we probably share less than 30 , 000 and probably maybe a dozen or more thousand different gene families .	如果你把所有動物放在一起 , 我們的基因族群大概只有不到三萬隻 , 也許是十多個以上 。
i view that these genes are now not only the design components of evolution .	現在我認為這些基因不僅僅是進化的設計元素 。
and we think in a genecentric view maybe going back to richard dawkins' ideas than in a genomecentric view , which are different constructs of these gene components .	我們從基因中心角度想 , 或許回到了理查•達金斯的想法 , 而不是基因組中心的觀點 , 這觀點不同於這些基因組成的構造 。
synthetic dna , the ability to synthesize dna , has changed at sort of the same pace that dna sequencing has over the last decade or two , and is getting very rapid and very cheap .	製造dna的能力和dna定序的速度差不多 , 和dna測序技術過去十年或二十年的速度差不多 , 而且成本很低 。
our first thought about synthetic genomics came when we sequenced the second genome back in 1995 , and that from mycoplasma genitalium .	我們對人造基因組學的第一個想法是當我們在1995年完成第二組基因組測序時 , 那是從mycoplas生殖器中得到的 。
and we have really nice tshirts that say , you know , " i heart my genitalium . "	我們有很棒的t恤 , 上面說: 「 我愛我的生殖器 。 」
this is actually just a microorganism .	這其實只是一種微生物 。
but it has roughly 500 genes .	但它有大約500個基因 。
haemophilus had 1 , 800 genes .	嗜血桿菌有1800個基因 。
and we simply asked the question , if one species needs 800 , another 500 , is there a smaller set of genes that might comprise a minimal operating system ?	我們會問 , 如果一個物種需要八百種 , 再加上五百種 , 有沒有一組比較小的基因 , 會是由最小的運作系統所組成 ?
so we started doing transposon mutagenesis .	所以我們開始進行轉位子突變 。
transposons are just small pieces of dna that randomly insert in the genetic code .	轉位子就是隨機插入基因編碼的一小段dna 。
and if they insert in the middle of the gene , they disrupt its function .	如果插入基因的正中間 , 就會阻斷其功能 。
so we made a map of all the genes that could take transposon insertions and we called those " nonessential genes . "	所以我們做了一張所有可以接受轉位子插入的基因圖譜 , 我們稱之為 「 非必要基因 」 。
but it turns out the environment is very critical for this , and you can only define an essential or nonessential gene based on exactly what's in the environment .	但事實證明環境是非常重要的 , 你只能依據環境的特性來定義一個必要或非必要的基因 。
we also tried to take a more directly intellectual approach with the genomes of 13 related organisms , and we tried to compare all of those , to see what they had in common .	我們還嘗試了更直接的方法來研究13種相似有機體的基因組 , 我們試著比較這些基因組 , 看看它們有什麼共通點 。
and we got these overlapping circles . and we found only 173 genes common to all 13 organisms .	我們找到了重疊的圓圈 。 我們找到了173個基因 , 共有13個有機體 。
the pool expanded a little bit if we ignored one intracellular parasite ; it expanded even more when we looked at core sets of genes of around 310 or so .	如果我們忽略一種細胞寄生蟲的話 , 池塘會稍微擴大一點 , 當我們研究核心基因組時 , 大約310組左右 。
so we think that we can expand or contract genomes , depending on your point of view here , to maybe 300 to 400 genes from the minimal of 500 .	所以我們認為我們可以根據你們的觀點 , 擴大或收縮基因組 , 擴展到約300到400個基因 , 從500個最小的基因 。
the only way to prove these ideas was to construct an artificial chromosome with those genes in them , and we had to do this in a cassettebased fashion .	要證明這些想法的唯一方法 , 就是用那些基因建造一個人造的染色體 , 我們必須以一種模塊式的方式來做 。
we found that synthesizing accurate dna in large pieces was extremely difficult .	我們發現 , 合成大型dna是極為困難的 。
ham smith and clyde hutchison , my colleagues on this , developed an exciting new method that allowed us to synthesize a 5 , 000base pair virus in only a twoweek period that was 100 percent accurate , in terms of its sequence and its biology .	hamsmith和clydehutchison , 我的同事們 , 研發出令人振奮的新方法 , 讓我們能在兩週內製造出5000個鹼基對的病毒 , 只精確到100%的準確度 , 且是它的生物學 。
it was a quite exciting experiment when we just took the synthetic piece of dna , injected it in the bacteria and all of a sudden , that dna started driving the production of the virus particles that turned around and then killed the bacteria .	這是一個相當令人興奮的實驗 , 當我們把人造的dna片段注入細菌中 , 突然間 , dna就開始驅動病毒粒子轉動並殺死細菌 。
this was not the first synthetic virus a polio virus had been made a year before but it was only one tenthousandth as active and it took three years to do .	這不是人造病毒的首次使用小兒麻痺病毒一年前被製成但是它只有原病毒1/100的活性它花了3年才完成
this is a cartoon of the structure of phi x 174 .	這是phix-174的結構 。
this is a case where the software now builds its own hardware , and that's the notions that we have with biology .	這是一個軟體能打造自身硬體的例子 , 這就是我們對生物學的概念 。
people immediately jump to concerns about biological warfare , and i had recent testimony before a senate committee , and a special committee the u . s . government has set up to review this area .	人們馬上開始關心生物戰 , 最近我在參議院委員會前發表了證詞 , 還有一個美國政府成立的專門委員會來檢視這個區域 。
and i think it's important to keep reality in mind , versus what happens with people's imaginations .	我認為 , 把現實留在心中 , 與人們的想像力比較 , 是很重要的 。
basically , any virus that's been sequenced today that genome can be made .	基本上 , 今天任何已經被定序過的病毒 , 都是可以被製造出來的 。
and people immediately freak out about things about ebola or smallpox , but the dna from this organism is not infective .	人們會對伊波拉病毒或天花感到驚恐 , 但這個有機體的dna並不具傳染性 。
so even if somebody made the smallpox genome , that dna itself would not cause infections .	所以即使製造出天花的基因組 , dna本身也不會造成感染 。
the real concern that security departments have is designer viruses .	真正讓人擔憂的是安全部門的設計師病毒 。
and there's only two countries , the u . s . and the former soviet union , that had major efforts on trying to create biological warfare agents .	僅有兩個國家 , 美國和前蘇聯 , 曾投入大量資源試圖打造生物武器元件 。
if that research is truly discontinued , there should be very little activity on the knowhow to make designer viruses in the future .	如果那些研究真的被終止了 , 在將來 , 應該不會再有任何人在製造設計病毒 。
i think singlecell organisms are possible within two years .	我認為 , 在兩年內 , 單細胞生物是可能的 。
and possibly eukaryotic cells , those that we have , are possible within a decade .	而很有可能的真核細胞 , 那些我們擁有的 , 在十年內就有可能實現的細胞 。
so we're now making several dozen different constructs , because we can vary the cassettes and the genes that go into this artificial chromosome .	我們現在正在製作數十種不同的構造 , 因為我們可以改變這些放入人造染色體的種類和基因 。
the key is , how do you put all of the others ?	關鍵是 , 如何把其他的全部都安置在一起 ?
we start with these fragments , and then we have a homologous recombination system that reassembles those into a chromosome .	我們從這些片段開始 , 然後我們有一個同源重組系統 , 將這些片段組成染色體 。
this is derived from an organism , deinococcus radiodurans , that can take three million rads of radiation and not be killed .	這源自一種生物 , 耐輻射奇異球菌 , 它能承受三百萬雷得的輻射 , 而不會被殺 。
it reassembles its genome after this radiation burst in about 12 to 24 hours , after its chromosomes are literally blown apart .	在輻射爆發後它會在12至24小時內重組自己的基因 , 在它的染色體被完全拆散後 。
this organism is ubiquitous on the planet , and exists perhaps now in outer space due to all our travel there .	這種生物在地球上普遍存在 , 可能因為我們在太空中旅行而存在 。
this is a glass beaker after about half a million rads of radiation .	這是經過50萬拉德輻射照射過後的一個玻璃杯
the glass started to burn and crack , while the microbes sitting in the bottom just got happier and happier .	玻璃開始碎裂 , 微生物的底部卻變得更快樂、更快樂 。
here's an actual picture of what happens: the top of this shows the genome after 1 . 7 million rads of radiation .	這是一張實際狀況的圖片上面的圖片顯示的是經過170萬拉德輻射後的基因組
the chromosome is literally blown apart .	染色體被完全打破了 。
and here's that same dna automatically reassembled 24 hours later .	同樣的dna在24小時後自動重新組合 。
it's truly stunning that these organisms can do that , and we probably have thousands , if not tens of thousands , of different species on this planet that are capable of doing that .	的確令人吃驚的是這些生物能夠做到這一點 , 地球上大概有成千上萬種不同的生物 , 可以做到這一點 。
after these genomes are synthesized , the first step is just transplanting them into a cell without a genome .	在這些基因組被製造之後 , 第一步就是將它們移植到一個沒有基因組的細胞中 。
so we think synthetic cells are going to have tremendous potential , not only for understanding the basis of biology but for hopefully environmental and society issues .	所以我們認為人造細胞將會有巨大的潛力 , 不僅僅是為了瞭解生物學的基礎 , 希望能對環境和社會議題有更多的了解 。
for example , from the third organism we sequenced , methanococcus jannaschii it lives in boiling water temperatures ; its energy source is hydrogen and all its carbon comes from co2 it captures back from the environment .	例如 , 從我們所測序的第三個有機體 , 珍納克斯奈兒在沸騰的水溫中生存 。 它的能量來源是氫 , 它所捕捉的二氧化碳來自環境 。
so we know lots of different pathways , thousands of different organisms now that live off of co2 , and can capture that back .	我們知道許多不同的途徑 , 數以千計不同的生物以二氧化碳為生 , 可以追溯回來 。
so instead of using carbon from oil for synthetic processes , we have the chance of using carbon and capturing it back from the atmosphere , converting that into biopolymers or other products .	與其從石油中提取人工合成過程中的碳 , 我們有機會從大氣中捕捉它 , 轉化成生物高分子或其他產品 。
we have one organism that lives off of carbon monoxide , and we use as a reducing power to split water to produce hydrogen and oxygen .	我們有一種生物 , 存在於一氧化碳之外 , 我們用水來當作減少的力量 , 來分解水來產生氫和氧 。
also , there's numerous pathways that can be engineered metabolizing methane .	此外 , 還有許多通路可以改造成甲烷代謝 。
and dupont has a major program with statoil in norway to capture and convert the methane from the gas fields there into useful products .	dupont在挪威使用石油作為補充及轉化因天然氣田裡的甲烷成為有用的產品
within a short while , i think there's going to be a new field called " combinatorial genomics , " because with these new synthesis capabilities , these vast gene array repertoires and the homologous recombination , we think we can design a robot to make maybe a million different chromosomes a day .	不久之後 , 我認為就會有一個新的領域叫做 「 組合基因組學 」 , 因為有了這些新的合成能力 , 這些廣大的基因陣列 , 以及同源重組 , 我們認為我們可以設計一個機器人 , 每天可以製造也許一百萬種不同的染色體 。
and therefore , as with all biology , you get selection through screening , whether you're screening for hydrogen production , or chemical production , or just viability .	因此 , 正如所有生物學一樣 , 通過篩選可以達到目的 , 不論是用氫氣生產 , 或化學生產 , 或只是可行性 。
to understand the role of these genes is going to be well within reach .	要了解這些基因所扮演的角色 , 將是非常容易的 。
we're trying to modify photosynthesis to produce hydrogen directly from sunlight .	我們試著修改光合作用從陽光直接產生氫氣 。
photosynthesis is modulated by oxygen , and we have an oxygeninsensitive hydrogenase that we think will totally change this process .	光合作用是由氧氣來調節的 , 我們認為有一種氧敏感的氫氣 , 將會完全改變這個過程 。
we're also combining cellulases , the enzymes that break down complex sugars into simple sugars and fermentation in the same cell for producing ethanol .	我們也將纖維素和分解複合糖的酵素結合成簡單糖和發酵在同一個細胞中 , 目的是產生乙醇 。
pharmaceutical production is already under way in major laboratories using microbes .	使用微生物的製藥生產已經在各大實驗室中進行 。
the chemistry from compounds in the environment is orders of magnitude more complex than our best chemists can produce .	環境中的化合物所產生的化學成份比我們所能產出的最好的化學家還要複雜許多 。
i think future engineered species could be the source of food , hopefully a source of energy , environmental remediation and perhaps replacing the petrochemical industry .	我認為未來的工程物種可以是食物的來源 , 希望是能源的來源 , 環境的補救措施 , 也許可以取代化工業 。
let me just close with ethical and policy studies .	讓我以倫理和政策的研究來結尾 。
we delayed the start of our experiments in 1999 until we completed a yearandahalf bioethical review as to whether we should try and make an artificial species .	在1999年我們延遲了實驗的開始直到我們完成了一個一年半的生物倫理審核是否應該嘗試製造一個人造物種 。
every major religion participated in this .	每一個主要的宗教都參與其中 。
it was actually a very strange study , because the various religious leaders were using their scriptures as law books , and they couldn't find anything in them prohibiting making life , so it must be ok . the only ultimate concerns were biological warfare aspects of this , but gave us the go ahead to start these experiments for the reasons we were doing them .	這真的是一項非常奇怪的研究 , 因為各種宗教領袖使用他們的教義作為法律 , 他們無法在禁止製造生命的條款中找到任何東西 , 所以這也沒關係 。 最終 , 唯一的關注是生物戰的方面 , 但也給了我們預先提供這些實驗的理由 。
right now the sloan foundation has just funded a multiinstitutional study on this , to work out what the risk and benefits to society are , and the rules that scientific teams such as my own should be using in this area , and we're trying to set good examples as we go forward .	現在sloan基金會已經資助了一個多機構的研究 , 致力於找出這方面的風險和益處 , 以及一些科學團隊 , 比如我自己應該在這個領域使用的規則 , 我們正在嘗試建立好的例子 。
these are complex issues .	這些都是複雜的問題 。
except for the threat of bioterrorism , they're very simple issues in terms of , can we design things to produce clean energy , perhaps revolutionizing what developing countries can do and provide through various simple processes .	除了生物恐怖主義威脅之外 , 它們是非常簡單的議題 , 我們是否能設計東西來產生乾淨能源 , 也許革命開發中國家能做些什麼 , 並提供各種簡單的處理方式 。
psychologist philip zimbardo says happiness and success are rooted in a trait most of us disregard: the way we orient toward the past , present and future . he suggests we calibrate our outlook on time as a first step to improving our lives .	心理學家菲利普•津巴多說 , 快樂和成功根植於我們大多數人不認同的特質:我們對過去、現在和未來的方向 。 他建議我們把前景視為改善我們人生的第一步 。
brain , business , happiness , mind , psychology , science	大腦、商業、快樂、心智、心理、心理、科學 ,
philip zimbardo prescribes a healthy take on time	菲利浦辛巴多處方一個健康的時光步驟
i want to share with you some ideas about the secret power of time , in a very short time .	我想和大家分享一些關於時光的秘密力量 , 很短的時間內 。
video: all right , start the clock please . 30 seconds studio .	影片:好了 , 開始計時 , 30秒 。
keep it quiet please . settle down .	保持安靜 , 安頓下來 。
it's about time . end sequence . take one .	時間快到了 。 快結束 。
10 , nine , eight , seven , six , five , four , three , two . . .	10、9、8、7、6、5、4、3、2......
philip zimbardo: let's tune into the conversation of the principals in adam's temptation .	菲利浦津巴多:讓我們看看這段對話:亞當的誘惑 。
" come on adam , don't be so wishywashy . take a bite . " " i did . "	「 來吧 , 亞當 , 別想要華麗 , 咬一口 。 」 我有 。
" one bite , adam . don't abandon eve . "	「 一口 , 亞當 。 不要忘了伊娃 。 」
" i don't know , guys .	「 各位 , 我不知道 。
i don't want to get in trouble . "	我不想惹上麻煩 。 」
" okay . one bite . what the hell ? "	「 好吧 , 一口 。 搞什麼鬼 ? 」
life is temptation . it's all about yielding , resisting , yes , no , now , later , impulsive , reflective , present focus and future focus .	生活充滿誘惑 。 重點是培養、抗拒 , 是的 , 現在 , 以後 , 衝動 , 關注現在 , 和未來 。
promised virtues fall prey to the passions of the moment .	保證美德會勝過當下的熱情 。
of teenage girls who pledged sexual abstinence and virginity until marriage thank you george bush the majority , 60 percent , yielded to sexual temptations within one year .	那些曾宣誓要在婚前不順的少女們 , 感謝小布希 , 大多數 , 60% , 一年內違背性別的誘惑 。
and most of them did so without using birth control .	他們大多數都沒有採取避孕措施 。
so much for promises .	太好了 。
now lets tempt fouryearolds , giving them a treat .	現在 , 讓我們來試試四歲的孩子 , 給他們吃得好 。
