they can have one marshmallow now . but if they wait until the experimenter comes back , they can have two .	現在可以有一顆棉花糖 。 但如果他們等到試驗員回來 , 他們就可以有兩顆 。
of course it pays , if you like marshmallows , to wait .	當然 , 如果你喜歡棉花糖 , 那就得等上 。
what happens is twothirds of the kids give in to temptation .	三分之二的孩子帶著誘惑的心情進入監獄 。
they cannot wait . the others , of course , wait .	他們不能等 , 其他人 , 當然 , 等等 。
they resist the temptation . they delay the now for later .	他們會抗拒誘惑 , 延後至今 。
walter mischel , my colleague at stanford , went back 14 years later , to try to discover what was different about those kids .	我在史丹佛大學的同事沃爾特•米歇爾14年後 , 試圖找出這些孩子與什麼不同之處 。
there were enormous differences between kids who resisted and kids who yielded , in many ways .	反抗的孩子和反抗的孩子在很多方面都有巨大的差異 。
the kids who resisted scored 250 points higher on the sat .	反抗的孩子在sat上得到了250分 。
that's enormous . that's like a whole set of different iq points .	這很巨大 。 這就像一整套不同的智商點 。
they didn't get in as much trouble . they were better students .	他們不會惹上那麼多麻煩 , 他們是好學生 。
they were selfconfident and determined . and the key for me today , the key for you , is , they were futurefocused rather than presentfocused .	她們是自信且堅定的 。 而今天對我來說 , 對你們來說 , 關鍵是 , 她們是以 " 將 " 為基礎 , 而非 " 以 " 為基礎 。
so what is time perspective ? that's what i'm going to talk about today .	所以 , 什麼是時間觀點 ? 這就是我今天要談的 。
time perspective is the study of how individuals , all of us , divide the flow of your human experience into time zones or time categories .	看待時間是研究個體 , 我們所有人 , 將你個人經歷的流向分為時區或時間類別 。
and you do it automatically and nonconsciously .	而且你會自動且無意識地做 。
they vary between cultures , between nations , between individuals , between social classes , between education levels .	不同文化、不同國家、不同社會階級、教育程度
and the problem is that they can become biased , because you learn to overuse some of them and underuse the others .	問題是 , 它們可能會有偏見 , 因為你會學會過度使用 , 且低估其他的部分 。
what determines any decision you make ?	你做了什麼決定 ?
you make a decision on which you're going to base an action .	你要做一個決定 , 要採取行動 。
for some people it's only about what is in the immediate situation , what other people are doing and what you're feeling .	對某些人來說 , 只有在當下情況 , 別人做的事和你的感受 。
and those people , when they make their decisions in that format we're going to call them " presentoriented , " because their focus is what is now .	而那些人 , 當他們做出那樣的決定時 , 我們會稱他們為 「 現實導向 」 , 因為他們關注的是現在 。
for others , the present is irrelevant .	對其他人來說 , 現在不重要了 。
it's always about " what is this situation like that i've experienced in the past ? "	重要的是 「 我過去曾經歷過的這種狀況是什麼樣子的 ? 」
so that their decisions are based on past memories .	他們的決策基於過去的記憶 。
and we're going to call those people " pastoriented , " because they focus on what was .	我們稱這些人為 " 懷舊主義 " , 因為他們關注的是過去 。
for others it's not the past , it's not the present , it's only about the future .	對另一些人 , 這不是過去 , 不是現在 , 而是未來 。
their focus is always about anticipated consequences .	他們專注於所期待的結果 。
we're going to call them " futureoriented . " their focus is on what will be .	我們稱他們為 「 未來導向 」 。 他們關注的是未來 。
so , time paradox , i want to argue , the paradox of time perspective , is something that influences every decision you make , you're totally unaware of .	所以 , 時間悖論 , 我想說的是時間觀點的悖論是影響你所做的每一個決定的 , 但你卻完全不知道 。
namely , the extent to which you have one of these biased time perspectives .	換句話說 , 你有著帶有偏見的時間觀點 。
well there is actually six of them . there are two ways to be presentoriented .	總共有六種 。 目前有兩種解釋方式 。
there is two ways to be pastoriented , two ways to be future .	有兩種方式可以被 " 懷舊 " , 兩種方式可以成為 " 未來 " 。
you can focus on pastpositive , or pastnegative .	你可以把焦點放在正面或負面 。
you can be presenthedonistic , namely you focus on the joys of life , or presentfatalist it doesn't matter , your life is controlled .	也可以是 " 享受主義者 " 也可以是專注於享受生活的樂趣或宿命論者這並不重要你的生活是被控制的
you can be futureoriented , setting goals .	你可以是 " 理想主義 " , 設定目標
or you can be transcendental future: namely , life begins after death .	或者你也可以是超越未來的:即生命從死後開始 。
developing the mental flexibility to shift time perspectives fluidly depending on the demands of the situation , that's what you've got to learn to do .	發展思維的靈活性 , 改變時間觀點的流暢度 , 取決於情況的需求 , 這就是你要學的 。
so , very quickly , what is the optimal time profile ?	很快地 , 什麼是最佳時光檔 ?
high on pastpositive . moderately high on future .	高度 " 正面懷舊 " , 適度 " 未來 。
and moderate on presenthedonism .	現代主義 。
and always low on pastnegative and presentfatalism .	總是把負面和現代主義降低 。
so the optimal temporal mix is what you get from the past pastpositive gives you roots . you connect your family , identity and your self .	所以 , 最佳時光的混合是你從過去積極的態度所得到的 。 將你的家人、身份和你的自我連結起來 。
what you get from the future is wings to soar to new destinations , new challenges .	未來從翅膀到翱翔到新的目的地 , 新的挑戰 。
what you get from the present hedonism is the energy , the energy to explore yourself , places , people , sensuality .	你從現在的享樂主義得到的能量就是探索你自己 , 地方 , 人 , 感性
any time perspective in excess has more negatives than positives .	任何過度的時光角度 , 其負面遠多於正面 。
what do futures sacrifice for success ?	未來要犧牲什麼才能成功 ?
they sacrifice family time . they sacrifice friend time .	他們犧牲家庭時間 , 犧牲朋友的時間 。
they sacrifice fun time . they sacrifice personal indulgence .	他們犧牲快樂時光 , 犧牲個人的沉溺 。
they sacrifice hobbies . and they sacrifice sleep . so it affects their health .	他們犧牲業餘愛好 ; 犧牲睡眠 。 這會影響到他們的健康 。
and they live for work , achievement and control .	他們活著是為了工作、成就和控制 。
i'm sure that resonates with some of the tedsters .	我相信 , 那會和一些ted成員產生共鳴 。
and it resonated for me . i grew up as a poor kid in the south bronx ghetto , a sicilian family everyone lived in the past and present .	這對我產生共鳴 。 我在南布朗克斯貧民窟長大 , 西西里島家庭 , 過去和現在都是 。
i'm here as a futureoriented person who went over the top , who did all these sacrifices because teachers intervened , and made me future oriented .	我是以未來為主的人 , 來到頂端 , 做出這些犧牲 , 因為老師介入 , 讓我有朝一日的方向 。
told me don't eat that marshmallow , because if you wait you're going to get two of them , until i learned to balance out .	告訴我不要吃那顆棉花糖 , 因為如果你等著你就會得到其中二顆 , 直到我學會去平衡 。
i've added presenthedonism , i've added a focus on the pastpositive , so , at 76 years old , i am more energetic than ever , more productive , and i'm happier than i have ever been .	現在我再加上 「 享樂主義 」 , 我把焦點放在正面 , 所以 , 在76歲時 , 我比以往更有活力 , 更有生產力 , 我比以往更開心 。
i just want to say that we are applying this to many world problems: changing the dropout rates of school kids , combating addictions , enhancing teen health , curing vets' ptsd with time metaphors getting miracle cures promoting sustainability and conservation , reducing physical rehabilitation where there is a 50percent drop out rate , altering appeals to suicidal terrorists , and modifying family conflicts as timezone clashes .	我只想說 , 我們正在把這個應用在許多世界問題上:改變輟學率 , 打擊毒品 , 提升青少年健康 , 用時間隱喻來治療退伍軍人的ptsd , 用奇蹟來治療永續性和保育 , 減少身體康復率 , 此舉減少了50%的輟學率 , 改變自殺式恐怖份子的念頭 , 以及修正家族之間的衝突 。
so i want to end by saying: many of life's puzzles can be solved by understanding your time perspective and that of others .	我想以一句話做結語:許多人生的難題都可以被解決 , 只要了解你的時間觀和他人的觀點 。
and the idea is so simple , so obvious , but i think the consequences are really profound .	想法是如此簡單 , 顯而易見 , 但我認為後果是如此深遠 。
how many of today's headlines will matter in 100 years ? 1000 ? kirk citron's " long news " project collects stories that not only matter today , but will resonate for decades even centuries to come . at ted2010 , he highlights recent headlines with the potential to shape our future .	今天的頭條有多少在一百年後才是重要的 ? 一千年後 ? 克雷克-凱特倫的 「 長新聞 」 計畫收集到這些故事 , 不但影響到今天的主題 , 還會有數十年的回響 。 在2010年的ted2010年 , 他強調了近期的頭條 , 可能影響我們未來的頭條 。
future , global issues , media , news , science	未來、全球議題、媒體、新聞、科學 ,
kirk citron: and now , the real news	kirkcitron:而現在 , 真正的新聞 。
we are drowning in news .	我們淹沒在新聞中 。
reuters alone puts out three and a half million news stories a year .	光是路透社一年就有350萬則新聞 。
that's just one source .	那只是其中一個源頭 。
my question is: how many of those stories are actually going to matter in the long run ?	我的問題是:這些故事當中有多少在長期來說是重要的 ?
that's the idea behind the long news .	那就是 「 長遠新聞 」 的想法 。
it's a project by the long now foundation , which was founded by tedsters including kevin kelly and stewart brand .	這是個長遠現在基金會的專案由tedsters所創辦包括kevinkellly和stewartbrand
and what we're looking for is news stories that might still matter 50 or 100 or 10 , 000 years from now .	我們要尋找的新聞故事可能在五、十或十萬年前仍然很重要 。
and when you look at the news through that filter , a lot falls by the wayside .	當你從那個篩選器中看新聞時 , 很多東西都倒在了 。
to take the top stories from the a . p . this last year , is this going to matter in a decade ?	拿去年美聯社的頭條新聞來說 , 十年後這還會很重要嗎 ?
is this going to matter in 50 or 100 years ?	這在50或100年後才會很重要嗎 ?
okay , that was kind of cool .	好吧 , 還滿酷的 。
but the top story of this past year was the economy , and i'm just betting that , sooner or later , this particular recession is going to be old news .	但去年的頭條是經濟 , 我敢說 , 遲早 , 這波經濟衰退將會是老式的消息 。
so , what kind of stories might make a difference for the future ?	所以 , 哪種故事對未來會造成改變 ?
well , let's take science .	嗯 , 就以科學為例 。
someday , little robots will go through our bloodstreams fixing things .	有一天 , 小機器人會穿過我們的血流 , 幫我們修理東西 。
that someday is already here if you're a mouse .	若你是老鼠 , 就已經有一天了 。
some recent stories: nanobees zap tumors with real bee venom ; they're sending genes into the brain ; a robot they built that can crawl through the human body .	最近的故事是:奈米蜜蜂用真蜂毒液殺死腫瘤 ; 它們把基因送入大腦 ; 一個他們建造的機器人 , 可以在人體爬行 。
what about resources ? how are we going to feed nine billion people ?	資源方面呢 ? 我們要如何養活90億人 ?
we're having trouble feeding six billion today .	我們今天餵飽了60億人
as we heard yesterday , there's over a billion people hungry .	正如我們昨天聽到的 , 已經有超過十億人在挨餓 。
britain will starve without genetically modified crops .	不用基因改造作物 , 英國人會餓死 。
bill gates , fortunately , has bet a billion on [agricultural] research .	幸運的是 , 比爾蓋茲投入了十億在農業研究上 。
what about global politics ?	那麼全球政治呢 ?
the world's going to be very different when and if china sets the agenda , and they may .	世界會變得非常不一樣 , 如果中國設立了 「 議程 」 , 且他們會做到 。
they've overtaken the u . s . as the world's biggest car market , they've overtaken germany as the largest exporter , and they've started doing dna tests on kids to choose their careers .	他們已經超過美國成為世界上最大的汽車市場 , 他們已經超過德國成為最大的出口國 , 他們也開始在孩子身上做dna測試 , 來選擇他們的事業 。
we're finding all kinds of ways to push back the limits of what we know .	我們正在尋找各種方法來把我們所知道的限制推回來 。
some recent discoveries: there's an ant colony from argentina that has now spread to every continent but antarctica ; there's a selfdirected robot scientist that's made a discovery soon , science may no longer need us , and life may no longer need us either ; a microbe wakes up after 120 , 000 years .	最近有些發現 , 阿根廷有一個蟻群現在散播到每個大陸 , 但南極洲 ; 自導導的機器人科學家很快就發現了 , 科學可能不再需要我們 , 生命就可能不再需要我們了 ; 一個微生物在十二萬年後醒來 。
it seems that with or without us , life will go on .	似乎沒有人類 , 生命會繼續下去 。
but my pick for the top long news story of this past year was this one: water found on the moon .	但我去年選了一篇長篇新聞報導 , 是這個:月球上有水 。
makes it a lot easier to put a colony up there .	使那裡的殖民地更容易被送到那裡 。
and if nasa doesn't do it , china might , or somebody in this room might write a big check .	如果美國太空總署不做 , 中國可能會做 , 也可能在座的某些人可能會寫一張大支票 。
my point is this: in the long run , some news stories are more important than others .	我的重點是:長遠來看 , 某些新聞故事比其他新聞更重要 。
planetary scientist carolyn porco shows images from the cassini voyage to saturn , focusing on its largest moon , titan , and on frozen enceladus , which seems to shoot jets of ice .	星球科學家carolynporco顯示了卡西尼航行到土星的影像 , 聚焦在它最大的衛星泰坦大衛星上 , 以及在結凍土衛二上 , 它似乎會射出冰束的噴射機 。
nasa , design , exploration , science , space , technology , universe , visualizations	nasa , 設計 , 探索 , 科學 , 空間 , 科技 , 宇宙 , 視覺化視覺化.
carolyn porco flies us to saturn	卡洛琳.波爾科請我們飛到土星 。
in the next 18 minutes , i'm going to take you on a journey .	在接下來的18分鐘裡 , 我要帶你們踏上一段旅程 。
and it's a journey that you and i have been on for many years now , and it began some 50 years ago , when humans first stepped off our planet .	這是你們和我相處了很多年的旅程 , 50年前就開始了 , 那時人類第一次踏出我們的星球 。
and in those 50 years , not only did we literally , physically set foot on the moon , but we have dispatched robotic spacecraft to all the planets all eight of them and we have landed on asteroids , we have rendezvoused with comets , and , at this point in time , we have a spacecraft on its way to pluto , the body formerly known as a planet .	在那50年裡 , 我們不僅成功地登上了月球 , 我們還將太空船發射到其中的八個行星上 , 我們著陸在小行星上 , 與彗星相遇 , 此時此刻 , 我們有一艘太空船正向冥王星駛去 , 它以前稱為 「 行星 」 的星球 。
and all of these robotic missions are part of a bigger human journey: a voyage to understand something , to get a sense of our cosmic place , to understand something of our origins , and how earth , our planet , and we , living on it , came to be .	所有這些機械裝置的使命都是人類更大的旅程之一:為了理解事物的旅程 , 為了理解宇宙 , 了解我們的起源 , 及地球 , 我們的地球 , 及我們居住的路程 。
and of all the places in the solar system that we might go to and search for answers to questions like this , there's saturn . and we have been to saturn before we visited saturn in the early 1980s but our investigations of saturn have become far more indepth in detail since the cassini spacecraft , traveling across interplanetary space for seven years , glided into orbit around saturn in the summer of 2004 , and became at that point the farthest robotic outpost that humanity had ever established around the sun .	在太陽系中所有我們想去的地方 , 找到這樣的問題的解答 , 包括土星 。 我們曾到過土星 。 1980年代早期我們探訪過土星 。 但我們對土星的研究更加深入 , 卡西尼號太空船穿過星際空間長達七年之久 , 在2004年夏天時已達到軌道 , 成為人類所見過最遠離太陽系的機械裝置 。
now , the saturn system is a rich planetary system .	土星系統是個很豐富的行星系統 。
it offers mystery , scientific insight and obviously splendor beyond compare , and the investigation of this system has enormous cosmic reach .	它提供神秘的、科學的洞見 , 並且顯然超出比較的光彩 , 而這個系統的調查 , 對於宇宙的可觸及範圍非常巨大 。
in fact , just studying the rings alone , we stand to learn a lot about the discs of stars and gas that we call the spiral galaxies .	事實上 , 單就研究光環 , 我們就能夠學到很多關於星星與氣體的光圈 。 我們稱之為螺旋星系 。
and here's a beautiful picture of the andromeda nebula , which is our closest , largest spiral galaxy to the milky way .	這是一張仙女座星系的美麗照片 , 這是我們最接近的 , 最大型的螺旋星系 。
and then , here's a beautiful composite of the whirlpool galaxy , taken by the hubble space telescope .	這裡有一幅美麗的旋風星系 , 由哈伯太空望遠鏡拍攝 。
so the journey back to saturn is really part of and is also a metaphor for a much larger human voyage to understand the interconnectedness of everything around us , and also how humans fit into that picture .	飛往土星的旅程是其中的一部分 , 也是一種比喻 , 比喻了人類更大的旅程 , 目的是要了解我們身邊所有事物的相互關聯性 , 以及人類對這張圖片的關聯性 。
and it pains me that i can't tell you all that we have learned with cassini .	這讓我很痛苦 , 我無法告訴各位 , 我們在卡西尼學過的一切 。
i can't show you all the beautiful pictures that we've taken in the last two and a half years , because i simply don't have the time .	我無法向各位展示我們在過去兩年半所拍攝的所有美麗照片 , 因為我根本沒有時間 。
so i'm going to concentrate on two of the most exciting stories that have emerged out of this major exploratory expedition that we are conducting around saturn , and have been for the past two and a half years .	我會專注於這次大型探險之旅當中 , 有兩件最令人振奮的故事 , 是我們在土星周圍進行的 , 兩年來都是如此 。
saturn is accompanied by a very large and diverse collection of moons .	陪伴在土星旁的是一大群不同的衛星 。
they range in size from a few kilometers across to as big across as the u . s .	它們的尺寸範圍從幾公里到大不等於美國 。
most of the beautiful pictures we've taken of saturn , in fact , show saturn in accompaniment with some of its moons . here's saturn with dione , and then , here's saturn showing the rings edgeon , showing you just how vertically thin they are , with the moon enceladus .	大部分我們拍攝土星的美麗圖片事實上 , 土星和它的一些衛星 。 這是土星和土星和土衛二 。 這是土衛六的圖像 , 這裡是土衛二的光環 , 顯示它們的直徑有多薄 。
now , two of the 47 moons that saturn has are standouts .	現在 , 土星47顆衛星中有兩顆特別裝備 。
and those are titan and enceladus . titan is saturn's largest moon , and , until cassini had arrived there , was the largest single expanse of unexplored terrain that we had remaining in our solar system .	這些是土衛六和土衛二的衛星 , 泰坦是土星最大的衛星 , 在卡西尼號到達之前 , 它是我們在太陽系中最大的未被探勘過的單獨地帶 。
and it is a body that has long intrigued people who've watched the planets .	它是長期以來關注這些行星的人們的身體 。
it has a very large , thick atmosphere , and in fact , its surface environment was believed to be more like the environment we have here on the earth , or at least had in the past , than any other body in the solar system .	它有很大、很厚的大氣層 , 事實上 , 它的地表環境被認為比較像我們在地球上的環境 , 至少在過去 , 與其它太陽系中的天體相比 , 它的地表環境更像 。
its atmosphere is largely molecular nitrogen , like you are breathing here in this room , except that its atmosphere is suffused with simple organic materials like methane and propane and ethane .	它的大氣中含有大量氮分子 , 就像你在這裡吸入的氮氣一樣 , 只不過它的大氣中有許多簡單的有機物質如甲烷、丙烷、丙烷等 。
and these molecules high up in the atmosphere of titan get broken down , and their products join together to make haze particles .	這些分子在泰坦的大氣層高高 , 分解 , 它們的產品結合在一起 , 製造出霧狀顆粒 。
this haze is ubiquitous . it's completely global and enveloping titan .	這霧狀物無所不在 , 它完全是全球化的 , 包圍著土衛六 。
and that's why you cannot see down to the surface with our eyes in the visible region of the spectrum .	那就是為什麼你不能用肉眼看到的光譜區域 。
but these haze particles , it was surmised , before we got there with cassini , over billions and billions of years , gently drifted down to the surface and coated the surface in a thick organic sludge .	但在卡西尼號到達之前 , 我們推測這些霧狀顆粒經過數十億年 , 溫和地漂浮在表面上 , 覆蓋在有機有機物的表面上 。
so like the equivalent , the titan equivalent , of tar , or oil , or what we didn't know what .	就像泰坦的焦油、油 , 或是我們不知道什麼 。
but this is what we suspected . and these molecules , especially methane and ethane , can be liquids at the surface temperatures of titan .	但這就是我們所猜測的 。 而這些分子 , 尤其是甲烷和乙烷 , 可以是土衛六地表溫度的液體 。
and so it turns out that methane is to titan what water is to the earth .	結果發現 , 甲烷是 「 土衛六 」 的標準 。
it's a condensable in the atmosphere , and so recognizing this circumstance brought to the fore a whole world of bizarre possibilities . you can have methane clouds , ok , and above those clouds , you have this hundreds of kilometers of haze , which prevent any sunlight from getting to the surface .	它在大氣中是冷凝的 , 所以認識到這種情況的存在 , 帶來了非常奇怪的可能性 。 你可以有甲烷雲 , 在這些雲之上 , 幾百公里寬的霧氣 , 阻止陽光照射到地表 。
the temperature at the surface is some 350 degrees below zero fahrenheit .	地表的溫度是華氏零下350度 。
but despite that cold , you could have rain falling down on the surface of titan .	儘管很冷 , 土衛六上還是會下雨 。
and doing on titan what rain does on the earth: it carves gullies ; it forms rivers and cataracts ; it can create canyons ; it can pool in large basins and craters .	如同地球上的雨水 , 它會雕刻水溝 ; 它會形成河流和白內障 ; 它能形成峽谷 ; 大型盆地和隕石 。
it can wash the sludge off high mountain peaks and hills , down into the lowlands . so stop and think for a minute .	它可以把泥土從高山丘上沖到低地帶 。 停下來想一想 。
try to imagine what the surface of titan might look like .	試著想像土衛六的表面會是什麼樣子 。
it's dark . high noon on titan is as dark as deep earth twilight on the earth .	那裡一片漆黑 , 土衛六上的正中午 , 和地球上昏暗一樣黑暗 。
it's cold , it's eerie , it's misty , it might be raining , and you might be standing on the shores of lake michigan brimming with paint thinner .	那裡很冷 , 陰影 , 陰影偏霧 , 可能正在下雨 , 你可能還站在密西根湖的密西根湖邊 , 旁邊塗上油漆 。
that is the view that we had of the surface of titan before we got there with cassini , and i can tell you that what we have found on titan , though it is not the same in detail , is every bit as fascinating as that story is .	這是我們和卡西尼一起到達土衛六之前的樣子 , 我可以告訴各位 , 我們在土衛六上發現的 , 雖然它的細節不盡相同 , 和故事一樣迷人 。
and for us , it has been like the cassini people it has been like a jules verne adventure come true .	對我們來說 , 這就像卡西尼人 , 一切都像是陪審團的凡爾納冒險成真一樣 。
as i said , it has a thick , extensive atmosphere .	如我所說 , 它有很厚的大氣層 。
this is a picture of titan , backlit by the sun , with the rings as a beautiful backdrop .	這是土衛六的照片 , 背著太陽光 , 光環是美麗的背景 。
and yet another moon there i don't even know which one it is . it's a very extensive atmosphere .	另外一個衛星 , 我甚至不知道是哪一個 。 它是一層非常大的大氣 。
we have instruments on cassini which can see down to the surface through this atmosphere , and my camera system is one of them .	我們在卡西尼號上裝了儀器 , 它能透過大氣層向下看到表面 , 我的攝影系統就是其中之一 。
and we have taken pictures like this .	我們拍了像這樣的照片 。
and what you see is bright and dark regions , and that's about as far as it got for us .	你所看到的是明亮、黑暗的區域 , 且那幾乎就是我們能達到的程度 。
it was so mystifying: we couldn't make out what we were seeing on titan .	它是如此的神秘:我們無法找出我們在泰坦上看到的景象 。
when you look closer at this region , you start to see things like sinuous channels we didn't know . you see a few round things .	當你仔細看這個區域 , 你會開始看到一些東西 , 像是航道 , 我們不知道 。 你會看到一些圓形的東西 。
this , we later found out , is , in fact , a crater , but there are very few craters on the surface of titan , meaning it's a very young surface .	後來我們發現 , 這原來是一個隕石坑 , 但土衛六表面的隕石數量很少 , 這意味著土衛六的表面很年輕 。
and there are features that look tectonic .	有些特徵看起來是地質構造 。
they look like they've been pulled apart .	它們看起來像是被拉開了 。
whenever you see anything linear on a planet , it means there's been a fracture , like a fault .	每當你看到行星上有線性的東西 , 意味著地裂 , 例如一個斷層 。
and so it's been tectonically altered .	所以它已經被地質地改變了 。
but we couldn't make sense of our images , until , six months after we got into orbit , an event occurred that many have regarded as the highlight of cassini's investigation of titan .	但我們無法理解我們的影像 , 直到我們進入軌道六個月後 , 發生了一件大事 , 許多人都認為卡西尼探測土衛六的亮光 。
and that was the deployment of the huygens probe , the europeanbuilt huygens probe that cassini had carried for seven years across the solar system . we deployed it to the atmosphere of titan , it took two and a half hours to descend , and it landed on the surface .	這就是惠更斯號探測器在歐洲被建造的惠更斯號探測器在太陽系裡航行了七年 。 我們把它發射到土衛六的大氣中 , 花了兩個半小時才下降 , 降落在地表上 。
and i just want to emphasize how significant an event this is .	我只想強調這一件事有多重要 。
this is a device of human making , and it landed in the outer solar system for the first time in human history .	這是人類史上第一次在外太陽系中登陸的裝置 。
it is so significant that , in my mind , this was an event that should have been celebrated with ticker tape parades in every city across the u . s . and europe , and sadly , that wasn't the case .	在我心中 , 這實在是太重要了 , 我本來應該在每座美國和歐洲各地都舉辦這個活動 , 但遺憾的是 , 並非如此 。
it was significant for another reason . this is an international mission , and this event was celebrated in europe , in germany , and the celebratory presentations were given in english accents , and american accents , and german accents , and french and italian and dutch accents .	這是另一個重要的原因 。 這是個國際使命 , 這個事件在歐洲、德國被慶祝 , 慶祝慶祝以英文口音和美國口音、德文口音、法文、義大利和荷蘭口音 。
it was a moving demonstration of what the words " united nations " are supposed to mean: a true union of nations joined together in a colossal effort for good .	這是在分析 「 聯合國 」 一詞的分析中 , 代表的意思是:國家的真誠結合 , 全國一起努力 , 為大眾利益著想 。
and , in this case , it was a massive undertaking to explore a planet , and to come to understand a planetary system that , for all of human history , had been unreachable , and now humans had actually touched it .	在這個例子中 , 探索一個星球是一項龐大任務 , 為了了解一個星球系統 , 這個星球系統是人類歷史上所有地方都無法修改的 , 而現在 , 人類已經摸到了它 。
so it was i mean , i'm getting goose bumps just talking about it .	所以 , 我的意思是 , 我會起雞皮疙瘩就談及它 。
it was a tremendously emotional event , and it's something that i will personally never forget , and you shouldn't either .	那是非常情緒化的一件事 , 我個人永遠不會忘記 , 你也不該如此 。
but anyway , the probe took measurements of the atmosphere on the way down , and it also took panoramic pictures .	探測器在降落過程中對大氣進行了測量 , 並且拍攝了全景照片 。
and i can't tell you what it was like to see the first pictures of titan's surface from the probe . and this is what we saw .	我無法告訴各位 , 看見泰坦表面的第一張照片是什麼樣子 。 這是我們看到的景象 。
and it was a shocker , because it was everything we wanted those other pictures taken from orbit to be .	很震驚 , 因為這就是我們期待其他從軌道上拍下的照片 。
it was an unambiguous pattern , a geological pattern .	這是個明確的模式 , 地質模式 。
it's a dendritic drainage pattern that can be formed only by the flow of liquids .	這種樹枝狀的排水模式只能透過液體的流動來形成 。
and you can follow these channels and you can see how they all converge .	你可以沿著這些管道看到它們如何合而為一
and they converge into this channel here , which drains into this region .	它們匯合到這條通道中 , 滲透到這個區域 。
you are looking at a shoreline .	你看到的是一條海岸線 。
was this a shoreline of fluids ? we didn't know .	這是液體的海岸線嗎 ? 我們不知道 。
but this is somewhat of a shoreline .	但這有點像是一條海岸線 。
this picture is taken at 16 kilometers .	這張照片是在16公里拍的 。
this is the picture taken at eight kilometers , ok ? again , the shoreline .	這是一張在8公里拍攝的照片 , 對吧 ? 再看一次 , 海岸線 。
okay , now , 16 kilometers , eight kilometers this is roughly an airline altitude .	好 , 現在 , 16公里 , 8公里--大概就是航空的高度 。
if you were going to take an airplane trip across the u . s . , you would be flying at these altitudes .	如果你要搭飛機橫跨美國 , 你會以這些高度飛行 。
so , this is the picture you would have at the window of titanian airlines as you fly across the surface of titan .	這是你在泰坦航空的窗戶上所能看到的景象 , 就在你飛越泰坦星表面的時候 。
and then finally , the probe came to rest on the surface , and i'm going to show you , ladies and gentlemen , the first picture ever taken from the surface of a moon in the outer solar system .	最後 , 探測器終於在表面上停留了下來 , 我會給你們看 , 女士們先生們 , 這是第一張外太陽系衛星表面的照片 。
and here is the horizon , ok ?	這是地平線 , 好嗎 ?
these are probably water ice pebbles , yes ?	這些可能是冰鵝卵石 , 對嗎 ?
and obviously , it landed in one of these flat , dark regions and it didn't sink out of sight . so it wasn't fluid that we landed in .	很明顯地 , 它落在了其中一塊平坦的黑色區域 , 它沒有沉沒在視野之中 。 所以它不是流體的 。
what the probe came down in was basically the titan equivalent of a mud flat .	基本上 , 探測器下降的速度相當於一片泥土平面 。
this is an unconsolidated ground that is suffused with liquid methane .	這是液態甲烷形成的半流體 。
and it's probably the case that this material has washed off the highlands of titan through these channels that we saw , and has drained over billions of years to fill in lowlying basins .	或許這種材料已經從土衛六的高地沖刷過 , 經過我們看到的這些通道 , 耗費了數十億年的時間來填滿低窪地帶 。
and that is what the huygens probe landed in .	這就是惠更斯號探測器著陸的地方 。
but still , there was no sign in our images , or even in the huygens' images , of any large , open bodies of fluids .	但是 , 我們仍然沒有出現在我們的影像中 , 甚至在惠更斯的影像中 , 任何大型開放的液體都沒有 。
where were they ? it got even more puzzling when we found dunes .	他們在哪裡 ? 當我們發現沙丘時 , 更讓人費解 。
ok , so this is our movie of the equatorial region of titan , showing these dunes . these are dunes that are 100 meters tall , separated by a few kilometers , and they go on for miles and miles and miles .	好 , 這是我們電影裡的赤道區域 , 展示這些沙丘 。 這些沙丘高度100公尺 , 由幾公里高的沙丘分離出來 , 它們跑上幾英里 , 走了好幾英里 。
there's hundreds , up to a 1 , 000 or 1 , 200 miles of dunes .	幾百英里高達一千或一千兩百英里的沙丘
this is the saharan desert of titan .	這是土衛六的撒哈拉沙漠 。
it's obviously a place which is very dry , or you wouldn't get dunes .	顯然這地方很乾燥 , 否則就不會有沙丘 。
so again , it got puzzling that there were no bodies of fluid , until finally , we saw lakes in the polar regions .	所以再一次 , 令人困惑的是沒有液體的體 , 直到我們終於看到極地的湖泊 。
and there is a lake scene in the south polar region of titan .	這是土衛六南極的一個湖 。
it's about the size of lake ontario .	它和安大略湖差不多大 。
and then , only a week and a half ago , we flew over the north pole of titan and found , again , we found a feature here the size of the caspian sea .	然後 , 一週半前 , 我們飛過北極 , 發現了相當於加勒比海大小的一個特徵 。
so it seems that the liquids , for some reason we don't understand , or during at least this season , are apparently at the poles of titan .	看來這些液體 , 是因為我們不了解的原因 , 或者至少這個季節 , 在泰坦的極地 。
and i think you would agree that we have found titan is a remarkable , mystical place . it's exotic , it's alien , but yet strangely earthlike , and having earthlike geological formations and a tremendous geographical diversity , and is a fascinating world whose only rival in the solar system for complexity and richness is the earth itself .	我想你會同意我們發現土衛六是個了不起、神秘的地方 。 它很奇怪 , 又像外星人 , 但又像地球 , 有著像地球的地貌和豐富的地理多樣性 。 它是一個非常迷人的世界 , 一個太陽系中唯一能和地球相對應的複雜性和豐富性才是地球 。
and so now we go onto enceladus . enceladus is a small moon , it's about a tenth the size of titan . and you can see it here next to england , just to show you the size . this is not meant to be a threat .	所以現在我們來到土衛二.土衛二是一個小型衛星 , 土衛六的尺寸只有土衛六的十分之一 , 你可以看到在英國旁邊的圖片 , 只是讓你們看看它的大小 。 這並不是說要當威脅 。
and enceladus is very white , it's very bright , and its surface is obviously wrecked with fractures .	土衛二很白很亮 , 它的表面有很明顯的裂痕 。
it is a very geologically active body .	它是地質上非常活躍的身體 。
but the mother lode of discoveries on enceladus was found at the south pole and we're looking at the south pole here where we found this system of fractures .	但在土衛二上的發現大多集中在南極我們現在看到的是南極 , 在這裡我們發現了這個系統斷裂 。
and they're a different color because they're a different composition .	它們的顏色不同 , 因為它們的成分不同 。
they are coated . these fractures are coated with organic materials .	它們被塗層 , 這些骨折覆蓋著有機物質 。
moreover , this whole , entire region , the south polar region , has elevated temperatures . it's the hottest place on the planet , on the body .	此外 , 整個南極地帶的溫度上升了 , 溫度在地球上最熱的地方 , 在身體上 。
that's as bizarre as finding that the antarctic on the earth is hotter than the tropics .	這有點奇怪 , 因為我們發現地球南極比熱帶地區還要熱 。
and then , when we took additional pictures , we discovered that from these fractures are issuing jets of fine , icy particles extending hundreds of miles into space .	然後 , 我們拍攝了更多照片 , 我們發現從這些地裂中 , 有細小的冰粒噴射出來 , 噴射到太空中數百英里 。
and when we colorcode this image , to bring out the faint light levels , we see that these jets feed a plume that , in fact , we see , in other images , goes thousands of miles into the space above enceladus .	當我們用顏色來編碼這個影像 , 以取得微弱的光線 , 我們可以看到這些噴射流在土衛二上方幾千英里處的空間裡 。
my team and i have examined images like this , and like this one , and have thought about the other results from cassini .	我和我的團隊檢視了像這樣的圖片 , 和這張圖片 , 想了卡西尼號的其它結果 。
and we have arrived at the conclusion that these jets may be erupting from pockets of liquid water under the surface of enceladus .	我們得出的結論是 , 這些噴流可能是從土衛二地表下的液態水坑噴發出來的 。
so we have , possibly , liquid water , organic materials and excess heat .	所以我們可能有液態水、有機物質和過剩的熱量 。
in other words , we have possibly stumbled upon the holy grail of modern day planetary exploration , or in other words , an environment that is potentially suitable for living organisms .	換句話說 , 我們有可能偶然發現了現代行星探索的聖杯 , 也就是說 , 一個可能適合生物生存的環境 。
and i don't think i need to tell you that the discovery of life elsewhere in our solar system , whether it be on enceladus or elsewhere , would have enormous cultural and scientific implications .	我想我不需要告訴各位 , 我們太陽系其他地方的發現 , 不論是土衛二或其它地方 , 都會有很大的文化和科學意涵 。
because if we could demonstrate that genesis had occurred not once , but twice , independently , in our solar system , then that means , by inference , it has occurred a staggering number of times throughout the universe and its 13 . 7 billion year history .	因為如果我們能夠證明創世紀已經發生過 , 不只一次 , 而是兩次 , 獨立在我們的太陽系中 , 那麼 , 推論一下 , 它已經發生了相當驚人的數次 , 遍及整個宇宙137億年的歷史 。
right now , earth is the only planet still that we know is teeming with life .	目前 , 地球仍是唯一一顆充滿生命的行星 。
it is precious , it is unique , it is still , so far , the only home we've ever known .	它很珍貴 , 它獨一無二 , 它依然是我們唯一的家 。
and if any of you were alert and coherent during the 1960s and we'd forgive you , if you weren't , ok you would remember this very famous picture taken by the apollo 8 astronauts in 1968 .	如果在座有人在1960年代時感到警覺和連貫 , 我們原諒你們 , 如果你沒有的話 , 你可能會記得1968年阿波羅8號太空人拍下的這張著名照片 。
it was the first time that earth was imaged from space , and it had an enormous impact on our sense of place in the universe , and our sense of responsibility for the protection of our own planet .	那是地球第一次從太空中拍攝出來 , 它對我們在宇宙中的位置產生了巨大的衝擊 , 我們對於保護地球的責任感也產生巨大的衝擊 。
well , we on cassini have taken an equivalent first , a picture that no human eye has ever seen before .	我們的卡西尼號同樣拍下了一張前所未見的照片 。
it is a total eclipse of the sun , seen from the other side of saturn .	它是日全蝕從土星的另一側拍攝的
and in this impossibly beautiful picture , you see the main rings backlit by the sun , you see the refracted image of the sun and you see this ring created , in fact , by the exhalations of enceladus .	在這個不可思議的美麗照片中 , 你看到背著太陽光的主光 , 你看到太陽折射的影像 , 還可以看到由土衛二的揭露出來的光環 。
but as if that weren't brilliant enough , we can spot , in this beautiful image , sight of our own planet , cradled in the arms of saturn's rings .	但如果這還不夠聰明 , 我們還能在這美麗的圖像中看到我們自己的星球 , 爬進了土星戒指的臂彎 。
now , there is something deeply moving about seeing ourselves from afar , and capturing the sight of our little , blueocean planet in the skies of other worlds .	對於從遠處看我們自己 , 有一點很深刻 , 深刻的感動 , 捕捉到我們在其他星球的視野 。
and that , and the perspective of ourselves that we gain from that , may be , in the end , the finest reward that we earn from this journey of discovery that started half a century ago .	而這個 , 和我們從中得到的認知 , 或許最終 , 我們從這次新發現之旅中獲得最好的獎賞 , 始於半個世紀前 。
as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped . this slows the delivery of aid after a disaster and hides the economic potential of unused lands and unknown roads . in this short talk , google's lalitesh katragadda demos map maker , a group mapmaking tool that people around the globe are using to map their world .	到了2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被繪製圖 。 這會減緩災難後的援助 , 還隱藏未被使用的土地和未知道路的經濟潛力 。 簡短的演講中 , 谷歌的拉特加迪加迪亞德莫斯繪製了全球各地的人使用的地圖工具 。
collaboration , design , map , technology	合作、設計、地圖、科技和技術 。
lalitesh katragadda: making maps to fight disaster , build economies	已故的卡特加達:對抗災難的地圖 , 建立經濟 。
in 2008 , cyclone nargis devastated myanmar .	2008年 , 塞隆納格斯摧毀了緬甸 。
millions of people were in severe need of help .	數百萬人非常需要協助 。
the u . n . wanted to rush people and supplies to the area .	聯合國想把人民趕到那個區域 。
but there were no maps , no maps of roads , no maps showing hospitals , no way for help to reach the cyclone victims .	但沒有地圖、沒有道路地圖、沒有地圖顯示醫院、也沒有地圖協助抵達氣旋受害者 。
when we look at a map of los angeles or london , it is hard to believe that as of 2005 , only 15 percent of the world was mapped to a geocodable level of detail .	當我們看洛杉磯或倫敦的地圖時 , 很難相信到2005年 , 世界上只有15%的人被配上可編碼的細節 。
the u . n . ran headfirst into a problem that the majority of the world's populous faces: not having detailed maps .	聯合國也解決了世界上大部分人口人口問題:沒有詳細的地圖 。
but help was coming .	但救兵來了 。
at google , 40 volunteers used a new software to map 120 , 000 kilometers of roads , 3 , 000 hospitals , logistics and relief points .	在谷歌 , 有40位志願者使用了一套軟體標記了12萬公里的道路 , 3000間醫院 , 物流和救護站 。
and it took them four days .	他們花了四天的時間 。
the new software they used ? google mapmaker .	他們使用的軟體呢 ? googlemapmaker
google mapmaker is a technology that empowers each of us to map what we know locally .	googlemapmaker是一種科技 , 賦予我們每個人對地圖上的認知 。
people have used this software to map everything from roads to rivers , from schools to local businesses , and video stores to the corner store .	人們用這個軟體繪製出道路、河流、學校、當地企業 , 和影片商店的地點 。
nobel prize nominee hernando de soto recognized that the key to economic liftoff for most developing countries is to tap the vast amounts of uncapitalized land .	諾貝爾獎提名人hernandodesoto認爲開發中國家要發展經濟的關鍵是去掌握大量未清潔的土地
for example , a trillion dollars of real estate remains uncapitalized in india alone .	舉例來說 , 光在印度就有價值一兆美元的房地產還沒有被列入管制 。
in the last year alone , thousands of users in 170 countries have mapped millions of pieces of information , and created a map of a level of detail never thought viable .	單單在去年170個國家數千名使用者已繪製了數百萬個資訊的地圖並創造了前所未有的精確度
and this was made possible by the power of passionate users everywhere .	這一切都是因為到處都有熱情的使用者的力量 。
let's look at some of the maps being created by users right now .	我們現在來看看使用者的地圖 。
so , as we speak , people are mapping the world in these 170 countries .	在這110個國家中 , 人們畫出世界地圖
you can see bridget in africa who just mapped a road in senegal .	你可以看到在非洲的橋樑剛剛為塞內加爾標了一條路
and , closer to home , chalua , an n . g . road in bangalore .	離家近一點 , chalua是班加羅爾一個n.g路口 。
this is the result of computational geometry , gesture recognition , and machine learning .	這是計算幾何學動作識別和機器學習的結果 。
this is a victory of thousands of users , in hundreds of cities , one user , one edit at a time .	這是數以千計使用者的勝利 , 在數百個城市中 , 一個使用者 , 一次一個編輯 。
this is an invitation to the 70 percent of our unmapped planet .	這是個邀請 , 邀請我們70%未開發的星球 。
welcome to the new world .	歡迎來到新世界 。
in 2003 , the palestinian village of budrus mounted a 10monthlong nonviolent protest to stop a barrier being built across their olive groves . did you hear about it ? didn't think so . brazilian filmmaker julia bacha asks why we only pay attention to violence in the israelpalestine conflict and not to the nonviolent leaders who may one day bring peace .	2003年 , 巴勒斯坦村莊布德鲁斯村舉辦了十個月長的非暴力抗議活動 , 阻止了他們在橄欖樹林中築起的障礙 。 你聽見了嗎 ? 沒這麼想 。 巴西的電影製作人茱莉亞•巴查問為什麼我們只關注以色列內的暴力 , 而不是去找可能有一天會帶來和平的非暴力領導人 。
arts , communication , compassion , entertainment , film , peace , violence , war	藝術、溝通、同情心、娛樂、電影、和平戰爭、戰爭 。
julia bacha: pay attention to nonviolence	茱莉亞.巴哈:請注意非暴力手段 。
for the last 8 years , i have dedicated my life to documenting the work of israelis and palestinians who are trying to end the conflict using peaceful means .	過去8年來 , 我致力於記錄以色列和巴勒斯坦試圖用和平的方式來結束衝突的人們 。
when i travel with my work across europe and the united states , one question always comes up: where is the palestinian gandhi ?	當我在歐洲和美國各地旅行時 , 總是會有一個問題:巴勒斯坦的甘地在哪裡 ?
why aren't palestinians using nonviolent resistance ?	為什麼巴勒斯坦人不用非暴力的方式抗爭 ?
the challenge i face when i hear this question is that often i have just returned from the middle east where i spent my time filming dozens of palestinians who are using nonviolence to defend their lands and water resources from israeli soldiers and settlers .	當我聽到這個問題時 , 我所面臨的挑戰是 , 通常我剛從中東回來 , 我在那裡花了很多時間拍攝數十位巴勒斯坦人 , 他們用非暴力手段來捍衛他們的土地和水資源 , 來自以色列的士兵和移民者 。
these leaders are trying to forge a massive national nonviolent movement to end the occupation and build peace in the region .	這些領導人正嘗試偽造一個龐大的全國非暴力運動 , 來終結這個地區的佔領和平 。
yet , most of you have probably never heard about them .	但 , 大部分的人可能從未聽說過這些事 。
this divide between what's happening on the ground and perceptions abroad is one of the key reasons why we don't have yet a palestinian peaceful resistance movement that has been successful .	國外發生的事與國際感知之間的分歧 , 正是其中一個關鍵原因為什麼我們還沒有一場巴勒斯坦和平抗爭運動成功 。
so i'm here today to talk about the power of attention , the power of your attention , and the emergence and development of nonviolent movements in the west bank , gaza and elsewhere but today , my case study is going to be palestine .	所以我今天要來談關注的力量你的關注的力量以及非暴力運動在約旦河西岸、加薩和其他地方的興起與發展但今天我的個案將是巴勒斯坦
i believe that what's mostly missing for nonviolence to grow is not for palestinians to start adopting nonviolence , but for us to start paying attention to those who already are .	我相信要促進非暴力手段 , 最缺乏的不是巴勒斯坦人開始採用非暴力手段 , 而是要我們開始注意那些已經是非暴力手段的人 。
allow me to illustrate this point by taking you to this village called budrus .	讓我帶你進入這個名為布德魯斯的村子來說明這個點 。
about seven years ago , they faced extinction , because israel announced it would build a separation barrier , and part of this barrier would be built on top of the village .	大約七年前 , 他們面臨絕種 , 因為以色列宣佈要築起一道隔離屏障 , 當中的一部分是在這個村子的上面建造的 。
they would lose 40 percent of their land and be surrounded , so they would lose free access to the rest of the west bank .	他們會失去40%的土地並被包圍 , 這樣他們就能自由地失去剩下的約旦河岸 。
through inspired local leadership , they launched a peaceful resistance campaign to stop that from happening .	透過當地領袖的鼓舞 , 他們發動了和平抗爭活動 , 來阻止這種事發生 。
let me show you some brief clips , so you have a sense for what that actually looked like on the ground .	讓我給你們看一些短片 , 你們可以了解在地面上到底是什麼樣子 。
palestinian woman: we were told the wall would separate palestine from israel .	巴勒斯坦女性:我們被告知 , 牆會和以色列分開巴勒斯坦 。
here in budrus , we realized the wall would steal our land .	在布德鲁斯村這裡 , 我們了解到那道牆將竊取我們的土地 。
israeli man: the fence has , in fact , created a solution to terror .	以色列人:這道牆其實是解決恐懼的方法 。
man: today you're invited to a peaceful march .	男人:今天你被邀請去一個和平的遊行 。
you are joined by dozens of your israeli brothers and sisters .	你加入了數十位你的以色列兄弟姐妹 。
israeli activist: nothing scares the army more than nonviolent opposition .	以色列抗議人士:軍隊害怕的就是非暴力抗爭 。
woman: we saw the men trying to push the soldiers , but none of them could do that .	女子:我們看到男人想推開士兵 , 但沒有人能做到 。
but i think the girls could do it .	但我認為女生們能做到 。
fatah party member: we must empty our minds of traditional thinking .	法塔赫黨員:我們必須清空腦中的傳統思想 。
hamas party member: we were in complete harmony , and we wanted to spread it to all of palestine .	哈馬斯黨員:我們是完全和諧的 , 我們想把它散播到巴勒斯坦 。
chanting: one united nation .	口號聲:一個聯合國 。
fatah , hamas and the popular front !	法塔赫、哈馬斯和受歡迎的陣線 !
news anchor: the clashes over the fence continue .	主播:圍牆上的衝突持續著 。
reporter: israeli border police were sent to disperse the crowd .	記者:以色列邊界警察被派來散播群眾 。
they were allowed to use any force necessary .	他們可以使用任何必要的力量 。
man: these are live bullets .	男子:這些是直彈 。
it's like fallujah . shooting everywhere .	這就像 「 費魯杰 」 射擊到處都是
israeli activist: i was sure we were all going to die .	以色列活動家:我相信我們都會死 。
but there were others around me who weren't even cowering .	但有些身邊的人甚至一點都不害怕 。
israeli soldier: a nonviolent protest is not going to stop the [unclear] .	以色列士兵:非暴力抗爭無法阻止這【不清楚】
protester: this is a peaceful march .	抗議者:這是和平的遊行 。
there is no need to use violence .	不需要使用暴力 。
chanting: we can do it ! we can do it !	口號聲:我們做得到 ! 我們做得到 !
julia bacha: when i first heard about the story of budrus , i was surprised that the international media had failed to cover the extraordinary set of events that happened seven years ago , in 2003 .	朱莉亞•巴查:當我第一次聽到布德鲁斯村的故事時 , 我很驚訝國際媒體竟然沒有報導這一連串驚人的事件 , 那是在七年前 , 2003年的事 。
what was even more surprising was the fact that budrus was successful .	更令人驚訝的是布德鲁斯村成功了
the residents , after 10 months of peaceful resistance , convinced the israeli government to move the route of the barrier off their lands and to the green line , which is the internationally recognized boundary between israel and the palestinian territories .	居民抗爭十個月後說服了以色列政府將這道牆從他們的土地移開到綠線上也就是國際公認的以色列和巴勒斯坦領土間的界線
the resistance in budrus has since spread to villages across the west bank and to palestinian neighborhoods in jerusalem .	布德鲁斯村的抗爭自此散播到整個西岸的村落 , 以及耶路撒冷的巴勒斯坦人社區 。
yet the media remains mostly silent on these stories .	但媒體還是沉默在這些故事上 。
this silence carries profound consequences for the likelihood that nonviolence can grow , or even survive , in palestine .	這種沉默帶來了很大的影響 , 影響非暴力手段可能會成長 , 甚至在巴勒斯坦生存 。
violent resistance and nonviolent resistance share one very important thing in common ; they are both a form of theater seeking an audience to their cause .	暴力抗爭和非暴力抗爭都有一個非常重要的共通點 , 它們既是劇院 , 尋求其目標的觀眾 。
if violent actors are the only ones constantly getting frontpage covers and attracting international attention to the palestinian issue , it becomes very hard for nonviolent leaders to make the case to their communities that civil disobedience is a viable option in addressing their plight .	如果只有使用暴力的人才能上頭版 , 並吸引國際媒體關注巴勒斯坦的議題 , 那對非暴力領袖是非常困難的 , 要向他們的社區證明公民不服從是個可行的選項 , 要處理他們的困境 。
the power of attention is probably going to come as no surprise to the parents in the room .	關注的力量可能不會對在場的父母感到驚訝 。
the surest way to make your child throw increasingly louder tantrums is by giving him attention the first time he throws a fit .	讓小孩吵鬧的最好方式就是讓他第一次受到他的注意力 。
the tantrum will become what childhood psychologists call a functional behavior , since the child has learned that he can get parental attention out of it .	這種吵架會變成童年心理學家所說的功能性行為 , 因為孩子知道他可以藉此得到父母的注意力 。
parents can incentivize or disincentivize behavior simply by giving or withdrawing attention to their children .	父母能透過給予孩童注意力或戒斷行為 , 激勵或抑制孩童的注意力 。
but that's true for adults too .	但對成人也是如此 。
in fact , the behavior of entire communities and countries can be influenced , depending on where the international community chooses to focus its attention .	事實上 , 整個社區和國家的行為可以被影響 , 取決於國際社會選擇聚焦它的注意力 。
i believe that at the core of ending the conflict in the middle east and bringing peace is for us to transform nonviolence into a functional behavior by giving a lot more attention to the nonviolent leaders on the ground today .	我相信 , 結束中東的衝突並帶來和平的核心 , 就是要把非暴力抗爭轉變成一種功能性行為 , 做法是要讓非暴力的領袖更關注於現今的地面上非暴力的領導人 。
in the course of taking my film to villages in the west bank , in gaza and in east jerusalem , i have seen the impact that even one documentary film can have in influencing the transformation .	在拍攝約旦河西岸、加薩及東耶路撒冷的村子時 , 我看到了即使是一部紀錄片也能影響到轉變 。
in a village called wallajeh , which sits very close to jerusalem , the community was facing a very similar plight to budrus .	在瓦拉杰村 , 座落在耶路撒冷附近 , 這個社區正面臨和布德鲁斯村非常相似的困境 。
they were going to be surrounded , lose a lot of their lands and not have freedom of access , either to the west bank or jerusalem .	他們會被包圍 , 失去許多土地 , 沒有自由可用 , 可能是西岸或耶路撒冷 。
they had been using nonviolence for about two years but had grown disenchanted since nobody was paying attention .	他們已經使用了兩年的非暴力手段 , 但已經開始變得不知所措 , 因為沒有人注意 。
so we organized a screening .	所以我們安排了一份篩檢 。
a week later , they held the most wellattended and disciplined demonstration to date .	一個禮拜後他們舉辦了目前為止最有成就感和紀律的示威
the organizers say that the villagers , upon seeing the story of budrus documented in a film , felt that there were indeed people following what they were doing , that people cared .	舉辦人說村民看到布德鲁斯村的故事被記錄在影片裡覺得確實有人在跟隨他們的腳步人們在乎
so they kept on going .	所以他們繼續前進 。
on the israeli side , there is a new peace movement called solidariot , which means solidarity in hebrew .	在以色列這邊有一個新的和平運動叫做索里德拉爾特 , 意即希伯來語中的團結 。
the leaders of this movement have been using budrus as one of their primary recruiting tools .	這項運動的領導人把布德鲁斯村當作主要的工具來招募 。
they report that israelis who had never been active before , upon seeing the film , understand the power of nonviolence and start joining their activities .	他們說以色列人從未參與過活動 , 在看過影片的時候 , 了解到非暴力的力量 , 並加入他們的活動 。
the examples of wallajeh and the solidariot movement show that even a smallbudget independent film can play a role in transforming nonviolence into a functional behavior .	瓦拉杰和索里德拉爾特的獨立製片的例子顯示即使只是一小段預算的獨立製片也能在將非暴力變成功能性行為中起到作用 。
now imagine the power that big media players could have if they started covering the weekly nonviolent demonstrations happening in villages like bil'in , ni'lin , wallajeh , in jerusalem neighborhoods like sheikh jarrah and silwan the nonviolent leaders would become more visible , valued and effective in their work .	想像一下大型媒體開始報導在村子裡每週的非暴力遊行時所產生的影響力 , 比如比利寧、尼林、瓦拉杰 , 在耶路撒冷的鄰里 , 像希克哈拉和西華的非暴力領導人 , 在他們的工作中變得更明顯、更有價值、更有效 。
i believe that the most important thing is to understand that if we don't pay attention to these efforts , they are invisible , and it's as if they never happened .	我相信最重要的是要了解 , 如果我們不注意這些努力 , 它們是看不見的 , 就好像從來沒有發生過一樣 。
but i have seen first hand that if we do , they will multiply .	但我首先看到了如果我們這樣做 , 它們就會繁殖 。
if they multiply , their influence will grow in the overall israelipalestinian conflict .	如果他們再乘上 , 他們的影響會在以巴衝突中成長 。
and theirs is the kind of influence that can finally unblock the situation .	而他們的影響力就是那種能夠解開情況的影響力 。
these leaders have proven that nonviolence works in places like budrus .	這些領導人證明了非暴力是可行的在布德鲁斯村這樣的地方
let's give them attention so they can prove it works everywhere .	咱們來關注他們 , 讓他們能夠在任何地方證明它是可行的 。
simon sinek has a simple but powerful model for inspirational leadership all starting with a golden circle and the question " why ? " his examples include apple , martin luther king , and the wright brothers . . .	西蒙奈克有個簡單而強大的模式 , 能鼓舞人心的領導 , 始於黃金圈和 「 為什麼 」 , 他的例子包括蘋果、馬丁路德金 , 以及萊特兄弟 。
bullseye , business , entrepreneur , leadership , sales , selling , success	bullseye , 商業 , 企業家 , 領導力 , 銷售 , 賣 , 成功 。
simon sinek: how great leaders inspire action	simonsinek:偉大的領導人如何啟發行動 ?
how do you explain when things don't go as we assume ?	你要怎麼解釋當事情不如我們所想時 ?
or better , how do you explain when others are able to achieve things that seem to defy all of the assumptions ?	或者更好的是 , 你如何解釋當其他人能夠完成似乎違反所有假設的情況 ?
for example: why is apple so innovative ?	比如:為什麼蘋果電腦這麼有創意 ?
year after year , after year , after year , they're more innovative than all their competition .	年復一年 , 年復一年 , 他們比他們所有的競爭都更有創意 。
and yet , they're just a computer company .	然而 , 他們只是一家電腦公司 。
they're just like everyone else .	他們就像其他人一樣 。
they have the same access to the same talent , the same agencies , the same consultants , the same media .	他們有同樣的機會可以接觸到同樣才華、同樣的機構、同樣的顧問、同樣的媒體 。
then why is it that they seem to have something different ?	那麼為什麼他們似乎有所不同 ?
why is it that martin luther king led the civil rights movement ?	為什麼是馬丁•路德•金恩領導民權運動 ?
he wasn't the only man who suffered in a precivil rights america , and he certainly wasn't the only great orator of the day .	他不是唯一一個在美國受到平等公民權苦難的人 , 而且他肯定不是當時唯一的偉大演說家 。
and why is it that the wright brothers were able to figure out controlled , powered man flight when there were certainly other teams who were better qualified , better funded . . .	為什麼是萊特兄弟能夠想出控制權 , 操控人類飛機當飛機的確有其他團隊更有資格 , 更有資金
and they didn't achieve powered man flight , and the wright brothers beat them to it .	他們沒有達成人類飛行的成就 , 萊特兄弟打敗了他們 。
there's something else at play here .	這裡還有其他東西在玩 。
about three and a half years ago i made a discovery .	大約三年半前我有一個發現
and this discovery profoundly changed my view on how i thought the world worked , and it even profoundly changed the way in which i operate in it .	這個發現深深地改變了我對世界運作方式的看法 , 甚至深深地改變了我運作的方式 。
as it turns out , there's a pattern .	事實證明 , 有一個模式 。
as it turns out , all the great and inspiring leaders and organizations in the world whether it's apple or martin luther king or the wright brothers they all think , act and communicate the exact same way .	結果是 , 世界上所有偉大、鼓舞人心的領導人和組織 , 不論是蘋果、馬丁路德金、華特兄弟 , 他們都用同樣的方式來思考、行動和溝通 。
and it's the complete opposite to everyone else .	這完全和其他人相反 。
all i did was codify it , and it's probably the world's simplest idea .	我所做的就是將它編碼 , 很可能是世界上最簡單的想法 。
i call it the golden circle .	我稱它為黃金圈 。
why ? how ? what ?	為什麼 ? 怎麼做 ? 什麼 ?
this little idea explains why some organizations and some leaders are able to inspire where others aren't .	這個小小的點子解釋了為什麼有些組織和一些領導人能夠激發別人不在的地方 。
let me define the terms really quickly .	讓我很快地定義這個詞 。
every single person , every single organization on the planet knows what they do , 100 percent .	每一個人 , 地球上的每一個組織都知道他們在做什麼 , 百分之百知道他們在做什麼 。
some know how they do it , whether you call it your differentiated value proposition or your proprietary process or your usp .	有些人知道如何做 , 不論你稱它為你不同的價值主張、屬性過程 , 或你的usp 。
but very , very few people or organizations know why they do what they do .	但很少人或機構知道他們為什麼要做他們的事 。
and by " why " i don't mean " to make a profit . "	我說的 「 為什麼 」 並不是 「 為了賺錢 」 。
that's a result . it's always a result .	這是結果 。 它永遠是結果 。
by " why , " i mean: what's your purpose ?	被 「 為什麼 」 我的意思是:你的目的是什麼 ?
what's your cause ? what's your belief ?	你的起因是什麼 ? 你的信念是什麼 ?
why does your organization exist ?	為什麼你的組織存在 ?
why do you get out of bed in the morning ?	為什麼你早上要起床 ?
and why should anyone care ?	為什麼有人要在乎 ?
well , as a result , the way we think , the way we act , the way we communicate is from the outside in .	結果就是 , 我們思考的方式、行為的方式、我們的溝通方式都來自於外在 。
it's obvious . we go from the clearest thing to the fuzziest thing .	這很明顯 。 我們從最清楚到最模糊不清的東西 。
but the inspired leaders and the inspired organizations regardless of their size , regardless of their industry all think , act and communicate from the inside out .	但激勵人心的領導者和激勵人心的組織 , 不論它們的規模 , 不論它們的產業都把思考、行動和溝通從內而外傳 。
let me give you an example .	讓我舉個例子 。
i use apple because they're easy to understand and everybody gets it .	我用蘋果電腦是因為它很容易懂 , 每個人都懂 。
if apple were like everyone else , a marketing message from them might sound like this: " we make great computers .	如果蘋果電腦和其他人一樣 , 它的行銷訊息可能會像這樣: 「 我們製造出很好的電腦 。
they're beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	它們有著完美的設計 , 簡單的使用 , 友善的使用 。
want to buy one ? " " meh . "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
and that's how most of us communicate .	這就是我們大多數人溝通的方式 。
that's how most marketing is done , that's how most sales is done and that's how most of us communicate interpersonally .	這就是多數行銷手段的運作方式 , 多數銷售手段也是多數人與人之間的溝通方式 。
we say what we do , we say how we're different or how we're better and we expect some sort of a behavior , a purchase , a vote , something like that .	我們說我們做了什麼 , 我們說我們如何不同或我們如何好 , 我們期待某種行為、購買行為、投票等等 。
here's our new law firm: we have the best lawyers with the biggest clients , we always perform for our clients who do business with us .	這是我們的新法律事務所:我們有最好的律師 , 裡面有最好的客戶 , 我們總是為和我們做生意的客戶做生意 。
here's our new car: it gets great gas mileage , it has leather seats , buy our car .	這是我們的新車:它有很好的氣體里程數 , 有皮革座椅 , 買我們的車 。
here's how apple actually communicates .	這裡是蘋果電腦實際溝通的方式 。
" everything we do , we believe in challenging the status quo .	「 我們所做的一切 , 我們相信挑戰現狀 。
we believe in thinking differently .	我們相信用不同的角度思考 。
the way we challenge the status quo is by making our products beautifully designed , simple to use and user friendly .	我們挑戰現狀的方式是把我們的產品設計得很漂亮 , 很容易使用 , 很友善 。
we just happen to make great computers .	我們剛好製造了很棒的電腦 。
want to buy one ? "	想買一台嗎 ? 」
totally different right ? you're ready to buy a computer from me .	完全不一樣嗎 ? 你準備從我身上買一台電腦 。
all i did was reverse the order of the information .	我所做的只是反轉資訊的順序 。
what it proves to us is that people don't buy what you do ; people buy why you do it .	這證明了人們不買你做什麼 ; 人們買你的為什麼 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
this explains why every single person in this room is perfectly comfortable buying a computer from apple .	這解釋了為什麼在座的每個人都對買蘋果電腦感到相當自在 。
but we're also perfectly comfortable buying an mp3 player from apple , or a phone from apple , or a dvr from apple .	但我們也非常舒服地買蘋果電腦的mp3播放器或蘋果電腦的手機或蘋果電腦的dvr
but , as i said before , apple's just a computer company .	但是 , 正如我之前所說 , 蘋果電腦只是一家電腦公司 。
there's nothing that distinguishes them structurally from any of their competitors .	沒有什麼能把他們和任何競爭者在結構上區別開來 。
their competitors are all equally qualified to make all of these products .	他們的競爭對手都是同樣有資格做出這些產品 。
in fact , they tried .	事實上 , 他們試過 。
a few years ago , gateway came out with flat screen tvs .	幾年前 , gateway推出了平面電視 。
they're eminently qualified to make flat screen tvs .	他們很明顯夠資格製作平面電視 。
they've been making flat screen monitors for years .	他們已經做平面螢幕好幾年了 。
dell came out with mp3 players and pdas , and they make great quality products , and they can make perfectly welldesigned products and nobody bought one .	戴爾博士發明了mp3播放器和pda , 他們也能做出很好的品質產品 , 而且他們能做出完美設計的產品 , 但沒有人買 。
in fact , talking about it now , we can't even imagine buying an mp3 player from dell .	事實上 , 我們現在甚至無法想像從戴爾電腦買一台mp3播放器 。
why would you buy an mp3 player from a computer company ?	為什麼你會從電腦公司買mp3播放器 ?
but we do it every day .	但我們每天都在做 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
the goal is not to do business with everybody who needs what you have .	目標不是與所有需要你所擁有的人做生意 。
the goal is to do business with people who believe what you believe .	目標是要和相信你所相信的人做生意 。
here's the best part: none of what i'm telling you is my opinion .	最棒的是:我告訴你們的都不是我的意見 。
it's all grounded in the tenets of biology .	這都是從生物學角度看的 。
not psychology , biology .	不是心理學、生物學 。
if you look at a crosssection of the human brain , looking from the top down , what you see is the human brain is actually broken into three major components that correlate perfectly with the golden circle .	如果你看一下人腦的橫切面從上往下看你會看到人腦其實是分成三個主要元素與黃金圈完美相關
our newest brain , our homo sapien brain , our neocortex , corresponds with the " what " level .	我們的最新大腦 , 我們的大腦 , 我們的新皮層 , 都對應到 「 什麼 」 層次 。
the neocortex is responsible for all of our rational and analytical thought and language .	大腦皮層負責我們所有的理性、分析的想法和語言 。
the middle two sections make up our limbic brains , and our limbic brains are responsible for all of our feelings , like trust and loyalty .	中間兩個部分組成我們邊緣的腦 , 我們的邊緣腦負責所有的感受 , 比如信任和忠誠 。
it's also responsible for all human behavior , all decisionmaking , and it has no capacity for language .	它也同時負責所有人類的行為所有的決策而且它沒有語言的能力
in other words , when we communicate from the outside in , yes , people can understand vast amounts of complicated information like features and benefits and facts and figures .	換句話說 , 當我們從外而內溝通時是的 , 人們可以理解非常複雜的資訊量像是特色、好處、事實和數字
it just doesn't drive behavior .	它就是無法驅動行為 。
when we can communicate from the inside out , we're talking directly to the part of the brain that controls behavior , and then we allow people to rationalize it with the tangible things we say and do .	當我們能由內而外溝通時 , 我們就正對著大腦控制行為的區塊說話 , 然後我們允許人們去合理化它 , 用我們所說的有形事物去做 。
this is where gut decisions come from .	決策就是這樣來的 。
you know , sometimes you can give somebody all the facts and figures , and they say , " i know what all the facts and details say , but it just doesn't feel right . "	有時候你會給別人所有的事實和數字 , 他們會說: 「 我知道事實和細節是什麼 , 但感覺就是不對的 。 」
why would we use that verb , it doesn't " feel " right ?	為什麼我們要用這個動詞 , 沒有 「 感覺 」 呢 ?
because the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking doesn't control language .	因為控制決策的腦並不控制語言
and the best we can muster up is , " i don't know . it just doesn't feel right . "	我們最多能整理出的是: 「 我不知道 , 感覺不太對勁 。 」
or sometimes you say you're leading with your heart , or you're leading with your soul .	或者 , 有時你說你在帶著你的心 , 或你在帶著你的靈魂領導 。
well , i hate to break it to you , those aren't other body parts controlling your behavior .	嗯 , 我很不想跟你們說 , 這些都不是身體的其他部位控制你的行為 。
it's all happening here in your limbic brain , the part of the brain that controls decisionmaking and not language .	這一切都發生在你邊緣的腦裡 , 控制決策的腦 , 而不是語言 。
but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道為什麼你做你所做的事 , 人們會回應為什麼你做你所做的事 , 那麼你如何才能讓人們為你投票 , 或是向你買東西 , 或更重要的是 , 忠誠和想要成為你所做的事的一部分 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	同樣的 , 目標不只是要賣給需要你所擁有的人 ; 目標是要賣給那些相信你所相信的人們 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不是只在雇用需要工作的人而是要雇用那些相信你所相信的事的人
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是這麼說 , 你知道 , 如果你雇用員工 , 因為他們可以做事 , 他們會為了你的錢而工作 , 但如果你雇用相信你所相信的人 , 他們將會用血汗和淚水幫你工作 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	沒有比萊特兄弟更好的例子了 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大部分的人不知道samuelpierpontlangley 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到二十世紀初 , 追求人類飛翔就像當時的網路公司一樣 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	samuelpierpontlangley曾經擁有 , 我們假設的成功之處 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	我的意思是 , 即使是現在 , 你也會問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或你的公司失敗了 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你同樣的三樣東西:不足以支配 , 不適合的人 , 市場環境不良 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	這三件事都是一樣的 , 所以讓我們來探討一下 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	samuelpierpontlangley從國防部得到5萬美金來研發這飛行機器
money was no problem .	資金根本沒問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他擔任哈佛大學的席位 , 在史密森工作 , 和他有著極為相連的關係 , 他認識了當天所有的大人 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他聘用了最好的心靈資金 , 而市場狀況非常好 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報跟著他到處跑 , 每個人都為langley加油 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	為什麼我們從來沒有聽過samuelpierpontlangley ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里外的俄亥俄州 , 俄維爾和威爾伯•萊特 , 他們完全沒有我們認為的成功關鍵 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 ; 他們付錢給他們的夢想 , 用他們的腳踏車店的收入 ; 萊特兄弟團隊沒有一個人受大學教育 , 連歐維爾或威布爾 ; 紐約時報也沒有在任何地方追蹤他們 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別在於 , 歐維爾和威爾布是因爲目標和信念而驅動的 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信 , 如果他們能想出這架飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的軌道 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	samuelpierpontlangley不同 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想變得富有 , 他想要成名 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在追求富人 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	你看 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	相信萊特兄弟的夢想的人用血汗和淚水和他們一同努力 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人則是為了賺錢而工作 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們會說故事 , 每當萊特兄弟出門 , 他們就得拿出五套零件 , 因為這是他們出門前會墜機的次數 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最後 , 在1903年12月17日萊特兄弟起飛 , 甚至沒有人能體驗它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們在幾天後發現這件事 。
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的證明langley被錯誤的動機所驅使當萊特兄弟起飛那天 , 他辭職了
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可能會說: 「 這真是很了不起的發現 , 各位 , 我會改善你們的技術 。 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是第一人 , 他沒有變有錢 , 也沒有變有名 , 所以他辭職了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談論你所相信的事物 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的人們 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但 , 為什麼吸引那些相信你所相信的人們很重要 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	所謂創意的散播法則 , 如果你不知道這個法則 , 你絕對知道這個術語 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	我們人口中前2.5%的人口是創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	接下來的13.5%是早期使用者 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	接下來的34%是早期的多數 , 晚期的多數和低落 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買觸控電話的唯一理由是你再也買不到輪迴電話了 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們在不同時間坐在不同地點 , 以這樣的規模坐在不同的地方 , 但創新的散播法則告訴我們 , 如果你想要大眾市場成功或大眾市場接受一個想法 , 你就不能擁有它 , 直到你達到了在15%到18%之間的市場侵犯點 , 然後系統就會一面倒 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你對新事業的轉變是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很願意很驕傲地告訴你: 「 喔 , 大約10% 。 」
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以追蹤超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有10%的 「 了解它 」 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	我們就是這樣描述它們的 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	就好像那種直覺的感覺: 「 喔 , 他們就是懂的 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:在你做生意之前 , 要如何找到那些拿到卻沒有拿到的人 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	正如同傑弗里•摩爾所說的 " 跨越鴻溝 " , 你看 , 早期大多數人不會嘗試什麼 , 除非他人先嘗試 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	這些人、發明家、早期採用者 , 他們都很自在地做這些直覺決策 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們對做這些直覺的決定感到更自在 , 驅動著他們對世界的信念 , 而不只是產品的可得性 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些人排了六個小時買了一支iphone剛上市 , 下星期你還可以走進商店買下一支離架上的iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些人剛上市時花了四萬美元在平面電視上即使這項科技還在未被實踐
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順帶一提 , 他們沒有這麼做 , 因為這項技術很棒 , 他們是為了自己而做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	那是因為他們想要當第一個 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼就證明了你相信什麼
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做那些證明他們所相信的事
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	人們買iphone的理由是在半小時內排隊排六個小時 , 是因為他們相信這個世界 , 以及他們希望所有人看到他們:他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個有名的例子 , 一個有名的失敗以及有名的成功關於創意的散播法則 。
first , the famous failure .	第一 , 著名的失敗 。
it's a commercial example .	這是一個商業上的例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如我們前面所說 , 第二 , 成功的關鍵就是金錢 , 對的人和對的市場環境 , 對嗎 ? 你當時應該要有成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	大約八、九年前 , tivo上市後 , 至今 , 它們是市場上最高品質的產品 , 手放下 , 完全沒有爭議 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	資金非常充足 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場的狀況很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們把tivo當作動詞 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我總是tivo東西在我時代華納dvr的垃圾上 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivo卻失敗了 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺到錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	他們上了ipo之後股票價格大約是30到40美元然後從未超過10美元交易過
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為在6號以上交易 , 除非有幾個小突點 。
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看 , 當tivo推出他們的產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們擁有的一切 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一個可以暫停現場電視的產品 , 跳過商業廣告 , 回播現場電視 , 記下你的收視習慣 , 連問都沒有 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	憤世嫉俗的大多數人說: 「 我們不相信你 。
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要它 , 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你嚇到我們了 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是那種想要完全掌控生活各個層面的人 , 各位 , 我們有一項產品給你 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它可以暫停現場電視、跳過商業廣告、記住你的收視習慣等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做什麼 ; 他們買你的為什麼而你做什麼僅僅是你相信什麼的證明
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我舉一個成功的例子來說明創意的散播法則 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天 , 25萬人來到華盛頓的購物中心聽金恩博士演說 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們沒有寄出任何一張邀請函 , 也沒有網站去查看日期 。
how do you do that ?	該怎麼做呢 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	金恩博士不是美國唯一一個偉大的演說家
he wasn't the only man in america who suffered in a precivil rights america .	他不是在美國唯一一個受到早期公民權威脅的人
in fact , some of his ideas were bad .	事實上 , 他的一些點子很糟 。
but he had a gift .	但他有一個禮物 。
he didn't go around telling people what needed to change in america .	他沒有到處告訴人們在美國需要什麼樣的改變 。
he went around and told people what he believed .	他四處告訴人們他所相信的 。
" i believe , i believe , i believe , " he told people .	「 我相信 , 我相信 , 我相信 。 」 他告訴人們 。
and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而相信他所相信的人們接受了他的觀點 , 使它成為他們自己的目標 , 他們也告訴人們 。
and some of those people created structures to get the word out to even more people .	有些人創造了一些結構 , 讓更多人知道 。
and lo and behold , 250 , 000 people showed up on the right day at the right time to hear him speak .	你看 , 25 , 000人在正確的日子裡 , 剛好聽到他的演說 。
how many of them showed up for him ?	有多少人為了他而出現 ?
they showed up for themselves .	他們為了他們自己出現 。
it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在八月中期 , 搭公車 , 在華盛頓的陽光下穿梭 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 重點不是黑人和白人25%的觀眾是白人
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	金恩博士相信在這個世界上有兩種不同的法律:一種由較高權威制定的法律 , 和由人類制定的法律 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	除非所有人類所制定的法律與更高權威制定的法律一致 , 否則我們將生活在一個公平的世界 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	正巧公民權運動是幫助他生命的最佳成就 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追隨 , 不是為了他 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順帶一提 , 他發表了 「 我有一個夢想 」 演講 , 而不是 「 我有一個計畫 」 的演講 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在聽政客用他們完整的12點計畫
they're not inspiring anybody .	他們沒有激勵任何人 。
because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有一些領導者 , 也有那些領導者 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者持有權力或權威的位置 , 但那些領導的人啟發了我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	不論是個人或組織我們跟隨那些領導的人不是因為我們必須而是因為我們想要
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們跟隨那些領導的人 , 不是為了他們 , 而是為了我們自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	是那些以 「 為什麼 」 開頭的人 , 能夠啟發他們身邊的人 , 或找到鼓舞他們的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要怎麼記住車子停在哪裡 ? 你要怎麼知道你正朝著正確的方向移動 ? 神經科學家neilburges研究我們周圍的神經機制 , 以及他們如何與記憶和想像力連結 。
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、神經科學、科學 ,
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neilburges:你的大腦如何告訴你你在哪裡 。
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們把車停在一個很大的停車場 , 我們要如何記得我們停在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	荷馬面對了一個問題 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著去了解他的大腦到底發生了什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	我們先從海馬體開始 , 用黃色標示 , 也就是記憶的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你的身體有損傷 , 就像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你就無法記住很多東西 , 包括你停車的地方 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它的名字是以拉丁文 " 海馬 " 命名 , 和它相似 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	如同其餘的腦 , 它是由神經元所構成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	人腦內有大約一千億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	神經元藉由電脈衝或電流刺激相互交流而彼此溝通
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	海馬體是由兩片細胞組成的 , 它們彼此緊密相連 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家開始了解空間記憶是如何運作的 , 藉由記錄老鼠在覓食或探索環境時的個別神經元所發出的聲音 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	想像我們紀錄單一個神經元在這隻老鼠的海馬體中
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它發出一小塊電流 , 就會有一個紅點和一個點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	我們可以看到這個神經元知道當老鼠進入某一特定的環境時 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	藉由發電尖刺激大腦向大腦發送訊號
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	我們可以將神經元的發射速率作為動物所在位置的函數 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們紀錄很多不同的神經元當動物移動到其周圍的不同區域時 , 我們會看到不同的神經元發射出訊號 , 就像這個方形的盒子裡看到的那樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	所以他們一起為大腦繪製一張地圖 , 持續告訴大腦: 「 我現在在自己的環境中了哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	位置細胞也會被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	癲癇患者有時需要大腦的電訊活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病患會玩一個電玩遊戲 , 在小鎮附近開車 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	海馬體中的位置細胞就會活躍起來 , 每當他們開車經過某個特定的小鎮時 , 就會開始發射電脈衝 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼 , 位置細胞又如何知道老鼠在其環境中的哪個位置 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們環境的邊界是特別重要的 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	上方的這一隻 , 像是在兩面牆之間開火 , 老鼠就在那兒 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你把盒子放大 , 發射地點就會擴大 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	下面這張圖是當南方靠近一面牆時就會發射出來 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你在盒子中放置另一道牆 , 細胞在兩處都會被激發 , 當動物在盒子裡四處探索時 , 南方都有一面牆 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以 , 這種預測就能感測你周圍的界限和邊界方向等等 , 對海馬體是特別重要的 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 由海馬體輸入的訊號 , 針對海馬體的哪些細胞 , 針對特定的界限或邊緣 , 在它四處探索時 , 會做出反應 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	你可以看到 , 左邊的細胞當動物碰到東邊的牆的時候就會被激發不管是方形盒子的邊緣還是圓形的邊緣或是圓形的邊緣也就是動物在桌子邊緣移動的邊緣
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	右邊的細胞當碰到南方邊界或是邊緣的時候就會被激發 , 不管是桌邊的邊緣還是坡 , 或甚至是兩張桌子之間的隔閡 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	所以這是我們認為位置細胞可以決定動物所在的位置 。
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也可以測試我們認為物體的位置 , 例如在簡單的環境中 , 或是車子的位置 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	所以我們可以讓人們去探索一個環境 , 看看他們需要記得的位置 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放回環境中 , 一般來說 , 它們很擅長把標記放到他們認為旗幟或車子在哪裡 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在一些試驗中 , 我們可以改變環境的形狀和大小 , 就像我們在位置細胞上做的一樣 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在這個例子中 , 我們可以看到他們認為旗幟位置的改變是如何改變環境的形狀和大小 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 你所看到的旗子是在一個小正方形的環境中交叉的地方 , 如果你問人們這是在哪裡的位置 , 但是你讓環境變大了 , 他們認為旗幟的位置會跟位置細胞被激發的位置完全相同 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就好像你還記得旗幟被激發的位置 , 先儲存你位置的位置細胞 , 然後你可以藉由四處走走走找到那個位置 , 這樣你就可以找到最適合你位置細胞被激發的模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	這會引導你回到你想要記得的地方 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們移動的方向 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以 , 若我們採取一些出去路徑──也許我們停車 , 我們會知道是因為我們自己的動作 , 整合這條路的方向──大約就是要回去的方向 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	位置細胞也會得到這種路徑整合 , 從一種稱為網格細胞的細胞中輸入 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	網格細胞也是在輸入海馬體時找到它們有點像位置細胞
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但當老鼠四處探索時 , 每個細胞都會發射出一系列不同的位置 , 這些位置會在整個環境中形成一個驚人的三角形網格 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你錄下數個網格細胞 , 分別用不同的顏色 , 每一塊都有一個網格狀的模式在整個環境中激發 , 而每一塊細胞的網格激發模式會稍微改變 , 移到其他細胞之間 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	紅色的會在這個格子上發射 , 綠色的會發射 , 藍色的在這個格子上 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	綜合起來 , 就好像老鼠可以在其環境中建立一個虛擬的位置網路──有點像是地圖上找到的緯度和經度線條 , 只是用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動的時候 , 電訊的活動可以從這些細胞傳到下一個細胞 , 以追蹤它所在的位置 , 這樣它就可以利用它自己的動作去知道它在環境中的位置 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有網格細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	由於所有的網格狀細胞激發模式都有相同的對稱軸 , 在這裡橘色標出的方位 , 這表示整個網格的運作會根據位置在六個方向之間的移動而有所改變 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	所以我們可以把人放進核磁共振儀儀器讓他們做一個像我剛剛展示給你們看的一個電玩遊戲並尋找這個訊號
