and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	確實 , 在人腦內部的輸送皮質也就是老鼠腦內的網格細胞
so back to homer .	回到荷馬 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能正在想他的車子在哪裡在遠方和方向的位置來延伸建築物和邊界在他停車的地方
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	這將由邊界偵測細胞的激發來呈現 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他還記得他從汽車停車場中走出的路線圖 , 圖上都是用網格細胞激發出來的 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	這兩種細胞都可以讓位置細胞發射 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他可以藉由移動找到他車子的位置 , 來找到目前位置與記憶中車子停放的位置 , 位置細胞的激發模式與他車子停放的位置 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那個位置 , 不考慮視覺暗示他的車子是否真的在那兒 。
maybe it's been towed .	可能已經被估價了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	除了空間記憶以外 , 如果我們觀察整個大腦內的網格狀激發模式 , 我們還可以在一系列的地點看到它 , 當我們在做各種自傳記憶工作時 , 例如你上次參加婚禮時 , 記得會發生什麼事 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以 , 神經機制代表我們周圍的環境 , 也能產生視覺上的影像 , 這樣我們才能重新創造空間的景象 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像那些事件時 , 曾經發生在我們身上的事件 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	如果發生這種事 , 你的記憶可以藉由位置細胞互相啟動 , 通過高密度的相互連接 , 再重新啟動邊界細胞 , 創造你觀點周圍的空間結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	網格細胞可以移動這個視野穿過那個空間 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另外一種我還沒提到的細胞頭向細胞它們就像是指南針一樣會根據面向不同方向而有不同的激發
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以從中找出你想要的視覺圖像的方向來定義你的視覺影像 , 所以你可以想像當你在這場婚禮時發生了什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是一個例子 , 一個存在於認知神經科學的新時代 , 我們開始了解到心理過程 , 像是你如何記得、想像 , 甚至是以數十億個獨立神經元為基礎的行為來思考 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下 , 一個由機構、政府、私營部門和大眾共同推動的全球安全推動的全球安全 。 這並不只是開放式保護風扇的遙遠希望 , 它是jamesstavridis的最高指揮官 , 北大西洋公約組織的最高統治者 , 他們和距離現今的軍方歷史 , 來解釋為何未來應該要建造橋樑而非牆 。
collaboration , global issues , opensource , peace , politics , social media , violence , war	合作、全球議題、資源、和平、政治、社交媒體、暴力、戰爭 。
james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯•斯特瓦里迪斯:北約的最高指揮官是如何看待全球安全的 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我將要談一點關於開放資源的安全性 , 因為在21世紀 , 我們必須在安全上變得更好 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	首先 , 讓我們回顧一下20世紀 , 了解一下安全的風格是如何為我們而工作的 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是verdun , 法國的戰場 , 就在北約在比利時總部的北方 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在verdun , 超過三百天 , 七十萬人被殺 , 約兩千人一天 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它向前推進到第二次世界大戰 , 你會看到斯大林格戰 , 300天 , 2百萬人死亡 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰 , 繼續建造圍牆 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一次世界大戰的壕溝 , 到二次世界大戰的馬其頓防線 , 然後進入冷戰 , 鐵幕 , 柏林牆 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的主題是 , 不要建造一道牆來創造安全 , 我們要建造一座橋 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲一座有名的橋 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	橋樑在drina河上 , 是由idevoandrice所創作的 , 它談到如何在歐洲和巴爾幹地區最麻煩的部分長時間一直以來都有巨大的牆壁 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近 , 在過去十年間 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始了 , 猶豫地聚集在一起 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我想再次強調 , 開放式安全是把國際的 , 跨部門的 , 私人的和公共的聯繫起來 , 用策略性的溝通 , 主要是在社交網路上 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我來談談為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們全球的公有物受到各式各樣的攻擊 , 沒有威脅到全球公有物的根源可以用建牆來解決 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	顯然 , 我是水手 。
this is a ship , a liner , clipping through the indian ocean .	這是一艘船 , 排列隊 , 在印度洋上航行 。
what's wrong with this picture ?	這張照片有什麼問題嗎 ?
it's got concertina wire along the sides of it .	在它的側邊有吉祥物鋼線 。
that's to prevent pirates from attacking it .	那是用來防止海盜攻擊海盜的 。
piracy is a very active threat today around the world . this is in the indian ocean .	海盜現今在世界範圍內是一個非常活躍的威脅 。 這是在印度洋 。
piracy is also very active in the strait of malacca .	海盜也在馬拉加的源頭非常活躍 。
it's active in the gulf of guinea .	它在幾內亞灣很活躍 。
we see it in the caribbean .	我們在加勒比海看到 。
it's a $10billionayear discontinuity in the global transport system .	這是全球交通運輸系統價值10億美元的不連續性 。
last year , at this time , there were 20 vessels , 500 mariners held hostage .	去年 , 當時有20艘船 , 500名船員被綁架 。
this is an attack on the global commons .	這是對全球公有物的攻擊 。
we need to think about how to address it .	我們需要思考如何解決它 。
let's shift to a different kind of sea , the cyber sea .	讓我們轉換到另一種海洋 , 網路的海洋 。
here are photographs of two young men .	這是兩個年輕人的照片 。
at the moment , they're incarcerated .	此刻 , 他們被監禁了 。
they conducted a credit card fraud that netted them over 10 billion dollars .	他們做了一個信用卡詐騙案 , 淨利超過一百億美金 。
this is part of cybercrime which is a $2trillionayear discontinuity in the global economy .	這是網路犯罪的一部分 , 是全球經濟2兆美元的不連續性 。
two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是英國的國民生產毛額而已 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	這片網路世界 , 我們知道這片網路開放是最基本的 , 在威脅之下也非常重要 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	我在全球公有物中擔憂的另一件事就是人口販賣所造成的威脅 , 如麻醉劑 , 鴉片 , 從阿富汗穿過歐洲到美國的流動所造成的威脅 。
we worry about cocaine coming from the andean ridge north .	我們擔心從andeanridge北部來的可卡因 。
we worry about the movement of illegal weapons and trafficking . above all , perhaps , we worry about human trafficking , and the awful cost of it .	我們擔心非法武器的運輸 。 最重要的是 , 我們擔心人口販運 , 以及它的成本 。
trafficking moves largely at sea but in other parts of the global commons .	大部分人口販賣活動在海洋上 , 但在全球的其他公有物上 。
this is a photograph , and i wish i could tell you that this is a very hightech piece of us navy gear that we're using to stop the trafficking .	這是一張照片 , 我希望我能告訴你這是一個非常高科技的美國海軍裝備 , 用來阻止人口販賣 。
the bad news is , this is a semisubmersible run by drug cartels .	壞消息是 , 這是販毒集團的半潛水服 。
it was built in the jungles of south america .	它是在南美叢林中建造的 。
we caught it with that lowtech raft — — and it was carrying six tons of cocaine .	我們用低科技的木筏逮捕了它 , 它帶著六噸的可卡因 。
crew of four . sophisticated communications sweep .	四個船員 。 精密的通訊掃描 。
this kind of trafficking , in narcotics , in humans , in weapons , god forbid , in weapons of mass destruction , is part of the threat to the global commons .	這種運送麻醉劑 , 人、武器、大規模殺傷性武器 , 這種運輸是對全球公有物威脅的一部分 。
and let's pull it together in afghanistan today .	讓我們一起來談今天在阿富汗 。
this is a field of poppies in afghanistan .	這是阿富汗的一塊平頂山
eighty to 90 percent of the world's poppy , opium and heroin , comes out of afghanistan .	世界上百分之八十到九十的小狗 , 鴉片和海洛因來自阿富汗 。
we also see there , of course , terrorism .	當然 , 我們也看到了恐怖主義 。
this is where al qaeda is staged from .	這就是基地組織建立的地方 。
we also see a very strong insurgency embedded there .	我們也看到一個非常強烈的暴動藏在其中 。
so this terrorism concern is also part of the global commons , and what we must address .	所以這種恐怖主義的擔憂也是全球公有物的一部分 , 也是我們必須處理的 。
so here we are , 21st century .	所以 , 在21世紀 ,
we know our 20thcentury tools are not going to work .	我們知道我們20世紀的工具行不通 。
what should we do ?	我們該怎麼做 ?
i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我認為我們不會僅僅依靠槍支來遞送安全 。
we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我們不能僅僅依靠槍支 。
we will need the application of military force .	我們需要軍事力量的應用 。
when we do it , we must do it well , and competently .	當我們這樣做時 , 我們必須要把事情做好 , 且要有競爭力 。
but my thesis is , opensource security is about international , interagency , privatepublic connection pulled together by this idea of strategic communication on the internet .	但我的論點是 , 開放式安全是關於國際的 , 跨部門的 , 私人和公共的聯繫 , 由互聯網的策略性溝通而引導 。
let me give you a couple of examples of how this works in a positive way .	讓我舉幾個例子 , 說明它如何以正面的方式運作 。
this is afghanistan . these are afghan soldiers .	這是阿富汗 。 這些是阿富汗的士兵 。
they are all holding books .	他們都拿著書 。
you should say , " that's odd . i thought i read that this demographic , young men and women in their 20s and 30s , is largely illiterate in afghanistan . "	你應該說: 「 這很奇怪 , 我想我曾讀到過這個人口統計數字在二十多歲和三十多歲的年輕人在阿富汗大多是文盲 。 」
you would be correct .	你可能會是對的 。
eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入阿富汗安全部隊時 , 85%是看不懂的 。
why ? because the taliban withheld education during the period of time in which these men and women would have learned to read .	為什麼 ? 因為 , 在這些男人和女人學會閱讀的時代 , 塔利班的沉重教育 。
so the question is , so , why are they all standing there holding books ?	問題是 , 為什麼他們站在那裡拿著書 ?
the answer is , we are teaching them to read in literacy courses by nato in partnership with private sector entities , in partnership with development agencies .	答案是 , 我們在教導他們閱讀 , 通過北約組織的課程 , 通過私人機構的合作 , 通過與發展機構的合作 。
we've taught well over 200 , 000 afghan security forces to read and write at a basic level .	我們已經教了超過20萬的阿富汗安全部隊 , 基本上就是要讀和寫 。
when you can read and write in afghanistan , you will typically put a pen in your pocket .	當你能在阿富汗讀和寫的時候 , 通常你可以把筆放在口袋裡 。
at the ceremonies , when these young men and women graduate , they take that pen with great pride , and put it in their pocket .	在畢業典禮上 , 當這些年輕男女畢業時 , 他們很驕傲地拿起筆 , 放在他們的口袋裡 。
this is bringing together international — there are 50 nations involved in this mission — interagency — these development agencies — and privatepublic , to take on this kind of security .	全球有50個國家參與這項任務 。 這些開發機構私人和公共的開發機構 , 來對付這種安全 。
now , we are also teaching them combat skills , of course , but i would argue , opensource security means connecting in ways that create longer lasting security effect .	我們現在當然也教他們打仗技能 , 但我認為 , 開放式安全意味著用創造更持久的安全方法聯繫在一起 。
this is a us navy warship .	這是美國海軍戰艦 。
it's called the comfort .	叫做舒適感 。
there's a sister ship called the mercy .	有一艘姐妹船叫做mercy 。
they are hospital ships .	他們是醫院的船 。
this one , the comfort , operates throughout the caribbean and the coast of south america conducting patient treatments .	安慰號在加勒比海和南美洲的海岸進行病人的治療 。
on a typical cruise , they'll do 400 , 000 patient treatments .	在一般的巡迴演出中 , 他們會進行四十萬個治療 。
it is crewed not strictly by military but by a combination of humanitarian organizations: operation hope , project smile .	船員不是嚴格地執政 , 而是結合人道主義組織:營運希望、微笑 。
other organizations send volunteers .	其他組織送來志工 。
interagency physicians come out .	內部的醫生出來了 。
they're all part of this .	這些都是其中的一部分 。
to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	舉個例子來說 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 跟他媽媽走了兩天來到安慰號上的眼科診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	在他裝好時 , 透過他的極端視野 , 他突然抬頭說: 「 媽媽 , veoelmundo 。 」
" mom , i see the world . "	「 媽媽 , 我看到世界了 。 」
multiply this by 400 , 000 patient treatments , this privatepublic collaboration with security forces , and you begin to see the power of creating security in a very different way .	把這個乘以四十萬名病人治療 , 這個私人和安全部隊的合作 , 你就會開始看到用非常不同的方式創造安全的力量 。
here you see baseball players .	這裡你可以看到棒球選手 。
can you pick out the two us army soldiers in this photograph ?	你可以在這張照片中挑出兩名美國陸軍士兵嗎 ?
they are the two young men on either side of these young boys . this is part of a series of baseball clinics , where we have explored collaboration between major league baseball , the department of state , who sets up the diplomatic piece of this , military baseball players , who are real soldiers with real skills but participate in this mission , and they put on clinics throughout latin america and the caribbean , in honduras , in nicaragua , in all of the central american and caribbean nations where baseball is so popular , and it creates security .	他們可能是這兩位年輕男子這可是棒球診所的一部分我們曾研究過大聯盟棒球聯賽、國務院這些人為外交官像是軍事棒球選手他們是真正的軍事棒球員但他們參與了這項任務他們到了拉丁美洲和加勒比地區 , 開到了霍勒斯 , 開到了美國和加勒比地區
it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它向年輕人展示了關於健身和生活的榜樣 , 也是我認為幫助為我們創造安全 。
another aspect of this partnership is in disaster relief .	這種合作的另一面是災難救援 。
this is a us air force helicopter participating after the tsunami in 2004 which killed 250 , 000 people .	這是美國空軍的直升機 , 在2004年在海嘯之後 , 造成25萬人死亡 。
in each of these major disasters — the tsunami in 2004 , 250 , 000 dead , the kashmiri earthquake in pakistan , 2005 , 85 , 000 dead , the haitian earthquake , about 300 , 000 dead , more recently the awful earthquaketsunami combination which struck japan and its nuclear industry — in all of these instances , we see partnerships between international actors , interagency , privatepublic working with security forces to respond to this kind of natural disaster .	在這些重大災難中2004年海嘯 , 250000死 , 2005年巴基斯坦的kashmiri地震 , 85000死 , 海地地地震 , 30萬人 , 更近期發生在日本發生的地震災難 , 以及其核工業--所有這些例子中 , 我們看到了國際間 , 跨部門的合作 , 和公私間的合作 , 與自然災害合作 。
so these are examples of this idea of opensource security .	這些是關於 「 開放式安全 」 的例子 。
we tie it together , increasingly , by doing things like this .	我們透過這樣的方式將它連結在一起 。
now , you're looking at this thinking , " ah , admiral , these must be sea lanes of communication , or these might be fiber optic cables . "	現在 , 你看著這個想法: 「 啊 , 米德 , 這些一定是通信的海道 , 或者這些可能是光纖電纜 。 」
no . this is a graphic of the world according to twitter .	不 , 這是twitter的圖表
purple are tweets . green are geolocation .	紫色是推特訊息 。 綠色是地點分配 。
white is the synthesis .	白色是合成 。
it's a perfect evocation of that great population survey , the six largest nations in the world in descending order: china , india , facebook , the united states , twitter and indonesia .	這很能喚起全世界六大人口調查 , 依次是中國、印度、臉書、美國、推特 , 和印尼 。
why do we want to get in these nets ?	為什麼我們要進到這些蚊帳呢 ?
why do we want to be involved ?	為什麼我們想要參與其中 ?
we talked earlier about the arab spring , and the power of all this .	我們之前談到阿拉伯之春 , 以及它的力量 。
i'll give you another example , and it's how you move this message .	我再舉一個例子 , 就是你如何傳遞訊息 。
i gave a talk like this in london a while back about this point . i said , as i say to all of you , i'm on facebook . friend me .	我在倫敦發表過這樣的演說 , 我對你們說 , 我在facebook上 , 朋友我 。
got a little laugh from the audience .	聽眾有點笑 。
there was an article which was run by ap , on the wire .	有一篇文章 , 文章是ap在電線上運行 。
got picked up in two places in the world: finland and indonesia .	世界上有兩個地方 , 芬蘭和印尼 。
the headline was: nato admiral needs friends .	標題是:北大西洋公約需要好友 。
and the story was a catalyst , and the next morning i had hundreds of facebook friend requests from indonesians and finns , mostly saying , " admiral , we heard you need a friend , and oh , by the way , what is nato ? "	這個故事是催化劑 , 第二天早上我有上百個facebook好友請求 , 來自印尼和芬蘭 , 大部分都會說: 「 阿德 , 我們聽說你需要一個朋友 , 喔 , 北約是什麼 ? 」
yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們會笑 , 但這是我們如何移動這個訊息 , 移動那個訊息就是我們如何連結國際 , 跨部門 , 私人 , 和這些社交網來協助創造安全 。
now , let me hit a somber note .	現在 , 讓我說個嚴肅的話 。
this is a photograph of a brave british soldier .	這是一位勇敢的英國士兵的照片 。
he's in the scots guards .	他在蘇格蘭衛隊 。
he's standing the watch in helmand , in southern afghanistan .	他正站在helmand , 在阿富汗南部 。
i put him here to remind us , i would not want anyone to leave the room thinking that we do not need capable , competent militaries who can create real military effect .	我讓他來提醒我們 , 我不希望任何人離開這個房間 , 認為我們不需要有能力、有能力的軍事人員 , 能創造出真正的軍事效應 。
that is the core of who we are and what we do , and we do it to protect freedom , freedom of speech , all the things we treasure in our societies .	那是我們是誰的核心 , 我們的工作 , 我們做這件事來保護言論自由 , 言論自由 , 所有我們在社會中珍視的東西 。
but , you know , life is not an onandoff switch .	但你知道 , 人生並不是個開端 。
you don't have to have a military that is either in hard combat or is in the barracks .	你不需要軍隊在戰鬥中 , 或在軍事中 。
i would argue life is a rheostat .	我會主張生命是rheostat 。
you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須調整 , 並且我認為我們該如何在21世紀建立安全 , 有時候我們會在真正的戰爭和危機中運用硬實的力量 , 但將會有很多時候 , 就像我們今天談到的 , 我們的軍隊可以使21世紀安全 , 國際 , 跨部門 , 公私部門 , 與溝通建立良好關係 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	最後我想說今天早些時候聽到的關於維基百科的消息 。 我時常用維基百科查一些事實 , 你們都知道 , 維基百科不是靠12位聰明的人把文章鎖在房間裡寫 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科是每天數萬人投入的資訊 , 數百萬人的提取信息 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這完美的形象就是沒有一個人能這麼聰明 , 能讓我們一起思考 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有一個人 , 沒有一個聯盟 , 沒有一個國家 , 沒有一個我們一起想的那麼聰明 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的宣言很簡單:一個所有人類都可以自由共享所有知識的世界 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的論點是 , 通過結合國際 , 跨部門 , 私人 , 戰略溝通 , 在21世紀 , 我們能創造出所有安全的總和 。
thank you very much . thank you . thank you .	非常謝謝 。 謝謝 。
